    三异笔谈　清　许仲元撰
    　　　序
    　　　道光丁亥，余罢官，羁棲武林柳泉太守郡斋，客来闲话，苦气弱不能剧谈，乃以笔代舌，自夏徂秋，积成卷帙，熙朝掌故，则询之柳泉，往代轶闻，则证之子寿，正淮两别风之舛，以及弄獐伏猎之讹，则闲蘥世讲之急我尤勤焉，辄题数语，名之曰《三异笔谈》一集。归里后，如有续纂，当再募资刊之。七十三翁许仲元识

    Explanation

    1

    Three Strange Talks
    By Xu Zhongyuan of the Qing Dynasty

    Preface
    In the year Dinghai of the Daoguang era, I was dismissed from office and temporarily lodged in the magistrate's office of Liuquan in Wulin. When guests came to chat, I found myself too weak to engage in intense conversation, so I resorted to writing instead. From summer to autumn, my writings accumulated into volumes. For anecdotes from the prosperous era, I consulted Liuquan; for stories from past dynasties, I verified them with Zishou. To correct discrepancies in different versions of the same story and errors in historical records, I relied heavily on the diligent assistance of my friend. I would jot down a few remarks and name the collection Three Strange Talks. If I continue the work upon returning home, I will raise funds for its publication.
    Seventy-three-year-old Xu Zhongyuan

    2

    三异笔谈卷一
    　　　茸城王氏
    　　　茸城阀阅，以王氏为冠。王氏有二，郡人以里第分，呼曰东王西王。西王前明时已簪缨相继，东王则于胜国并无科第，科第自农山侍御始。武英总宪，司农兄弟皆侍御子也。侍御少孤，寄鞠于叔处，弱冠补诸生，寄于学宫。数里外有村翁姚姓，延之课子，暑月，黎明赴馆，翁方登楼观稼，隐约间，有双灯前导而来者，讶而迹之，稍近则灯隐，而塾师至。晚复覘焉，才越一阡，月影黄昏中，复有双灯前引矣。意其必贵，家有及笄女，遣人与其叔议婚，叔以贫辞，强而后可，遂赘焉。逾数年翁殁，姻娅中颇有加白眼者，姚夫人谓侍御曰："婿本赘也，翁亡何赘？盍归乎？"侍御怃然曰："我乃无家！"夫人曰："未婚时岂露处耶？"曰："寄斋夫舍。"曰："何不即与斋夫商之？"乃赁一庑楼棲焉。未几，遭鼎革，叔本乡居，挈家来城，觅避乱所，议于僧寮暂托。

    Explanation

    2

    Three Unusual Events: Volume One
    The Wang Family of Rongcheng

    In Rongcheng, the Wang family is the most distinguished among the gentry. There are two branches of the Wang family, and the people of the prefecture divide them based on their neighborhoods, calling them East Wang and West Wang. The West Wang family had held official positions one after another during the Ming dynasty, while the East Wang family had no members who passed the imperial examinations in the previous dynasty. The East Wang family's success in the imperial examinations began with Mr. Nongshan, the Attendant. Mr. Wuying, the Grand Censor, and Mr. Sinong, his brothers, were all sons of the Attendant. The Attendant was orphaned at a young age and was entrusted to the care of his uncle. At the age of twenty, he was selected as a student and entrusted to the care of the school. A few miles away, there was an elderly man named Yao, who invited the Attendant to teach his son. During the summer months, the Attendant would go to the teaching hall at dawn. The elderly man would just climb a tower to observe the crops, and in the distance, there were two lights leading someone. Surprised, the elderly man followed him. As he got closer, the lights disappeared, and the tutor arrived. In the evening, the elderly man spied again and just crossed one thousand steps. In the moonlight at dusk, he saw two lights leading the way again. He thought the person must be noble. The elderly man had a daughter of marriageable age, so he sent someone to discuss marriage with his uncle. The uncle refused because he was poor, but after being forced, he agreed, and the Attendant married into the family. After several years, the elderly man died, and many relatives gave the Attendant a cold look. Lady Yao said to the Attendant, "You originally married into the family, and the elderly man died. Why not return home?" The Attendant sadly replied, "I have no home!" Lady Yao said, "Before marriage, how could you live in the open?" He replied, "I was entrusted to the care of the caretaker's house." She said, "Why not immediately discuss it with the caretaker?" So, he rented a small building to live in. Soon after, the dynasty changed, and his uncle, who lived in the countryside, brought his family to the city to find a place to hide from the chaos. They discussed temporarily staying in a Buddhist monastery.

    3

    公挈二子先往，司农方在妊，仓惶中胎震欲娩，适土寇又至，急避人家竹园中，倚竹坐地，朦胧见一白衣老媪，为之扶掖，砺甲断脐，裂裳作褓，料理甫毕，而侍御寻踪已至。举儿付之，乃告其叔，觅人舁产妇至寓，一家团聚，招呼老媪，则已不见。数月后，皇朝定鼎，又逾年，岁丁亥，叔谓侍御曰："频年离乱，举业已荒，不得不作揣摩计。明年可谢遣问字者，我虽贫，助汝脱粟十石，夫妇诸儿尚可不馁。"夫人应曰："甚荷虀盐膏火，妇以十指襄之。若来秋复落，亦无颜见叔矣。

    Explanation

    3

    The official took his two sons ahead, while the pregnant woman, who was the granary official's wife, felt her baby was about to be born in the midst of panic. Just then, a band of local bandits arrived, and they hastily retreated to a bamboo garden belonging to someone. They sat against the bamboo, and in a daze, they saw an elderly woman dressed in white. She assisted them, cutting the umbilical cord with a sharp object and tearing her clothing to make swaddling clothes. After tending to the newborn, the official found his trail and arrived. He handed the child over to the woman and then informed his uncle. They found someone to carry the pregnant woman to their residence, and the family reunited. When they called out to the old woman, she had already disappeared.

    Several months later, the new dynasty was established, and another year passed, it being the year of Dinghai. The uncle told the official, "Years of turmoil have neglected your studies. You must now take preparatory measures. Next year, you can dismiss those who come to ask for instruction. Although I am poor, I will help you with ten shi of coarse rice, and your wife, children, and others can still avoid hunger." The wife replied, "We greatly rely on the salt, vinegar, oil, and fire. I will use my ten fingers to assist. If next autumn again fails, there would be no face to see the uncle anymore."

    Done.

    4

    "初，侍御邂逅一僧，谛视曰："君大贵人也，苦为发所压，能从我游，刘秉忠不足数也。"笑而置之。至是僧又来，笑且诧曰："我言应矣！"更审度久之，曰："君当一品，而又似不真，其故何也？"时瑁湖方八岁，捧茶出饮客，僧惊起，曰："是矣，此真一品，君乃封爵。"薛澱五岁，匍匐闯门，曰："此亦一品，稍逊乃兄。"横云在抱，亦携以出，曰："又一品也，位亚于兄，而贵乃先于兄。"后一一吻合。而所遇白衣老媪者，遍访不得，惟于神龛旁，供一栗主，即题曰：白衣老媪之位。至今司农诸裔，岁时享之不衰。
    　　　张尚书前生

    4

    At the beginning, a low-ranking official encountered a monk unexpectedly. The official examined closely and said, "You are a very important person, suffering from being weighed down by hair. If you follow me, Liu Bingzhong will not be worth mentioning." The official smiled and set it aside. When the monk came again, he smiled and said in surprise, "My words have come true!" He examined more carefully for a long time, saying, "You will hold a first-rank position, but it seems not entirely true. What is the reason for this?" At that time, Maohu was eight years old, holding tea and serving the guests. The monk was startled and stood up, saying, "Yes, this is truly a first-rank person, you are a noble." Xueding was five years old, crawling to the door, and the monk said, "Another first-rank person, with a lower rank than his older brother but higher status." The monk also took Maohu in his arms and said, "Another first-rank person, with a lower rank than his older brother but higher status." Later, everything matched perfectly. As for the white-clad old woman I met, searching everywhere but not finding her, only in front of the shrine, a wooden tablet was placed, inscribed as "The position of the white-clad old woman." Until today, the descendants of Si Nong still offer sacrifices to her regularly. Zhang Shangshu's previous life.

    5

    轮回之说，说部记载颇多，以余所闻，若张尚书之为断臂和尚、钱中翰之为天童寺僧，尤觉其信而可徵也。断臂和尚，不知所从来，以钝根求悟，效二祖所为，尚书祖母钱太夫人重之，供养朱家阁指松庵中。时太翁农部家居，宅在秀野桥西，母王恭人方妊，将就蓐，农部饬家人呼乳医，恇扰彻夜，于厅事隐几假寐，曙色朦胧间，恍惚见僧人入，即呼之曰："和尚，且上高阁小坐，家有急事，不能偷闲共话也。"僧不答，径入，惊而醒，闻有关于门者则舟子与阍者争，阍云："断臂僧不来，何得索夜航钱？"舟子云："明明宿我后艄，辩色即起，其伞尚在！"方争论间，而庵中人来报，僧于半夜圆寂矣，遽返中堂，婢已报夫人举雄，乃凿然知宿德再来也。颖慧绝人，五岁时，农部以其多言，名之曰默。一日，闻客呼少马字者，问其义，客曰："伯名集，析其字，成佳成木。"尚书譁曰："我必更名，否则异时必字我黑犬耳！"乃易之曰照，即以得天字焉。

    Explanation

    5

    The doctrine of rebirth is well-documented in literary works. According to what I have heard, cases like that of Minister Zhang, who was reborn as a monk with a single arm, and that of Scholar Qian, who was reborn as a monk at Tiantong Temple, are especially credible and verifiable. The monk with a single arm, whose origin is unknown, sought enlightenment with a dull mind, imitating the actions of the Second Patriarch. Lady Qian, the grandmother of the Minister, highly regarded him and cared for him in the Zhujia Pavilion, Pine Hermitage. At the time, the grandfather, Minister of Agriculture, was living at home, and his residence was located west of Xiu Ye Bridge. His mother, Lady Wang, was pregnant and about to give birth. The Minister instructed the family to call a midwife, and he was disturbed and anxious all night. He leaned on a table in the hall and took a nap. In the dim light of dawn, he saw a monk entering in a daze and called out, "Monk, please sit upstairs for a moment; there is an urgent matter at home, and I cannot spare time for conversation." The monk did not answer and entered directly. The Minister woke up in surprise and heard a dispute between the boatman and the gatekeeper. The gatekeeper said, "The armless monk did not come; how can you demand payment for the night ferry?" The boatman replied, "He clearly stayed at the back of my boat, got up as soon as it was light, and his umbrella is still there!" While they were arguing, someone from the hermitage came to report that the monk had passed away at midnight. The Minister quickly returned to the main hall, and the maid reported that the lady had given birth to a boy. Thus, it became clear that the previous virtue had returned. The child was exceptionally intelligent and wise. At five years old, the Minister named him "Mo" because he spoke too much. One day, he heard a guest call for a name with the character "少马" (few horse). He asked the guest its meaning, and the guest said, "The elder brother's name is Ji, and if you split the character, it becomes '佳' (good) and '木' (wood)." The Minister exclaimed, "I must change my name; otherwise, they will call me 'Black Dog' in the future!" So he changed his name to "Zhao," which means "to illuminate," and was given the courtesy name "Tian."

    6

    十四入泮，十七乡举，十八捷南宫，选庶常时。末奉钦点，尚书仰奏云："臣张照年幼，未娴吏治，恳圣恩教习，愿尽中秘书。"带领官掖之不起，圣祖顾左右曰："小蛮童，乃颇有胆！"笑而颔之。散馆后，以检讨供奉内廷者十八年。世宗即位后，偶问张文和："廷臣中有通禅悦者否？"对曰："族侄照，曾阅内典。"因召对，即问曰："视朕何人？"对曰："是佛。""汝自视何人？"对曰："干屎橛。"言下大契，即得放缺。十余年，位至卿贰，未必非当年龙华一会中香火因缘也。所著《天瓶诗》二卷，多採择典题，多用字如生老病死、衣衾棺椁及梦幻泡影露电等，不离梵筴，读者笑此真伽陵集也。后扈从，山庄坠马，仍折右臂，得蒙古医，疗之而痊。又三年，丁艰归，卒于道。余谓和尚误矣，此福缘亦孽果也，不如天童僧之能来去自如矣。余又见一卷书，杜陵苦热诗，大醉后伏地，作者墨沈淋漓，后题款云得地居士，为稷堂先生备端阳贡，收入内庭。

    Explanation

    6

    At the age of fourteen, he entered the school; at seventeen, he was recommended by local officials; at eighteen, he passed the palace examination and was selected for the Hanlin Academy. Upon his final selection, the minister Zhang Zhao, who was young and inexperienced in administrative affairs, respectfully requested to be taught and to serve in the imperial library. The imperial librarian tried to support him, but the emperor, looking around, said, "This little barbarian boy is quite bold!" He smiled and nodded in approval. After graduating from the Hanlin Academy, he served in the inner court as a censor for eighteen years. After Emperor Shizong ascended the throne, he once asked Zhang Wenhe, "Are there any officials in the court who understand Zen Buddhism?" Zhang Zhao replied, "My nephew, Zhang Zhao, has studied the Buddhist scriptures." The emperor then summoned him for an audience and asked, "What do you see me as?" Zhang Zhao replied, "You are a Buddha." The emperor then asked, "What do you see yourself as?" Zhang Zhao replied, "A piece of shit." The emperor was greatly pleased with his response and immediately granted him a vacant position. Over the next ten years, he rose to the rank of a high official, which may have been due to the karmic connection from the Dragon Flower Assembly. He wrote a collection of poetry titled Tianping Shi, which often chose classic themes and used words like birth, aging, sickness, death, clothing, coffin, and the illusions of dreams and bubbles, reflecting Buddhist teachings. Readers laughed and said this was truly the collection of King Jambudipa. Later, while accompanying the emperor on a trip, he fell off a horse at the imperial hunting grounds and broke his right arm. He was treated by a Mongol doctor and recovered. Three years later, he returned home due to the death of a close relative and died on the road. I believe the monk was mistaken; this good fortune is also a bad result, not as good as the ability of the monk Tiantong to come and go freely. I also saw a scroll of poems by Du Fu on the heat, written in great drunkenness, with the author lying on the ground, the ink flowing profusely. The inscription at the end read, "The recluse of the earth," prepared as a gift for Mr. Jitang for the Dragon Boat Festival, and collected into the inner court.

    7

    钱中翰前生
    　　　前明钱少马士贵，五十无子，祈嗣天童。住山长老，耆宿也，为入定，覘之，则曰："钱宰官有家无子，有子无家。"言下有省，乃归而施舍，蓄资四十万，三年而罄。复往四明，住山僧曰："可矣！"乃设斋饭，僧堂头晓众曰："今有钱宰官，无子祈嗣，大众谁愿往？"众皆愕眙，惟担饭僧向钱一笑，堂头曰："汝亦可。"乃下座，送钱出，而担饭僧即于烧火凳上坐逝矣。归而生中翰芳标，肩有肉骈起，与担饭僧绝肖。初名鼎瑞，字宝汾，更名后乃字葆汾，以康熙丙午孝廉，官中翰，诗号金门，词名湘瑟。多工艳体，绝无蔬筍气语。奏销狱起，镌秩家居，性好奕，方与客对，设楸枰，忽阍持信入曰："天童山寄来。"拆视，乃空缄也，恍然大悟，即作偈曰："来从天童来，去向天童去。笑指天童山，白云最深处。"遂示微疾，数日而逝。其孙长泽，棋入第二品，余见时已八十余，述之甚悉。

    Explanation

    7

    A Former Life of Minister Qian

    During the Ming dynasty, there was a scholar-official named Qian Shaoma, who was fifty years old and had no children. He prayed for descendants at Tian童 Mountain. An elderly monk residing in the mountains, a respected elder, entered a meditative state and observed him. The monk then said, "Mr. Qian, you have a home but no children; if you have children, you will have no home." Upon hearing this, Qian realized the truth and returned home to give alms and make charitable donations. He accumulated wealth of forty thousand units, which was depleted over three years. He then went to the Four Brightness region, where a mountain-dwelling monk said, "It is possible!" Qian then prepared a vegetarian meal. The head monk of the temple informed the congregation, "Now there is a Mr. Qian, a government official, who has no children and is praying for descendants. Who among the congregation wishes to go?" Everyone stared in astonishment, but only the monk who carried the food smiled at Mr. Qian. The head monk said, "You can also." He then got up from his seat and sent Mr. Qian out. The monk who carried the food immediately sat on the stove seat and passed away.

    Qian returned home and gave birth to a son named Fangbiao, who later became a scholar-official. Fangbiao had shoulders with flesh growing together, and he looked exactly like the monk who carried the food. Initially named Dingrui, with the courtesy name Baofen, after changing his name, his courtesy name became Baofen. He passed the imperial examination in the year Bingwu of the Kangxi era and served as a scholar-official. He was known as a poet with the pseudonym Jinmen and a lyricist with the pseudonym Xiangse. He was skilled in elegant and delicate style, and his works were completely devoid of the air of vegetables and bamboo shoots. When a financial scandal arose, he was demoted and lived at home. He enjoyed playing chess and was setting up a chessboard with a guest when suddenly a messenger brought a letter from Tian童 Mountain. Upon opening it, it was an empty envelope. He suddenly realized the truth and composed a Buddhist verse: "I come from Tian童 Mountain, I go to Tian童 Mountain. I smile and point to Tian童 Mountain, where the clouds are deepest." He then showed slight illness and passed away after a few days. His grandson Changze was a chess player of the second rank. I met him when he was over eighty and he described everything in great detail.

    8

    钱月江学士
    　　　国初十郡大社，以宋即庭尤西堂诸君执牛耳，华亭钱学士金甫与焉。金甫字月江，人颇伉爽，会行觞于千人石，有中翰邵君延龄，卒然问月江曰："松有钱芳标，岂君族耶？"月江对曰："无服族叔。"邵君即曰："此乃非人，前欲补我缺，再三挽我许金五百，我昨往索，转令阁人饰词拒我。"改国初铨政，尚沿明例，科中需次，若今之侯廪截缺，可上下其手也，因大诟。月江时亦被酒，攘臂而起曰："不知我叔而詈之，是詈叔也，已不可；知我叔而詈之，即詈我也，乌乎可？"势将用武，幸十郡士交为之解，乃罢去。未几有宏词之举，月江被征，而举主则殊未谋面。促迫就道，至都进谒，修师生礼，谛视其人，似曾相识，握手问曰："君知仆相攀之意乎？"对曰："必有行卷流传，谬尘青目。

    Explanation

    8

    Qian Yuejiang, a scholar,
    At the beginning of the dynasty, there was a grand assembly of scholars from ten prefectures, with Song Jiting and You Xitang leading the way. Qian Jinfu, a scholar from Huating, was also present. Qian Jinfu, whose courtesy name was Yuejiang, was known for his strong will and straightforwardness. One day, during a gathering at the Thousand People Stone, a scholar named Shao Yanling suddenly asked Qian Jinfu, "Is there a Qian Fangbiao in Song? Is he your distant relative?" Qian Jinfu replied, "He is not a blood relative." Shao Yanling then said, "That man is not a proper person. He tried to fill my vacancy and repeatedly persuaded me to accept 500 taels of gold. I went to ask for it yesterday, but the servant used polite words to refuse me." In the early period of the new dynasty's official selection system, the practices were still influenced by those of the Ming dynasty. The ranking system for officials allowed for manipulation, and Shao Yanling scolded loudly. Qian Jinfu, who was also under the influence of alcohol, raised his arm and stood up, saying, "It is not right to scold someone you do not know; that is scolding your relative, which is unacceptable. Knowing my relative and scolding him is scolding me, how can that be?" The situation was about to turn violent, but fortunately, the scholars from the ten prefectures mediated, and the conflict was resolved. Soon after, there was a literary competition, and Qian Jinfu was summoned. However, the person who recommended him had never met him before. He was hurriedly ordered to travel to the capital, where he paid his respects to the person who had recommended him. Upon seeing the person, he realized he had seen him before and asked, "Do you know why I am here?" The person replied, "There must be a collection of your works that has been passed around, and you have caught my attention."

    9

    "曰："非也！"曰："然则知交扬诩乎？"曰："亦非也！君之得举，以老拳得之，仆即千人石上作鸡肋者。《国策》云：昔为人妻，则不欲其詈我也；今为我妻，则欲其詈人也。君为族叔，几不反兵，兹幸结衣簪缘，庶友朋之詈仆者寡耳。"时征车未齐，许以庠生入北闱举秋试。明年南宫复第，殿试二甲，选庶常，宏词榜发，复列上卷，免其散馆，即授编修，居官不改儒素，足不登要人之堂，与竹垞最莫逆，朱归后亦引退。

    Explanation

    9

    "Then do you know about my friend Yang Xu?" I replied, "No, either! You were elected by force, and I am like a chicken rib on a stone. The Guo Ce says: 'When I was someone's wife, I did not want them to curse me; now that I am my wife, I want her to curse others.' You are my cousin, and you almost drew your sword. Fortunately, we have a connection through our social ties, so hopefully fewer friends will curse me." At that time, the imperial carriages were not yet ready, and they allowed me to enter the northern examination as a student. The following year, I passed the southern examination, ranked second class in the palace examination, and was selected as a scholar-official. The list of distinguished writers was issued, and I was listed in the top scroll. I was exempted from the probationary period and immediately appointed as an editor. While in office, I did not change my simple scholar's demeanor and did not enter the halls of important people. I had the closest friendship with Zhu Cha, and after Zhu returned, I also retired.

    10

    有老友刘君最狎，刘君业医，月江病，药之，竟卒。刘君大恨，录其方，置书中，以志戒不复为人治病。后妻方妊，梦月江来而生，因名梦金，字曰甫来，与月江生平性情语言，无一不肖。月江素工奕，梦金四五岁时，立足踏上，观父与客奕，指点胜负，不爽圭撮，品入第二。后父病，仓悴间叩父何方可用，指书中方，遂用之。即服，乃大惊曰："孽矣，此即月江所误也！"翌日而殁，窃叹密友关切，而粗工自用，即以卤莽报之。好谈歧黄者，尚慎旃哉！

    Explanation

    10

    I have a close friend named Liu Jun, who is a doctor. Once, a friend named Yue Jiang fell ill, and Liu Jun treated him, but Yue Jiang ultimately died. Liu Jun was greatly resentful, recorded the prescription, and placed it in a book to serve as a warning not to repeat such a mistake in future treatments. Later, his wife was pregnant and dreamed of Yue Jiang coming and being born. Thus, they named the child Meng Jin and gave him the courtesy name Fu Lai, who resembled Yue Jiang in every aspect of his character and speech. Yue Jiang was always skilled at chess, and when Meng Jin was four or five years old, he would stand on tiptoe to watch his father play chess with guests, nodding and gesturing to assess the outcomes, never being off by a hair, and ranked second in skill. Later, when his father fell ill, in a moment of desperation, Meng Jin asked his father what medicine to use. His father pointed to the formula in the book, and Meng Jin used it. Upon taking it, Meng Jin exclaimed in shock, "This is exactly what Yue Jiang made wrong!" The next day, his father died. I secretly lamented the close friend's concern and the unskilled doctor's self-will, which was repaid with carelessness. Those who love to talk about medicine should still be cautious.

    11

    两世人
    　　　外祖蔡方沚府君，其大母张，为少司马姊，故与百庚观察为中表昆弟，家居秀野桥之北，曰安素堂。东偏石榴一本，旁植柽柳两枝，意取萧梁五仄句义也。年四十五时，夏午摊饭，偃卧竹榻，恍惚见二青衣出树间，曰："官中奉取！"时观察未冠，家事昕夕共商也，强起行，觉足下如践氈茹，目中眊眊不见一物，谓二仆曰："此何地也？"仆应曰："是名黑海，毋怖，凭肩而步可也。"乃掖之趋。府君意怪之曰："此必梦也！"幼习陀罗尼咒，每遇噩梦，诵一过，辄醒，此独不验。约数刻，始觉足履地上，开目见身立廷中，面南室三楹，东一室壁间作花瓶式，中绿纱窗六扇，床上坐一少妇，窗前椅上，一中年媪，袭夹纱，叠菊衣，旁婢妪数人周遮侍。一媪失声曰："殇矣！"继又曰："惜哉，男也！"似闻少女啜泣声，中年者慰藉声。青衣拍肩曰："可归矣！"倏忽觉身卧榻上，大以为异，即详记之占梦书后。

    Explanation

    11

    Two Worlds

    My maternal grandfather, Cai Fangzhi, whose great-grandmother Zhang was the sister of a high-ranking official, thus making him a cousin of Bai Geng, who held the title of "Observing" (Observing is a title of a high-ranking official). They lived north of Xiu Ye Bridge, called An Su Tang. On the eastern side, there was a single pomegranate tree, with two cypress willows planted beside it, inspired by the poetic structure of the Southern Dynasties (Liang Dynasty). At the age of forty-five, on a midsummer afternoon, after spreading out food, he lay down on a bamboo bed, and dimly saw two servants emerge from between the trees, saying, "We are summoned from the palace!" At the time, the Observing was not yet of age, and family affairs were discussed morning and evening. He forced himself to rise and walk, feeling as if his feet were stepping on felt, and his vision was dim, seeing nothing. He asked the two servants, "Where am I?" The servants replied, "This place is called Black Sea. Do not be afraid; you can walk by leaning on our shoulders." They then supported him as he walked. My grandfather was puzzled and thought, "This must be a dream!" In his youth, he had learned the Dharani mantra, which he would recite whenever he had a bad dream, and it would wake him up. But this time, it did not work. After about an hour, he finally felt his feet on the ground, opened his eyes, and saw himself standing in the courtyard, facing south, with three rooms. In the eastern room, the wall was shaped like a vase, with six green silk windows, and a young woman sat on the bed. In front of the window, on a chair, sat an elderly woman in a layered gauze robe, with a chrysanthemum pattern, surrounded by several maidservants. One of the maidservants exclaimed, "It's too bad! It's a boy!" Another said, "What a pity, it's a boy!" It seemed as if a young girl was sobbing, and the elderly woman was consoling her. The servant patted his shoulder and said, "You can return now!" Suddenly, he felt himself lying on the bed again, greatly puzzled, and immediately recorded this experience in his book of dream interpretation.

    12

    后五年，观察就婚曲阜公府，馆之二室，即之骇然，如重入梦境也，缘婚礼未行，秘之，但问曰："此间壁上旧非花瓶式乎，何为改作？"应曰："恐妨迎花烛者，故易双扉耳。"即弥月，将同归，欲释此疑，即以前所记示观察，观察访之孔恭人，恭人询之母陈太夫人，夫人曰："信也异哉！五年前从子馆选，迎妇入都，水道迂滞，已届弥月。

    Explanation

    12

    Five years later, the Inspector married into the Qufu Public Office and was lodged in two rooms. Upon entering, he was startled, as if he were re-entering a dream. Because the wedding had not yet taken place, the situation was kept secret, and he asked, "Wasn't there a vase-like structure on the wall here before? Why was it changed?" The response was, "We were afraid it would obstruct the reception of the bridal torches, so we replaced it with double doors." Immediately after the full month, the couple was about to return together, and the Inspector wished to resolve this doubt. He showed the previous record to the Inspector, who then consulted with Mrs. Kong. Mrs. Kong asked her mother, Lady Chen, who said, "Indeed, it is strange! Five years ago, when she was selected for the Imperial Academy, the bride was welcomed into the capital, and the water route was slow and obstructed, so it was already the end of the month."

    13

    予得耗，乃遣力迎之来，假馆于此，生子而殇，其日月皆符吻，中年媪即太夫人，貌癯而庄；幼妇为陈庶常妻，丰下颇福泽，与所记一一合。"观察谑曰："君若不殇，则中表依然，而昆弟易位矣。"黄松石经时同行曰："吾闻之梵筴，此借生魂入舍也，何以必借之故，殊不可解。"然生魂则信有之，即观察世泽堂中，常延高僧焰口施食，后诵六字真言，遣一鬼独不去。主坛令家中男女，有睡者悉唤醒，一舆夫方酣睡庑下，蹴之起，而鬼去，拭目曰："主人赐脯甚甘美，何事促我归也？"后外祖年八十余，常曰："余两世人，其多寿固宜。"

    13

    I received news and sent someone to fetch her here. She gave birth to a child who died young, and the days and months all matched exactly. The middle-aged woman was her mother, dignified and thin; the young wife was the wife of Chen Shuchang, with a plump lower body and a lot of good fortune, matching exactly what was recorded. The official joked, "If you had not died young, the relationship between in-laws would remain unchanged, but the positions of brothers would be reversed." Huang Songshi, who was traveling with him at the time, said, "I heard from Buddhist scriptures that this is borrowing a living soul to enter the house. Why it must be borrowed is very difficult to understand." However, a living soul is indeed real. In the official's Shize Hall, he often invited high-ranking monks to perform the ritual of feeding hungry ghosts, and later recited the six-syllable mantra. He sent away one ghost, but one remained. The master of the ceremony ordered the men and women in the house to wake up all those who were sleeping. One porter was sound asleep under the eaves, and he shook him awake, and the ghost left. Wiping his eyes, he said, "The master gave me very sweet and delicious meat. Why did you make me return?" Later, my maternal grandfather, who was over eighty years old, often said, "I have lived two lives. It is natural that I have lived a long life."

    14

    沈丹彩
    　　　六壬之术，托始于黄帝，然总以管邵为宗，学者如牛毛，大都皮传，能窥其奥，实有前知之哲，余所见者，以沈丹彩凤辉为最。沈嘉定人，迁崑山陆家浜，少孤露，育于其祖。祖有姊婿唐翁，精壬学，唐翁无子，授以书，上有题词云："元女之遗，授诸管邵。玉帐中黄，尤窥秘奥。会逢其适，尽忠报效。舍之则藏，枕中鸿宝。鬻及借人，皆为不孝。"且曰："此道中绝四十年，汝子合夭，有遗腹孙目重瞳者，应传此术。"后丹彩生，果重瞳，颖慧过人，于易尤为别晤。余晤于古与草堂，借通志堂经解与悦，大半俱曾流览，于易尤邃，每举一部，即能言其纲目，且备言优劣大旨。以易乃卜筮之书，非可空谈心性，于王程诸说，均有微词，最服膺者则黄石斋之易象正，及倪鸿宝之儿易各部，其所宗尚可知矣。在松时，有西山林塘曹姓祖茔，忽生一木，甲桃则乙李，子瓜则丑豆，变易不常。有顽童採其实，食之而毙，因群呼为毒树。

    Explanation

    14

    Shen Dancai
    The art of the Six Rens divination is said to have originated from the Yellow Emperor, but it ultimately traces its roots to Guan Zhong and Zhao Dun. There are countless students of this art, but most only learn the surface-level aspects; those who can truly understand its depths possess the wisdom of foresight. Of those I have encountered, Shen Dancai Fenghui is the most skilled. Shen Dancai was originally from Jiading but later moved to Lujia Bang in Kunshan. He lost his parents at a young age and was raised by his grandfather. His grandfather's sister's husband, Tang, was an expert in the Six Rens divination. Since Tang had no sons, he passed on his knowledge to Shen Dancai. The book given to Shen Dancai contained an inscription that read: "The teachings of the Original Female were passed down to Guan and Zhao. In the Yellow Jade Tent, one must especially delve into its hidden mysteries. When the time is right, one should devote oneself wholeheartedly to serve and repay. When not in use, it should be kept hidden, like a treasure in one's pillow. Selling or lending it to others is all considered filial impiety." It also stated, "This art has been lost for forty years. Your son will die young, but there will be a grandson with double pupils who should inherit this art." After Shen Dancai was born, he indeed had double pupils and was extraordinarily intelligent and wise, especially profound in understanding the I Ching (Book of Changes). I met him at the Ancient Grass Hall, where he borrowed Tongzhi Tang Jingjie for my pleasure. He had read most of these texts, with a particular depth of understanding of the I Ching. Whenever he mentioned a book, he could immediately speak of its main points and structure, and he could fully discuss its strengths and weaknesses. He believed that the I Ching is not something that can be discussed abstractly about the mind and nature, and he had subtle criticisms of the teachings of Wang Yangming and Cheng Yi. He most respected the Yi Xiang Zheng by Huang Zongxi and the various sections of Er Yi by Ni Zhi, and his preferences are evident. During his time in Songjiang, there was an ancestral tomb of the Cao family in Xishan Lin塘. Suddenly, a tree grew in the tomb, producing different fruits and vegetables in alternating months—peaches in the first month, plums in the second, cucumbers in the third, and beans in the fourth. The tree's fruit changed unpredictably. A mischievous child picked and ate the fruit, and died as a result. The locals then called the tree a "poisonous tree."

    15

    以沈公多识，询之，即为占之，断曰："此树出海外，有海鸟衔其子，飞倦坠此，合于申年申月申日申时，应遭雷火。"众以为妄。丙申七月，果为雷击，因劈其木示沈，类杨而颇香，余尚见之。又余妇之姑丈杨，延沈占病，适其家扶乩，乩上忽书曰："沈丹彩已泊河干，可延入。"比启门，则已上岸矣。告之，沈愕然，进为作礼，乩即书曰："汝知无子之故乎？皆习数之累，若能戒之，可得一子。"从此不肯为人作课。

    Explanation

    15

    Because Mr. Shen was knowledgeable, they consulted him, and he divined the matter, concluding: "This tree originates from beyond the sea; a sea bird carried its seed, grew tired from flying, and dropped it here, coinciding with the year, month, day, and hour of the monkey. It should be struck by lightning." The people thought this prediction was nonsense. In the seventh month of the year Bing Shen, the tree was indeed struck by lightning. They split the tree open to show Mr. Shen, who found it resembled a willow but had a pleasant fragrance. I still see it. Another time, my mother-in-law's husband, Mr. Yang, invited Mr. Shen to predict his illness. Coincidentally, their family was performing a divination with a spirit tablet, and the tablet suddenly wrote: "Mr. Shen Dancai has already docked at the riverbank; you may invite him in." By the time the door was opened, Mr. Shen had already stepped onto the shore. They told him, and Mr. Shen was startled, going in to perform a ritual. The tablet then wrote: "Do you know the reason for having no children? It is all due to the burden of learning numbers. If you can abstain from it, you can have a son." From then on, Mr. Shen refused to predict for others.

    16

    一日五更，有叩门者甚急，延之则嘉定尹，握手跪地曰："予有急，非君不能解！"询其详，则劫盗二人越狱也，曰："予已遴干役四十名、八桨船四只，分四路追捕，惟君所指。"沈筮之，曰："毋虞，但派船两只，向直北二十里外，转而东，有枯庙，庙之外有树，树有鹊巢，盗寝其内，睡正酣，缚之易耳。"方为设食，炊未就，已纍然鱼贯而来矣。词后有乞筮，即引此二事拒之，曰："盗固应死，然伯仁由我，未必非乏子之缘，此五岁儿勿作孤注矣。"余欲学之，为言子未精西法，太阳过宫，尚难算准，何从定将乎？乃废然而罢。

    Explanation

    16

    One morning at the fifth watch, there was an urgent knock on the door. When invited, it was the governor of Jiading who knelt down and held hands, saying, "I am in a hurry, only you can solve this!" Upon inquiring about the details, he explained that two robbers had escaped from prison. He said, "I have already selected forty capable men and four boats with eight oars each, divided into four routes to pursue, as you direct." Shen performed divination and said, "Do not worry, but assign two boats, head directly north for twenty miles, then turn east. There will be an abandoned temple, outside which there is a tree with a magpie's nest. The thieves are sleeping inside, soundly asleep, and it is easy to bind them." Just as they were setting up a meal, the cooking was not yet done, and the thieves had already arrived in a line like fish. Afterward, there was a request for divination, and he cited these two examples to reject it, saying, "The thieves should indeed be executed, but I am responsible for Bo Ren, and it might not be due to a lack of good fortune. Do not make a five-year-old a lone bet." I wanted to learn from this, but I said that Zi is not proficient in Western methods, the sun passing through a palace is still difficult to calculate accurately, how can we determine the outcome? Thus, I gave up and stopped.

    17

    叶忠节公
    　　　叶忠节，余外母祖也，父中丞公有声，《明史》有传。六七岁时，塾师督之仿字，暑昼倦而隐几，师呼之醒，告曰："梦一人，口授余诗，令录之行间，今固在。"师视其诗云："君是王魁三世身，桂英仍著石榴裙。一枝遥寄湘江水，半幅平裁楚岫云。弔古有情怜贾谊，请缨无路叹终军。"忘其第七句，末云：莫负香罗帕上人。后于顺治丁酉登秋试，万金记狱起，同年中名士如吴汉槎、陆子元皆战栗不能终卷，公与张相国、叶学士、吴詹事等从容挥洒而出，辛丑捷南宫。越数年大参楚省时，三藩底定，裁兵令下，公以粮道署藩篆，议奏明缓办，三年中有缺无补，可不动声色而汰矣。巡抚某不从，遂劫饷而畔，以夏包子为首，夜戕巡抚于署。公闻变，遣长子蘨护太夫人从水门出，朝衣冠坐厅事，拔剑自刎。

    Explanation

    17

    Ye Zhongjie, the loyal and righteous, was my maternal grandmother's father. His father, Vice-Chancellor Ye Yousheng, has a biography in the History of Ming. At the age of six or seven, his private teacher supervised him in copying characters. In the hot midday, he grew tired and leaned against the desk. The teacher called him awake and told him, "I had a dream where a person recited a poem to me, instructing me to write it down between the lines. It is still here." The teacher looked at the poem and recited: "You are the reincarnation of Wang Que for three generations, Guiying still wears the pomegranate skirt. A branch is sent far to the Xiang River, half a piece is evenly cut from the clouds of Chu mountains. To mourn the ancients with emotion, showing compassion for Jia Yi, to ask for a mission with no path, lamenting Zhong Jun." He forgot the seventh line, the last line reads: "Do not辜负the person on the fragrant silk handkerchief." Later, during the Dingyou year of Shunzhi, he passed the imperial examination. During the Wanjinji case, many famous scholars from the same year, such as Wu Hancha and Lu Ziyuan, all trembled and could not finish the exam. Ye Zhongjie, along with Zhang, the Chancellor, Ye, the Scholar, Wu, the Grand Tutor, etc., calmly and freely wrote their answers and passed the imperial examination in the Xinchou year. After several years, when he was the governor-general of Chu province, the Three Feudatories were pacified, and the order to reduce the army was issued. Ye Zhongjie, as the grain commissioner, temporarily took charge of the governor-general's duties and proposed to the emperor to delay the implementation. In three years, there were vacancies but no replacements, and the army could be reduced without causing a stir. The governor-general did not follow the proposal, and thus, they seized the pay and rebelled, with Xia Baizi as the leader. At night, they assassinated the governor-general in his office. Ye Zhongjie heard of the rebellion, sent his eldest son, Ye, to protect the dowager mother and leave through the water gate, dressed in court attire, he sat in the hall, and drew his sword and committed suicide.

    18

    僮奴或泣而掣其肘，公叱之，谓纪纲仆某曰："汝助我，谕诸仆，勿作细人姑息，致误乃公事。"某乃助之断喉，血淋漓遍身，目犹瞠视也。洞开重门，贼入见之，皆泣曰："恩主何至如此！"罗拜而散。仆某走告太夫人，欲从死，夫人曰："不可！汝大有事在。"以遗疏授之，令入京师，上闻震悼，赠工部侍郎，谥忠节。翠辇南巡，召见太夫人，赐长子蘨一品荫，选沂州刺史，旋改陛府，即以蘨为郡守。再巡，又赐次子芳员外郎，即妻之外祖也。三巡，复问，奏云第三子已前卒，止有孙凤毛在，复赐中书。太夫人深嘉其仆，以为能成主忠，遂以为族孙，削主仆籍。初，公有妾某，小忤，指斥之，妾愤，自缳，应童时梦中诗谶。至正命时，妾亦见，公叱之，拜曰："君今归冥，婢又当复侍巾栉耳。"此与说部中张睢阳妾事相类，第以索命而适得全忠，非怨耦而嘉耦也。此仆此妾，均可附公不朽矣。

    Explanation

    18

    The servants wept and pulled at his arm, but the official rebuked them and told the head servant, "You assist me, instruct the other servants, do not indulge in petty kindness, which will lead to the neglect of my affairs." The head servant then helped to cut off his throat; blood flowed everywhere, and his eyes still stared wide open. The heavy gates were opened, and the bandits saw him, all wept and said, "How could our benefactor have come to this!" They prostrated themselves in sorrow and then dispersed. The head servant rushed to inform the lady-in-waiting, intending to follow him in death, but she said, "No! You have important duties to fulfill." She gave him the official's last will and ordered him to go to the capital. When the emperor heard of it, he was deeply moved and mourned, posthumously granting the official the title of Minister of Works and the posthumous name of Loyalty and Integrity. The green imperial carriage toured south, and the lady-in-waiting was summoned. The eldest son, 蘨, was bestowed the first-class favor and appointed as the governor of Yizhou, and was later transferred to the capital, where he became the prefect. On a second tour, the second son, 芳, was granted the position of Imperial Councillor, who was also her father-in-law. On a third tour, when asked about the third son, it was reported that he had died earlier, leaving only the grandson, 凤毛, who was then granted the position of Chancellor. The lady-in-waiting greatly praised the head servant, believing that his loyalty had helped to complete the official's integrity, and thus he was adopted as a clan member, removing his status as a servant. Initially, the official had a concubine who had slighted him, and he rebuked her harshly. The concubine, in anger, hanged herself, fulfilling a prophecy from his childhood dream. At the time of his death, the concubine also appeared, and the official rebuked her, to which she bowed and said, "Now that you have returned to the underworld, I shall once again serve you." This is similar to the story of a concubine in historical records who sought revenge but instead found a way to preserve loyalty, not out of resentment but out of affection. Both this servant and this concubine can be associated with the official's immortality.

    19

    痴和尚
    　　　痴和尚不知所来，或云沈姓，或云孙姓，冬夏一衲，与人言，无庄语，问且谩骂，然事后多奇验。不饮酒，惟好食肉，无多寡皆尽。张大木先生耽禅悦，多方外交，乐与晋接。时圣祖春秋高，理密亲王再废，主鬯末卜，意和尚前知，作禅语探之曰："佛将成道，谁能受衣钵者？"瞪目曰："何问为？衣钵久已付汝！"未几世宗登极，以大木行四，故作廋词，计其时庙讳已藏正大光明殿匾内矣。王少宰母蒋太君季赐尤重之，供养宅中。一日忽曰："今夕我欲卧太夫人床上。"告之，太夫人曰："和尚放颠，必有所为。"即迁别室，让榻与之。夜半栋折榱崩，举室惊起，太夫人曰："吾有压厄，和尚感我恩，故以身代。

    Explanation

    19

    The Foolish Monk

    The Foolish Monk's origins are unknown; some say he is surnamed Shen, others say he is surnamed Sun. He wears the same robe in winter and summer, and when speaking to people, he does not use formal language, often cursing or scolding when asked, but his actions and predictions often prove to be strange yet effective. He does not drink alcohol but enjoys eating meat, regardless of the amount. Mr. Zhang Daimu, who is deeply interested in the joy of meditation, engages in various diplomatic efforts and enjoys meeting and interacting with others. At the time, the Kangxi Emperor was advanced in age, and the Prince Yinti, a prominent Qing prince, had been disgraced twice, and the succession was uncertain. It was believed that the monk had foreknowledge, and a Buddhist saying was used to test him: "When the Buddha is about to attain enlightenment, who will receive the robe and bowl?" The monk stared blankly and replied, "Why ask such a question? The robe and bowl have long been entrusted to you!" Soon after, the Yongzheng Emperor ascended the throne, and because Mr. Zhang was the fourth son, a riddle was used to hide the emperor's secret name, which was already stored in the "Zhen Duo Guang Ming" (True, Broad, and Bright) Hall. The mother of the high-ranking official, Lady Jiang, who was particularly fond of the monk, kept him in her household. One day, the monk suddenly said, "Tonight, I wish to sleep on Lady Jiang's bed." When informed, Lady Jiang said, "The monk is acting foolishly; he must have a reason." She then moved to another room and gave up her bed to him. In the middle of the night, the beam broke and the rafters fell, startling the entire household awake. Lady Jiang said, "I am under a pressing calamity, and the monk is grateful for my kindness, so he has taken my place."

    20

    "方抢攘间，和尚从瓦砾堆中闯然出曰："谁恶作剧，妒我卧此，竟拆屋去矣，我梦未醒，无已，当另觅一觉耳。"后太夫人殁，去住西林寺之万佛国，一衲之外，无他物，惟挟一竹筍，缄之甚固，每出，必告常住曰："慎视我箧，勿得私启！"复有一游方来，闻其语，意必有鞋笠资，窃发之，止一敞包袱，一狗子似初出腹，目尚未瞬，急缄之，和尚归，即怒骂曰："戒若等勿启，今违之，此地不可居矣！"即跃秀野桥湍流中，视之死矣，三日不流，亦不仆，第四日不知所在。后启筍审之，并狗子亦渺，群谓畜生道中得悟者，余笑谓斯真宿德所呵，襄样节度者衰相现前狗子也，会佛法也。或传有皇太后前翻筋斗事，则多附会，圣祖召问，默不能对，且作战栗状，乃放归。或谓其辟支小果慑于天威，或谓不爱紫衣，故作此态。然总与木陈天岸辈，以奏对夸机缘者异矣。

    Explanation

    20

    In the midst of chaos, a monk suddenly emerged from a pile of rubble and exclaimed, "Who is causing mischief, envying me lying here, and tearing down the house? My dream has not yet awakened. There is no choice but to find another place to sleep." After the respected madam passed away, he went to reside in the Ten Thousand Buddha Kingdom of Xiling Temple, carrying nothing but a single robe. He only carried a tightly sealed bamboo shoot. Whenever he left, he would instruct the resident monks, "Be careful with my box, do not open it privately!" Another wandering monk came, heard his words, and thought he must have something valuable like shoes and a hat. He secretly opened the box, finding only a worn bundle and a puppy, which seemed to have just been born and had not yet opened its eyes. He quickly sealed it again. When the monk returned, he immediately shouted, "Forbid you to open it! Now that you have disobeyed, this place is no longer habitable!" The monk then jumped into the swift current of the bridge in Xiu Ye, appearing dead. For three days, he did not float away, nor did he sink, and on the fourth day, he was nowhere to be found. Later, when the bamboo shoot was opened and examined, both the puppy and the monk were gone. The crowd said it was one who attained enlightenment in the animal realm. I laughed and said this was truly the rebuke of ancient virtue. The dog is a sign of the decline of the Xiang-style general, in line with Buddhist law. It is said that there was a story of the Empress Dowager doing somersaults, but much of it is fabricated or embellished. The Sage Ancestor summoned him to ask, but he remained silent and showed signs of trembling, and he was then sent back. Some say that the pratyekabuddha was intimidated by the heavenly power, while others say that he did not love the purple robe, so he acted this way. But it is different from those who boast about their karmic connections in their responses.

    21

    竹林七贤
    　　　余曾祖姑适盛，即王史亭先生之外母也，家北郭之拗茭滨，厅事曰孟迁堂。正月呼僮种牡丹，锄声铿然，知其下有石也，深掘及寻，得一石板，修及丈，横半之，上有字，题曰竹林七贤。再掘之，果见瓮七，制甚朴，泥封殊固，启视，清泉滃然。俗传藏镪久，多化为水，煮之可复原质。乃析薪烹之，百沸而泉如故。烹者怒，倾去，曝其瓮于墙角。

    Explanation

    21

    The Seven Sages of the Bamboo Grove
    　　　My great-grandmother married into the Sheng family, who were the maternal grandparents of Mr. Wang Shiting. They lived near the northern outskirts, by the bend of the river, and their main hall was called Mengqian Hall. In the first month, they called the servant to plant peonies. The sound of the hoe was clear, indicating that there was a stone beneath the soil. They dug deeply, reaching a depth of about ten feet, and found a stone slab that was one zhang long and half a zhang wide. There were characters on it, inscribed as "Seven Sages of the Bamboo Grove." Upon digging further, they indeed found seven jars, which were very simple in design, with a very solid mud seal. When they opened them, clear water rose up. According to folk belief, buried treasure turns into water over time, and boiling it can restore its original form. They chopped wood and boiled the water, but even after a hundred boilings, the water remained unchanged. The cook became angry, poured it out, and exposed the jars at the corner of the wall.

    22

    越翌日，史亭先生来，告之故，史亭先生嗜辨古器，据而摩挲，忽有莹莹触目者，意余沥未净，拨之乃一小锞，作梅花式，余幼时犹及玩之，真精鏐也。姑两孙，皆以孝廉作宰，一蜀一陇，迂儒拙宦，清贫綦甚，余数年前遇之，门庭如故，牡丹憔悴尽。问以水瓮，云尚在其下，第七贤则删为六逸矣。《谐铎》中有饮水吐银事，固属寓言，然银可化水，水亦何必不化银？第一两一铢，皆有定数，而徇者乃欲以智力取之，谬矣！观锦江事，更当怳然：某年蜀旱，江流顿浅，共传张献忠所藏有漏出者，乃请于官，戽下流选手手摸捞之，果得金一万七千有奇，核计人工货食，适足抵付，无毫厘盈缩，补山相国乃饬罢之。

    Explanation

    22

    The next day, Mr. Shiting came, and I told him the story. Mr. Shiting, who loved to identify ancient artifacts, held and rubbed it carefully, when suddenly something shiny caught his eye. He thought that the remaining traces were not yet clean, and when he brushed it, it turned out to be a small ingot in the shape of a plum blossom. I still remember it from my childhood, truly a fine ingot. My two grandsons, both became officials through the examination system, one in Sichuan, one in Gansu. They were scholars of limited practical skills and clumsy officials, extremely poor and frugal. I met them a few years ago, their courtyard remained the same, but the peonies had withered completely. When I asked about the water jar, they said it was still beneath it, and the seventh sage has been reduced to the sixth recluse. There is a story in Harmonious Bell about drinking water and spitting out silver, which is indeed a fable. But silver can be turned into water, and water can also be turned into silver. All have a fixed amount, but those who seek to take it by force or intelligence are wrong. Consider the incident at Jinjiang River, one should suddenly realize: in a certain year, Sichuan suffered a drought, the river suddenly became shallow. It was commonly believed that some of Zhang Xianzhong's hidden treasures had surfaced. They then petitioned the government to scoop the lower reaches and let people search for it. They indeed found gold, more than 17,000 units. When calculated for labor and food costs, just enough to cover the expenses, without any surplus or deficit. The Grand Councillor Buzhan then ordered the operation to stop.

    23

    胡道人
    　　　余客燕台时，表祖姑夫王史亭翰编，话胡道人事甚悉。燕台多缁而少黄，惟郊外白云观，为元邱长春修錬处，重九日，各省全真皆来集焉。胡道人亦必一至，然不住观，与程仪曹世淳习，多主其邸。程云遇一老民云，舞勺岁曾见之，状貌已如八九秩，有女嫁通州，女白发堆雪，而颜同少女。道人嗜酒不谷食，日饮无何而已，史亭先生招之饮，即来，醉又留宿，卧一方杌，纵横尺有咫，猧盘蠖屈，辗侧欠伸，绰绰然也。

    Explanation

    23

    Master Hu

    When I was a guest in Yan Capital, my maternal grandfather's brother-in-law, Mr. Wang Shiting, the compiler, spoke very clearly about the affairs of Master Hu. In Yan Capital, there are many Buddhist monks but few Taoists; only the White Cloud Temple in the suburbs, where Master Qiu Changchun of the Yuan dynasty practiced, is a notable exception. On the Double Ninth Festival, Taoists from all provinces gather there. Master Hu also definitely comes once, but he does not stay in the temple. He is familiar with Mr. Cheng Yice, an official of the Ministry of Rites, and often stays at his residence. Mr. Cheng said he met an old peasant who said, "I saw him when I was a young boy." His appearance was already like that of someone in their eighties or nineties. He has a daughter who married in Tongzhou, and his daughter has white hair like snow, but her face is like that of a young girl. Master Hu enjoys drinking wine and does not eat grains. He drinks daily without any particular reason. When Mr. Wang invited him to drink, he came immediately, and when drunk, he stays overnight. He sleeps on a small stool, one foot and a few inches wide, lying curled up like a snake, turning and stretching, looking relaxed and comfortable.

    24

    资郎汪员外秀峰者，嗜奔走，内行不修，与仪部同里閈，闻道人名，欲见，坚辞不可，乃与程谋，阚其来也即之，道人色然起曰："汝汪启淑耶？见我何为！汝某日作某事，可见我否？"枚举数十端，皆屋漏暧昧事，汪汗出如浆，惶窘伏地。程出不意，强为解曰："公真大醉，狂药祟人，无以为意。"答人曰："否否!若得见我，尚为有缘，能痛改前非，幸保首领，不信试志吾言，三日后即有奇祸，亦可小惩大诫也。"后三日，以坐快车出顺治城门，触石坠车，碎首几殒，疗月余始瘥，跡稍敛，而胡仙人之名逾著，求见者益多，叩以吉凶，道人终不言，常谓史亭曰："此口只宜饮酒耳。"后有强嬲之者，道人去不复来。翰编子徵士秋泉，方髫龀，值其卧，辄戏弄之，一张目，即复睡，再弄之，鼾声起矣。肤鳞鳞皴如古松，弹其额，声出金石，俾壮夫竭力推之，不坠。或云本西山老狐，秋泉云，容或有之。

    Explanation

    24

    Zī Láng Wāng Yuàn Wài Xiùfēng, fond of being active and with poor moral conduct, lived in the same neighborhood as Yí Bù. Hearing of the Daoist's name, he wished to meet him, but the Daoist firmly refused. Then, he planned with Chéng, and when the Daoist came, they approached him. The Daoist looked up and said, "Are you Wang Qishu? What do you want to see me for! On a certain day, you did a certain thing, can you see me now?" He listed dozens of points, all of which were secretive and ambiguous matters. Wang's sweat poured out like water, and he was in a state of panic, falling to the ground. Chéng was caught off guard and forcefully explained, "You are truly drunk, the madness of drugs has possessed you, don't take it seriously." The Daoist replied, "No no! If you can see me, there is still a chance, if you can deeply repent and change your ways, you will be fortunate to keep your head, if you don't believe, try to remember my words, three days later, you will face a great disaster, which can also serve as a small punishment and a great warning." Three days later, while riding a fast carriage out of the Shunzhi city gate, he hit a stone and fell off the carriage, nearly dying, and took over a month to recover. His behavior became more restrained, and the name of the Daoist became even more famous, with more people seeking to see him, asking about good or bad omens, but the Daoist never spoke, often saying to Shǐ Tíng, "This mouth is only suitable for drinking wine." Later, those who persistently bothered him, the Daoist left and never returned.

    Hàn Biān Zǐ Zhēng Shì Qiūquán, a young child, would play with him when he was sleeping. When he opened his eyes, he would fall back asleep. Playing with him again, he started snoring. His skin was rough and scaly like an ancient pine tree, and tapping his forehead produced a sound like metal and stone. Even strong men pushing him with all their strength could not make him fall. Some say he is an old fox from Xīshān, and Qiūquán says, it might be true.

    25

    朱太守得官得孙
    　　　功名子嗣，皆有定数，或意中而失之，或意外而得之，营营者自不知耳。前凤翔守朱公，又韩沂总宪大千椿祖也，少孤贫，落拓殊甚，挟布四匹、钱两缗，徒步入陕访其戚，至则戚已罢官去。无聊中邂逅一旧邻人，讯之，则现在通渭陶令署中办差，朱在穷途，急不择事，即恳作曹邱。偕至通渭，而署中颇患人满，邻为筹划："此间无位置，主人将赴省，盍同往再觅机会？"遂行。甫半途，忽接制府急檄，仓卒无捉刀者，乃呼诸仆从，问曰："若辈有能作楷者乎？文吾自为之。"邻乘间进曰："傔有戚朱偕来，似可。"即召与谈，如旧相识，及谂家世，责邻曰："若不早白我，屈辱朱君甚矣，肯为任记室乎？"朱诺诺，即于旅次订交焉。时方征葛尔丹，回通渭未几，奉旨派陕西协济车辆出嘉峪关，通渭分造五百，限一月成。

    Explanation

    25

    The Governor Zhu and His Descendants

    Achievements and descendants, all are predestined. Sometimes one loses them despite expectations, and sometimes one gains them unexpectedly; those who are busy and anxious do not realize it. Former Governor of Fengxiang, Zhu Gong, was also the great-grandfather of Han Yi, the Grand Censor. He was orphaned and impoverished in his youth, living a very aimless life. He carried four bolts of cloth and two strings of coins, walking to Shaanxi to visit his relatives. Upon arrival, he found that his relatives had already been dismissed from their official posts. In his boredom, he met an old neighbor, who informed him that the neighbor was currently working in the office of Tao Ling in Tongwei. Zhu, in his desperate situation, did not choose carefully and immediately asked to become a clerk. They went together to Tongwei, but the office was already crowded with people. The neighbor suggested, "There is no place for you here. The master is going to the provincial capital. Why not go together to look for another opportunity?" They set off. Just halfway, they suddenly received an urgent edict from the provincial governor. In a hurry, there was no one to write on his behalf, so he called his servants and asked, "Are any of you capable of writing in a neat hand? I will compose the text myself." The neighbor took the opportunity to say, "Among the attendants, there is a relative named Zhu who has come with him; he seems suitable." Zhu was immediately summoned for a conversation, and they seemed to be old acquaintances. When they learned of his family background, the governor scolded the neighbor, "You did not inform me earlier. You have greatly humiliated Mr. Zhu. Will you take on the role of secretary?" Zhu agreed, and they made friends immediately on the journey. At the time, there was a campaign against Galdan. After returning to Tongwei, he was soon ordered to provide vehicles to assist in passing through the Jiayu Pass for Shaanxi. Tongwei was tasked with producing five hundred vehicles, to be completed within one month.

    26

    陶公集幕中人熟商，朱公进曰："毋躁！"命于关厢悬示，有以旧车来售者，需双输完，无好丑皆纳，第一日来，与之金五十，来者潮涌；再三日即减其半，继而数金可售矣，十日车已盈千，乃整理之，韅靷鞅靽咸备，又旬而毕。将戒途，朱曰："毋躁，能如限，已见干办，太速则非新造之情见矣，为我徴黄牛之革。"革集，令缝巨囊如其车，乃令车载一櫜。依限将戒途，朱曰："毋躁。"呼解车人来，授以密缄，令行至爱曼河干启示，则令櫜中载水也。

    Explanation

    26

    In Tao Gong's camp, someone was thoroughly discussing a matter, and Zhu Gong said, "Do not be hasty!" He ordered notices to be posted in public places, inviting those who wished to sell old carts to do so, requiring full payment in two installments, and accepting all carts regardless of quality. On the first day, he offered fifty gold pieces, and many came to sell their carts. By the third day, he reduced the offer to half, and by the fifth day, only a few gold pieces were needed to buy a cart. Within ten days, a thousand carts had been collected, and they were then organized, with all parts of the carts—reins, harness, straps, and other fittings—prepared. After another ten days, the preparations were complete.

    As the journey was about to begin, Zhu Gong said, "Do not be hasty. If you can meet the deadline, it shows you are capable. If you go too quickly, it will not reflect the careful planning and effort that has gone into this. Gather oxhide from yellow cattle." When the oxhide was gathered, he ordered large sacks to be made, each the size of a cart, and instructed that each cart should carry one of these sacks. As the journey was about to begin, Zhu Gong said, "Do not be hasty." He called the person responsible for unloading the carts and gave him a sealed note, instructing him to proceed to the banks of the Eman River and reveal the contents, where he would find that the sacks were filled with water.

    27

    时沙漠外多戈壁，无泉，军官饮乳酪，驼马皆齕枯箕，多倒毙，水至，士马欢腾，圣祖大悦，破格擢陶监司，陶即为朱君援櫜驼例授县佐，不十年荐陟郡守，后以负气多忤，罢归。时总宪父年十七，将婚而夭，凤翔独子，无可继者，乃抚甥王永椿为子，家居多悲咤。半年后，妪婢辈窃窃私语，谓少君故有子，今寄缝工沈姓家，遂迎之返，即总宪也。盖少君私一婢，有身，惧父不敢告，又将婚，不得已嫁之。缝人娶婢，五月生儿，凿然知朱氏子也。后总宪贵，封典有父而无母，盖嫡母未婚，父亡，已别字。生母嫁缝人，又不可封，乃以貤封庶祖母盖之。

    Explanation

    27

    Beyond the desert lay much Gobi, devoid of springs. The officers drank milk and cheese, while camels and horses chewed dry stalks, many of which died. When water arrived, the soldiers and horses were jubilant, and the Holy Ancestor was greatly pleased. He promoted Tao Jian to a supervisory post out of the ordinary. Tao immediately followed the example of Zhu Jun, who used a camel to assist in his promotion to county assistant, and within ten years, he was recommended and promoted to the position of prefectural governor. Later, due to his stubbornness, he often offended others and was dismissed from office.

    At the time, the father of the chief censor was seventeen years old. On the verge of marriage, he died young, leaving Fengxiang's only son with no one to succeed him. Thus, he adopted his nephew Wang Yongchun as his son. At home, he often grieved and raged. Six months later, the maids and servants whispered among themselves, saying that the young master had an illegitimate son who was now living with a tailor named Shen. They then brought him back, and that was the chief censor. The young master had a relationship with a maid, and she became pregnant. Afraid of his father, he dared not tell him. And he was about to marry. He had no choice but to marry her off. The tailor married the maid, and five months later, she gave birth to a son, clearly a son of the Zhu family.

    Later, the chief censor became wealthy. The honorific titles had a father but no mother, as the legitimate mother was unmarried when the father died and had already taken a different name. The biological mother married the tailor and could not be honored. Thus, the honor was conferred on the maternal grandmother.

    28

    朱总宪际遇
    　　　朱总宪娶于许，为云南臬司鹤沙公孙婿，行人司副尧衢公婿也。鹤沙中顺治巳酉进士，齐年若王伊人、张曼园、袁丹叔、周宿来诸君，或用部属、或用中行评博、或径授监司郡守，惟鹤沙公独选庶常。时尚沿前明习俗，乡绅最重翰林，以入阁之阶也，于是投势寄产者毕集。上世本显宦，至公乃益富，中年即告归，苦无子，养子三，一姊子，一妻侄，惟七垣重以嫡侄嗣，六十余始举尧衢。不事生产，产既为诸兄瓜分，纲纪又从而蚕食之，四十万家资，至司副暮年荡然矣。一子以修书叙州别驾，选直隶之开州，以官为家，不能归。

    Explanation

    28

    Final Translation

    Zhu Juntian's Life and Family

    Zhu Juntian, the Censor-in-Chief, married into the Xu family, becoming the son-in-law of Xu Heisha, the Governor of Yunnan, and the son-in-law of Xu Yaoqu, the Vice Director of the Ministry of Rites. Xu Heisha passed the imperial examination in 1659. His contemporaries, such as Wang Yiren, Zhang Manyuan, Yuan Danshu, and Zhou Sulu, were appointed to various positions, either as departmental officials, as evaluators in the Hanlin Academy, or directly as governors of prefectures and counties. However, Xu Heisha alone was selected as a candidate for the Hanlin Academy. At the time, the customs of the Ming dynasty still prevailed, and local gentry highly esteemed members of the Hanlin Academy, seeing them as stepping stones to the cabinet. As a result, many people sought his protection and entrusted their properties to him. Xu Heisha's ancestors were prominent officials, and under his management, the family became even wealthier. However, he retired early due to the lack of a biological son. He adopted three sons: one was his sister's son, another was his brother-in-law's son, and the third, Xu Qiuan, was his legitimate nephew. Xu Heisha was over sixty when he finally had a biological son, Xu Yaoqu. Zhu Juntian did not engage in business, and the family's wealth was divided among his brothers, who further depleted it. By the time Xu Yaoqu became the Vice Director of the Ministry of Rites, the family's fortune of forty thousand households had been squandered. One of Xu Yaoqu's sons, Zhu Juntian, was appointed as the Deputy Governor of Xuzhou Prefecture and later selected to serve in the prefecture of Kaizhou in Zhili. He made his official post his home and never returned.

    29

    司副八十余，棲北莫家弄，一舍如舟，上漏下湿，恋之若广厦，以前后左右皆妓舍也。四干仆皆拥厚资，轮供之，供亦甚简，然日必需钱四百，尽以买花。冬月则翦彩者起最早，辨色即往妓家，送花必遍。间遇雨雪，不知笠屐，淋漓踯躅，不颠踬也。在都时，与于襄勤成龙最契，同官司副，又副榜同年。时襄勤持节清江，督办荆隆口，八驺过访，室不可坐，即立委巷间，询君有子弟胜官者乎，答以无有，固问之，则曰："有婿朱似可，然不知其愿去否也。"于即登之夹袋，檄召朱去。朱有吏才，勤于职事，功成以别驾衔叙司马，选处州同知，后晋陟巡抚，内陛左都。然当其发轫，亦于无意中得之，真可谓巷遇矣。

    Explanation

    29

    A deputy official, more than eighty years old, lived in a small alley called Mo Family Lane in the north. His dwelling was like a boat, leaking from above and damp below, yet he cherished it as if it were a spacious mansion because the brothels surrounded it on all sides. Four hundred servants, all of whom were wealthy, took turns providing for him, though the provisions were very simple. However, he needed four hundred coins daily, which he spent entirely on buying flowers. In winter, the paper flower makers would rise earliest, and as soon as it was light, they would go to the brothels to deliver flowers to all of them. Even in the rain or snow, they did not wear hats or shoes, walking wet and stumbling but not falling. When he was in the capital, he had the closest relationship with Yu Xiangqin Chenglong, who was also a deputy official and had the same year of passing the imperial examinations. At the time, Yu Xiangqin was holding a staff in Qingjiang and overseeing the Jinglong Pass. When eight attendants visited him, his room was not suitable for sitting, so they stood in the alley. They asked if he had any children or relatives who were better suited for official positions. He answered that he did not, but they pressed the question further. He then said, "I have a son-in-law named Zhu, but I do not know if he wishes to go." Yu Xiangqin immediately added Zhu to his list of candidates and issued an order to summon him. Zhu had administrative talent and was diligent in his duties. After completing his tasks, he was promoted to the position of Chief Clerk and later selected as the Deputy Magistrate of Chuzhou. He was subsequently promoted to Governor and appointed as the Left Capital Censor. However, his rise to prominence occurred unexpectedly and by chance in the alley, truly a case of an accidental encounter.

    董大宗伯
    　　　董大宗伯邦达，少綦贫，父某亦诸生，性迂介，工篆隸，作室匾及楹联，剥灰堆钿皆精。时张茹英员外方修西谿山庄，招往奏技，仆辈憎之，背呼董漆匠，与余外祖暨黄君松石独相得。雍正癸卯，得天司寇以侍讲到八闽试，董君与二人商曰："余子幸充拔萃，将应朝考，无以行，侍讲肯挈之乎？"得天至，即言之，一见大赏识曰："三山一榜中，无此材也！"未几将北上，得天谓外祖曰："董君寒士，昨以二十金襄车价，亟持还之。

    Explanation

    30

    Dong Dazongbo, also known as Dong Bangda, was extremely poor when he was young. His father, a scholar, was also poor and had a straightforward and honest nature. He was skilled in seal script and clerical script, and his work on room plaques and couplets, as well as the decorative technique of peeling off old plaster and layering it with new, was highly refined. At the time, Zhang Ruying, an official from the Waiwai rank, was repairing the West Creek Villa and invited Dong to demonstrate his skills. The servants resented him and called him derogatorily behind his back as "Mr. Paintbrush." However, Dong got along well with my maternal grandfather and Mr. Huang Songshi.

    In the year 1733 during the reign of Emperor Yongzheng, Tian De, a senior official holding the rank of Siku, arrived in Fujian Province as a tutor for the imperial examinations. Dong discussed with Tian and two others: "My son was fortunate to be selected as a top candidate and is about to take the imperial examination, but we have no means of traveling. Would you be willing to take him along?" When Tian arrived, he immediately mentioned this, and upon meeting, he greatly appreciated Dong's son, saying, "There is no one of this caliber in the top ranks of the San Shan category!" Soon after, Dong was preparing to travel north. Tian told my maternal grandfather, "Dong is a poor scholar. Yesterday, I gave him twenty gold pieces to help with the carriage fare, and I quickly returned them to him."

    北土苦寒，视其衣甚凉薄，即以备御冬可也。"翌日来谢，则凉薄依然，诘之，曰："家本无资，此二十金亦贷之戚友者，寒士宜寒，骨颇耐霜雪，不愿以子故，增父累也。"司寇闻，即以己衣两袭赠之，同寓皆赆以表里，得衣盈箧。至都朝考入选，以户部小京官用，又三年联捷选庶常。其父就养入都，附粮艘行至天津，暴疾遽殁，东山仓卒徒跣三百里，扶榇归，至台庄阻浅，颇为旗丁白眼，议迁柩古庙中，孑身先归，另筹雇舟来迓。

    The northern lands are cold and harsh, and upon seeing his clothes, they appear very thin and light, yet sufficient for winter protection.     方相度间，忽遇枫溪人程香篁，亦以守牐散步，字呼曰："董孚臣，何事至此？闻君骤贵，乃憔悴如许？"董即稽颡月河旁，备告近状，程曰："吾方入都坐监，挟二百金，计此间去，八十金可达，今君有急，即以百二十金为赙。"且助之料理乃别。服阕起复，遍告同人，为香篁说项，虽麦舟之谊不啻也。又数年，香篁竟以东山本房中式，司寇谑之，谓移孝作廉，以秦关贱售矣。后司寇身后，以亲家蒋中丞籍没，其狱中寄妇诗卷存女处，卷中不日不月句，纯庙疑其怨望，入宫方沉吟，惟中官郑侍，郑素在内廷掌载籍，急检毛诗进曰："句似出此。"上取阅，乃释然。

    32

    Just when Dong Fuchen was considering his next move, he suddenly encountered Cheng Xianghuang, a man from Fengxi, who was also guarding a gate and taking a walk. Cheng called out to him by name, "Dong Fuchen, what brings you here? I heard you have risen to prominence suddenly, yet you look so haggard!" Dong immediately knelt down by the Moon River and fully reported his recent situation. Cheng said, "I am just about to enter the capital to take up my post, carrying two hundred taels of silver. It costs eighty taels to get here. Now that you are in urgent need, I will use one hundred and twenty taels of silver as a funeral gift." He also helped with the arrangements and then took his leave. After the mourning period, Dong resumed his official duties and informed everyone, advocating for Cheng Xianghuang, though the friendship was no less than that of the "Wheat Boat."     33
    1. 考九香府君寓伯庚农部所 - This phrase indicates the location where the author was visiting, with "九香府君" and "庚农部" being titles or names of respected individuals.
    2. 举室劻勷 - This phrase describes the state of the entire household being busy or in a state of turmoil.
    3. 言毋贻害他人，即最上妙品不敢惜 - This phrase emphasizes the importance of not harming others, even if it means destroying the finest and most precious works.
    4. 过午，忽传董宗伯来 - This phrase describes the sudden arrival of Dong Zongbo in the afternoon.
    5. 吾生矣 - This phrase expresses relief or safety.
    6. 仓惶间出接 - This phrase describes the hurried action of going out to meet someone.
    7. 见即述上恩旨，令往西苑崩角 - This phrase describes the immediate reporting of an imperial decree and the order to go to a specific location in the imperial garden.
    8. 复荷不必革职之谕 - This phrase indicates the receipt of an instruction not to be dismissed from office.
    9. 呈请先臣手泽颇伙 - This phrase refers to the submission of a considerable number of the late minister's writings.
    10. 且饶藏书古绘 - This phrase indicates the possession of a rich collection of ancient books and paintings.
    11. 求赏贡十年，俞之 - This phrase describes the request for a ten-year exemption from tribute, which was granted.
    12. 于是帐颜袖幅，一梅数竹，皆以充贡 - This phrase describes the presentation of paintings and scrolls, including one plum and several bamboo, as tribute.
    13. 而得天司寇之真迹尽矣 - This phrase indicates that all of Tian's genuine works were presented.
    14. 苦后人不振 - This phrase expresses disappointment in the lack of continuation in later generations.
    15. 孙鑑接驾苏州，高宗召入行在，命题特试，誊写甚劣，谕令习字，三年再试 - This phrase describes the actions of Sun Jian, including his reception by Emperor Gaozong and the subsequent test and order to practice calligraphy.
    16. 后归，字仍不习，试亦不再也 - This phrase indicates that Sun Jian did not continue practicing calligraphy and the test was not retaken.
    17. 而宗伯子蔗林相国，犹承父志，眷眷恩门，数十年通好勿替 - This phrase describes the continuation of Zongbo's legacy and the maintenance of close ties with the imperial court for many years.
    18. 余幼年犹见宗伯赠外祖一小立幅，烟云缭绕，有逸气，真朝披一品、夜抱九仙者，张宗苍瞠乎后矣 - This phrase describes the author's memory of a small vertical scroll given by Zongbo to his maternal grandfather, with swirling clouds and a free-spirited atmosphere.

    Translated Text:

    At the time, I was visiting the residence of the respected Nine Fragrances Lord, a guest of the official with the title "庚农部." Upon hearing the news, the entire household was in a state of turmoil. The lord ordered the front and back doors to be closed, not allowing anyone to leave. Only the works of Tian were inspected, and any that seemed to be suspected or disliked were immediately destroyed. He said, "Do not harm others, even the finest and most precious works are not to be spared." After noon, it was suddenly reported that Dong Zongbo had arrived. The official said, "I am saved!" Hurriedly, I went out to meet him. Upon seeing him, I immediately reported the imperial decree, ordering to go to the corner of the Western Garden. I again received the instruction not to be dismissed from office. The official submitted a request for a considerable number of the late minister's writings and also had a rich collection of ancient books and paintings. He requested a ten-year exemption from tribute, which was granted. Thus, paintings and scrolls, one plum and several bamboo, were all presented as tribute, and thus, all of Tian's genuine works were presented. Later generations did not continue the tradition. Sun Jian received the emperor in Suzhou, and Emperor Gaozong summoned him to the imperial residence, set a special test, but his writing was very poor, so the emperor ordered him to practice calligraphy and retake the test after three years. After returning, he still did not practice calligraphy, and the test was not retaken. But Zongbo's son, Sugulin, continued his father's legacy, maintaining close ties with the

    米乔林
    　　　廓尔喀之役，补山相国奉命入藏督饷，从行者中书周肖廉、别驾胡雪方。蜀道本难康卫，藏则难之难矣，崎岖过察木多数站，至墨竹工卡，支帐前就，忽有浙客米乔林请谒，相国喜曰："真空谷足音也！"问之，乃肖廉姻连。肖廉娶山阴马，寄籍（氵乐）阳，米父亦以北籍来教授，颇相周旋。乔林以佻达为父所逐，其戚有倅于蜀者，依之，流转至此。献越酿一小瓶，云居停主以革囊携至，尝之如挹天浆，即留共饭，情话良久别去。明晨欲行，乌拉不集，滞留竟日，此弊途中时有之，盖番人言语不通，理谕势驱，均属无用，需檄土司始办。

    34

    In the Campaign against Nepal, Bu Shan, a high-ranking official, was ordered to enter Tibet to oversee the supply of provisions. Accompanying him were Zhou Xiaoqian, a Middle Secretary, and Hu Xuefang, a Deputy Magistrate. The road through Sichuan is already difficult, but the journey to Tibet is even more challenging. They traveled through many stations in Tashilhunpo, arriving at Mozhu Gongka, where they set up their tents before proceeding. Suddenly, a guest from Zhejiang named Mi Qiaolin came to visit. The Viceroy was delighted and said, "This is like hearing footsteps in the vast emptiness!" Upon inquiry, it turned out that Mi Qiaolin was related to Zhou Xiaoqian by marriage. Zhou Xiaoqian had married a woman from Shanyin and was registered in Le Yang. Mi Qiaolin's father, who came from the north to teach, had a good relationship with them. However, Mi Qiaolin was expelled by his father for being frivolous. His relative in Sichuan took him in, and he wandered to this place. Mi Qiaolin offered a small bottle of wine from Zhejiang, saying that the host brought it in a leather bag. Tasting it was like drinking nectar from the sky. They invited him to join them for a meal, and they talked for a long time before parting. The next morning, they wanted to leave, but the porters did not gather, so they were delayed for a whole day. This problem often occurs on the way, because the local people do not understand Chinese, and persuasion or force is ineffective; only when they issue an order to the local chieftains can it be resolved.

    乔林适来，告以故，曰："吾试筹之。"米故无赖，昵一蛮妓，译云坐鸦头，因与土民浃洽，且通蛮语，乃诏之，俾召乌拉。婢遣父兄招之，薄暮大集，五更行矣，相国更大喜，复令番民等，前站晓谕后站，蝉递而下，由是无复阻滞。至杨八井驻扎，乃以米生功上闻，乞以八品用，得旨竟与七品。将补州邑，肖廉力阻，告相国米生轻躁，宜且试之，乃借补州判，旋改县令，不十年陟刺史，居然水晶顶子挂朝珠矣。予客成都时，于肖廉处遇之，雪方谑之曰："君已驱五马，曾迓宝眷否？"曰："已遣人往（氵乐）。"肖廉曰："非也，谓佛国中散花人耳！"乔林大惭。

    蠢子数
    　　　蠢子数托名康节先生，在晋省某府，今移太原，其书汗牛充栋，其法先问父母生卒，及娶妻生子岁月，不合即令查，查或历数日，亦有终不得者。合即掣一幅付之，始末胪列，真名称其实也。其语或骈或散，或文或俗，若隐若明，若庄若谑，则又狡狯殊甚。余曾见三纸，一为袁方伯柏田，由誊录起家，繇辞似科第而非科第，微词嘲讽，殊见滑稽。初任金华佐，两字借点极巧，继而题长兴。晋西防，保堪陛，擢福州，以至被议捐复，语皆暗合。

    Explanation

    36

    Cunning Scholars and Divination

    The so-called "Cunning Scholars" claimed to be disciples of Mr. Kangjie (Sima Guang). They once resided in a certain prefecture in Shanxi Province and later moved to Taiyuan. Their writings were abundant, filling countless volumes. Their method involved first inquiring about the birth and death dates of one's parents, as well as the marriage and childbearing dates. If the conditions did not align, they instructed the person to check further, a process that could take several days or sometimes never yield a result. When the conditions aligned, they would draw a piece of paper and give it to the person, listing the beginning and end of the divination, revealing the true name or identity. The language used in the divination could be either parallel or free, formal or colloquial, vague or clear, serious or humorous, and was often highly cunning.

    I have seen three such pieces of divination. One was for Yuan Fangbo Baitian, who began his career as a copyist. His words resembled those of a scholar-official but were not actually those of a scholar-official. They contained subtle criticism and mockery, and were particularly humorous. He was initially appointed as an assistant in Jinhua, where the two characters used were extremely clever. Later, the divination was used to predict the situation in Changxing. He was later promoted to positions in western Shanxi, the capital, and then to Fuzhou. Eventually, he was criticized and demoted, but all the statements were indirectly correct.

    37

    戊午春余，方以观察需次，出书示客，是年下一联以飞霜对明月，时都匀宰程栋尚为运司主藏吏，偶至，诧曰："作转运矣！不见司署前石柱乎？"后数月，果符所注，方伯喜，屡出书索解，补首道晋闽臬，皆可意揣。后数岁有中流砥柱字，不得其说，方伯意或当调陕。嘉庆十一年，余以运铅入楚，过黄鹄矶，见中流砥柱四字，大书深刻，不啻泰山碑也，以告方伯，共为恍然。嗣再作旬宣，内召放还，一一皆可意会，膝下三人，书云："两子送终。

    Explanation

    37

    In the spring of the year of the Horse, I was serving as an observer in preparation for a higher position, showing my books to guests. That year, I composed a couplet with "flying frost" opposing "bright moon." At the time, Cheng Dong, the magistrate of Duyun, was still a lower-ranking official managing the treasury under the transport commissioner. He happened to visit and exclaimed, "You will become a transport commissioner! Haven't you seen the stone pillar in front of the office?" A few months later, the prophecy came true, and the provincial governor was delighted. He frequently asked for explanations, and I was promoted to the position of governor of Fujian, which could be inferred from the events. A few years later, there was a phrase "pillar in the middle of the stream," but I could not understand its meaning. The governor thought I might be transferred to Shaanxi. In the eleventh year of the Jiaqing era, I was transporting lead into Chu, passing by Huanghu矶, where I saw the inscription "pillar in the middle of the stream" clearly inscribed and deeply carved, no different from the famous monument on Mount Tai. I informed the governor, and we both were enlightened. Later, I was appointed to a position of greater authority, and I was summoned back to the capital. All these events could be understood in the same way. I had three children, and in a letter, it was written: "Two sons will take care of the funeral."

    38

    "长君厚堂竟前卒，亦验。一为完颜制军魁伦，时制闽浙，以阅兵驻武林，萼楼张观察邮寄以示僚属，前半节目，众均未悉，制军则曰甚验。后则纶綍簪缨作联，众皆贡谀谓入阁且袭爵也，魁亦居之不疑，盖尔时以参伍浦，眷甚隆，拜相封公，亦意中事，但杂以生死字样，疑之，则曰："大约极品后，即考终耳。"其后仍有恩膏优渥，锡予频频等语，益信其吉，岂知为赐帛谶。异哉！生死关头，乃严旨中语，尤奇。死后仁宗念其前功，恤还没产，且录其子。

    Explanation

    38

    A high-ranking official named Changjun Hou Tang died prematurely, and it was verified. One of them was Wanyan Zhijun Kui Lun, who controlled Fujian and Zhejiang at the time, and stationed in Wulin for reviewing troops. Zhang Guancha from E Lou sent it by mail to show his subordinates. The first half of the program was unknown to everyone, but the military leader said it was very effective. Later, high-ranking officials formed a connection, and everyone flattered the idea of the military leader entering the cabinet and inheriting a title, which he accepted without doubt. At that time, he was highly favored by the court, and becoming a chancellor and being ennobled was also an expected thing. But mixed with words about life and death, it raised doubts. He said, "Approximately after reaching the highest rank, one would die peacefully." Later, there were still frequent bestowals of favor and generous treatment, increasing the belief in good fortune. Who knew it was a prophecy involving the bestowal of silk? Strange! A matter of life and death, mentioned in a strict edict, is particularly unusual. After his death, Emperor Renzong remembered his previous achievements, consoled his orphaned children, and appointed his son.

    39

    末路亦无一字不验，其一独不验，则钱星垣榆所藏也，隐其姓名，造中载连捷科名，宦场尤利。弱冠余以进士分部，六十陟侍郎，出作巡抚。后忽直书曰："天颜大怒，臣罪当诛。"又一行云："魂归玉笥峰头鹤，血染云阳市上花。"考玉笥在江西，而星垣系闽中人，又云其人初官额外，寄晋问命，得此怖绝，弃官归，长斋事佛，年四十归道山，计已减龄忏劫矣。三纸皆粗疏朽败，字更恶劣，潦草不可解。星垣复云，或以高宗圣造试自，则只四大字，曰"万寿无疆"，疑其附会。

    Explanation

    39

    Even the most obscure details are verified without exception, except for one item that does not hold true. This exception is found in the collection of Qian Xingyuan Yu, who concealed his own name. The text contains records of continuous success in imperial examinations, which is particularly advantageous in the bureaucratic career. At the age of twenty, he was appointed as a Jinshi and assigned to a specific department. At sixty, he reached the rank of Shilang and was appointed as a provincial governor. Later, the text abruptly states, "The emperor's face is filled with anger, and my crime is punishable by death." Another line reads, "My soul returns to the crane on the peak of Yusi, and my blood stains the flowers in the market of Yunyang." It is known that Yusi Peak is located in Jiangxi, while Qian Xingyuan Yu is from Fujian. It is also said that the person initially held an extra position and was later formally appointed. Upon seeing this, he was terrified and resigned from his official position, dedicating himself to religious practices, specifically Buddhism. He passed away at the age of forty, and it is believed that his early death was a reduction in lifespan due to karmic retribution. The three documents are all rough, worn, and the handwriting is poor and illegible. Qian Xingyuan Yu further mentioned that someone might attribute the text to the reign of Emperor Gaozong of Song, and it contains only the four large characters, "Long life and prosperity," which is suspected to be an embellishment.

    醉死
    　　　南洲茅祖母舅，簉室吴孺人父吴翁，无子，寄食余家，髫时见之，已七十余，为余言：余以嗜酒故，得两死。壮时以贩缯入闽，来往温陵，其友业教曲，适领班至郡，厨烧春方熟，群伶少年选事，谓曰:"翁称善饮，能尽一杓，吾曹度曲以侑。"杓以量酒，一杓得茗碗十八，翁曰："可！"曲终杓已罄，笑曰："何伤乎，甜美甚可口也！"方逾阈，触风而仆，幸署中有知医者，教以大长桶置井泉，卧其中，发及手足甲中，出血如缕，以生腐置臆即焦熟，尽一箱乃已。医曰生矣，仍以腐浆灌之，三日始能餔糜，病卧月余，百日始复初，此一死也。继又以洪醉夜归，迷路走荒郊，遇一僵尸攫之，彼醉不知，以为人也。

    Explanation

    40

    Drunk to Death

    My maternal uncle, the second wife's father of my grandmother from Nan Zhou, had no son and relied on my family for sustenance. I saw him in my early childhood, and by then he was already over seventy years old. He told me, "Because of my fondness for alcohol, I have experienced two near-death experiences." In his prime, he traveled to Fujian to trade silk, coming and going between Wenling. One of his friends made a living teaching music, and just happened to lead a troupe to the prefecture. The kitchen had just finished cooking the spring wine, and a group of young actors selected tasks. They said to him, "You are known for your excellent drinking skills; can you finish a ladleful? We will accompany you with songs." The ladle was used to measure the wine, and one ladle contained eighteen tea bowls. He said, "Sure!" By the end of the song, the ladle was empty. He laughed and said, "What harm is there? It is very sweet and delicious!" As he was crossing the threshold, he was knocked down by the wind. Fortunately, there was a doctor in the office who instructed him to place a large bucket filled with well water in the courtyard, lie down in it, and let the water seep into his hair and the nails of his hands and feet, causing a continuous flow of blood. He then placed raw and cooked meat on his chest, which quickly became hot and cooked. It took an entire box of meat to complete the treatment. The doctor said he had been saved, and continued to feed him with a mixture of raw and cooked meat. After three days, he could start eating porridge, and after more than a month of illness, he fully recovered after a hundred days. This was one near-death experience. Later, he returned home heavily intoxicated at night, lost his way in the wilderness, and encountered a corpse that grabbed him. He was drunk and did not realize it was a corpse, thinking it was a person.

    41

    时手一蔗竿，翁素武勇，力击之仆，倦极，迷惘中触一野厝，意即家中卧榻，据之酣寝。黎明，趁墟人过，见尸喧噪，翁乃惊起，怖绝，遂不敢夜行，此又一死，然皆幸免，若蔡孝廉则真死。孝廉名焜，余中表兄馨山上舍子，素不甚酒，秋捷后，公车北上。燕赵苦寒，饮烧春甘之，遂非此不饭。量固不洪。日不尽数两，第廿年来日饮无何，铢铢而积之，腹贮者已可盈缶矣。一夕扃户寝，煦午犹不起，家人怪之，抉扉而入，室中滃然，衾帐皆焦，半身烬矣，手犹握菸管，竟与《本草》所载倚马焚身事同，盖菸火引线，倏如爆竹之发耳。嗜饮者曰，如此反真，洵大佳事，殊深辗转床褥者，亦愿为陶土，意险诨也。倖际太平，何必觅山中千日？

    Explanation

    41

    At that time, the old man held a sugarcane pole. He was usually brave and martial, striking it with force until it fell. Exhausted, he wandered dazedly and accidentally touched a rural house, thinking it was his home bed, and leaned against it to sleep deeply. At dawn, people going to market saw a corpse and made a commotion. The old man was startled awake, utterly terrified, and thereafter dared not travel at night. This was another near-death experience, but he narrowly escaped. As for Scholar Pao Xianliang, he truly died. Scholar Pao's name was Kun; he was the eldest son of my cousin from Xingshan. He was not much of a drinker. After passing the imperial examination in autumn, he traveled north by imperial carriage. The regions of Yan and Zhao were extremely cold, and he found the strong liquor called "burnt spring" sweet, to the point that he wouldn't eat without it. His capacity was indeed not large; he drank no more than a few ounces daily. Over twenty years, he drank nothing each day, accumulating bit by bit, and what was stored in his belly could fill a jar. One night, he locked the door and went to sleep. At midday, he still hadn't gotten up. His family members found it strange and pried open the door to enter. The room was smoky, the bedding all burned, and half of his body was reduced to ashes. He still held a smoking pipe. This turned out to be the same as the incident recorded in the Bencao where someone burned himself while leaning on a horse. The firework fuse suddenly ignited like a firecracker exploding. Those who love drinking said, "Like this, it turns out to be true; indeed, it's a great good thing." Especially those who are restless in bed, also wish to be clay, meaning it's a dangerous jest. Fortunately, we live in a time of peace, why bother seeking a thousand days in the mountains?

    沈转运
    　　　沈转运树声，本名云际，工制艺，试辄冠曹偶，第性落拓，好狎邪游。以乾隆癸酉拔萃，充八旗教习。丙子丁丑速捷乡会，功令教习，期满引见，以知县教职分别铨用，时兼管国子监事。陆少宗伯宗楷，以其进士也，另援雍正间旧例，书绿头笺作部属知县兼用，上疑其市恩也，黜之。沈君亦以教职用，乃易今名，寒氈数年，始以本班选江西之弋阳。岁中秋，署中小宴，酒酣，戚友戏之曰："君素跌宕，邑有流娼某颇韵，盍往观乎？"君曰："诺。"即趋而出，阍者见之，讶本官之微服也，以小竖缀之，急呼舆从身押往，不过以县多地棍，恐其不识挟诈，无他意也。
