    Se Transpo
    　　　Se Transpo Shusheng, originally named Yunji, was skilled in literary composition and consistently excelled in his exams. However, he had a carefree and debauched nature. In the year of Qianlong's reign, he was selected as an outstanding candidate and appointed as a teacher for the Eight Banners. In the years of Bingzi and Dingchou, he quickly passed the provincial and metropolitan examinations. After completing his term as a teacher, he was formally presented to the emperor and assigned to various posts, including that of a county magistrate, with the additional responsibility of overseeing the Imperial Academy. Lu Shaizongbo Zongkai, recognizing his status as a Jinshi (imperial scholar), recommended him according to an old precedent from the Yongzheng era, using a green-headed note to suggest his appointment as both a departmental official and a county magistrate. The emperor suspected this of favoritism and demoted him. Se Shusheng was then appointed to a teaching post and changed his name. He endured years of hardship before finally being selected to serve in Yiyang, Jiangxi. During the Mid-Autumn Festival, a small banquet was held in his office. After drinking deeply, his close friends teased him, saying, "You are always so unrestrained. There is a particularly elegant prostitute in the county. Why don't you go and see her?" He replied, "Yes," and immediately left. The gatekeeper, seeing him in disguise, was surprised and thought the magistrate was in disguise. He had a young servant follow him and quickly summoned a carriage and entourage to escort him, fearing that he might be unfamiliar with the local ruffians and could be deceived, with no other intention.

    竖导之行，重门深闭，人声甚隐，立户外稍久，舆从至，足音跫然，有阚于隙者，举室大扰。觉有异，排閮而入，见异言异服者数人，急窜奔迸，苦巷窄不四达，悉就擒。至县研讯，则邻邑大伙，得赃避此俵分也，遂以获盗功迁司马焉。到任迟延，复被议，入都蒙恩转陛建昌太守。居数年，又以失人案，倒降三级，上复命送部，奏对甚契，适太原守缺，晋抚已奏调平阳沈君之燮应补所遗，得旨即以沈树声补太原，异数也，隆隆日上，藩臬督抚，皆意中事。不数年陟长芦运使，乃以奏销不及额，鹾使登之白简，放归。与沈果之师最昵，常云："兄遭际大奇，或掖之而踬，或抑之而升，吉凶相倚。而无心获盗事尤奇，真可谓入穴得子也。流妓合以举主属之，李宫保绪论洵灼见也，石榴裙底，乃不得作逋逃薮矣！"

    The Upright Guide's Journey

    The upright guide embarked on his journey, passing through heavily guarded gates and deep into a secluded place where human voices were barely audible. Standing outside for a while, he noticed the arrival of a carriage and its attendants, and the distinct sound of footsteps echoed in the quiet. Someone peeked through a crack, causing a great commotion in the household. Feeling something strange, he pushed open the door and entered, only to see several people with unusual speech and clothing. They rushed to flee in panic, but the narrow alley made it difficult to escape, and all were captured. Upon arriving at the county for investigation, it was discovered that they were a gang from a neighboring town who had obtained loot and divided it there. As a result of his success in capturing the thieves, he was promoted to the position of司马 (a military or administrative rank).

    However, there was a delay in taking up the new office, and he faced further criticism. He was then transferred to the capital and received favor to be appointed as the governor of Jianchang. After serving for several years, he was demoted three ranks due to a case involving the loss of people. The emperor ordered him to be sent to the Ministry, but his response was very satisfactory. Just as the position of太原 (Taiyuan) governor was vacant, the governor of Shanxi had already recommended Shen Junxi to fill the vacancy. Upon receiving the imperial decree, Shen Shusheng was appointed as the governor of Taiyuan, an unusual honor. His career continued to rise, and he eventually became a high-ranking official, including provincial governors, judicial officials, and military commanders, all of which were within his expectations.

    Within a few years, he was promoted to the position of长芦运使 (salt commissioner), but due to the failure to meet the required quota in the report, the salt commissioner reported him to the court, and he was dismissed and returned home. He was closest to Shen Guo's teacher, who often remarked, "My brother had a very unusual fate, sometimes helped and sometimes stumbled, sometimes suppressed and sometimes promoted, with good and bad interdependent. And the unintentional capture of thieves is especially strange, truly, it can be said that he found a treasure in a cave. The courtesan combined the recommendation with the host, and Li Gongbao's subsequent discussion is indeed insightful. The bottom of the peony skirt, which could not serve as a refuge for fugitives."

    盗名出入有冥报
    　　　申韩家每以从宽为造福，晓岚所谓四救先生是也，然死者衔冤，冥责亦无少贷。汪润亭师罗凤翁常言其友有幕于三山者，则忘其为闽为侯官也，与司钱谷者分东西室下榻，中一室为办事公所。一岁秋间，居停有嘉会，署演剧，诸客观且饮，钱谷友适为疟不出。昏后疟作，热不可卧，起步室中，迷罔间忽闻曳纸声历历，即簾隙阚之，见中室灯光如豆，一人翻卷太息，审睇之则无首，大惊仆地。署中多铺杉板，震声轰然，宾主皆惊，辍席问讯，答以疟发猝倒，无他也。明晨独招刑名友来，询以案上何卷，答曰："此一劫案，吾以枭斩太多，欲活一二囚耳。"钱谷告以宵来所见，且告之曰："恐欲贷者必宿盗，故被戕者现形。

    44

    Stealing fame and entering/exiting have karmic retribution.

    The Legalist school often advocates being lenient as a way to do good, as Ji Xiaolan referred to the Four-Saving Master. However, even those who die with grievances will face karmic retribution without leniency. Wang Runteng's teacher Luo Fengong often mentioned a friend who served in an official capacity in Fuzhou, though he forgot whether it was in Fujian or Houguan. This friend shared a room with the official responsible for managing finances and grain, with the office located in the middle room. One autumn, the host held a grand gathering, and a performance was staged in the official residence. The guests were watching and drinking when the friend of the finance and grain official was ill with malaria and could not attend. After dusk, the malaria worsened, and he was too hot to sleep. He walked around the room, and in his dazed state, he suddenly heard a clear sound of paper being dragged. Looking through the curtain gap, he saw a dim light in the middle room, and a person flipping through documents while sighing. Upon closer inspection, he saw that the person had no head, and he was greatly shocked and fell to the ground. The official residence had many pine boards, and the sound of the fall was loud, startling the guests and the host. They stopped their banquet to inquire, and the friend replied that he had fainted due to malaria. The next morning, he summoned a friend knowledgeable in criminal law, asking what documents were on the table. The friend replied, "This is a case of execution, and I want to save one or two prisoners because there have been too many executions." The friend of the finance and grain official told him about what he had seen the previous night and warned him, saying, "The person you want to save must be a habitual thief, which is why the victim is appearing."

    "刑名友故愎，曰："我闻狱贵求生，不闻求死，我自用我法，弗乱人意。"竟用宽稿。稿出而病，不及月竟死。然此为故出，意尚无他，若以故入邀功，则得祸。自应速且酷耳。钱刺史亮工以州司马需次时，捐二千四百金市大盗三，得保举。盖楚北恶习，应捕人择少年丐，饲以酒肉，恣其嫖赌，继乃诲之窃盗，渐乃习于焚杀，有购之者即缚以充戮，如畜羊豕然，盗亦视为固然，慷慨就死，不怨不怖，解付司院，绝无翻异者。亮工以是得刺沔阳，明年莅任，眷属尚在省，妻陆宜人梦有送瓜者，启其盒，则赫然三级也。惊醒，急足来报亮工病矣，未几竟死，死之日，即三囚正法之日也，尤奇。又数月，陆亦卒。人命至重，鬼神难欺，奈何以贫民断头，博热官进爵哉！

    A Judge Stubborn and Obstinate

    A judge, known for his stubbornness, said, "I have heard that in the law, the emphasis is on seeking life, not death. I will use my own methods without confusing others' intentions." He ultimately used a lenient judgment. The lenient judgment led to the prisoner's illness and death within a month. However, this was a deliberate release, with no other intention. If one deliberately convicts someone to gain merit, then they will suffer misfortune. Such cases should be handled swiftly and severely. Zhang Lianggong, the magistrate of Mianyang, while serving as a deputy governor, spent 2,400 taels of silver to buy three major bandits, and received a recommendation for promotion. This was a corrupt practice in northern Hubei, where captured individuals would select young beggars, feed them with alcohol and meat, allow them to indulge in gambling and prostitution, and then teach them to steal. Gradually, they would be trained in arson and murder. When someone was bought, they would be tied up and executed, treated like livestock. Thieves also regarded this as normal, dying bravely and willingly, without complaint or fear, and sent to the judicial department, where no one ever changed their plea. Zhang Lianggong received the appointment as magistrate of Mianyang. The following year, he took office, but his family was still in the provincial capital. His wife, Lady Lu, dreamed of someone bringing melons. When she opened the box, there were three severed heads inside. She woke up in shock and immediately sent someone to report that Zhang was ill. Soon after, he died. The day he died was the same day the three prisoners were executed, which was especially strange. A few months later, Lady Lu also died. Human life is extremely precious, and ghosts and gods are hard to deceive. How can one cut off the heads of poor people to gain promotions for high officials?

    张长生
    　　　余宰兰豁时，有催解委员陶贰尹来，留之署不住，乃送船上居。陶君固戴莲士相国婿，以为贵倨态耳。数日，忽遣仆递一失单，窃去八十金，且失一委牌，无以消差。余大疑，即嘱段尉迹之，俄顷带一人来，名张长生，即招陶君共讯之，供云："昨夜四更，若尚与客饮，若上坐，某妓比肩，左坐钱店客叶，右坐袜店伙颜，若欲赠妓无资，假叶姓四洋与之，安所得八十金？委牌置几上，若醉倾，烟烬烧其套，我得之无用，计当尚在船内。所窃者一短褂、一雨衣，皆颜客物，不信，呼某妓讯之。

    Zhang Changsheng
    When I was the magistrate of Lanhuo, a commissioner for expedited delivery named Tao Ernyin came. He refused to stay at my office and was sent to live on a ship. Tao Jun was the son-in-law of Dai Lianshi, a high-ranking official, and he acted with a pretentious attitude. A few days later, he suddenly sent a servant to deliver a loss report, claiming that eighty silver dollars had been stolen, along with a commissioner's plaque, and that he could not resolve the matter. I was greatly suspicious and immediately instructed Officer Duan to investigate. In a short while, he brought a man named Zhang Changsheng, and I summoned Tao Jun to interrogate him together. Zhang Changsheng stated: "Last night at the fourth watch, you were still drinking with guests. You were seated at the head of the table, next to a courtesan, with Mr. Ye from a money shop sitting to your left and Mr. Yan from a sock shop sitting to your right. You wanted to give the courtesan something but had no money, so you borrowed four silver dollars from Mr. Ye and gave them to her. How could you get eighty silver dollars? The commissioner's plaque was placed on the table, and you were drunk and knocked it over. The ashes from the cigarette burned the case, and I got it but found it useless. It should still be in the ship. What was stolen was a short jacket and a raincoat, both belonging to Mr. Yan's guest. If you don't believe me, call the courtesan to verify it."

    "陶君瑟缩间不辞而别，余乃薄责二十，赏以青蚨四缗，谕令改业，长生则大泣，崩角曰："公杀我矣！此地商贾多，波面笙歌竟夜不绝，胠箧殊易，偶窘迫，同侪中有无相通，否则捕人周其乏也。今从公策，良者以为我窃，窃者以为我良，无容身所；捕者仇我更甚，有案即以充贼，拘挛敲扑，无已时矣。"余叱之，则曰："无已，再日乞八合米，所赐足办盐菜，置我翼房中，终公任，我乃理故案耳。"斯事庸琐不足记，第思陶君故望族，且贵人婿，以不自检束，身乃与驵侩伍，为偷儿所笑。张长生性非凶恶，一堕下流，欲求自拔而不可得，无论贵贱，均当刻刻作执玉捧盈想也，可畏哉！

    Explanation

    47

    Tao, in a state of fear, left without saying goodbye. I then lightly reprimanded him twenty times and rewarded him with four strings of copper coins. I instructed him to change his profession. Zhang Changsheng then wept bitterly and fell to his knees, saying, "You have killed me! Here, there are many merchants, and the music and singing on the water continue all night long, making it very easy to break into chests. If I am in dire straits, my peers will help each other, but otherwise, those who catch thieves will help those in need. Now, following your advice, the honest will think I am a thief, and the thieves will think I am honest, leaving me with no place to stand. Those who catch thieves will hate me even more, and any case will be used to label me as a thief, leading to endless binding and beating." I rebuked him, and he said, "If there is no other way, I will ask for eight units of rice for two days. The gift you gave is enough to buy salt and vegetables, and I will stay in a side room until your term ends, handling old cases." This matter is trivial and not worth recording, but I reflect on Tao, who comes from a former noble family and is the son-in-law of a wealthy person, yet due to his lack of self-discipline, he has fallen into the company of merchants and traders, being laughed at by thieves. Zhang Changsheng is not inherently evil, but once he has fallen into a lower social class, he finds it impossible to escape. Regardless of social status, one should always think of oneself as holding precious objects, symbolizing a high moral standard. How awe-inspiring!

    48

    吴婢念旧
    　　　绍所盐商汪君大丰，为予言其族母有婢吴，颇婉顺，母怜之。后病且死，嘱二子善遣，子亦孝，体母意，厚赐之，遣老仆王送归其家。婢父母均前卒，两兄皆无赖，所赍既诱尽，更以二百金鬻之远所，音耗遂绝。久之，王仆急事往闽，渡海遇蔡谦，被掳，驱至一艇中，忽有呼之者："若非汪孺人家王伯乎？"仆谛视，急呼曰："吴姐乃在此，救我！救我！"吴叱左右解其缚，谓两兄匪人，荡我资，复计陷我此间，夫出海捐千金购我，颇厚我，然所为不道，我微讽之，渠亦自危，然以群伙牵制，不能决，行当与之俱烬矣。

    Explanation

    48

    The Female Servant's Affection for the Past

    Wang Daofeng, a salt merchant from Zhao, told me about his clan mother who had a servant named Wu. She was quite gentle and obedient, and the mother loved her dearly. After falling ill and nearing death, the mother instructed her two sons to treat Wu well and send her back home. The sons were filial and followed their mother's wishes, giving Wu generous gifts and sending the old servant Wang to escort her back to her home. Wu's parents had both passed away before this, and her two brothers were both unreliable. They had already squandered all the money they had given her, and then sold her to a distant place for two hundred gold pieces, cutting off all communication with her. After a long time, Wang, the servant, had urgent business to attend to in Fujian. He crossed the sea and met Cai Qian, who captured him and drove him to a boat. Suddenly, someone called out to him: "Are you not Wang Bo from the household of Mr. Wang?" The servant carefully looked and cried out, "Sister Wu is here! Save me! Save me!" Wu ordered those around her to untie his bonds and said that her two brothers were not good people, had squandered her wealth, and then plotted to trap her there. Her husband had gone out to sea and spent a thousand gold pieces to buy her, treating her quite well, but his actions were not right. She gently criticized him, and he also felt uneasy, but was constrained by his group and could not make a decision. Soon, they would all burn together.

    49

    俄倾，蔡谦夹群盗传呼曰："出海至！"盖出海者，舶主尊称，非如宋江之假保义头衔也。谦短衣裤褶，悉以红毾毭为之，妇则我服襄头，居然压寨夫人，但男女均徒跣耳。指王谓谦曰："此我旧主仆，昔蒙其惠，老且贫，勿责其赎也，幸送之归。"蔡诺之，赠之金，并一旗，曰："执此海道无阻。"王与婢大泣而别。归以告其兄，二兄鬻妹金已罄，计为盗亦得，入海投之，妹闻之即怒曰："人之无良，我以为兄，必杀之！"谦为宛转解释，始抱头鼠窜而归。后余宰永嘉，晤邱军门，言蔡谦败后，以巨礟自沉其舟，则真与之俱烬矣。吴虽遇人不淑，陷为盗妇死，殉夫无名，然与王翠翘之人尽夫者，不尚有从一而终之节哉！

    Explanation

    49

    In a short while, Cài Qiān, surrounded by a group of bandits, shouted: "Arriving from overseas!" This term "arriving from overseas" is a respectful title for the ship's captain, unlike the false title of loyalty that Sòng Jiāng used. Cài Qiān wore short clothing, specifically pants and jackets, all made of red carpeting. The woman wore traditional Chinese headwear and was indeed the lady who suppresses the camp, but both men and women went barefoot. Pointing to Wáng, he told Cài Qiān: "This is my old master and servant. He once received my favor, and now he is old and poor. Do not demand his ransom. Please send him back." Cài Qiān agreed and gave him gold and a flag, saying: "Holding this flag will ensure no obstacles on the sea route." Wáng and the maid cried bitterly and parted. Upon returning home, he told his brother. The brother, whose money from selling his sister had run out, thought that becoming a bandit would also work, and he joined the sea. Upon hearing this, the sister became angry and said: "The person is not good. I thought he was my brother, but I will kill him!" Cài Qiān explained in a gentle and persuasive manner, and the brother fled home in a panic, hiding his head like a rat. Later, I served as an official in Yongjia and met Military Officer Qiu, who told me that after Cài Qiān's defeat, he sank his ship with a large cannon, and truly burned together with it. Wú, though she encountered an unworthy person and died as a bandit's wife, died for her husband without a name. However, compared to Wáng Cuìqiào, who was involved with many men, does she not still have the virtue of remaining faithful to one partner until death?

    三异笔谈卷二
    　　　飞云洞
    　　　予以饥驱，踏万里路，足迹遍天下，未至者惟两粤奉天甘肃及福建五省，佳山水遭逢不少，惜无济胜具，能效谢公蜡屐，每读《名山记》而怅然。幼时在家，最爱横云小赤壁，巍然一邱，居然壁立千仞。家住泖滨，扁舟过塔下，亦有临风飘然、遗世独立之致，壮而之四方。于苏则喜书院前柳阴小桥，夏月坐其下终日。于润喜金山，然以为未若昇之燕子矶，入矶尾尤胜，柳暗花明，绝似天台。明岩下村落，惟梳妆一楼，无谓辽后安得至此，酒佣附会陈妙常，尤可供哂。于杭则冷泉亭第一，西溪里菴，均以幽胜，佳绝处不在杭而在岩，七里钓台，真仙境也。

    Explanation

    50

    Translation

    Three Strange Talks, Volume Two
    Flying Cloud Cave

    I was driven by hunger, traveling ten thousand miles, with footprints covering the world. The only places I have not reached are the two Guang provinces, Fengtian, Gansu, and Fujian. I have encountered many beautiful mountains and waters, but unfortunately, I lack the means to travel further. To be able to emulate Xie Gong's waxed shoes, every time I read The Record of Famous Mountains and feel disappointed. As a child, I loved the small Red Cliff of Horizontal Clouds, majestically a single hill, as if it were a thousand feet high and sheer. My home is by the shores of Maobin, and crossing the tower in a small boat, I also felt the wind and appeared to float away, with a sense of detachment from the world. As I grew up, I traveled to all directions. In Suzhou, I liked the willow-shaded bridge in front of the academy, sitting under it all day during the summer. In Runzhou, I liked Jinshan, but I thought it was not as good as Sheng's Yanzijī. Entering the tail of the cliff was especially beautiful, willows dark and flowers bright, absolutely like Tiantai. At the foot of Bright Rock, there are villages, with only one building for dressing up. It's meaningless to say the Liao empress could have been here; the wine seller added Tanchuochang to the story, especially for ridicule. In Hangzhou, the Cold Spring Pavilion is the best, and the temple in Xixi, all are secluded and beautiful. The best places are not in Hangzhou but in the rock. The Seven Li Fishing Platform, truly a fairyland.

    51

    于扬惟虹桥可，一片蒨丽，皆工笔画，李将军金碧丹青，非龙眠白描手。之楚则丹崖碧障，与黄鹄矶均属大观。一至蜀道云栈，乃步步引人入胜，炫人耳目。予过时正盛夏，毫无暑意，当新雨初霁，峰峰挂瀑，喷珠溅沫，阑入筍舆，鸟声和之，马头冲处，衣袂生云，如李杜诗、韩苏文，不作一苇平衍也。壬子岁，谒陈桂堂于辰州，是岁山水大发，望大小酉山，风雨迷离，云烟出没，可望而不可即。嗣是捧檄赴滇，离会城四十里，驿曰板桥，宿焉，脚靴手版，将料理折腰耳。食后行饭，出逆旅展眺，忽见一岫横前，夕阳映之，金碧辉煌，落霞万顷，与山一色。盖山皆石筍，筍皆碧色，又均嵌空玲珑，成此奇特。

    52

    石湖之万笏朝天，与黄山之千株临荡，均黄石，且质纯，殊有仙凡之别。晨起，初（目敦）乍出，另成艳景，恋恋几不成行，马上犹回首数四。后每逢迎送，辄留一宿，然终未若黄平之飞云洞，至今犹梦寐遇之也。言山水之胜，曰雄曰奇，曰秀曰丽，飞云洞咸背焉。将至数里，见千寻挺立，前后左右，古杉参天，无所谓洞也。寻之在绝户之下，翳荟交蔽，水簾一桁，无路可通，由其侧螺旋而入，已倏在水簾内矣，盖沸泉据山顶，奔腾而下，至半山，石忽横裂一罅，瀑布千仞，自天而下，冬夏不绝，似山灵珍秘，不不容人窥。洞中石如朵朵碧云，乘风欲去。

    Explanation

    52

    The landscapes of Shihu, where countless tablets point to the sky, and Huangshan, where thousands of trees lean over a vast expanse, are both composed of yellowish rocks and pure in quality, yet they possess a distinct difference between the divine and the mundane. At dawn, as the sun (目敦) just begins to rise, the scenery transforms into a stunning spectacle, so captivating that one hesitates to leave, even turning back several times while on horseback. Later, whenever I met or saw off guests, I would always stay for a night, yet it was never like the Feiyun Cave in Huangping, which I still dream of encountering even now. When speaking of the beauty of mountains and rivers, one describes them as majestic, strange, beautiful, and elegant, but the Feiyun Cave defies all these descriptions. Approaching the cave, one sees towering cliffs thousands of feet high, with ancient pines reaching the sky, and there seems to be no cave at all. Searching for it, one finds it below a sheer cliff, overgrown with dense vegetation, with a waterfall like a curtain blocking the entrance, making it impassable. Entering by spiraling around the side, one suddenly finds oneself inside the waterfall. The hot spring is at the top of the mountain, rushing down, reaching halfway up the mountain, where the rock suddenly splits open, creating a waterfall thousands of feet high, falling from the sky, never ceasing, winter or summer. It seems as if the mountain spirit keeps it hidden, not allowing people to see it. Inside the cave, the rocks resemble blooming blue clouds, as if they are about to be carried away by the wind.

    53

    最高处立大士一身，庄严妙相，善财龙女，丹鹦绿柳皆具，据云天生，不假雕琢也。佛像藻绘，或少可着色，若云之为云，断非人间世矣。玉泚潺湲，芳草芬缛，四时皆春，亦仙亦佛，内一碑镌王阳明记，略云：人即有山水癖，至黔而倦，盖登陟剧劳，危险可怖，且佳胜颇多，心目皆餍，独至此则佣夫贩妇，不解寻幽者，亦如淮南鸡犬，一晌升天，飘飘乎羽化登仙也。读此不啻以洞云持赠矣，予谓冷泉以秀胜，虹桥以丽胜，丹崖以雄胜，碧鸡以奇胜，飞云兼而有之，真能集大成者。予癃老，咫尺西湖，懒于杖履，良由曾经沧海，除却巫山，难为云水缘也。然如飞云洞者，常在梦魂中，每拟仿宗少文卧而游之。

    Explanation

    53

    At the highest point stands a bodhisattva, majestic and wondrous in appearance, accompanied by Shanzhai and Naga Princess, with colorful parrots and green willows all around. It is said that it was naturally formed, without any carving or polishing. The Buddha statue is adorned with intricate designs, some of which can be colored. If the clouds are like clouds, it is definitely not of this world. Clear, flowing water and fragrant, lush grass create a serene and beautiful landscape, where all seasons are spring. The place is both divine and sacred. Inside, there is a stele inscribed with a record by Wang Yangming, which roughly states: If someone has a fondness for mountains and waters, they will become tired after reaching Guizhou, as climbing is extremely laborious and dangerous, and the journey is fraught with peril. There are many beautiful and excellent places, satisfying both the eyes and the heart, but here, common laborers and vendors, who do not understand the search for seclusion, are like the chickens and dogs of Huainan, ascending to heaven for a moment, floating away like immortals. Reading this is no different from holding the cave clouds as a gift. I say that Cold Spring is beautiful, Rainbow Bridge is splendid, Red Cliff is majestic, Blue Rooster is unique, and Flying Cloud combines all these qualities, truly a master of all arts. I am old and weak, and even though West Lake is just a short distance away, I am too lazy to go there, as it is because I have seen the vast ocean, and apart from Mount Wushan, it is hard to appreciate the clouds and waters. However, places like Flying Cloud Cave are often in my dreams, and I often imagine following the example of Zong Bing, lying down and traveling through it.

    54

    苗俗
    　　　猺獞狼猡，字皆从犬，明其在人兽之介也。黄陶菴先生"百姓皆以王为爱也"题文云，杀人不闻以牛代，若迤东三府，则此语殊未确矣。昭通东川开化，俗狞且蠢，命案最多，皆不办，明目张胆。呈于有司曰："恪遵苗例，谨以牛充。"牛亦视家之贫富，富者至千，贫者数百，不尽牛也。首曰牛头，末曰牛尾，中曰牛腰，必以牛，外则束缣牛也，炊甑牛也，甚至双履亦牛也，罄其家之所有而已。当事者或绳之以法，则大哗，谓此伧非人情，我家不幸死于斗，孤儿寡妇，赖牛以活，故曰偿。若诛其人，虽菹醢之，于死者何益，于生者更何益，安所谓偿？无已，分其牛为贽，以间执其口。一牛折金四，或十或八，则分防之公费也，上游亦无从禁之。不然，凶手固无辞，尸亲必违抗，案终不了矣。

    Explanation

    54

    The Miao Custom

    The Miao people, whose names all contain the character for "dog," are clearly situated between humans and animals. Mr. Huang Tao'an commented on the text "The People All Thought the King Was Loving," stating that in other regions, killing someone is not replaced by a cow. However, in the three eastern prefectures of Zhaotong, Dongchuan, and Kaihua, this statement is not entirely accurate. The customs in these regions are cruel and stupid, with the most frequent cases being murders, all of which are not handled and are committed openly. When presented to the officials, the perpetrators say they strictly follow the Miao custom and use a cow as compensation. The number of cows depends on the family's wealth, ranging from a thousand for the rich to several hundred for the poor. The compensation can be anything from the head of a cow to the tail, the middle part, or even non-cow items like bundles of silk, cooking pots, or even shoes, using up everything the family has. If officials try to enforce the law, there is great uproar, claiming that this practice is not humane, and that the families of the deceased rely on the cow to survive, hence it is called compensation. If the perpetrator is punished, even if they are executed, it would not benefit the dead or the living, so what is the point of compensation? As a compromise, the cow is divided as a gift to avoid further conflict. One cow is worth four, ten, or eight units of currency, which is used as public funds, and the higher authorities cannot stop it. Otherwise, the murderer would have no defense, and the family of the victim would resist, leaving the case unresolved.

    55

    昔岁额薇垣以滇臬升此，犹笑问此间惜无此例，得无重劳案牍乎。然此尚等人于畜，若迤南边外，则更畜之不如。腾威之交，有曰三角毛者，剃其发，留三綹作髻，故名，是人中之枭獍。父母老，则杀而食之，谓是龙钟潦倒者，吾见之恻然，殊不忍。藏之腹中，庶得其所哉，以告父母，父母尚强，或丐徐徐云尔。至笃老，则亦甘心作脯，欣然就烹，戚好均分以杯羹。或偶至病毙，则群詈其不孝，不可以为子，不可以为人矣。若猛缅之以囚犯饲老卡，藏卫之以尸骸喂鱼鸟，犹觉罪可末减矣。羁縻荒服，王化之所不及，圣教之所不通，第彼一方，皆邻西域，而活佛亦复救不得，应以乾闥婆阿修罗人非人等身得度者，即以人非人等身而为说法，魔王世界何时渐入皈依。若近佛国，俟父母死而食其尸，不愧近佛之名哉！

    Explanation

    55

    In the past year, E Wei Yuan, having been promoted from his position as the governor of Yunnan, still joked about the lack of precedent for such a case here, wondering if it would not be a heavy burden of paperwork. However, in this place, people are treated like livestock; in the southern frontier regions beyond the borders, they are treated even worse. In the area near Teng and Wei, there is a group called San Liao Mao, who shave their heads and leave three strands of hair to form a bun, hence their name. They are the most vicious among people. When their parents grow old, they kill and eat them, calling them old and useless. I feel deep sympathy for them and cannot bear it. To put them in one's stomach, perhaps finding a proper place for them, and inform the parents, if the parents are still strong, one might ask for a gradual approach. When they become extremely old, they willingly become dried meat, happily accepting being cooked, and relatives and friends share the soup equally. If they die of illness by chance, they are collectively criticized for being unfilial, cannot be a son, cannot be a person. If in Mianmarn, prisoners are fed to the elderly, and in Tibet, dead bodies are used to feed fish and birds, the crimes can be slightly reduced. The remote and uncivilized regions beyond the empire's control, beyond the reach of the king's influence and the teachings of the sages, these regions, all neighboring the Western Regions, even the living Buddha cannot save them. One should use the form of beings that are neither fully human nor fully divine to help them, and use the form of such beings to preach to them. When will the world of demons gradually enter the path of enlightenment? If close to the Buddhist realm, waiting until the parents die and then eating their bodies, how could one live up to the name of being close to the Buddha?

    56

    陈涌金案
    　　　陈涌金，四川慈谿人，以贩药川湖起家。生四子，长前卒，次美思，守药肆于杭，三贡元多病，四尚幼。长与三皆娶于吴，以女兄弟为先后，次媳乐，黑腯而媚，如南汉宫人，性狡狯。长子无嗣，遗一女曰阿猫；美思有二子，伦序相当，大陈吴氏与阿猫不欲，欲以贡元妇小陈吴氏子为后，且私告所亲。乐氏佚荡，不堪以吕易嬴也，乐氏切齿，乃诈为代夫子职，就养无方。涌金本无赖，竟陷以聚尘焉，自此倾陷阿猫母子者愈急。值大陈吴氏病疟，乐氏诈为秤药量水，赚阿猫取炭，于剂中入生鸦片三钱才、木鳖子一钱，服后寒战不止，遂绝。众者不察，阿猫独心疑之，哭泣中间以怨詈，且微及新台秽迹，乐氏乃与涌金合谋，诬其与长年奴高宏道奸，以铁籖自口揕其脑，杀之，乘夜埋于旷野。时令慈谿者，楚人黄兆台，入涌金妹婿叶生言，以杀有罪子孙寝其事，族中有请检者，反扑而逐之，慈民大哗。

    Explanation

    56

    Teng Yongjin Case

    Teng Yongjin, a native of Cixi, Sichuan, rose to prominence through the sale of medicine in Sichuan and Hubei. He had four sons: the eldest died before him, the second was named Meisi and managed a pharmacy in Hangzhou, the third was a candidate for the imperial examinations but often fell ill, and the fourth was still young. The eldest and third sons both married women from Wu, with the sisters-in-law marrying in sequence. The second wife, named Le, was dark-skinned and alluring, resembling a concubine of the Southern Han royal court, and was cunning and sly. The eldest son had no heir, leaving behind a daughter named A Miao; Meisi had two sons who were of equal status. Da Chen Wu and A Miao did not want it, desiring to make the son of Xiao Chen Wu, the wife of the candidate for the imperial examinations, the heir, and privately informed their relatives. Le, being licentious and unrestrained, could not bear to replace the legitimate heir with an illegitimate one. Le gnashed her teeth in anger and pretended to take over her husband's duties, neglecting proper care. Teng Yongjin, originally a scoundrel, eventually accused her of gathering dust, and from then on, the accusations against A Miao and her mother became more urgent. When Da Chen Wu was suffering from malaria, Le pretended to weigh the medicine and measure the water, tricking A Miao into fetching charcoal. She added three liang of raw opium and one liang of brucea javanica seeds to the medicine, causing A Miao to shiver uncontrollably and die after taking it. The others did not understand, but A Miao alone suspected it, crying out in grief and anger, and hinting at the disgraceful deeds of the new palace. Le then conspired with Teng Yongjin, falsely accusing A Miao of having an affair with the elderly servant Gao Hongdao, and stabbed her in the head with an iron spike through her mouth, killing her. They buried her in the wilderness at night. The magistrate of Cixi at that time was Huang Zhaotai from Chu, who was a brother-in-law of Teng Yongjin's sister. He suppressed the case by claiming the victim was a guilty descendant. When someone from the clan requested an investigation, he attacked and drove them away, causing great outrage among the people of Cixi.

    57

    时予奉迈功中丞檄，清理积案，寄居府署，一日秋坪郡伯仓惶来曰："殷主薄煦自慈谿来，有所闻否？"予曰："铁桥现在某先生斋，无所言也。"秋坪遣仆邀至，促膝密问之，铁桥云："惟闻陈姓有故杀女孙一案，闺门事秘，无从悉其委曲。"予谓秋坪盍遣人消息之，秋坪曰："铁桥甚精细，尚不能得其委曲，何人可遣？黠者任偏私，愚者受蒙蔽，翻豐其部矣。"明晨，秋坪又来曰："富观察亦有所闻，顷以询我，我答以昨有风闻，以未得端倪，不敢遽禀。"予曰："然则遣人不宜缓。"秋坪即商其人于予，予曰："家人不习地里，胥役叵信，惟计天一阁管书人邵姓，充学院吏，明干忠实可往。"秋坪曰："我亦仿彿认得。"即密召之，授以方略，邵曰："陈姓侦探者多，一归泄矣。"即乘府署差轿以行。二更归，报命曰："胥有戚家邻于陈，托为探戚者，里閈群议颇详。亦访于数里同事某家，所言皆同，大约通奸事虚，谋产事实，故杀事亦实。

    Explanation

    57

    At that time, I was serving under the order of Governor Maigong, tasked with clearing up accumulated cases, and residing temporarily in the government office. One day, Autumnping, the county magistrate, came in a hurry and said, "Mr. Yin, the magistrate of Cixi, has come from Cixi. Do you have any news?" I replied, "Tieqiao is currently at a certain scholar's study, and he hasn't said anything." Autumnping sent a servant to invite him, and we asked him closely and privately. Tieqiao said, "I only heard about a case involving the Chen family where a granddaughter was killed. Family matters are kept secret, and it is impossible to know the full details." I suggested to Autumnping that he send someone to investigate, but he replied, "Tieqiao is very meticulous, and he still couldn't get the full details. Who else can we send? The cunning ones will act out of favoritism, the foolish ones will be misled, and it will become even more complicated." The next morning, Autumnping came again and said, "Governor Fu also heard something. He recently asked me, and I told him that I had heard a rumor yesterday but hadn't found any leads, so I didn't dare to report it immediately." I said, "Then we shouldn't delay sending someone." Autumnping immediately consulted me about who to send, and I said, "Our family members are not familiar with the local area, and servants and officials cannot be trusted. The only option is to consider the person in charge of the Tianyi Pavilion named Shao, who serves as a clerk at the academy. He is clearly capable and trustworthy." Autumnping said, "I vaguely recognize him." He then secretly summoned Shao, gave him instructions, and Shao said, "There are many people investigating the Chen family. If I return, it will be revealed." He then went by the official carriage. He returned at the second watch of the night and reported, "There is a relative of a servant who lives near the Chen family. He pretended to visit the relative, and the local gossip is quite detailed. I also visited a colleague several miles away, and what they said was the same. Generally, the affair of adultery is false, the plot to seize property is true, and the act of killing is also true."

    58

    棺埋丛葬处尚存，且闻阿猫所字夫洪姓，现谋赴省上控。"秋坪转告观察，观察即嘱其提讯，予曰："提讯太骤，恐万一参差，难于转手。鄙见欲易提为调勾回，甚善。"乃飞札慈谿来府，至，黄令感于劣幕某，执迷不悟，议三日不决，秋坪乃提府亲审，十日而得其要领，廿日而悉其端委，匝月而为鬼蜮，胥无遁影矣。定案之前夕，秋坪宿城隍庙之左厢，祈神印证。

    Explanation

    58

    The burial site with multiple graves still exists, and it is known that Ah Māo's husband is surnamed Hong, and he is currently planning to go to the provincial capital to file a lawsuit. Qiu Ping reported this to the observer, who then instructed him to conduct an interrogation. I said, "Interrogating too hastily, fearing that there might be discrepancies, making it difficult to handle. My suggestion is to change the interrogation to a summons and return, which is very good." A letter was sent to the prefecture of Cixi, and upon arrival, the magistrate was influenced by a certain inferior official, remained stubbornly ignorant, and took three days to decide. Qiu Ping then took the case to the prefecture for a personal review, obtaining the main points in ten days, understanding the details in twenty days, and by the end of the month, all the villains had no place to hide. The night before the case was finalized, Qiu Ping stayed in the left wing of the City God Temple, praying to the gods for verification.

    59

    署中家人周姓，素勤慎，派令守夜，犯证三更后分别管押，嘱周轮视之，至晓乃已。是夕闻门外呵殿声，意谓主人归也，恍惚间，中门閕然，一凉舆入，坐进贤冠蓝袍者短而髯，非主人也，惊起瞻之，殊无踪迹，心讶之，不敢言也。初秋坪恭人瞿，略解案牍，一切妇女幼孩讯后，均送内衙安顿抚慰之，且诱使尽言，故鞫狱常窃听。是夕梦见秋坪向东坐，中坐古衣冠人，两青衣锁一少女入，白衣衫上血迹如雨点。中坐人略诘问，即饬放之，女起，向北叩首，复向西谢秋坪，又前趋一步东向叩首，若知己之在后也。

    Explanation

    59

    In the office, there were Zhou family servants who were usually diligent and cautious. They were assigned to guard at night, and after the third watch, the suspects were separately detained. They were instructed to take turns watching them until dawn. That night, he heard the sound of officials' attendants outside, thinking it was the master returning. In a daze, the middle door creaked open, and a cool sedan chair entered. Inside sat a man wearing a jinxiang cap and a blue robe, short and bearded, who was not the master. Startled, he looked around but saw no trace of it. He dared not speak of it. Initially, Lady Qiu Ping, who was somewhat familiar with official documents, questioned all the women and children after they were interrogated. They were all sent to the inner office to be settled and comforted, and she induced them to speak freely, so she often secretly listened to the interrogations. That night, she dreamed of Qiu Ping sitting facing east, with an anciently dressed person sitting in the middle. Two attendants in green clothes escorted a young girl in, whose white clothes were stained with blood like raindrops. The person in the middle asked a few questions and immediately ordered her to be released. The girl stood up and bowed to the north, then bowed to the west to thank Qiu Ping, and took a step forward to bow to the east, as if she knew someone was behind her.

    60

    见秋坪躬身如有所问，神伸三指示之。朦胧间，闻升炮开门，霍然醒，则军门前鸣炮也。案遂定，乃以本府单衔请检焉，时予已委权金华令，奉调赴省，迈功中丞清问甚切，乃手书二十余条以答，中丞即以付问官，承审者棣华太守、主稿者兼山别驾，提棺至省检验。而黄令复百计挠之，贿高自认奸夫，挺身作证，且诬阿猫曾有私胎埋某处，惟工妇陈吴氏独报义愤，藏阿猫被难前三日月布一缚，嘱其洗换者，高乃伏罪。

    Explanation

    60

    Qiu Ping bowed as if asking a question, and the spirit extended three fingers to indicate something. In a daze, I heard the sound of a cannon signaling the opening of the gate, and suddenly woke up to find that it was the cannon being fired at the military gate. The case was thus settled, and I then requested an inspection with the official seal of the prefecture. At that time, I had been entrusted with the temporary authority of the magistrate of Jinhua and was summoned to the provincial capital. Dai Gong, the Censor-in-Chief, asked very thoroughly, and I wrote over twenty points in response. The Censor-in-Chief then gave these points to the interrogating official, who was Dihua Prefect, the presiding judge, and Jianshan Deputy Magistrate, the chief drafter. The coffin was brought to the provincial capital for inspection. However, Magistrate Huang repeatedly tried to obstruct the process. He bribed Gao to confess as the adulterer, stood up to testify, and also accused Amiao of having previously had a secret pregnancy buried somewhere. Only the female worker Chen Wushi reported out of righteous indignation, hiding a piece of cloth worn by Amiao three days before her death and instructing her to wash and change it. Gao then confessed his guilt.

    61

    陈欲购而毁之，许以百金不动，十室之邑，必有忠信，谅哉！两吴公推勘周匝，织悉入奏，惟新台一节太秽，删之，定乐氏立斩，美思绞侯，赶入秋审；涌金满徒，高奴流。涌金猾甚，声明年已七十，例得免罪，验其监照，乃减年报捐，指驳无可自白也。后部文回，提乐氏监绑，涌金见之，一恸而绝，洵白首同归矣，李三郎迁此情种哉。初秋坪乍莅四明，颇不理于众口，至此乃六邑交颂之，好事者至演为杂剧，严禁之，始止。黄令部议革职，特旨发军台，后遇赦，始放归。

    Explanation

    61

    Tian sought to buy and destroy it, offering a hundred gold coins to not move. In a village of ten households, there must be someone who is loyal and trustworthy, indeed! The two Wu officials thoroughly investigated and reported everything in detail. Only the section about the New Pavilion was too vulgar, so it was deleted. It was decided that the Le family should be executed, Mei Si should be hanged as a marquis, and they should be sent for autumn review. Yongjin was sentenced to full imprisonment, and Gao Nu was exiled. Yongjin was particularly cunning. He claimed to be seventy years old, eligible for exemption from punishment. Upon verifying his records, it was found that he had falsely reported his age to avoid taxes and donations, leaving him with no defense against the charges. After the departmental document returned, the Le family was summoned and bound. When Yongjin saw them, he was overcome with grief and died. Indeed, they shared the same fate until the end. Li Sanlang, who moved this seed of affection? At the beginning of autumn, Qiu Ping suddenly arrived in Siming but was not well received by the public. From then on, all six counties praised him. Some好事者 (people with a keen interest) even turned it into a play, but it was strictly forbidden, and only then did it stop. The yellow magistrate was stripped of his position by departmental decree, then sent to the military post, and later released after encountering a pardon.

    62

    犍为冤妇
    　　　乾隆五十九年，予自滇入蜀，道出嘉州，闻途人犹啧啧语姚方伯宰犍为时雪冤妇事。妇忘其姓，待年夫家，夫出负贩，姑待之无恩，小姑尤狡狯，数恃母凌之。一日互讦，小姑不胜愤甚，乃以菜虫药置粥中毒嫂。姑不知也，啜之，诸窍沸血，暴卒，小姑诡甚，转以诬嫂，众信之，前任某令亦信之，案已定。一如莅任，独疑之，请于制府，展限覆讯，研鞫兼旬，迄无端倪，乃置狱城隍庙中，屏人，令两女同室，使人窃听之，亦不流露。至第三夜，夜将半，一如假寐，隐几神旁。

    Explanation

    62

    The Wronged Woman of Jianwei

    In the 59th year of the Qianlong Emperor's reign, I traveled from Yunnan to Sichuan, passing through Jiaozhou. I heard that people still talked excitedly about how Governor Yao cleared the case of the wronged woman when he was in charge of Jianwei. The woman had forgotten her surname, and she was living in her husband's family while waiting for him to return. Her husband was a traveling merchant, and her mother-in-law treated her without kindness. Her younger sister-in-law was particularly cunning and often relied on her mother to bully her. One day, they accused each other, and the younger sister-in-law, overwhelmed by anger, poisoned her sister-in-law's porridge with insecticide. The mother-in-law, unaware of the poison, ate the porridge, and blood gushed from all her orifices, leading to her sudden death. The younger sister-in-law, being very deceitful, turned around and accused her sister-in-law of the crime. The people believed her, and the previous magistrate also believed her, and the case was already decided. When I took office, I alone had doubts about it and requested an extension of time to re-investigate the case. After investigating for several days, no new clues were found, so I placed the woman in prison in the city god temple, secluded from others, and ordered the two women to share a room, with someone secretly listening to their conversation. However, they did not reveal anything. On the third night, just before midnight, I pretended to sleep, leaning against a table near the deity.

    63

    二囚争折既久，疲倦欲卧，惝怳间，木偶起立，势将扑人，小姑大惊曰："休矣！不敢矫矣，药实侬置，然毒嫂，非毒母也，母自啜之，伤哉！"盖方伯幕后置人，推神而起之，小儿女畏鬼，真情遂毕现。予有乐府纪其事云："犍为有妇，君姑虐之，小姑尤惎，置鸩毒之。置鸩本毒妇，误食乃中母，小姑恣反唇，嚚嚚口戕口。憝姑众著，杀母何堪，众曰可杀。孰宥之三，妇亦俯厥首，刀锯自甘。公独心疑，妇愿且慈，蜂目豺声，惟小姑有之，敢不慎之又慎，而陷人凌迟。移狱庙中谳，狱定称神灵。几筵纷牲醴，醉后隷漏言，隷实拥其背，土偶灵何来？使君小游戏，色听诚审矣，设教果神哉。君不见塔旁榴花冤妇栽，杜鹃啼罢榴花开。"按二姚两狱，四明之神真，犍为之神假。然假神何必非真，真神何必非假，神之为灵昭昭也，侯其祎而。

    Explanation

    63

    Two prisoners had been arguing for a long time, growing tired and wanting to sleep. In a daze, a wooden doll stood up, its momentum about to strike someone. The younger sister was greatly surprised and said, "Enough already! I dare not pretend anymore. The medicine was indeed placed by me, but it was meant to poison the sister-in-law, not the mother. The mother drank it herself, how pitiful!" It is said that the magistrate arranged for someone to be placed behind the scene, pushing the spirit and making it stand up. The young children were afraid of ghosts, and the true feelings were finally revealed. I have a poem that records this event:

    "There was a woman in Jianwei, whose mother-in-law mistreated her. The younger sister especially hated her and placed poison to kill her. The poison was originally meant to kill the wife, but mistakenly consumed by the mother. The younger sister spoke back defiantly, quarreling with harsh words. The wicked mother-in-law was notorious, and how could she kill the mother? Everyone said she should be killed. Who forgave her three times? The woman also bowed her head, willing to be executed. The magistrate alone had doubts, as the woman was willing and kind, with a bee's eyes and a wolf's voice, only the younger sister had it. How cautious one must be, and yet陷人 into a slow death. The trial was moved to the temple for judgment, and the verdict was declared by the gods. The tables were set with food and wine, and after drinking, the servant revealed the secret. The servant actually pushed her back, where did the spirit of the clay figure come from? The magistrate's little game, he listened carefully. Is the teaching truly divine? Have you not seen the wronged woman planted beside the tower, after the cuckoo cries, the pomegranate flowers bloom?"

    According to the two cases of Yao, the true spirit of Siming, the false spirit of Jianwei. But why must a false spirit be false, and why must a true spirit be true? The spirit's divinity is clear, the magistrate's glory.

    64

    咒水
    　　　补山节相自藏回川，仆沈姓，坠马伤脊而伛，乃呼之曰沈驼，惠瑶圃谑曰："不意司马家仆，化作柳州种树奴也。"闻土人有张刀刀者，工咒水，使治之，张治病用两刀，得此名。饬役唤之至，了无术家诸具，但索净水一瓯，令沈隐几，露其背，对水咒数四，以手蘸涂之，上下既遍，乃出其刀，刀不甚锐，刃甚薄，迫脊骨划之，自项至尻，约二尺许，无点血，沈亦不觉也。

    Explanation

    64

    Casting Spells with Water

    When 补山节相 returned to the area of 回川, his servant, Shen, fell off a horse and injured his spine, causing him to hunch over. He was then called "Shen Camel." 惠瑶圃 made a witty remark: "Who would have thought that a servant from the Sima family had transformed into a tree-planter in Liuzhou!"

    Hearing that there was a local practitioner named 张刀刀 who specialized in water incantations, they summoned him. 张刀刀 arrived with no magical tools, only a bowl of clean water. He instructed Shen to lean against a table, exposing his back, and performed several incantations over the water. He then dipped his hand into the water and applied it to Shen's back, covering the entire area. Finally, he took out a thin blade, not very sharp but very thin, and carefully traced along Shen's spine from the top of his neck to the base of his buttocks, about two feet in length. There was no blood, and Shen did not feel any pain.

    65

    刀划处已成一沟，另以小钩爬挲得一物，如琴之少絃，引其端掣之，亦径二尺许，颇纫。又划其右亦如之，仍蘸水涂而祝之，吻然无少痕迹，而如钩者竟复如絃矣。时胡别驾青上，患下马痈，未溃，痛不可忍，闻其技神，亦使视之，张曰："此内症，非予所及，但蒙君相属，而不一显其能，愧矣。"乃亦咒水涂患上，扶胡曰起，胡方转侧窐碍，张迫之曰："勿虑！"掖之起，坐床沿，进履，曰"立"，挽其手，曰"步"，立而步，即赴墙隐小便，了不觉有旧患也，旋与众共饭，安寝竟夕。

    Explanation

    65

    The place where the knife was drawn became a groove, and another small hook was used to scrape and find something, like a string of a lute. Pulling it from one end, it was also about two feet long and quite flexible. Another cut on the right side revealed the same thing, and he still sprinkled water and applied it while reciting a spell. Smoothly, without leaving any trace, the string-like object was restored to its original state. At that time, the Prefectural Magistrate Hu Qing was present, suffering from a boil on his horse's buttocks, which had not yet ruptured and caused unbearable pain. He heard of Zhang's miraculous skill and asked him to examine it. Zhang said, "This is an internal ailment, beyond my ability. But because you have entrusted me, I cannot fail to show my skill, and I am ashamed." He then also sprinkled water and applied it to the affected area, helping Hu up. Hu was struggling and feeling discomfort, so Zhang urged him, saying, "Do not worry," and helped him stand up. He sat on the edge of the bed, put on his shoes, and said, "Stand." He took Hu's hand and said, "Walk." Standing and walking, Hu immediately went to the wall to relieve himself, completely unaware of his previous ailment. Soon, he joined the others for a meal and slept peacefully all night.

    66

    至黎明而渐楚，以次加增，及昨咒水时，则仍如故，盖所治惟折伤一科耳。予在滇中，一日游五华山，舆人失足仆石上，伤其膝盖骨，已中裂，不能举步，乃借马乘之归，而舆人已来，视其膝完好无恙，云倩一咒水治之，费五百文。予以一缗势之，欣然去，明日复来执役矣。肖廉云，军营非若辈不可，虽铅子洞胸着背，胥能搜而出之，与蒙古医人分驰争胜也。闻亦有能疗痈者，祖气诵咒，撮其患，作势掷柱上，或墙上，翌日则患者病顿消，而土木无端溃烂矣，此术之最高者。

    Explanation

    66

    By dawn, the condition had gradually worsened, with each passing moment adding to the pain. By the time of the ritual water treatment yesterday, it remained unchanged, as the practitioner only treats fractures. While in Yunnan, I once traveled to Wuhua Mountain, and one of the porters tripped and fell on a stone, injuring his knee, which was already split open. Unable to walk, he borrowed a horse to ride back home. When the porter returned, his knee was completely intact and unharmed. He mentioned that he had asked a healer to perform the ritual water treatment, which cost five hundred coins. I offered him one string of coins to persuade him, and he left happily. The next day, he returned to his duties. Xiao Lian remarked that the military cannot do without such people, as they can even search out and remove bullets that have pierced through the chest and stuck to the back, competing with Mongol doctors for superiority. I have also heard of healers who can treat abscesses, reciting incantations with ancestral breath, gathering the ailment, and making a gesture to throw it onto a pillar or wall. The next day, the patient's illness suddenly disappeared, but the wood and earth inexplicably rotted. This is the highest level of the technique.

    67

    其次须有生气者代之，草木禽兽，皆可视其术之深浅。尝缚一犬，撮疮空掷，嗥然长吠，如负重创。下者能移于本身，以要害处置闲散地，今痘科有入眼者，可移出著臂上，尚其遗也。术虽不正，以其疗疾，罕有禁止者。猺獞间中有金蝉蛊或腿为邪人所易，亦须土人疗之，然皆师巫，且妇女居多，亦属禁之所不能绝也，垓埏之广，诚无所不有哉。又见《桐下听然》载，苗人能咒人腹中所食熟肉变为小猪，啮人臓腑，然其辞但云"东池王母瑶，西池王母瑶"，无他秘幻也。然咒之奇验，此与诵苕帚二字得道者，同为不可思议矣。

    Explanation

    67

    The next step requires someone with vitality to take over. Plants, animals, and birds can all be observed to assess the depth of a technique or skill. Once, a dog was tied up and subjected to a ritual where a ball was thrown into its wound, causing it to bark loudly as if it were carrying a heavy wound. Those with lesser skills can transfer effects to themselves or to less critical areas. Today, in the field of smallpox, if a condition affects the eye, it can be moved to the arm. Although the method is not orthodox, it is rarely forbidden because it is effective in treating diseases. Among the Yao and Miao peoples, there are practices involving gold cicada poisons or leg-related rituals. These conditions require treatment by local healers, who are often shamans or women. These practices, though banned, cannot be completely eradicated. The vastness of the world is truly filled with all kinds of phenomena. As recorded in the text "Tongxia Tingran," the Miao people believe that a curse can turn cooked meat in a person's stomach into a piglet, which then bites into the person's internal organs. The incantation used in this curse is "East Pool Mother Yao, West Pool Mother Yao," and its effectiveness is beyond comprehension.

    68

    孙补山轶事
    　　　补山节相丰功伟绩，载在本传者，众皆见之，第其济变之才，机牙四应，真得韩魏公遗意。有一二轶事，得之所闻所见，谨誌之以备家乘之缺，且俾后之为封疆者则效焉。驻节前藏，督办军需，时梅乐子二等侍卫某，奉旨省亲，势张甚，至襄塘，从骑鞭挞夷人，乌拉逃散，粮台传误，委员飞禀报闻，节相即通札各站，风闻有某人骚扰驿站，今发到令箭一枝，不拘何处擒获，许以军法从事，本院已夹片密奏在案矣。某闻之不敢驰驿，自乘军骑星驰而去，越旬日已接后藏来信，某人已至军前矣。方小濂曰："中堂此举，未免太过。"笑曰："无此大胆委员，就擒亦必告我，且某虽骄，亦非痴绝，断无见此告示，自就显戮。虑或倔强，故以密奏吓之，此等琐屑，何足渎圣聪也！"凯旋后，节相即返都，惟办善后者，一道二府暨同通州县佐杂数十员，尚短商上尾欠银二十四万，禀请迅速解往。

    Explanation

    68

    孙补山轶事

    补山节相的丰功伟绩，记载在本传中，众人皆知。然而，他应对变故的才能，机敏应变，确实继承了韩魏公的遗风。有一些轶事，是根据我所见所闻，谨记下来以填补家族记录的空白，并且希望未来的边疆官员能够效仿。他在前藏驻节，督办军需时，当时有一位名叫梅乐子的二等侍卫，奉旨省亲，势力很大。他来到襄塘，随从鞭打夷人，导致人群四散，粮台传误，委员紧急禀报。节相随即通令各站，听说有人骚扰驿站，现发令箭一支，无论何处擒获，均可按军法处置，本院已秘密奏报在案。那人听说后不敢使用驿马，自己骑马星夜兼程离开，过了十天，接到后藏来信，那人已到达军前。方小濂说：“中堂此举，未免太过。”节相笑着说：“不会有这么大胆的委员，被擒获后必定会告诉我，况且他虽骄横，但也不至于愚蠢到自投罗网。我担心他倔强，所以用密奏吓唬他，这些琐事，何足挂齿！”凯旋后，节相即返回都城，只处理善后事宜，一道二府及同通州县佐杂数十员，仍欠银二十四万，请求迅速解往。

    69

    承宣使闻嘉言，谓军需无著之项已多，诸君但计目前，不虑日后，掯不肯解，各承办道府之先回，如符如石如赵如沈，皆群起争之，相国谕曰："君等当日为边陲用兵，若先筹惜帑，岂能集事。藩司计臣，勾稽核算，乃其专责，何妄争也！"绝口不道。第三日，身自拜晤闻公，谓入藏诸公，用帑太费，自须查核，但自臬司以下均有经手，惟老司长无所回护。本应老夫自行，缘新自藏回，且批准多由本院，亦须回避，拟奉烦一行，明日即当移徼。老夫七十余人，居然雪（山责）万里，司长壮猷强壮，尤宜勉力报国。塞外望帑如岁，迟到恐别生事端，一定行期，当摺报起程，兼飞饬委员珍重而别。闻藩惶窘，即日飣鞘委员且多给盘费，饬令星驰而去。查核一说，闻藩固不敢问，节相亦不复言也，一如肖濂偶一提及，节相必曰："好藩司，符石诸君原未免太不撙节，若彼竟毅然请行，我转不敢遣之矣。"

    Explanation

    69

    The Governor-General, Wen Jiayan, remarked that the military needs were already excessive, and the officials were only concerned with the present, not the future, and were reluctant to release funds. The officials who had returned from handling affairs in various prefectures and counties, such as Fu, Shi, Zhao, and Shen, all competed over the issue. The Prime Minister then stated, "When you were involved in military operations on the border, if you had first considered conserving the treasury, how could you have accomplished anything? The officials responsible for calculating and managing the finances are in charge of that, so why are you frivolously competing over it?" The Prime Minister did not mention it further. On the third day, he personally met with Wen Jiayan and said, "The officials who went to Tibet used the treasury funds excessively, so an investigation is necessary. However, all officials below the judicial bureau have been involved, and only the older official has no one to protect him. I should have handled this matter myself, but since I just returned from Tibet and many approvals were made by this court, I must recuse myself. I will request that you undertake this task, and I will submit a formal report tomorrow. The journey to Tibet is long and arduous, and the official, who is in his seventies, is strong and determined, and should strive to serve the country. The people on the frontier are eagerly awaiting the funds, and a delay could cause other problems. A definite date for the journey will be reported, and the officials will be instructed to travel swiftly and take care." Wen Jiayan was in a state of panic and immediately prepared the officials, providing them with ample travel expenses and sending them off quickly. The matter of the investigation was not questioned by Wen Jiayan, and the Prime Minister also did not mention it again. If someone like Xiao Lian were to bring it up, the Prime Minister would likely say, "Good officials at the finance bureau, Fu and Shi, were indeed too extravagant. If they had insisted on undertaking the task, I would have been hesitant to send them."

    70

    百菊溪轶事
    　　　嘉庆丁卯，菊谿师以两粤开府，乞病内用。时海寇荡平，许由水道缓程，仲时在籍，迎谒于秀州之陡门。将别，颇申颂祷，师曰："三十年老师弟，不合说句良心话乎？"盖北语谓箴规也。仲起曰："师今稳上黄麻金鑑家风，愿正色立朝，益养曲江风度。"师蹙然曰："尔言良是，第吾以刑部尚书用，汉员为金兰畦光悌，其人张汤郅都也，吾不与衡，如民命何？"仲对曰："昔径山示童子公案云：汝进一步则死，退一部则亡，作么生？童子曰：吾旁行一步何妨？"师首肯者再，面圣即力陈病尚未痊，乞闲散自效，遂改总宪。

    Explanation

    70

    Bai Juxi Anecdotes

    In the Ding Mao year of the Jiaqing era (1807), Master Bai Juxi was appointed as the governor of the two Guang provinces and requested a leave of absence due to illness, which led to his recall to serve in the capital. At that time, the sea bandits had been pacified, and he traveled by water at a leisurely pace. When I was still in my hometown, I met and greeted him at the steep gate of Xiu Prefecture. As we were about to part, I expressed much praise and prayer. Master Bai said, "After thirty years of being teacher and disciple, isn't it time to say something honest?" In northern dialect, this means admonition or advice. I replied, "Master, now that you are steadily ascending the ranks of the prestigious Jin family, I hope you will stand upright in court and further cultivate the refined demeanor of Qujiang." Master Bai looked troubled and said, "Your words are indeed true, but if I am appointed as the Minister of Justice, Han officials like the Jin family will be like Zhang Tang and Zhi Du, who were known for their strict legalism. How could I agree to such a role without considering the lives of the people?" I responded, "There is a Zen koan from the Jing Shan Temple that says: 'If you take one step forward, you die; if you take one step back, you perish. What should you do?' The child said, 'Taking a step to the side is not a problem.' " Master Bai nodded in agreement twice. When he appeared before the emperor, he strongly argued that his illness had not yet fully healed and requested to serve in a minor capacity. He was then appointed as the Chief Censor.

    71

    庚午，师以两江节钺底定李家楼漫口，仲谒之袁浦，方工次乍旋善后事宜，羽书旁午，见罢，谕以傍晚再来。晚鼓复入，小室中惟廉山万生侍，师谓万曰："明晨拟谢神，兼发赏，冗集无暇，今日向君乞半日假，小欧欲叩奇闻，须与畅谈耳，偶有遗忘，予仍补之。"即言廉山在废籍已久，予以夹片请之，俾考功无从指驳，第一快事。仲方申感谢，师摇手曰："累渠不浅，尚未同作波臣，已为大幸。"又言初授节时，自揣虽扬历中外有年，而行水金鑑，未曾细考，顿首固辞，上谕卿才自足办此，有所陈赐无畏，徐议用人理财各策，乃以大司马吴菘圃璥为监理、鹾院阿勒精阿为协办。

    71

    On the day of Gengwu, the Master, wielding the authority of the Two Jiang provinces, stabilized the situation at the breach at Li Family Tower. Zhong paid his respects at Yuanpu, where he was just returning to handle post-disaster matters when urgent military dispatches came pouring in. After a meeting, he was instructed to return in the evening. In the evening, he returned once more, and in the small room, only Lianshan Wansheng was present. The Master said to Wansheng, "Tomorrow morning, I plan to thank the gods and also distribute rewards. With a large gathering, I have no time, so today I ask for your half-day leave. Xiao Ou wishes to inquire about some strange news, and we need to have an open discussion. If I occasionally forget something, I will still make up for it." He then mentioned that Lianshan had been on the list of dismissed officials for a long time. He submitted a petition requesting his reinstatement, making it impossible for the Office of Performance Evaluation to find fault. This was the most joyful thing. Zhong expressed his gratitude, but the Master waved his hand and said, "I have burdened him significantly, and he has not yet become a low-ranking official, which is already a great fortune." He also said that when he was first appointed to his rank, he considered himself, despite having traveled and served both inside and outside the country for many years, that he had not examined the gold mirror of hydraulic engineering in detail. He knelt and firmly refused, but the imperial edict stated that his abilities were sufficient to handle this task, and he could present his proposals without fear. They gradually discussed strategies for employing officials and managing finances, and thus appointed Grand Marshal Wu Songpu Jing as supervisor and Salt Administration Officer Alejinga as deputy.

    72

    既至，开引河，筑长堤，粗有就绪，忽接陕督书，言塞外大雪封山，来岁春融，建瓴而下，施工愈难，合龙尤宜迅速。节署设一乩，师素崇信，乃祷于神，占于三月二十一合龙，乩许之，但云尚有惊恐。于是庀材鸠工，下埽筑坝，择二十一日合龙，龙竟合矣。二十二日三更后，天大风雨，继之以雪，祁寒如窿冬。大坝蛰陷数十丈，坝下水沸如汤，吴司马急令聚铁数万斤鎔只不过是，先投其半，约三刻许，觉腥气扑鼻，泛出黑水二股，可四五里。掀翻少定，复以其半灌入，将军埽巨舟载而沉之，师偕吴阿二公，暨河帅陈竹香凤翔亲自坐扫，俄顷波平如镜，始报巩固，计距合龙已逾两日云。

    Explanation

    72

    Upon arrival, the river was opened and diverted, and a long embankment was built, roughly completed. Suddenly, a letter was received from the governor of Shaanxi, stating that heavy snow in the frontier region had blocked the mountains, and next spring when the snow melts, the water would flow down like water poured from a high place, making the construction even more difficult, and the completion of the dam should be done quickly. The governor's office set up a divining board, and the teacher, who had always been devoutly believed, prayed to the gods. The divination predicted the completion of the dam on March 21st, and the divining board agreed, but it also said there would still be some surprises or fears. Therefore, materials were gathered, and workers were assembled. The dam was laid down and built, and March 21st was chosen for the completion of the dam, which was indeed completed. After midnight on the 22nd, heavy rain and strong winds followed by snow occurred, extremely cold, like the middle of winter. The dam sank several tens of feet, and the water below the dam boiled like hot soup. The governor of Wu urgently ordered to gather tens of thousands of pounds of iron to melt it. First, half of it was thrown in, and a strong fishy odor was smelled, with two streams of black water spurting out, about four or five miles. After being overturned, it settled slightly, and then the other half was poured in. The general commanded large boats to be loaded and sunk. The teacher accompanied the two gentlemen from Wu, and the river chief Chen Zhuxiang Fengxiang personally sat on the boat. In a short while, the waves became calm like a mirror, and it was finally reported that the dam was stable. It was calculated that more than two days had passed since the completion of the dam.

    73

    明晨复观师龙王庙拈香行礼竣，僚属以至卒徒，均叩谢且贺。师忽一例还跪，众大骇曰："卑职与小底曷敢！"师喟然曰："当时在坝上时，何所分大人卑职老爷小底也，惊涛一刷，贵贱同流，诸君不顾身命，为朝廷事，皆吾好兄弟好朋友。"指帽上红顶曰："永矢此心，群公皆可戴耳，王侯将相宁有种乎？"众均崩角，至有泣不能起者。仲进曰："向曾祝师养相度，今知师兼擅将略，不谓挟纩投醪，复见今日。"师大笑。是夕小饮，师微酣后，忽吟仲前题《天际识归舟行看》句云："才高破浪乘风易，恩重抽帆到岸难。"回环再四，兼以累嘘，亦望山公鸟入青云倦亦飞意也。师丰功伟烈，志传炳如，门下士私誌二三轶事，亦窃仿《柳氏旧闻》云尔。

    Explanation

    73

    Early the next morning, the teacher again visited the Temple of the Dragon King to burn incense and perform rituals. Upon completion, subordinates, officials, soldiers, and servants all bowed and thanked him, congratulating him. Suddenly, the teacher knelt down in unison, and the crowd was greatly startled, exclaiming, "How dare we, your subordinates and lowly servants!" The teacher sighed and said, "At that time on the dam, what distinction was there between high-ranking officials and lowly servants? The surge of waves equalized the high and low. All of you, regardless of life and death, served the state, and you are all my good brothers and friends." Pointing to the red hat on his head, he said, "I will always hold this heart, and all of you can wear it. Are kings, marquises, generals, and prime ministers born of a special kind?" The crowd all bowed their heads, and some even wept and could not stand up. Zhong said, "I once prayed for the teacher's wisdom and insight, and now I know the teacher is also skilled in military strategy. I did not expect to see such warmth and comfort again today." The teacher laughed heartily. That evening, they had a small drink, and after the teacher became slightly intoxicated, he suddenly recited a line from Zhong's previous poem Tianji Shigzhou Xingkan (Recognizing the Returning Boat from Afar): "It is easy to ride the waves with high talent, but it is difficult to reach the shore with heavy gratitude." He repeated the line again and again, sighing deeply, as if expressing a desire to rise despite fatigue. The teacher's great achievements and glorious deeds are recorded clearly in his biography, and his disciples privately recorded a few anecdotes, secretly imitating the style of Old News of the Liu Family.

    74

    炎凉异态
    　　　趋炎附势，志士所羞，然不觞朝士而接贺拔，亦吾行吾志，若尘埃中能识宰相，则尽人而物色之矣，哀王孙而进食，岂望报乎？第怨不在大，患不在多，往往于无意中得济者，不报其人而报其人之天也。海昌云岩方伯先德，慷慨好施，官甘肃之平番，凡出口者糗糒刍茭，馈遗必腆。一日适赴乡检验，满洲查公以小谪往新疆，归时已过，公蹙然曰："旧识远谪，不可无将意也。"乃遣健仆囊三百金，追越两站，具禀申款，兼致珍味，查亦祗登而去。去经年，忽奉命开府秦陇，召陈问曰："君性挥霍，得无亏空否？"陈曰："不敢欺，以将及亿矣。"查沉吟再四曰："幸吾来尚可，然亦大费调停矣！"乃破格调宁夏，旋调皋兰。越三年，曰粗可抽身郎君已得刺史，何恋恋鸡肋乎，为请乞休，且以千金为赆，曰："无使漂母笑人。"陈归，又数年而卒，云岩公已晋群伯，尚寄金为翁补苴也。

    Explanation

    74

    The Strange Behavior of People Towards Power

    Fawning on power and following the trend is a disgrace to a man of principle. However, if one does not offer wine to court officials and welcome guests like Ge Ba, it is also a matter of one's own will. If one can recognize a prime minister among the dust, then one can seek out all such people. To pity a prince and offer food, is one expecting repayment? Grievances do not have to be great, and troubles do not have to be many. Often, those who receive help unintentionally repay the person's fate rather than the person themselves. The Viceroy Yunyan Fang of Haichang, known for his generosity and charitable nature, served as an official in Pingfan, Gansu. He always provided generous gifts and provisions to those who left his jurisdiction. One day, he was on a mission to inspect his hometown. At that time, the Manchu official Zha was exiled to Xinjiang. When Zha returned, it was already too late to meet him. The official was concerned and said, "An old acquaintance has been exiled far away; we cannot leave without conveying our intentions." He then sent a strong servant with 300 gold pieces to catch up with Zha, who had already passed two stations. The servant presented a detailed report and fine delicacies. Zha accepted them and continued on his way. After a year, Zha was unexpectedly appointed to open a government office in Qin and Long. He summoned Chen and asked, "Given your generous nature, are you not running a deficit?" Chen replied, "I dare not deceive you; I am close to a deficit of one million." Zha pondered for a while and said, "Fortunately, I am here, but it will still require significant adjustments!" He then appointed Chen beyond the usual ranks to Ningxia and soon after to Gaolan. After three years, Chen said it was time to step down, as his son had already obtained the position of Prefect. Why should he cling to such a trivial matter? He requested retirement and received 1,000 gold pieces as a farewell gift. Zha said, "Do not let the story of the woman who fed a prince and was repaid by him be a laughingstock." Chen returned home, and several years later, he passed away. By then, Viceroy Yunyan Fang had been promoted to a high official and still sent money to Chen's father to make up for any deficiencies.

    75

    又杭理事伊司马，言前在甘肃时，兰州守德公初度，道府以下群聚申祝，方张筵观剧，忽邮递报倭大人什布到驿，德公言倭虽旧宪，第已降七品，例不迎迓，明晨起行，一往送别，现作主人，安敢不奉陪也。少时，客有潜去者，为碾伯庄令、邑丞某、训导某，德守曰："渠等因酒，假此遁逃。"即遣人促之，俄倾复至，群问曾晤倭公否，答曰："出城三里即遇之，下舆一揖，彼第于舆中举手而已。"众揶揄之，入席复饮。又数巡，忽传邸报本省制宪调任闽浙，所遗员缺奉旨以倭什布补授，乃仓惶撤宴，相率进谒。

    Explanation

    75

    The official in charge of affairs in Hangzhou, Yi Sima, recounted that before he was stationed in Gansu, when Governor De of Lanzhou celebrated his birthday, officials below the governor's level gathered to offer congratulations. They were just setting up a banquet and watching a play when suddenly a postal report arrived stating that Wei Shibu, a high-ranking official, had arrived at the post station. Governor De explained that although Wei was a former superior, he had been demoted to the seventh rank and, by custom, did not need to be greeted. He planned to leave early the next morning and go once to see him off. Since he was now acting as the host, how could he not attend? After some time, some guests quietly left, including the magistrate of Nianbo Village, a county assistant, and a school supervisor. Governor De said, "They left because of the wine, using this as an excuse to escape." He immediately sent someone to urge them to return. Shortly after, they came back. Everyone asked if they had met Wei Shibu, and they replied, "We met him three miles out of the city. He stepped down from the carriage and bowed once. He simply raised a hand from the carriage and nothing more." The others mocked them, and they returned to their seats to continue drinking. After several more rounds, suddenly a report came that the provincial governor of their province had been transferred to Fujian and Zhejiang provinces, and the vacancy was filled by imperial decree with Wei Shibu. They hastily withdrew the banquet and went one after another to pay respects.

    76

    时已薄暮，两司见毕，惟请三人，使阍人辞于众曰："现将拜摺，邀庄令君等捉刀，无暇晤谈。"期以翌日。德太守大窘，浼两司为解，至第五日才见，曰："吾与弟中表，记前日为弟华诞，特来申祝，既而知署中宾客甚多，兄以谪员，手板脚靴，无能为役，至今忽促，尚欠申祝也。"德公无地自容，崩角而已。后庄公得调大邑，荐陟同知，旋擢平凉太守，贰尹亦调善地，曰："君才非肆应，不欲以宰累也。"训导兼一书院，曰："聊佐苜蓿盘也。"两事均在皋兰，故合誌之。又鄂韫田制军，以廓尔喀失事，枷号军前，惠瑶圃制军命一守备一通判赍往，皆鄂戚也。守备托公云太，不觉涕泗交颐，判少年呃声一笑。后鄂公再督四川，判即乞病去，托以军功荐擢总戎。

    Explanation

    76

    The sun had already set, and after the two provincial officials had finished their audience, they requested only three people. They sent the gatekeeper to explain to the others: "We are about to present our memorial, and we have invited Mr. Zhuang to draft it for us, so we have no time for conversation." They set a meeting for the next day. The prefect of De was greatly embarrassed and asked the two officials to mediate. It wasn't until the fifth day that he saw them, saying, "I am related to your younger brother by marriage, and I remember that I came to congratulate you on your birthday the day before. However, I later learned that there were many guests at your office, and as a demoted official, I was only able to perform minor duties, and I have not yet had the chance to offer my congratulations." The prefect of De was so embarrassed that he could barely stand, his head bowed in shame. Later, Mr. Zhuang was transferred to a large city and recommended for promotion to the position of same-level official, and soon after, he was promoted to the position of governor of Pingliang. The deputy official was also transferred to a better position, saying, "Your talents are not suited for such duties, and I do not want to burden you with the role of a prefect." He was appointed as a tutor and assigned to a school, saying, "Just to assist with simple fare." Both events took place in Gaolan, so they are recorded together. Another high-ranking military official, E Yun Tian, faced a military failure involving the Gurkhas, and was shackled and publicly displayed in front of the army. Hui Yao Pu, another high-ranking military official, ordered a guard commander and a magistrate to take him there, both of whom were relatives of E Yun Tian. The guard commander, Tu Gong Yuntai, could not help but weep, his tears and snot streaming down his face, while the young magistrate let out a sound of relief followed by a smile. Later, E Yun Tian was again appointed as the governor-general of Sichuan, and the magistrate resigned due to illness, but was recommended for promotion to a high military rank based on military merit.

    杨花救主
    　　　江右孝廉徐某，以大挑试用长安，有雏伶杨花者，年十四，一见目成，以三百金售焉。逾年教匪起，徐奉檄催趱粮运，杨花能左右之，畜青骡，一日行二百余里，常乘以从。丁巳，寇乱方炽，徐催运至郃阳驿，卒遇高均德股匪，杨乃教徐伪作贼探马状，持箭乘青骡逸去，杨乃下马住馆舍，贼目有识之者，谓杨掌班闻已跟官，何忽在此？答曰："吾代主催饷，俟此数日矣！"贼目顾其党曰："聆其言，似饷尚未来，且遇旧知，今晚当留此。"即置酒聚饮，令杨歌曲。杨略不抗拒，尽献所长，且流目送媚，以醉贼目。度以沈酣，猝掣贼佩刀刺之，应手而中，贼党惊，群起刃之，贼亦败兴，逡巡委去。居人重其义，筑土葬之。树碣曰：义伶杨花救主处。予友孟久我延烺于役过此，作纪颇详，复写杨花救主图示予，予为作长歌以纪云：诗人孟浩然，示我杨花传，为写杨花救主图，贞心侠骨千秋见。

    Explanation

    77

    Yanghua Saves His Master

    A certain scholar named Xu from Jiangxi, known as a "孝廉" (xiao lian), was temporarily appointed to Chang'an through a selection process called "大挑" (da tiao). There was a young actor named Yanghua, who was only fourteen years old. Upon their first meeting, they formed a connection through mutual glances, and Xu purchased Yanghua for three hundred gold pieces. A year later, a rebellion broke out, and Xu was ordered to expedite the delivery of grain supplies. Yanghua was able to assist Xu in this task, and he kept a gray mule that could travel over two hundred li in a single day, often riding it alongside Xu.

    In the year 1857, during a period of intense rebellion, Xu was tasked with delivering grain to the relay station in Hanyang. He unexpectedly encountered a group of bandits led by Gao Junde. Yanghua instructed Xu to pretend to be a bandit scout, holding an arrow and escaping on the gray mule. Yanghua then dismounted and stayed at an inn, where some of the bandit leaders recognized him. They asked, "We heard that the head of the troupe had already followed the official. Why are you here?" Yanghua replied, "I am here to deliver the grain on behalf of my master. I will stay here for a few more days."

    The bandit leader, upon hearing this, looked at his comrades and said, "It seems the grain has not yet arrived, and we have met an old acquaintance. We should stay here tonight." They immediately set up a feast and ordered Yanghua to perform. Yanghua did not resist at all, fully displaying his skills and casting a flattering gaze. He intoxicated the bandit leader, gauged his deep intoxication, and suddenly pulled the bandit leader's dagger, stabbing him. The bandit was immediately hit, and his comrades, startled, rose up to attack Yanghua. The bandits were also disappointed and hesitated before leaving.

    The locals valued Yanghua's righteousness and built a mound to bury him. They erected a stone tablet inscribed with the words: "The place where the righteous actor Yanghua saved his master." My friend Meng Jiuyi, who was on duty and passed by this place, wrote a detailed account of the event. He also copied the painting of Yanghua saving his master and showed it to me. I wrote a long poem to commemorate the event. The poet Meng Haoran showed me the biography of Yanghua and wrote the painting, which records the loyal heart and chivalrous spirit of Yanghua, to be seen for a thousand autumns.

    78

    每从花底说秦宫，幕置青油变态工，自向梨园传艳节，不教断袖没英雄。杨花旧隷华林部，小队梁州按歌舞，垂杨婀娜不禁风，落花漂泊还无主，破镜徐郎意气豪。量珠携得郑樱桃，当筵独谱秦风壮，倚帐同看塞月高，一朝忽唱从军曲，细马驮来增绰约。射虎晨随绣纛驰，飞鸿暮逐金丸落，那知记室走孤城，正值风高夜劫营。子弟八千人散尽，眼前惟见贼纵横。可怜生小娇无力，手挽徐郎出荒驿，牵到青骡让主骑，幸郎得免侬何惜。

    Explanation

    78

    In the refined elegance of the Qin palace, tales are spun beneath the blossoms, the stage adorned with oil-laden canvases, transforming into a marvel of artistry. From the imperial theater, the enchanting performances of the graceful and the bold are shared, without diminishing the valor of heroes. The willow catkins, once part of the imperial entourage, now dance in the breeze with a gentle sway, while the fallen flowers drift aimlessly, without a master. The broken mirror, Xu Lang, exudes a bold and spirited demeanor. With pearls measured and the precious Ving Cherry in hand, a grand Qin-style melody is composed at the banquet, while together, leaning on the curtain, we gaze upon the high moon over the frontier. Suddenly, a military song is sung, and with a small horse, the grace is enhanced. In the morning, hunting tigers, following the embroidered banner, and in the evening, chasing golden balls as wild geese fly by. Who knew that the clerk would flee to a lonely city, just as the wind was high and a night raid was launched. The eight thousand followers scattered, and before our eyes, only the rampant bandits remain. Pitifully, the young and weak, taking Xu Lang by the hand, leave the desolate post station, leading a gray donkey for the master to ride, fortunate that the master is spared, what regrets do I have?

    战场生缚献诃摩，千队娄罗一笑哗，满面怨愁双泪雨，争教掩得貌如花。轩眉瞋目呼狂贼，身惰淤泥心白璧，只愿魂依厉鬼雄，久拼血化苌宏碧。叹息无情渭水寒，弔花鸳冢泪阑干，怜他捍刀真情种，殉主还输脱主难，君不见如荼如火军千屯，望尘拜寇何殷勤。国殇独有汪锜在，一片杨花气薄云。此郎芳节，更胜丁期，较之《琑（王吉）杂记》所载白狼主人事，真大相反也。白郎冢在华阴，亦有碣，故附论之。其碣在大道旁，众所共见，不具录。

    Explanation

    79

    On the battlefield, someone was captured alive and presented as a gift, and the thousand-strong crowd laughed and cheered. With a face full of resentment and sorrow, tears streaming like rain, it was impossible to hide their beauty. With raised eyebrows and angry eyes, they shouted at the mad thief, their body degraded like mud but their heart pure as a white jade. They wished to join the spirits of heroic ghosts and were willing to shed blood for a noble cause, turning it into a deep blue color. They sighed at the cold, unfeeling nature of the Wei River and wept at the tomb where lovers were buried, their tears streaming like a railing. They sympathized with the brave and true-hearted warrior, who faced the moral dilemma of sacrificing oneself for a master versus leaving a master. They pointed out the vast armies that were as numerous as tea plants or as fiery as flames, and the eagerness of people to bow down to invaders. Among those who died for their country, only Wang Qi remained, a fragile cloud made of willow catkins. This man's noble character surpassed even that of Ding Qi, and it was truly the opposite of what was recorded in the Wang Ji Zaji about the White Wolf Master. The tomb of Bai Lang is located in Huayin and has a stele, so it is mentioned here as well. The stele is located by the main road and is visible to everyone, so it is not recorded in detail.

    滴血
    　　　滴血之说，起于萧综，《南史》笔之甚著，今表为功令，然谳牍不甚据之，防诈伪也，予亲临视，乃灼知其凿然可异者。昌化一章姓，失耦后，贫不能再娶，与一妇通，妇夫以废疾卧床，买奸图活。未几夫死，订嫁娶焉，半年举一子。章得妇生子后，力穑自殖，本有山田一顷，至是倍之，族人有涎其产，呈其子非章出，一则前夫亡仅数月，安知非其遗腹；再则妇既不贞，人尽可夫，不能以吕易嬴。前两任均不能决，予曰："此非滴血不辩。

    Explanation

    80

    The Blood Test
    The practice of the blood test, which originated with Xiao Zong, is recorded in great detail in the Nan Shi (Southern History). It has now been officially recognized as a legal decree. However, official documents do not heavily rely on it, as it is used to prevent fraud and deception. I personally examined the case and clearly knew that it was distinctly different. In Changhua, there was a man named Zhang who, after losing his partner, was too poor to remarry. He had an affair with a woman whose husband was bedridden due to a disability. She was bought to live with him. Soon after, her husband died, and they arranged their marriage. Half a year later, they had a child. After Zhang got married and had a child, he worked hard to support himself. He originally had one hundred mu of mountain land, and by then it had doubled. A relative coveted his property and claimed that the child was not Zhang's. Firstly, her former husband had only died a few months ago, how could it not be a posthumous child? Secondly, since the woman was not chaste, anyone could be her husband, and it cannot replace one woman with another. The previous two officials could not decide, and I said, "This cannot be resolved without the blood test."

    81

    "取一七寸碗，亲以温水涤之，满贮天泉，父立而左，子立于右，以红绒约臂，巨针刺之，血缕缕然注碗中，左者渐趋而右，右者渐趋而左，初甚纡徐，愈近愈速，翕然合同而化矣，观者啧啧叹异，即原呈亦俯首诧绝。乃断章某杖八十，奸无自首，法不援免也；原呈亦杖八十，诬告有因，照不应例也。断章出钱二千，酒脯告祠，即飨族众；出田十亩给原呈子，以章前妇殁时，曾以期服侄主丧也，族众咸服，受责者亦欣喜感诵。予卸事后，薄游，尚郊迎三十里也，然可见昌民之易治。又一事，责非礼之礼，非义之义，大可入《轩渠集》《嗢噱录》者。

    Explanation

    81

    Take a seven-inch bowl, personally wash it with warm water, and fill it with heavenly spring water. The father stands on the left, and the son stands on the right. They tie red silk around their arms, and a large needle is used to pierce them, causing the blood to drip into the bowl. The one on the left gradually moves to the right, and the one on the right gradually moves to the left. At first, the movement is very slow, but it becomes faster as they get closer. Suddenly, they merge and transform. The spectators murmur in amazement, and even the original petitioner bows in astonishment. The court then sentences someone to eighty strokes of the cane, as those who commit adultery without confessing cannot be exempted by law; the original petitioner is also sentenced to eighty strokes of the cane, as false accusations based on reasons are not exempted according to the law. The court orders someone to pay two thousand coins, offers wine and meat to the ancestral shrine, and immediately feasts the clan members. Ten acres of land are given to the son of the original petitioner, because the woman's husband had died, and her brother-in-law had served as the chief mourner. The clan members all accept it, and those who were punished are also happy and moved to recite. After I completed my duties, I went on a brief tour, and they still met me thirty miles out of town. Thus, it can be seen that the people of Chang are easily governed. Another case, where the punishment for improper propriety and improper righteousness is so absurd that it could be included in Xuanqu Ji and Wajue Lu.

    82

    有争山者，言祖葬此山，例得管业，诉者绘图贴说，具呈家册粮串，里胥及保长均助之，乃饬销案。一日方坐堂皇，见十余人肩一碣至，中题云：正穴妣某孺人之墓，左云长夫潘某府君配葬之墓，右云次夫李某府君配葬之墓。盖两造之祖，潘与李二友莫逆，潘既娶，谋为李亦娶，李曰："我綦贫，耗君资无理，且娶而不淑，将间吾两人，凶终隙末奈何？"潘云："不娶无子，大不孝也，然如弟言亦正长虑。无已，吾有一策，嫂甚顺，惟兄言是从，亦甚爱弟，请与弟共之，不惟绥子孙子，更足宜尔室家。议以一索属兄，再索属弟。

    Explanation

    82

    A dispute arose over a mountain, with the claimant arguing that his ancestors had buried their remains there, and thus he had the right to manage the property. The claimant presented detailed documentation, including maps, family records, and tax receipts, and was supported by local officials and village leaders. The case was then dismissed.

    One day, while the magistrate was sitting in his official hall, he saw a group of people carrying a stone tablet. The tablet had inscriptions on it: the main burial site of the mother, the burial site of the husband on the left, and the burial site of another husband on the right. It turned out that the ancestors of both parties were close friends, and after Pan married, he planned for Li to marry as well. Li, however, felt it was unreasonable to spend Pan's resources, especially since he was very poor. Moreover, if the marriage was unhappy, it would create discord between the two friends, leading to a bad end. Pan argued that not having children was a grave act of filial impiety, but Li's concerns were valid.

    There was no other choice but to propose a plan. The sister-in-law was very obedient and loved her brother-in-law. They decided to share the wife, ensuring the continuation of their lineage and maintaining a harmonious household. The first child would belong to the older brother, and the second to the younger brother.

    "妇固多男，竟得六子焉，故佳城创此奇观也。予笑谓若等不足争，先辩此身是潘是李，前人相厚如此，妻子且可与共，尔等乃争此山毛野蔌，宜各扑数十。且若祖共妻肇隙，尤罪之魁，封一巨板于二坟，各杖四十，并令掘出其骸，饬子若孙曾数十人，各刺血滴之，方能辩孰李孰潘也。时潘族有一武生一监生，知而来求，因碎其碣，焚其案，曰无使章氏父子笑人也。后熊四之垣，言尝游甘肃，彼地方五男二女，兄弟同妻习以为常，子以次抚之，无相夺伦也。予曰："此乃一家可，尚无异姓乱宗之嫌。"方大湛崖笑曰："君自不学，未读《焦氏易林》，不云子无姓氏，父不可知耶！"今已二十年，昌化人犹有道之者。

    Explanation

    83

    A woman indeed had many sons, and she finally obtained six sons, thus creating this marvel at the fine tomb. I laughed and said that you are not worth arguing with, first argue whether this body is Pan or Li. The predecessors treated each other so well, even wife and children can share, but you are fighting over these wild herbs, it is appropriate to beat each of you dozens of times. And your ancestors started the quarrel, especially the chief of the guilty, seal a large board on the two tombs, each receive forty strokes, and order to dig up their remains, order dozens of descendants, each prick their blood and drop it, only then can we distinguish who is Li and who is Pan. At that time, the Pan clan had one martial scholar and one scholar-official, who knew and came to request, therefore, they smashed their steles and burned their cases, saying, "do not let the Zhang father and son laugh at us." Later, Xiong Si said he had traveled through Gansu, in that place, there were five men and two women, and it was common for brothers to share a wife, the sons would take turns caring for them, without disrupting the order. I said, "This is acceptable within one family, there is no concern of outsiders disrupting the clan." Fang Da Zhan Ya laughed and said, "You have not studied, you have not read the Jiao's Book of Changes, it does not say that the child has no surname, the father is unknown!" Now it has been twenty years, and people in Changhua still talk about it.
