    塑匠
    　　　塑匠之工，以滇南为最，蒙元刘銮之遗规也。城隍庙东偏名臣像一堂，首诸葛忠武，羽扇纶巾，居然遗像，肃清高也。次包孝肃，进贤冠绛袍，亦白面书生，较武侯稍戌削。又次瞻思，赭面无鬚髯，服式如貂璫。又次则沐黔国，少年玉貌，惟赤髭异人。又次则皆本朝名宦：鄂文端尔泰、陈文恭宏谋、杨文定名时、阿勤襄里衮、裴少宰宗锡，暨尹文端继善咸列焉，像俱得其真，写之肖甚。中尹公尤妙，一手按膝，一手捻数珠，呼之欲应，若向人微笑者。共谓三像最佳，葛公似仙，包公似神，尹公则似佛焉。不塑李侍尧，尤见直道之遗。今又三十余年，不知尚完好否？但包孝肃莅滇，不见正史，当广考之。又东为圆通寺，塑列代高僧，梵相与紫衣相间，外域自一祖诃摩迦叶，中土始初祖达摩。世庙时释教大盛，李宫保遣人于名刹影堂图归，其梵相则本之三才图绘，非如今时之禅林罗汉堂，伸臂裂胸，作诸幻相也。

    Explanation

    84

    The Craft of Sculptors
    The skill of sculptors is most renowned in southern Yunnan, following the traditions established by Liu Luan during the Mongol-Yuan dynasty. In the east wing of the City God Temple stands a hall dedicated to the statues of famous ministers. First among them is Zhuge Liang, the Wuzi, who appears solemn and dignified, with a high, noble bearing, wearing a feather fan and a black silk headband, truly resembling his portrait. Next is Bao Zheng, the Xisuzi, dressed in a scholar's cap and a red robe, also appearing as a scholarly young man, though somewhat more austere than Zhuge Liang. Following him is Zhan Si, with a ruddy face and no beard, dressed in attire like that of a high-ranking official. Then comes Mu Qian Guo, a young man of jade-like beauty, distinguished by his red beard. After these are several officials from the Qing dynasty: E Wen Duan Er Tai, Chen Wen Gong Hong Mou, Yang Wen Ding Ming Shi, A Qin Xiang Li Gun, Pei Shaozai Zong Xi, and Yin Wen Duan Ji Shan, all of whom are represented in lifelike statues, capturing their true likenesses. Among them, the statue of Yin Gong is particularly exquisite, with one hand resting on his knee and the other holding prayer beads, seeming to respond to a call, as if smiling gently at someone. It is generally agreed that the three best statues are those of Zhuge Liang, who resembles a deity; Bao Zheng, who resembles a god; and Yin Gong, who resembles a Buddha. The absence of Li Shi Yao's statue is especially notable, as it reflects the integrity and straightforwardness of the tradition. Now, thirty years have passed, and it is uncertain whether the statues remain in good condition. However, Bao Zheng's visit to Yunnan is not recorded in official histories, and further research is needed to verify this. To the east of the temple is the Yuntong Temple, where statues of eminent Buddhist monks from various dynasties are displayed, their appearances alternating with those of high-ranking monks in purple robes. The first patriarch from the West is Kasyapa, while the first patriarch from China is Bodhidharma. During the reign of Emperor Jiajing, Buddhism flourished, and Li Gongbao sent people to famous temples to copy images of high-ranking monks. The appearance of these Buddhist figures is based on depictions found in the "Three Talents" paintings, unlike the exaggerated and fantastical depictions found in modern Zen temples, where statues often stretch their arms and chests, creating various illusionary forms.

    85

    圆通寺有柏二株，其高入云，真少陵所咏"霜皮溜雨四十围，黛色参天二千尺"者，土人云有蝴蝶朝王之异。予羁棲无俚，日日往观，六月望后，即见柏杪渐有翔集者，予本短视，树高物小，不甚了了。积增至十九日，满柏顶皆白，如梅花盛开，土人云，南海者皆归矣。至廿二三，则低枝曲干，亦稠叠合并，无少间隙。然皆常蝶，殊非罗浮仙品，何所谓王也，土人神之，虽小儿女莫敢扑。廿五晨兴往视，则翠柏森然，杳然不得一蝶。

    Explanation

    85

    Yuntong Temple has two cypress trees, their height reaching into the clouds, truly embodying the description in Du Fu's poem: "Their bark, thick and smooth, is forty chi in circumference, and their dark green color reaches up to the sky, two thousand chi tall." Locals believe there is a strange phenomenon of butterflies paying homage to a king. I, being idle and aimless, visited the trees every day. After the full moon in June, I began to see butterflies gathering at the tips of the cypress trees. Due to the height of the trees and the small size of the butterflies, they were not very clear to see. Over the next few days, the tops of the trees became covered with white butterflies, resembling blooming plum blossoms. By the nineteenth day, it was said that all the butterflies from the South Sea had returned. By the twenty-second and twenty-third days, even the lower branches and curved trunks were densely packed with butterflies, leaving no space between them. However, they were all ordinary butterflies, far from the rare, mystical species of Lufu. What then is this "king" referred to? The locals revered the butterflies, and even small children dared not catch them. On the twenty-fifth day, I woke up early to visit again, but the cypress trees stood tall and green, with no butterflies remaining.

    86

    考六月廿四为火把节，段功被难之日，或有忠魂毅魄殉于兹山，此栩栩者无乃碧血所化，亦或阿（礻盍）主埋玉于此，则青陵台外，复为春驹添一佳话，曾倩茂苑梅君作图状之，藏于寺中。又见《渔洋杂著》有云：六诏未入版图时，以逸少为圣人，荐蘋释菜皆主之。予识滇中博士颇伙，询之无知此故事。后历游外郡，儒释均无祀右军者。点苍亦不甚精八法，丝绣金装以媚笔阵，恐未必然。归后考《鮚埼亭集》剡溪九曲辞中，第一曲亦名云南有逸少祠焉，疑缘此传误。又西湖上花神祠，李宫保不远万里召滇工所塑，故像皆意态如生。今数经修改，无复本来面目，圆通古像，能无恙乎？

    Explanation

    86

    The 24th day of the sixth month is the Fire Festival, the day when Duan Gong faced adversity. Perhaps there were loyal spirits and steadfast souls who sacrificed themselves on this mountain. This vivid image might be the result of the transformation of green blood, or perhaps it is the burial place of a noble person. Thus, outside the Qingling Terrace, another beautiful story has been added to the spring horse. Maoyuan Mei Jun was once commissioned to create a painting depicting this scene, which is now stored in the temple. Additionally, in the Fish Pond Miscellaneous Writings, it is recorded: "When the Six Kingdoms were not yet part of the Chinese empire, Wang Xizhi was regarded as a sage, and offerings of rice and vegetables were made to him." I know many scholars in Yunnan, but none of them were aware of this story. After traveling through other regions, I found that neither Confucians nor Buddhists worship Wang Xizhi. The Diancang region is not very skilled in the eight methods of calligraphy, and their ornate and decorative style may not be accurate. After returning, I studied the Jiaoti Pavilion Collection and found that in the Shanyi Nine Bends Ode, the first bend is also named after the Wang Xizhi Temple in Yunnan. I suspect this is the source of the error. Moreover, the Flower Goddess Temple on West Lake, Li Gongbao summoned craftsmen from Yunnan over a great distance to create statues, and all the statues appear lifelike. Now, after multiple modifications, they no longer resemble their original form. The ancient statues at Yuntong Temple, could they remain unharmed?

    87

    滇医
    　　　六诏远在天末，不但风土人情与中原异，至医药一途尤非平素所喻。乾隆壬子，予游滇中，督学萧韶亭先生，山东日照人，以世讲稔予，其弟九仪病肿，浼为诊视。同事者武林庞君，议以五皮饮利之不效，以五福饮加减复不效，用八正散。韶亭先生亦解医，曰："予弟好饮而多欲，肾气不固，故湿痰难逐，肾气丸可服否？"庞与予皆力赞之。守服此方几十剂，愈服愈肿，由股而腹而腰，循至胸脯间，众皆惶急。一老胥进曰："此间有专门医瘇胀者，甚验，何不试之？"俯仰间已呼至，其人面目黧黑，短褐不完，竹冠草履，长揖而不敢坐。

    Explanation

    87

    The Dian Medical Case

    The Six Zao tribes are far away at the edge of the world, and their customs and manners differ significantly from those of the Central Plains, especially in the field of medicine, which is particularly unfamiliar to us. In the year 1782 during the reign of Emperor Qianlong, I traveled to Yunnan, where Mr. Xiao Shaoting, the provincial supervisor of education, a native of Rizhao, Shandong, became acquainted with me through our shared acquaintances. His younger brother, Mr. Jiu Yi, fell ill with edema, and he asked me to examine him. My colleague, Mr. Pang from Wulin, suggested using Wu Pi Yin (Five Peel Decoction), but it did not work. He then tried modifying Wu Fu Yin (Five Happiness Decoction), but that also proved ineffective. Finally, they used Ba Zheng San (Eight Correcting Powder). Mr. Xiao Shaoting, who also understands medicine, said, "My younger brother enjoys drinking and has many desires, leading to weak kidney qi, which makes it difficult to expel damp phlegm. Could we try Shen Qi Wan (Kidney Qi Pill)?" Both Mr. Pang and I strongly supported this suggestion. After taking this formula for several dozen doses, his condition worsened, with the swelling spreading from his thighs to his abdomen and waist, and eventually reaching his chest. Everyone was in a state of panic. An old clerk suggested, "There is a specialist here who treats edema very effectively. Why not try him?" Within moments, the specialist was summoned. He had a dark complexion, wore a tattered short jacket, and a bamboo hat with straw sandals, and he bowed deeply but did not sit down.

    88

    萧公礼之，令诊脉，曰："无庸，某治此三世矣，疗之易耳！"令开方，又曰："无庸，予自有药。"萧公曰："未达不尝，圣有谟训，子方或秘，但一开示予，立即付内。予忝视学，断不能舍翰林而就太医，以攘子世案。"强之良久，乃嗫嚅曰："愚不解书，口授而公录之可。"公笑从之。一曰上天龙，二曰千头参，三曰著地鞭，公茫然搁笔，以问土著，亦无有能辨者，医乃曰："我固曰无庸。"出药一裹，计二钱，曰："昏后以米饮调之，然性颇烈，腹中作跋扈，勿畏也！"萧公虑之，商曰："先服参，顾其本，可乎？"即以询之，医亦云可。

    Explanation

    88

    Xiao Gong showed respect and ordered a diagnosis of the pulse. The doctor said, "There's no need; I have treated this condition for three generations, and it's easy to cure!" When ordered to prescribe medicine, he again said, "There's no need; I have my own medicine." Xiao Gong replied, "Without understanding, one should not taste it. The sages have wise teachings, and your family's expertise may be secret, but if you just show me, I will immediately provide the necessary resources. I am honored to be a scholar-official and would never abandon my position as a scholar-official to become a court physician, to appropriate your family's expertise." He persisted for a long time, and the doctor finally hesitantly said, "I am ignorant of writing; you can dictate and I will write it down." Xiao Gong smiled and agreed. The doctor said, "The first is Shangtianlong, the second is Qian Tou Shen, and the third is Zhuo Di Bian." Xiao Gong put down his pen in confusion and asked the locals, but none could identify them. The doctor then said, "I said there's no need." He took out a bundle of medicine, weighing two qian, and said, "Take it with rice gruel after dusk, but it has a strong nature and may cause discomfort in the stomach; do not be afraid!" Xiao Gong was concerned and consulted, "Should I take the ginseng first, considering the root, is that alright?" He immediately asked about it, and the doctor also agreed.

    89

    乃以次第进之，腹痛大作，至晓而跳掷不可忍，一炊许，乃呼围桶，洞然一泄，而肿以顿退矣。午余来视，自诩曰如何，俗病固不烦文治。庞公曰："我闻逐水者多速效，再发，恐不可救奈何？"曰："固也。"留药钱许，作一剂，曰："十日再肿，服此；又十日再肿，服此。"又以数分作一剂："后此不复作矣！"如其言，信然，至今遍询诸货药人，亦从未有知其名者。未几，余假令广通，蒋观察荐一仆常熟人，居一月疾作，鸡胸鳖背，如承蜩丈人，且尫瘠不见肉。乃置罗川厂中，令主税吏视其食息。

    Explanation

    89

    The treatment was administered in sequence, and severe abdominal pain ensued. By dawn, the pain was so intense that he could not bear it. After a short while, he called for a chamber pot, and suddenly released, the swelling subsided immediately. In the afternoon, I visited, and he boasted, "How about it? Common illnesses don't require elaborate treatments." Pang Gong said, "I've heard that those who use diuretics often see quick results, but if it recurs, it might be incurable, what then?" He replied, "Indeed." He left a small amount of medicine and prepared a dose, saying, "If the swelling returns in ten days, take this; if it returns again in another ten days, take this." He then made another dose with a few more parts, saying, "There will be no recurrence after this." As he said, indeed so. To this day, I have asked many medicine sellers, and none have known its name. Not long after, I was appointed to Guangtong. A servant from Changshu, recommended by Governor Jiang, developed a disease after living there for a month. He had a chicken chest and a turtle back, like an old man carrying a cicada, and was thin and bony with no visible flesh. He was placed in the Luochuan factory, and I ordered the tax official to observe his eating and breathing.

    90

    半月来署，博硕肥腯，非复曩状矣，问之，曰："有土人教以觅七年老鸭，出药末掺之，缚胸前，一夜而胸平。越数日复得一鸭，缚诸背亦如之，乃霍然耳。"考其药则均不知何草也，腑肺能语，其洞见一方人哉！虽张刘李朱迁其地不能为良矣，然以边医中土，则捷于操刃。在杭时，同寅郎锦骐拉予视疟，视其脉，虾游雀啄均见，无可为矣，诘之曰："昨一友来钞一经验方，服之不觉委顿。"视之，柴胡一两，麻黄五钱，熟地一两，附子三钱，余不能记，大抵仿此，敛手而退。其同乡孔君龙璋尚为疏剂，翌日而卒，七窍皆血，与中毒无异。今江湖一带，提囊售医者此辈不少，予谓有司当以蛊毒杀人治之，庸医不足蔽辜也，庶几郑重民命之一端乎。

    Explanation

    90

    Half a month in the office, I found myself fat and strong, no longer in my former state. I asked him about it, and he said, "A local taught me to find a seven-year-old duck, mix medicine powder with it, tie it to my chest, and after one night, my chest became flat. After several days, I found another duck, tied it to my back in the same way, and then suddenly it was gone." Investigating the medicine, none knew what herbs were used. The organs could speak, how deeply they understand the people of this place! Even if Zhang, Liu, Li, and Zhu moved to this place, they could not be good, but if used in the central lands, it would be as effective as wielding a knife. When in Hangzhou, my colleague Lang Jinqi dragged me to see a case of malaria. Examining the pulse, both shrimp swimming and birds pecking were seen, and there was nothing that could be done. I asked him, "A friend came yesterday with a tried-and-true formula, and after taking it, he did not feel weak." I saw the ingredients: one ounce of Bupleurum, five ounces of Ephedra, one ounce of Rehmannia, and three ounces of Aconite. I could not remember the rest, but it was largely similar. With folded hands, I withdrew. His hometown friend Kong Junlong still prepared a decoction, and he died the next day, with blood from all seven orifices, no different from poisoning. Nowadays, there are many such people selling medicine in the rivers and lakes. I believe the authorities should treat them as poisoning and murder; ordinary doctors are not enough to cover their guilt. Perhaps this is a way to take the people's lives seriously.

    91

    王二先生
    　　　王立人，忘其名，越之山阴人，工摺奏，刑钱均擅，居滇久，尤熟其风土人情，遂执梃为幕宾盟长，馆于近花圃，园林戏台咸备。督及抚尚可折简招，道府以下有君前、无士前也。承宣为德清许君祖京，提刑为江夏贺君长庚，皆其儿女姻亲，首府为武林庄君肇奎，缟紵尤笃。左鞹贮刑名，右鞹藏钱谷，视王二先生点定，即遣奴呈两府施行，无烦斟酌也。一缺出，官须两司议详、两院商定，幕则立翁片言而决，当局者不敢参一词。

    Explanation

    91

    Wang Er, the Master

    Wang Liren, whose full name is forgotten, was from Shanyin, Zhejiang. He was skilled in drafting official documents and proficient in both criminal law and finance. Having lived in Yunnan for a long time, he became very familiar with the local customs and people. Consequently, he held the position of chief advisor and strategist, residing in a nearby garden that was well-equipped with all the necessary facilities, including gardens and theater stages. The governor and the provincial commissioner could still summon him with a simple letter, while those below the level of the governor addressed him as "lord" but none as "scholar." The official in charge of communications was Xu Zujing from Deqing, and the official in charge of judicial affairs was He Changgeng from Jiangxia. Both were his in-laws or close relatives. The head of the local administration was Zhuang Zaoqi from Wulin, and they had a particularly close friendship. His left bag held legal matters, and his right bag held financial matters. When Wang Er reviewed and approved, the servants would present the decisions to the two offices for implementation, without the need for further deliberation. When a vacancy occurred, officials had to consult with two departments and two courts, but the chief advisor, however, would make a decision with just a few words, and those in charge dared not add a single word.

    92

    滇省修脯最优，即至薄者亦六百金，繁缺倍之，皆其门下士，然亦甚公，以技之长短分高下，不少轩轾也。各府厅州县衙参大府后，午必麕集，谒贵者于斯，访友者于斯，审案者亦于斯，娱戏者尤必于斯，一厅则敲扑喧哗，一厅则笙歌婀娜，不相闻，不相混。夜必设筵，器物多创造，如大方机、阔茶几，皆其新制，人占一机一几，进食单以笔点之；一壶一簋，不并案。或欲遍尝，或不兼味，惟其便，绍酒大尊价纹银十二两，夜必罄一尊。
    同乡之赋闲者，悉馆谷之，故王二先生，大府有投赠，司道有缟紵，府厅以下有进奉，而终不足供其挥霍，于是谋于当事，总办各省铜运，除京运八起，及粤省以盐交易外，期余各省以铜本交藩库，即以运本交王寓。届期则于百色兑铜，既速且逸，运员以恬以娱，省之近者，且可暂假归省。

    Explanation

    92

    Yunnan Province offers the highest salaries, even the lowest positions earning six hundred taels of silver. For busy or important positions, the salaries are doubled, and all are disciples of the master, yet the ranking is very fair, based on the length or quality of their skills, with no bias. After visiting the provincial governor, officials from various administrative levels gather in large numbers at noon. They visit the wealthy here, meet friends here, judge cases here, and entertain here, especially in the latter case. One hall is noisy with the sound of wooden blocks, while another is filled with graceful music and singing, and they do not interfere with each other. Every night, a banquet is set up, with many newly created utensils, such as large tables and wide tea tables. Each person has one table and one tea table, and the menu is marked with a pen. One pot and one bowl are not placed on the same table. Some want to try everything, while others do not want to eat multiple dishes, as they please. Shaoxing wine in a large jar costs twelve taels of silver, and a jar is consumed every night.

    Idle fellow townspeople are all provided for, so Mr. Wang Er receives gifts from the provincial governor, silk and cloth from officials, and offerings from those below the level of prefecture and county. Still, it is not enough to satisfy his extravagance. He then consulted with the relevant authorities to oversee the copper transportation across provinces, except for the eight shipments to Beijing and the trade of salt with Guangdong Province. The copper from the remaining provinces is to be delivered to the provincial treasury, and the transportation costs are to be paid to Mr. Wang's residence. At the appointed time, the copper is exchanged in Baise, both fast and easy. Transport officials are at ease and entertained, and those close to the province can also temporarily take leave to return home.

    93

    计运本羡余，一年原可数万金，奈局面愈宽，酬应愈广，办十余年，总计短廿四万，乃告两司曰："公等以铜厂钱局膏润，多者七八十万，少者亦不下二三十万，非臣力不及此。今与公等约，若助我十六方，若助我八方，宦囊太丰，非福也。以济我急，且减君装也，见机而作，予从此逝矣。"召诸委员代草公禀，讼已；复为两司代草详稿，罪己，以边省犯事，调戌四川，搜合余烬，尚存万余金。八十余，卒于蜀。近闻其幼子聘于许者，以军籍举秋试，次子赘贺者，亦以县佐分发。至今越人之幕于滇者，犹啧啧称王二先生不置云。若其一传而为金刚钻，再传而为金玉堂，所谓画虎不成，反类犬也，王先生岂易学哉！

    93

    The surplus funds from operations, originally amounting to several hundred thousand gold coins per year, dwindled as the scope of expenses and obligations expanded. After managing affairs for over a decade, the total shortfall amounted to twenty-four thousand gold coins. He then addressed the two highest-ranking officials, saying, "Your Excellencies, the copper smelting and coin minting facilities have provided ample revenue, with some officials earning as much as seven or eight hundred thousand gold coins, and others no less than two or three hundred thousand. It is not that I lacked the ability to achieve such figures. I now propose a mutual agreement: if you assist me with sixteen thousand gold coins, or even eight thousand, it would be excessive for an official's purse. By helping me in this time of need, you would also reduce your own expenses. Acting in accordance with circumstances, I shall depart from here." He summoned the commissioners to draft a joint petition, which was submitted. He then drafted a detailed report for the two officials, confessing his own faults. Due to a crime committed in the border province, he was reassigned to garrison duty in Sichuan. After gathering the remaining resources, he still had over ten thousand gold coins left. In his eighties, he passed away in Sichuan. Recently, it was learned that his younger son, who had passed the imperial examination, was married into the Xu family, while his second son, who was appointed as a county assistant, was also in good standing. To this day, those from Yuezhou who served in Yunnan continue to highly praise Mr. Wang Er. If one tries to emulate him and fails, ending up resembling something inferior, Mr. Wang is not easily imitated.

    朱秋芳
    　　　竹垞先生之裔，曰秋芳，性刚介。幕于滇，晨起，日日令奴襆被，一言不合，即可褰裳也，脯修以十日为断，不过支。居停有以处分隔阂商者，必遭呵斥，谓足下官职岂与生俱来耶！或前人遗留，或己身遭际，傥来之物，奈何以民命徇之。上官或有偏倚，必再三顶覆，得申其意乃已。然良有司乐其严，明大府重其正，依然到处逢迎也。

    Explanation

    94

    Zhu Qiu Fang
    　　　Descendant of Mr. Zhuca, named Qiu Fang, he was a man of strong and principled character. He served as a retainer in Yunnan, and every morning he would order his servant to pack the bedding. If there was even a slight disagreement, he could immediately leave. He stayed for only ten days, which was just enough to get by. If the host tried to resolve any conflicts or misunderstandings, he would certainly be scolded, asking, "Is your official position something you were born with? It might have been left by your ancestors or gained through your own experiences, but how can you sacrifice the lives of the people for such things?" If the superior officer was biased, he would repeatedly argue and plead until his intentions were fully expressed. However, competent officials appreciated his strictness, and high-ranking officials respected his integrity, so he still found support and approval wherever he went.

    95

    嶍峨有土豪李监生，富而横，悦佃人妇吴氏，妇性贞烈，利诱之不动，势劫之不动，贿其夫若父交逼之，终不动，乃老羞变怒，遣数力缚妇里绷大树，炽火炙杀之。夫若父跪求，益怒，且劫令其夫手蓺之，即瘗之山，三年无敢发其事者，独一执爨人抱义愤，然无以发。旗员某廉干有识，部选是邑，履任岁余，访得之。上省密禀，诸上游均难之，宰愠，欲乞病，朱曰："何弱也，君不办此案，终不得白矣。我通详已定，连夜发之，等罢官耳，去乃有名。"宰奋袂从之，搜得执爨人，藏之署中以为证。案即定，纤悉皆入奏，大府皆夺俸镌级，二本府皆实降，前任令三者禠职，宰以莅任已二年，亦在议中，奉特旨宽免，且与引见。

    Explanation

    95

    In Yexiao, there was a local tyrant named Li Jiansheng, who was wealthy and domineering. He was attracted to the wife of a tenant farmer, Wu Shi, who was chaste and resolute. Despite being tempted with material incentives and coerced with force, she remained unmoved. Her husband and father, bribed to pressure her, also failed to change her mind. In a fit of rage, Li Jiansheng had her bound to a tree in the village and burned to death. Her husband and father knelt and begged, but he became even angrier and forced her husband to carry out the act. He then buried her in the mountains. For three years, no one dared to report the incident, except for a kitchen worker who held a sense of justice and anger but had no means to expose it. A certain official, known for his integrity and wisdom, was appointed to the county and, after serving for more than a year, investigated and found out about the incident. He reported it secretly to the provincial government, but all the higher officials were hesitant. The magistrate was angry and wanted to request to be excused due to illness. The official said, "How weak are you? If you do not handle this case, it will never be resolved. I have already made a comprehensive report and will send it out tonight; I am ready to be dismissed from my position, but this will make my departure famous." Moved by the argument, the magistrate agreed to proceed. He found the kitchen worker and kept him in the office as evidence. The case was then settled, and all details were reported to the emperor. The provincial governors were all demoted and had their salaries reduced, two prefectural governors were demoted, and three former magistrates were dismissed from their positions. The magistrate, who had served for two years, was also under consideration, but he received a special imperial pardon and was recommended for an audience with the emperor.

    96

    李监生已畏罪自缢，仍戮尸，为从二人发新疆为奴，籍其家，以半给夫家，以半给妇家，吴氏旌表。于是朱秋芳之名，猺獞至奉之为神。又有某者以能办案著，地方有隔阂案件，妙于回斡，边境犹宜。永北厅素称难治，时有劫杀巨案，生苗七犯反狱脱逃。司马某闻报，不知所为，中夜叩门问计，某卧而应曰已知，且安睡，明当料理。司马返，蹀躞竟夜，黎明复往，某曰："何早也！"呼僮延主坐，盥沐竟，主将陈词，某俯而笑曰："已久知，恇搅何为。"饬僮邀同事数友来，曰："今日主人心绪不宁，邀诸君以局戏解之。"遂共博。

    Explanation

    96

    Li the scholar-official hanged himself out of fear of punishment, and his body was still executed. The two accomplices were sent to Xinjiang as slaves, and his property was confiscated, with half given to the husband's family and half to the wife's family. The Wu family was honored with a plaque. Thus, the name of Zhu Qiufang became revered even among the Yao and Zhuang people, who worshiped him as a god. There was another person skilled in handling cases, who was adept at mediation in local disputes, making him still suitable for border areas. The Yongbei Hall was always known to be difficult to govern, with frequent major cases of robbery and murder. Seven convicts escaped from prison. Commander So-and-so heard the report and did not know what to do, so he knocked on the door in the middle of the night to ask for advice. The person lying down replied, "I already know, just rest, I will handle it tomorrow." The commander returned, pacing all night. At dawn, he went again. The person said, "Why so early?" He called a servant to invite the host to sit, and after finishing washing and grooming, the host was about to speak. The person bowed and smiled, saying, "I already know, why are you so anxious?" He instructed the servant to invite several colleagues and friends, saying, "Today the host is anxious, inviting all of you to play a game to relieve it." And they all played together.

    97

    饭后，僮向某小语，某起立曰："有日行件，须了之即来。"遂趋出，须臾，归局复博。至夜分，主戚戚，某怡怡，诸友皆惘惘。忽闻外间欢呼驰报曰："囚已尽获矣！"某乃促主人急召营弁，略诘数语，缚出斩之。详稿出诸袖中，略云生苗反狱，逻者觉之，丞乃亲率丁壮，囚尚抗拒，营弁亦来，斗而检之。然苗甚黠，颇多徒党，且擒时中有受伤将毙者，援边防例，即正典刑，防其逸或死，得逃显戮也。疏防及擅刑，均开参请议，盖去者不可追，别获七苗，李代桃僵也。丞不惟无罪，且以能书功，斯真妙手回斡，能排难者。但生苗逢人即杀，有可死之道，而雉纲鸿雁，此心何以自安哉，未识秋芳闻之，又当如何也。

    97

    After dinner, the servant whispered something to someone, who stood up and said, "There is a matter that needs to be handled; I will return immediately after taking care of it." He then hurriedly left. After a short while, he returned to the gaming house to resume gambling. By midnight, the host was anxious, the person was cheerful, and the friends were all confused. Suddenly, they heard shouts from outside announcing, "The prisoners have all been captured!" He then urged the host to quickly summon the military officers, questioned them briefly, and had them bound and executed. He took out a detailed report from his sleeve, which roughly stated that the rebels had escaped from prison, the guards discovered them, the magistrate personally led the militia, the prisoners still resisted, and the military officers also came, and they fought and searched for them. However, the rebels were very cunning, had many accomplices, and some were injured and close to death when captured. According to border defense regulations, they were immediately executed to prevent them from escaping or dying, thus avoiding public execution. The negligence in defense and the unauthorized execution were both reported for discussion, as the escapees could not be pursued, and seven other rebels were captured instead, a case of "substituting the plums for the peaches." The magistrate not only escaped blame but also received praise for his writing skills, truly a masterful hand that could resolve difficulties.     苗匪教匪启衅
    　　　苗匪之后，继以教匪，高宗、仁宗相继宵旰，几十年欃枪始扫。第其初皆起于纤细，昏吏之昏、悍民之悍、墨吏之墨、愚民之愚，泯泯棼棼，成此浩劫，可恨可哀，亦正大可嗢噱也。乾隆五十七年，予在滇南，住元江施刺史寓中，襄理笔墨。滇省事简省，例多不回本任也，刺史族兄锦仕黔，官巡检，求调苗疆，刺史辞以隔省，难于为力迟之。其兄总戎鑑，时官都閬，亦以书来曰："事非破例，本省额中丞已诺，惟制宪处必须一臂耳。"遂得古州。莅调年余，忽风闻苗寨中有蠢蠢欲动者，召头入诘之，头人曰："夫何敢！"乃责令出，不敢生事，具结，释之出。

    Explanation

    98

    The Miao bandits and religious bandits sparked a conflict. After the Miao bandits, religious bandits followed, and during the reigns of Emperors Qianlong and Jiaqing, the imperial court worked tirelessly for decades to finally quell the rebellion. Initially, these conflicts arose from minor issues, such as the corruption of officials, the ferocity of commoners, the greed of corrupt officials, and the foolishness of the populace. The situation descended into chaos, culminating in a great disaster, which is both pitiable and laughable. In the 57th year of the Qianlong era, I was in the southern region of Yunnan, staying in the residence of Magistrate Shi in Yuanjiang, assisting with administrative tasks. It was customary in Yunnan for officials to not return to their original posts, so Magistrate Shi's relative, Jin, who served as a patrol inspector in Guizhou, requested a transfer to the Miao region. Magistrate Shi refused, citing the distance and difficulty in making such arrangements. Jin's brother, General Jian, who was then serving in Duling, also wrote to say, "This is not an exceptional case; the provincial governor has already agreed, but the highest provincial authority must be involved." Thus, Jin was transferred to Guchou. After a year in his new post, I suddenly heard rumors that there was unrest in the Miao villages. I summoned the village head to question him, and he replied, "How dare we!" I then ordered him to ensure no trouble would arise, and he submitted a formal pledge, after which I released him.

    群苗聚而问："皇帝召汝何事？"苗人谓官无大小文武，皆曰皇帝，谓隶则曰官，书吏幕宾曰军师，至尊乃曰京师老皇帝。然畏官畏军师，皇帝不畏，老皇帝更不畏也；头人曰："闻汝辈多事，令我出结耳。"曰："出乎？"曰："出矣。"苗曰："我辈嫉汉奸久，方拟治兵攻之，汝乃出结，即仇汝！"拥头人围巡检署索结，不可，杀而夺之，诸寨应之皆起，夫苗已反矣，索结何为？亦苗已反矣，藏结又何用？苗之为苗噩噩耳，施与苗如一邱之貉。何居？施得祸最惨，尽室并命，而因由如此。易云：勿过防之，從或戕之。哀哉！然苗疆终止西南一隅，施君以身徇之，犹可自解，若戴如煌之墨而愎，乃至流毒天下矣。教匪狱起，通饬州县严查，蜀中素多邪教，达州牧戴如煌者，无材而嗜利，任人牵鼻。

    99

    The Miao people gathered and asked, "What business does the Emperor have with you?" The Miao people call all officials, regardless of rank or role, "Emperor." They call subordinates "officials," scribes and attendants "military advisors," and the supreme leader "the old emperor of the capital." However, they fear officials and military advisors, but not the Emperor, and even less so the old emperor of the capital. The leader said, "I heard that you have many troubles, so I came to settle them." They asked, "Did you come to settle them?" The leader replied, "Yes, I came to settle them." The Miao said, "We have long been envious of the Han traitors and were planning to gather troops to attack them. Now you come to settle things, so we will make you our enemy!" They surrounded the leader and the inspection office, demanding to settle the issue. When refused, they killed and took it by force. All the villages rose up, and the Miao had already rebelled. What is the point of settling the issue now? Even if they had not rebelled, what use would hiding the settlement be? The Miao are just as simple-minded as they seem. The Han and the Miao are like foxes from the same den. Why? The Han suffered the most in the end, with their entire families being exterminated, all because of this. The I Ching says, "Do not overprotect, for it may lead to harm." Alas! The Miao region is confined to the southwestern corner, and the Han official sacrificed himself for them, which can still be justified. But if someone like Dai Ruhuang, who is stubborn and arrogant, were to follow, it could spread disaster throughout the land. The case of the "heretical bandits" arose, and the governor-general ordered all prefectures and counties to conduct strict investigations. In Sichuan, there are many heretical sects. Dai Ruhuang, the governor of Dazhou, was incompetent and greedy, allowing others to manipulate him.

    役王姓者狡狯，戴久为所挟制，奉到通饬，王役怂恿戴牧，某里某村阖族奉教，川俗多聚类而居；戴即簽差王役密查。族必有祠，祠必有产，集议以虎贲赂，寝其事。越旬日，王役又访知某里某村族更大，奉教者更多，依例密查，其族亦依例以三千为赂，戴与王计是族人数几倍于前，不能依样画葫芦也，益至甲盾乃已。蜀人忌而悍，事同而贿异，心已不甘，且切得系王役牵指，王亦教中人按图索骏，当无漏网，而叛教尤为大憝，群议不如缚王而杀之，即议抵而祸根绝矣。鸠众千人赴难，王已侦知，亦聚党千人御之。戴惶急以民变闻，时制宪方征苗，驻平块，省中惟薇垣英贵以推升贵抚未行，一如以养疴回成都，武员则参将杨公以养伤坐镇，兵不盈三百。

    Wang, a cunning man, had long controlled Dai, who received an official order. Wang urged Dai to secretly investigate a certain village where the entire clan followed a teaching. In Sichuan, people often live in clusters. Dai immediately signed an order for Wang to conduct a secret investigation. Every clan has an ancestral hall, and the hall must have property. They gathered to discuss offering a bribe of tiger guards to suppress the matter. After ten days, Wang learned that another village's clan was larger and more numerous in following the teaching. He conducted a secret investigation, and the clan also offered a bribe of three thousand gold coins. Dai and Wang calculated that the number of people in this clan was several times that of the previous one, and they could not follow the same pattern, so they increased the bribe to a thousand gold coins. Sichuan people are suspicious and fierce. The same matter but with different bribes made them dissatisfied.     柳役
    　　　达州教匪，以一隶肇之，而成都叛匪，以一隶擒之，洵若辈亦未尝无人耳。乾隆癸丑，予在泸州，闻省中几有异变，岁首上省始悉其事。有杜先生为村学究，屡试不第，乃萌逆志，召集好乱之徒，结盟歃血，拟于明岁元旦起事，乘会府拜牌，百官皆在，聚而歼之，能戕某官者，即以其官官之。成都府役柳姓，素能事，侦知其谋，然苦无确据，遂诈入其党，尽得名籍。时已廿六，众方匿近郭某家，约趁除夕热闹中窜入，乃请见本官告密。一如大骇，谒大府会营选兵，亦因其聚而缚之，百余人无一得脱。

    102

    The Capture of the Rebels

    Rebels in Dazhou were initiated by one of their subordinates, while rebels in Chengdu were captured by one of the governor's subordinates. Indeed, such events are not uncommon. In the year 1783 during the Qianlong era, while I was in Luzhou, I heard that there was almost a significant disturbance in the provincial capital. At the beginning of the year, upon returning to the provincial capital, I learned the details of the matter. There was a Mr. Du, a village teacher, who had failed many times in the exams and thus developed rebellious intentions. He gathered troublemakers, formed an alliance by drinking blood, and planned to start a rebellion on New Year's Day of the following year. They intended to take advantage of the governor's office during a ritual, when all officials would be present, to gather and annihilate them. Those who could kill a specific official would be given that official's position. A subordinate of the Chengdu governor, surnamed Liu, was skilled and aware of their plans, but lacked solid evidence. He pretended to join their group and obtained a complete list of their members. By the 26th, the rebels were hiding in a house near a certain Mr. Guo, planning to sneak in on New Year's Eve. Liu then reported the plan to the governor, who was greatly alarmed. The governor visited the governor's office, gathered troops, and captured the rebels as they gathered, resulting in the complete capture of over a hundred people.

    委员分鞫，为首者一幼孩，诘之号泣，言身本姓周，年止十四，业剃发，杜先生鬻我，易我姓曰朱，使众人拥而拜我，殊不知所为也，顾欲扑我，冤哉！盖杜先生所弄狡狯，计成，将借以号召，托诸蜀王遗裔也。余亦大半乡愚，惟杜先生窃窥断烂朝报，欲效康熙年间邱监生家群奴故智。谳者悯其愚，坐杜先生为首，凌迟，死罪仅四人，军流及徒杖数十。周童得长繁，今遇赦，出狱矣。相传有李自成嫁母，号流寓旧太后，今周童可谓威逼草头王。蕞尔乱民，亦未尝无对。杜监绑时，补山师叹曰："光天化日之下，不安耕凿，自求族灭，是何肺肠！"杜俯而泣曰："中堂训谕良是，但某一念之差，此时悔之晚矣！"肖濂雪方群居虐谑，或弈战斗棋失算，不竞辄曰："杜先生有言，悔之晚矣。"柳役赏以百金。同一役也，官与民皆阴受其福，与戴如煌所倚仗攫金者，其功罪岂可以道里计哉！

    宝石翡翠纹石
    　　　滇中物产与中土异者颇多，自吾家鹤沙按察及张观察泓、吴开化大勋，各有记载，均以详尽。其最异者宝石，石产井中，在缅酋之祖墓旁，红者尤贵，蓝次之。红之明透者，以一丸置盎中，注水其内，则满盎红霞，真玉碗盛来琥珀光也，予曾见一拳，重八两余，索价万金，患瑶圃尚书许七千不受。次则碧玺之老坑者，其新坑者一年而滞，二年而淡，三四年如水晶矣，虽地不爱宝，亦由渐而杀乎？翡翠出野人国，蕴黄石中，剖之乃得，大者綦难，东川守萧丈文言在滇三十年，集成数珠一挂，玲珑剔透，玉润珠圆，中惟七八颗尚江水绿，百余颗皆鹦鹉羽。带而行日中，青霞蔚起，不可睇眎。料不必言，即玉工已数千金。时福郡王督滇，福晋得一手钏，欲偶之，悬万金终不可得。以一石之微而糜费若此，诚物妖也。

    Explanation

    104

    Jade and Gemstones in Yunnan

    The products of Yunnan that differ from those of the Central Plains are numerous. Since my family's Inspector Heshaha, as well as Zhang Observer Hong and Wu Kaihua Daxun, each have records, all of which are detailed. Among these, the most extraordinary are the gemstones, which are found in wells near the ancestral tomb of the Burmese chieftain. The red ones are particularly precious, followed by the blue ones. The bright and transparent red ones, when placed in a vessel with water, fill the vessel with red clouds, truly like a jade bowl holding amber light. I once saw a piece weighing over eight taels, which was priced at ten thousand gold pieces, but even the scholar-official Yu Yao Pu offered seven thousand and was refused. Next are the old mines of tsavorite (emerald), while the new mines become dull after one year, pale after two years, and resemble crystal after three to four years. Though the earth does not love its treasures, perhaps it gradually diminishes them? Jadeite comes from the land of the wild people, hidden within yellow stone, and can only be obtained by cutting it open; the larger ones are extremely difficult to find. Governor Xiao of Dongchuan, who served in Yunnan for thirty years, collected a string of beads, each one exquisitely clear and translucent, as smooth as jade and round as pearls, with only seven or eight still having the color of river water green, and over a hundred with the color of parrot feathers. When worn in the sunlight, they create a vivid blue haze that cannot be looked at directly. The material itself is not worth mentioning, but even the jade workers are valued at thousands of gold pieces. At the time, Prince Fu, the governor of Yunnan, had a wife who obtained a bracelet, which she wanted to match with another, but offered ten thousand gold pieces and could not find it. For such a small stone to cause such waste, it is truly a thing of wonder.

    105

    瘠土之奇珍，贫儒之雅玩，庶几思州之丈石乎？补山相国督黔学时，觅得尤者百规，筑一竹室，遍置水盆养之，曰百一山房，缘一规面幕皆像形，黑质白章，诸景咸备。最异者两岸陡崖，长松交荫，急峡中孤舟如驶，上坐一人垂钓，石不盈二寸，人仅一粟，而须发眉目，神彩如生，绝似大痴富春笔意，百规皆有赞，见《一山房稿》中，不具录。予运铅在楚，购一盘七枚，余多碎锦纹，不足异，惟一枚作一远树，桠枝四罩，薄霭蒙之，题之曰月中桂，后为姚生仲常乞去。

    Explanation

    105

    A rare treasure from barren land, a refined plaything for poor scholars, perhaps the stone from Sizhou? When Complement Mountain, the Viceroy, oversaw education in Guizhou, he found one hundred particularly fine specimens, built a bamboo room, and placed water basins all around to keep them, naming it "One Hundred and One Mountain Room." The reason for this name was that one of the stones had a face and form resembling images, with a black body and white markings, and all scenes were complete. The most extraordinary scene depicted steep cliffs on both sides, tall pines overlapping their shade, a lone boat speeding through a narrow gorge, with a person sitting and fishing. The stone was no more than two inches in size, and the person was as small as a grain of rice, yet with hair, eyebrows, eyes, and spirit vividly depicted, it was absolutely resembling the style of Dai Jin's Fuchun River. All one hundred stones had inscriptions, which can be found in Yi Shan Fang drafts, but they are not fully recorded here. I was transporting lead in Chu and bought one tray with seven pieces, most of which had fragmented patterns, not particularly unusual, except for one piece that depicted a distant tree with branches spreading in four directions, covered by thin mist. I named it "Moonlit Osmanthus," and later, it was given to a student named Yao Zhongchang.

    106

    又周肖濂守思赠予一器六枚，中一枚作一塔，七级颓然。旁一日影，云气联之，俨然雷峰夕照也，不知八千里外，山灵作此狡狯何意？后为清平阶中丞索去。至翡翠则在滇三年，朱市一物，惟武定邱君赠女孙一耳璫，明灿可爱，圆不及半寸，闻其价已三两。又骆君以翡翠根作黑子，云南玉作白子，赠惠尚书，分饷予黑白各一，今亦以播迁失去。若《归田录》所记翡翠能屑金一说，则殊不然，中云制以为罂，则当宋时恐未必有此大料。然遍考诸书，无有石同名翡翠者，俟再考。

    Explanation

    106

    Zhou Xiaolian, while guarding thoughts, gave me a set of six items. One of them was a pagoda, seven stories high but in a state of decay. Beside it was a shadow of the sun, connected by clouds, resembling the evening glow on the Leifeng Pagoda. I wonder what the mountain spirits were playing at, eight thousand miles away? Later, the Qingping Middle Officer took it away. As for jadeite, it was in Yunnan for three years, and there was a red market item. Only Wuding's Master Qiu gave his granddaughter an earring, which was bright and lovely, less than half an inch in diameter. I heard that its price was three taels. Master Luo made black beads from jadeite root, and Yunnan jade was used to make white beads. He gifted them to the Minister of Works and gave me one black and one white bead. Now they have also been lost due to relocation. If the Record of Returning to the Fields records that jadeite can cut gold, then it is not true. It says that it was made into a flask, so during the Song dynasty, there might not have been such large pieces of jadeite. However, after examining various books, there are no stones with the same name as jadeite, so further examination is needed.

    107

    鸦片
    　　　天下物之恶，莫恶于鸦片，鸩毒不啻也，且色恶臭恶、味之恶可想，而嗜者甘以身殉。人之愚莫愚于吸鸦片，待决之犯，亦无不觊缓须臾；临毙之夫，尚无不求延片刻，吸乌烟者乃日促之，恣纵少年不足惜，而士大夫亦复为之。予在滇时，郑六施七，均以此废且死，施与予尤昵，弥留时惨苦万状，较善终者迥别。闻狄都阃言，滇中此时吸者尤多，几于比户有铺矣。尝见一丰润摺扇，画一躯枯瘠无人状，共一少妓，翘足并卧炕上，挑灯对吸，两瘦鬼伺其旁闻香嗅气，以手招烟，作垂涎状。蛇鼠亦僵卧如蛰，闻烟蠢蠢作亦欲动态，龙眠妙手，一片救世婆心也。然欲绝之，亦非甚难，予在永嘉，知库书张元龙犯此，欲绳之，诉曰已绝此二年。曾以办船料，渡海至苏禄国，亲见鸦片本质，故毅然不敢食耳。询其详，云国俗皆裸葬，一亩之地，百祖共之，积累百年，其地之值不资矣。

    Explanation

    107

    Opium

    The most detestable thing in the world is opium, no less so than the poison of a sparrowhawk. Its appearance, smell, and taste are all unpleasant, yet those who crave it are willing to sacrifice their lives for it. There is no greater foolishness than smoking opium. Even those awaiting execution cannot help but hope for a moment's delay; even those on the brink of death still seek to prolong their lives. Those who smoke opium hasten their own demise, wasting the youth is not worth lamenting, and even scholars and officials partake in it. When I was in Yunnan, Zhang Liù and Shi Qī both became addicted and died as a result. Shi was particularly close to me, and in his final moments, he suffered immensely, the agony being starkly different from a peaceful death. According to Di Dukun, there are many opium users in Yunnan now, almost every household has a shop. I once saw a fan with a picture of a body so emaciated it seemed lifeless, accompanied by a young courtesan, they lie on the kang, smoking together while a lamp is lit. Two thin ghosts stand by, sniffing the air and beckoning for the smoke, drooling with desire. Even snakes and mice lie stiffly, as if hibernating, they seem to be stirred by the smell of opium, as if they too want to partake. The artist's skillful hand, with a heart full of compassion for the world. However, to quit is not very difficult. When I was in Yongjia, I knew that Zhang Yuanlong, the keeper of the treasury, was addicted. I wanted to punish him, but he claimed he had quit two years ago. He once traveled to the Sulu Kingdom to procure ship materials, personally seeing the nature of opium, therefore, he firmly decided not to smoke it. When I asked for details, he said that in the country, they practice sky burial, a single acre of land is shared by a hundred ancestors, after a century of accumulation, the value of the land is incalculable.

    108

    造法先掘土数丈，筑其底极坚，并四方亦筑，取掘出之土捣之极细，筛之极净，曝之极干，乃于坑中铺石灰一层，加土一层，罂粟瓣一层，糯米粥一层，覆以芦席，盖以毡，再压以板，自春及夏至秋而成，以金易土，价且倍蓗。然大约吸数百年前陈人之膏血，故一见誓死不再食也。绝之法以十全大补汤加鸦片灰，俟瘾发时服之，初甚委顿，渐服渐愈，两月余复初，书其方，以告世之能自悔者。

    Explanation

    108

    To construct, one must first dig several zhang of earth, building a very strong foundation and also constructing the sides. Take the excavated soil, pound it into a very fine powder, sieve it until it is extremely clean, and dry it until it is extremely dry. Then, in the pit, lay a layer of lime, add a layer of soil, a layer of poppy seeds, and a layer of glutinous rice porridge. Cover it with reed mats, cover it with felt, and press it with boards. The process takes from spring to summer to autumn to complete. Replacing the soil with gold would be many times more expensive. However, it essentially uses the labor and resources of people from hundreds of years ago. Once the process is complete, one swears never to eat again. To stop a habit or addiction, use a ten-ingredient tonic with opium ash. Take the remedy when the craving or addiction manifests. Initially, one feels very weak, but gradually improves with continued use of the remedy. After two months, one returns to their original state. Write down the formula and inform those who can repent themselves.

    又有所谓潮烟者、所谓水烟者、所谓生烟者，率皆游手徒自戕自贼者也，而其根总起于淡巴菰一物，藉称辟瘴，而辟瘴远逊槟榔；藉称御寒，而御寒莫如火酒，世宗有"毫无裨益，尤为妨农"之谕，方学士灵皋先生陈之尤力。无如朝臣多耽之者，陈相元、龙史相贻直尤嗜，即贤如韩尚书菼亦复不免，故阳奉阴违，终不能绝。合计寰中土地，种菸草者几及十之二，一种利倍他植，然三年之后即成废土，非数年不复，蠹国病农，莫此为厉。且士农工商，均以此旷其日力，今且染及闺阁，江浙尤甚。予有句云："习化全家怜绿鬓，离难片刻笑华颠。财消功耗犹闻可，忍变膏腴再易田。"唏哉！
    　　　滇省命案

    Explanation

    109

    There are also what are called "coastal smoke," "water smoke," and "raw smoke," all of which are used by idle people who harm themselves. The root cause of these problems is the use of tobacco, known as "tobacco." It is said to ward off miasma, but it is far inferior to betel nut in this regard. It is also said to resist cold, but nothing is more effective than spirits or alcohol. Emperor Yongzheng issued a decree stating that tobacco provides no real benefit and is especially detrimental to agriculture. Fang Xue Shi, a scholar and official, strongly advocated against its use. Despite this, many officials, including Chen Xiangyuan, Long Shixiang, and Han Shangyu, were fond of smoking. Publicly, they supported the ban, but privately, they disobeyed it. About one-fifth of the land in the empire is used for tobacco cultivation. Tobacco cultivation is highly profitable, but after three years, the land becomes barren and takes several more years to recover. This corrupts the state and harms agriculture, causing more damage than any other crop. Moreover, all social classes are affected by the time wasted on tobacco use. The habit has even spread to women, especially in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. I have a poem that says: "The whole family imitates, pitying the green hair; a moment of difficulty, laughing at old age. Wasting wealth and effort, it is still heard; suffering the transformation of fertile land, changing the fields again." Alas! In Yunnan Province, there are cases of murder, highlighting the severity of the issue.

    110

    幕友脯修，滇省最腆大缺，或至千金，至简者亦必五百。然案牍则易易也，命案止两套，一索欠理直，衅起还殴；一衅起调奸，殴由义愤，笑者谓可刊两板，但填姓名可耳。且死者万分强暴，凶手一味温柔，凶器无不金刃，皆受刃者自备资斧，从无有操刀而来者也。然其实情，真有百思不到者，虽陶皋告我，我不信也。一元江某村中，忽殇幼孩三四，其父母聚而谋曰："此必尸头蛮为祟！"尸头蛮《赤雅》载之，妇人能飞头食儿粪，儿即悸疾以死。今某家新娶妇，眼多白，可疑，不亟毙之，一村无幼孩矣，强其夫执而倒埋之。后母家知而讼之，相验审讯既确，而案第以角口斗殴结也。一新平县夷民为端公执一扇，上有夷字，字如丛草不可辨，保甲报县署，县卢饬役押侯，役谓是有术，夜必遁，惟炙其蹠可免，炙之焦，顿毙。乃坐以邪术，字系符咒，炙痕系履火所伤，竟置不论，冤哉！至宜良一案，死者数十，灭门者数家，虽使孝肃谳狱，亦无从料理也。

    Explanation

    110

    Scholar-officials' assistants in Yunnan province receive the most generous and prestigious salaries, sometimes reaching up to a thousand taels of silver, and even the simplest positions are at least five hundred taels. However, their official duties are very easy; murder cases are only two types: one involves a justified dispute over a debt that escalates into a physical fight, and the other involves a conflict over adultery that results in a beating out of righteous anger. Some jokingly say these cases can be printed on two boards, with only the names filled in. Moreover, the victims are always depicted as extremely violent, while the perpetrators are always portrayed as extremely gentle. The weapons are always sharp metal, and all are prepared by the victims themselves, with no one ever being shown as coming with a knife. Yet the true nature of these cases is often so perplexing that even if told by Tao Gao, I would not believe it. In one village in Yuanjiang, several young children suddenly died, and their parents gathered to plot, saying, "This must be the work of the flying head woman!" The flying head woman, as recorded in the Chiyajia (《赤雅》), is a mythical creature that can fly and eat children's feces, causing illness and death. The new wife of one of the families had unusually large white eyes, which seemed suspicious. To prevent the entire village from being without young children, they forced the husband to take action and bury her upside down. Later, the mother's family learned of this and brought a lawsuit. After investigation and interrogation confirmed the facts, the case was categorized as a verbal and physical altercation. In another case in Xinping County, a local ethnic person was caught holding a fan by a shaman, which had mysterious symbols that were like a tangle of grass and could not be deciphered. The neighborhood watch reported this to the county office, and the magistrate ordered the local authorities to detain him. The officials believed he had supernatural abilities and would escape at night, so they decided to burn his feet to prevent this. They burned him until he was charred and he died instantly. The court then convicted him of witchcraft, claiming the symbols were magical incantations and the burn marks were from walking on fire. The case was dismissed without further consideration, an injustice indeed! In the case of Yiling, dozens of people died, and several families were wiped out. Even if Tao Gao were to adjudicate the case, he would be unable to resolve it.

    111

    宜良民有娶于邻村者，相距十余里，同村均相助，留二人执炊，以待归来食饮。滇中盐贵，觅得一器，乃纳之蔬与肉中，不足，另于陉中见一纸裹，取而益之。少顷，娶者归，女家亦阖村来送，嘉礼才毕，饥渴方殷，聚而大啖，须臾两村数十人皆死，盖仓卒间误以种地信砒霜末益盐煮馔也。地处山僻，两村既尽死，阒无知者，经匝月后，远村人有经其地，见累累稠叠，大骇，遂相传告。

    Explanation

    111

    A man from Yiliang married a woman from a neighboring village, which was separated by more than ten li. The villagers all helped out, leaving two people to cook to wait for their return to eat and drink. Salt was expensive in Yunnan, and they found a container, which they put into the vegetables and meat. It was not enough, so they saw another paper-wrapped item in the pass and took it and added it. After a short while, the newlyweds returned, and the bride's family and the whole village also came to send them off. The wedding ceremony was just completed, and they were extremely hungry and thirsty. They gathered and ate heartily. In a moment, dozens of people from both villages died. It turned out that in the rush, they mistakenly added ground arsenic to the salt while cooking food. The area was remote and mountainous, and both villages were completely wiped out, with no one knowing about it. After a full month, people from a distant village passed through the area, saw many bodies piled up, were greatly shocked, and spread the news.

    权令施延良得其耗，密往勘之，则骨发狼籍，不辨何貌，并不计何数。至近村细访，得迎娶事前说，亦意揣得之。然非盗非仇则凿然可见，至陉中蓄信尚有存者，据以定狱，固无从谳详，付之劫数而已。施戚沈耕霞，使役偕夷众聚而焚之，以灭其迹。耕霞尝同予述之，谓滇中事不得不然，若一经详禀，不特牵累多人，经年累月，案终难结耳。予应之曰："焚骸之惨，谁为尸之？"沈云："夷人大都火葬，亦从其俗。"沈木元和刑房吏，非苏人无此巧思，非刑吏问此辣手，然非滇省可乎哉？

    The authority ordered Shi Yanliang to obtain the details and secretly went to investigate.     万氏升沈
    　　　我师万梅皋先生几嗣君廉山，均慕杜季良之行，皆以佼召衅，然先生卒以免难，廉山行且受知，皆于绝路逢生，词其中具有天焉。先生壬申庶常，散馆外用，宰良乡，牧通州，以东路厅事，牵涉抵罪者颇众，乃以一身任之，拟绞。后得长系。廉山兄弟皆于狱中督课，仲乙亥下第，薄游保阳，依表舅李明府宏照于清苑，蒋丈云师介引执贽焉。同塾者蒋丈婿曹州吴太守阶、参戎刘存子陆丰令遵，陆及其弟逵，廉山兄四郎，廉山年十五，才已出诸人上。庚子夏旋京师，嘱仲曰："子归见吴太史，予将谋纳赎，能于掌铨和相国前一探可否乎？"至都，即以师意告，祖姑丈抚然曰："梅皋衙门前辈，余素知其人，试乘间询之。"越月余，谓仲曰："万事且缓，至斋守文以案情重，捐须加倍，恐非大力不办。

    Explanation

    The Rise and Fall of the Wan Family

    My teacher, Mr. Wan Meigao, and his heir, Lian Shan, both admired the conduct of Du Jiliang. Due to their excellence, they were involved in disputes, but Mr. Wan ultimately avoided disaster, while Lian Shan is about to be recognized. Both found salvation in dire situations, suggesting a sense of destiny or divine intervention in their circumstances.

    Mr. Wan, a member of the Hanlin Academy in the year Renxu, was assigned to an external post after leaving the Hanlin Academy. He served as the magistrate of Liangxiang and the prefect of Tongzhou due to matters related to the Eastern Road Hall. Many were implicated and punished, and he took responsibility for all of them, facing a sentence of death by hanging. Later, he was imprisoned for a long time.

    Lian Shan and his brothers were supervised in their studies while in prison. The second brother failed the imperial examinations in the year Yihai and went on a brief trip to Baoyang. He stayed with his maternal uncle, Li Hongzhao, the magistrate of Qingyuan, and was introduced by Mr. Jiang Yun, a teacher, and presented his credentials. He studied together with Mr. Jiang's son-in-law, Wu Taishou of Caozhou, and Liu Cunzi, the magistrate of Lufeng, along with Liu Cunzi and his younger brother Kuai, and Lian Shan's elder brother, Si Lang. At fifteen, Lian Shan was already surpassing others in talent.

    In the summer of Gengzi, he returned to the capital and told the second brother, "When you return, see Mr. Wu. I plan to pay a ransom. Can you inquire about its feasibility before Chancellor He, who oversees appointments?" Upon arriving in the capital, he immediately conveyed Mr. Wan's intentions. His maternal grandfather sighed and said, "Mr. Wan is a respected elder from the previous administration. I have known him for a long time. Let's try to inquire opportunistically." After more than a month, he told the second brother, "Everything should be delayed, as the case is serious. The donation required is double. It's probably not something that can be handled without significant resources."

    且福堂不堪设教，何汲汲为？闻竹井师有摄保督之耗，其人有肝胆，且重梅皋，若果，当共图之。"仲依语覆师。阅二年，竹井相果督保定，上巡幸津淀，过通，见崇墉屹然，无少残缺，与他处异，垂问系何员承修，英督即对以原任知州万延兰，旋命查卷核办，不日出狱放归，归十余年，考终，寿九十余，犹见廉山兄弟并为司马也。廉山宰元和，承审寿州熏板案，后经初颐园平反，有所诘责，辄自引咎，且据案力辩。

    廉山口给甚，初抚数至词屈，憎之，被谴独重，革职永不叙用。嗣后呈请捐复，本省一驳，吏部再驳，军机处请加倍捐复又驳。忽遇减坝漫溢，菊溪师以爽片得请，不能驳，亦不必捐也。然以廉山之才，接武花砖，亦复何愧，乃屡吟归燕，仅以副车从军，叙州别驾。至小廉学不及父祖远甚，而少年科第，出典试差，抗颜为师，人且谓厚福将与和圃阁学匹，乃竟不永年，且先廉山殁，天之所以忽与忽夺者，诚何意哉？豫章习俗，雅尚堪舆风水一说，容或有之乎？

    Explanation

    115

    Lian Mountain was severely criticized at first, repeatedly arriving but exhausting his words, and was hated, resulting in a particularly harsh punishment, being dismissed from office and never to be re-employed. After that, he submitted a petition to offer a donation to restore his position, which was rejected by the provincial government, then by the Ministry of Personnel, and finally by the Military Affairs Office, which requested a doubled donation but was still rejected. Suddenly encountering a levee overflow, Master Juqi gained approval with a brief note, and could not be rejected, nor did he need to donate. However, with Lian Mountain's talent, following in the footsteps of a predecessor, what is there to be ashamed of, yet he repeatedly sang of returning swallows, only joining the army as a secondary member, holding a specific official position in Xuzu. As for Lian's studies, far less than those of his ancestors, yet passing the imperial examinations at a young age, presiding over an examination, holding his head high as a teacher, people said that great fortune will match that of He Pu Ge Xue, yet he did not live long, dying before Lian Mountain, the heavens' sudden bestowal and sudden taking away, what is the meaning of it? The customs of Yuzhang, elegantly preferring the practice of geomancy and feng shui, perhaps there is any?

    姚西垣听讼
    　　　姚西垣明府锡龄，宰广东惠州府和平县时，地产断肠草，所在多有，民以小忿构隙，辄採服之，并无人命可抵。而一入讼庭，吏役藉饱欲壑，或不饬簠簋，亦间一染指，君听此时不汲汲于所指害之人，必先切究其致死之由及弟子之视其死而不救者，则讼者且惧得罪，于是挟诈之术不行。初莅时，月报毒毙必二三起，后乃渐绝。有同谋打死流丐，伪认为弟以图诈某姓者，君立往勘验，尸在某姓田中，而所过草间沾有血迹，君舍某姓不问，独诘责其伪兄，一鞫得实。此案颇如鬼蜮，不三日而审明。地与江西赣属毗连，边幅辽阔，君巡行四境，不辞劳瘁。时大宪檄严保甲，君更认真查缉，绝无外境匪徒潜入，君缉捕严密，全获邻境钜案盗犯首伙二十余名，人以迁秩贺君，君谓营弁功多，且委员协同，以同寅之意让之，告部，君仅加一级云。

    Explanation

    116

    Yao Xiyuan Hearing Cases

    Yao Xiyuan, the magistrate of Pinghe County in Huizhou Prefecture, Guangdong Province, served during a time when the local area was known for producing the deadly herb duanchangcao. Minor disputes often led to enmity, and people would resort to ingesting the herb, resulting in no one being held accountable for the deaths. However, whenever a case came before him, the officials and clerks would take advantage of the situation to satisfy their greed, and some would even neglect their duties and occasionally partake in the herb. The magistrate, when hearing these cases, did not rush to condemn those accused of causing the deaths but instead carefully investigated the cause of death and those who saw the death and did not rescue. As a result, the accusers were often afraid of being punished, and thus, deceitful schemes were less likely to succeed. Initially, when he took office, there were often two or three reports of poison deaths each month, but this gradually ceased. There was a case where someone conspired to kill a vagrant and falsely claimed him as a brother to defraud a certain family. The magistrate immediately went to investigate. The body was found in the field of the family in question, and there were traces of blood in the grass. The magistrate ignored the family and instead questioned the false brother, and after a thorough investigation, the truth was revealed. This case was particularly like the secretive and deceitful behavior of a ghost or a demon, and it was resolved within three days. The region borders Jiangxi Province, and its boundaries are vast. The magistrate traveled extensively throughout the area, sparing no effort. At the time, the provincial governor issued strict orders to enforce the household registration system, and the magistrate carried out the investigation with even greater diligence. There were no bandits from outside the jurisdiction who sneaked in. The magistrate's strict pursuit of criminals led to the capture of over twenty major criminals from neighboring regions. People celebrated the magistrate's promotion, but he attributed much of the credit to the military officers and the commissioners who worked together, and he modestly yielded the credit to his colleagues. He reported to the central government, and he only received a promotion to a higher rank.

    三异笔谈卷三
    　　　西洋巧器
    　　　高宗七十万寿，普天祝嘏，禁大僚毋许贡金玉。粤督昭信伯李备进自行洋人一套，仿偃师遗意也，奁广仅盈尺，高稍过之。启其鑰，有黄发婢辟门而出，逡巡复入，携出一椅一几，几上置多盛盘，文房悉具。安置甫毕，奁中一碧眼夷官，闯然来就坐，婢为磨墨展纸，碧眼人握管作"万寿无疆"四字。婢献茶一杯，夷官饮之，乃起入奁，婢捡点既尽，亦敛身入，而门自铿然闭矣。后昭信以进，御需用国书，尤为得体。呼承办两道科改之两人，以羽纱裹首，缚之数匝，携手步层楼，竟夜跃然曰："得之矣！"乃增小轮一规，并拨易发条数处，夷官所写已成清汉合璧。谓智出于脑，须缚之急，乃能构思，何其神也。又见芸台中丞作马脑草虫百种，藏一柜中。如今药笼百眼箱式，大如蟾蜍，小如蟋蟀，无不须眉毕具，灵动如生。

    Explanation

    Three Strange Notes Volume Three
    Western Ingenious Devices

    During the seventieth birthday of Emperor Gaozong, blessings were offered universally, and high officials were forbidden from presenting gold and jade. Governor Li Beipin of Guangdong presented a set of self-operating devices from foreigners, imitating the intention of Yan Shi. The box was slightly over a foot wide and a bit taller. Opening its lock, a gray-haired woman emerged from the door, hesitantly re-entering, and then carried out a chair and a table. The table had many dishes, and all stationery was prepared. After the setup was complete, a blue-eyed foreign official boldly came to sit down. The woman ground ink and spread paper, and the blue-eyed person wrote the four characters "May your reign last forever." The woman presented a cup of tea, which the foreign official drank, then stood up and entered the box. The woman checked everything and then entered the box, and the door closed with a clunk. Later, Governor Li presented it, and the emperor used it for official documents, which was very appropriate. Two officials from the Two Roads Office were called to modify it. They wrapped their heads with feathered silk and tied it several times, walking hand in hand on the upper floors, excitedly saying, "We've got it!" They then added a small wheel and adjusted several springs, and the foreign official's writing became a combination of Chinese and Manchu. They believed intelligence comes from the brain, and it must be tightly bound to think. How miraculous it is! Also, the Vice Minister of the Ministry of Rites created a hundred kinds of insect carvings from coral, stored in a cabinet. Like a medicine box with a hundred compartments, some as large as toads and some as small as crickets, all with complete features and lifelike.

    118

    先以氍毹铺桌，柜背走线一拽，百种皆跳跃而出，缤纷满架，尚作蠕蠕欲动状。复振其机，则仍尽入柜，门亦自阖矣。识者谓此本木牛流马之遗，今四海昇平，无所适用，仅为耳目之玩，足发洴澼纩之叹。又见穆庵都转处睹验晴雨器，将晴针左旋，将雨针右旋，百不一失。验寒暖器尤异，格中有物如黍粒，暖则下垂，寒则上缩，不知何药，是复以人巧夺天工也。又如各种镜法，远者能近，近者能远，大者可小，小者可大，备极狡狯。至温镜一法，使寸穗之焰，满室生春，更为奇绝。他若筋斗小儿、劝酒美女，止供婴孩戏剧，尤不足道。然皆其苗裔，惟自来火枪，发虽便捷，而中的终不及火绳之准。又水龙用羊肠，虽可曲折如意，无间楼阁，然激水倒泻，难比鹤颈之得力，此又可悟巧不如拙之一证也，予因是而于西法之舍弧矢而用三角，亦窃有疑焉。

    Explanation

    118

    First, lay a fur rug on the table, pull a string on the back of the cabinet, and hundreds of things leap out, colorful and full on the shelves, still in a wriggling, about-to-move state. Then activate its mechanism, and they all return to the cabinet, with the door closing by itself. Those who understand say this is a legacy of the wooden ox and flowing horse; now that the world is at peace, it has no practical use, only for the enjoyment of sight and hearing, sufficient to evoke a sigh like that of the man who could only weave mats. At the Mu'an Pavilion, one can see the device for predicting the weather, with the needle turning left for clear weather and right for rain, never failing in a hundred trials. The device for measuring cold and heat is especially remarkable, with something inside like a grain of millet, dropping when warm and contracting when cold, though it is unknown what kind of medicine it is, this is again the work of human ingenuity surpassing nature's craftsmanship. Also, various mirror techniques, far things appear near, near things appear far, large things can appear small, small things can appear large, extremely ingenious and clever. As for the method of the warm mirror, making a small flame fill the room with spring, even more extraordinary. Others, like acrobatic children and wine-serving beauties, only for the entertainment of children, especially unworthy of mention. But all are descendants of these inventions, only the self-igniting gun, its firing is convenient, but its accuracy in hitting the target is not as good as the matchlock. Also, the water dragon uses a sheep intestine, though it can be bent to one's will without hindrance by buildings, the force of the water rushing back is not as effective as the swan's neck, this is again a proof that cleverness is not always better than simplicity. I therefore consider the Western method of abandoning the bow and arrow for the use of triangles, I have some doubts about it.

    百风子
    　　　湖府之长兴，有小家女，不为强暴所污，慷慨自缢，邑令甘肃邢君审得实情，照例拟绞。郡守善，惑于劣幕之言，谓强奸并无证见，缢时已越三日，欲活狡童，改拟轻减。时菊溪师陈臬阅案大愠，驳饬强奸安得有证见，有证见，即不能奸矣。至迟死之故，或缘冤苦未诉，或以守护难行，今矫揉若此，非受贿狥情而何！奸者已杀其躯，谳者更污其节，罪在尤狂且上，必当参办。初仲侍坐时，纵言至二千石贤能，师甚夸湖州操守，询仲信否，仲应曰信，第性多偏僻，亦是一病，师应曰："廉者必狷，气质未化耳。

    A Woman Named Bai Fengzi

    In the town of Changxing under the Lake Prefecture, there was a girl from a humble family. She chose to hang herself rather than be defiled by a violent assault, acting with noble resolve. The county magistrate, Mr. Xing of Gansu, investigated the matter and confirmed the truth of her actions, proposing the usual punishment of hanging according to precedent. The prefect, however, was misled by the words of a low-ranking official, claiming that there was no evidence of rape and that it had been three days since her death, wanting to save the cunning youth involved, and thus proposed a lighter sentence. At the time, Teacher Ju Xi and Official Chen Niece, upon reviewing the case, were greatly angered. They criticized and ordered that how could rape have evidence; with evidence, it cannot be rape. They also questioned the reason for the delayed death, suggesting that it might be due to unjust suffering not yet reported or because it was difficult to protect her. Now, twisting and bending like this, what else could it be but accepting bribes and favoring personal feelings! The rapist has already killed her body, and the judge further defiles her virtue. The crime lies especially in the case of the extremely mad and must be investigated and punished. When Chū Zhòng was sitting in attendance, they spoke freely up to the excellent officials of the rank of two thousand stones. The teacher greatly praised the integrity of Huzhou and asked whether Chū Zhòng believed it. Chū Zhòng responded, saying yes, but noted that his nature is often biased, which is also a flaw. The teacher responded, saying, "The honest must be narrow-minded, their temperament has not been transformed."

    "至是谓仲曰："汝言不谬，然岂止偏僻，直倒行而逆施，乌乎可？"仲曰："善守诚误，然渠素有风子之名，师申宪令，而首及狂夫，无乃太亵？"师意少解，故曰："汝不闻都中人亦呼余为百风子乎？"翌日，上院抚宪送司道，至巡捕厅值房，且行且语，已出大堂，菊师植立曰："大人慈祥，慎于白简，龄责在纠参，不得不迳尘天听矣！"旁观悚然，袁观察更为吐舌。芸台先生满面春风，趋前握手曰："断不至此，老前辈尊见已定，晚无不追随。"第事宽则据详径咨，该守断无掣肘也，师亦不觉意消。回署旅见时，谓仲曰："湖守不足惜，吾感中丞之和衷，不得不屈己以从。

    草衣道人
    　　　明季多奇女子，若柳是之殉节保家、方芷之相夫死国，次之则李香之却币洁身、玉京之潜使入道，皆可入《青泥莲花记》，然终不如草衣道人之绝伦拔萃者。道人从先黄门为女记室，奉太夫人命随侍入都，值魏珰初用事，杨忠烈疏上，留中未发，黄门纠同刊继之。道人计祸必烈，不言负太夫人，乃于嘱缮疏稿时，以滷和墨。熹宗尸位，疏辍数月不阅，时经溽暑，进御已腐不可揭，乃以他事放归。归未几，蓼洲忠介公约黄门偕往虎邱，毁珰生祠，宿于家荣寿堂三夕，谋既定，买舟鑿行。太夫人年已九十，闻自起尼之，逾阈仆，折其一齿。道人进曰："已矣，在朝则君为重，在野则亲为先，太夫人耄耋，亦不欲作滂母也。"忠介乃辞公独行。未几烈皇嗣统，珰难既平，起公都谏，复以为乌程媢嫉，与文起孩未诸君同被逐，道人复谏公曰："君方火烈，臣尽披靡，衮衮诸公，皆一邱之貉，堂堂七尺何必虚捐？"公遂闭门不出，筑小桃源以避世。

    Explanation

    123

    The Grass-Cloth Daoist

    During the late Ming dynasty, there were many extraordinary women. Some, like Liu Shi who died to protect her family and country, and Fang Zhi who died with her husband for the nation, were notable. Others, such as Li Xiang who rejected bribes and maintained her integrity, and Yu Jing who secretly entered the Daoist order, were also worthy of mention. All of these women could be recorded in the Qingni Lotus Record, but none were as unparalleled and outstanding as the Grass-Cloth Daoist. She served as a female secretary to the former grand secretary and followed the orders of her grandmother to accompany her into the capital. When Wei Zhongxian, a notorious eunuch, first gained power, Yang Zhonglie, a loyal official, submitted a memorial, which was kept in the palace without being issued. The grand secretary joined in to publish a follow-up memorial. Considering the impending disaster, the Grass-Cloth Daoist did not speak ill of her grandmother. Instead, she mixed salt with the ink when she was instructed to prepare the memorial draft. Emperor Xizong, a figurehead ruler, left the memorial unread for several months. During the hot summer, the memorial had rotted and could not be opened, so it was released back home under the pretext of other matters. Shortly after returning, Liu Zhi, a loyal and upright official, invited the grand secretary to go to Huxi together to destroy the temple built for Wei Zhongxian. They stayed at the family's honor hall for three nights, and once the plan was decided, they bought a boat and set off. The grandmother, who was already ninety years old, heard about it and got up to stop them, but she fell over the threshold and broke one of her teeth. The Grass-Cloth Daoist said, "It is done. In court, the ruler is paramount; in the countryside, the family comes first. The grandmother is old and frail; I do not want to be in a situation like Yu Pang's mother." Liu Zhi then declined the grand secretary's invitation and went alone. Soon after, Emperor Chongzhen ascended the throne, and the troubles with Wei Zhongxian were resolved. The grand secretary was appointed as a censor, but he was again accused of jealousy and envy and exiled along with Wen Qi and others. The Grass-Cloth Daoist advised him, "You are at the height of your power, and I will follow suit. The many officials in power are all the same, and with a height of seven feet, why waste your life in vain?" The grand secretary then closed his door and did not leave, building a small Peach Blossom Spring to avoid the world.

    甲申之变，太夫人尚寿考，道人奉缁衣以进曰："此公忠孝两全之策也。"后南都再建，起公光禄寺少卿，不起，曰："我不为乌程屈，肯为贵阳役乎！"初公与虞山雅善，虞山晚节不臧，阿附马阮，欲引公自助，再四通书，公不答。道人礼诘蘼燕君曰："尚书终始参差，已成小草，重负阿姊，今复濡首下泉，昂友入谷，家公坚白不渝，岂为腐鼠吓也。"明亡，筑小庵下发，岁时至家一省太夫人而已。李夫人自九十七考终，公亦七十矣。

    The fall of Beijing in 1644, the elderly woman still enjoyed longevity. The monk presented a robe and said, "This is a strategy that achieves both public loyalty, filial piety, and filial loyalty." After the Southern capital was rebuilt, he was appointed as the Vice Minister of the Imperial Household, but he refused, saying, "I will not bend for Wucheng, how can I serve for Guiyang!" Initially, he was close friends with Yushan, but Yushan's later years were dishonorable, flattering Ma and Ruan, wanting to bring him in to assist, sending letters multiple times, but he did not respond. The monk questioned Mí Yàn Jūn, saying, "The Chancellor's actions were inconsistent, already like a small grass, heavily burdening the elder sister, now wetting the head and descending into the depths, raising a friend and entering the valley, the father-in-law remains firm and unchanging, how can he be intimidated by a rotten mouse?" After the fall of the Ming Dynasty, he built a small hermitage and shaved his head, visiting home at regular intervals to see the elderly woman once. Li's wife died at the age of ninety-seven, and he was also seventy years old.

    125

    本朝康熙中，征江苏遗臣十六人，以原官起用，公以逃禅免，事载《明史》。姚甥椿有过南村草堂，感弔霞城给事七律云："残荷犹被半池幽，曾溯前贤屐齿留。子姓清贫洲橘灭，宾朋寥落墅棋收。全家净土皈黄面，四海新知笑白头。可惜蓬瀛名士少，一虁空遣汙清流。"前贤指忠介，末句谓鹤沙，以己丑庶常归，公斥之不使见也。公葬横港，去墓二十步即草衣道人从葬坟，子孙岁岁奉瓣香焉，遗像尚存仲处，便服，面微黄，憔悴有病容，知为入道后所写。闻前有董思翁题语，今已亡失，思翁黄门朱陈戚。

    125

    During the reign of Emperor Kangxi in the early Qing dynasty, sixteen former officials from Jiangsu were recruited and reappointed to their original positions. However, the public (or the person in question) was exempted due to his retreat into monastic life, and this event is recorded in the History of Ming. Yao's nephew Chun visited the Nan Village Grass Hut and expressed his feelings and paid tribute to Xiacity's Censor with a seven-character regulated verse: "Withered lotuses still adorn the half-pond with their secluded beauty, once tracing the footprints of past sages. The descendants are poor, and the citrus orchards have vanished; guests are few, and the chessboards have been put away. The whole family has turned to Buddhism, becoming monks; friends from all over the world laugh at my white hair. It is regrettable that there are few famous scholars in the mythical lands of Penglai and Yingzhou; a single gourd cup (or person) is sent to pollute the clear stream." The past sages referred to here are Zhongjie, and the last line refers to Hesh, who returned as a scholar-official in the year Jichou. The public (or the person in question) rejected him and did not allow him to see him. The public (or the person in question) was buried in Henggang, and twenty steps away from the tomb is the burial site of Caoyi Dao Ren, who was buried alongside him. Descendants offer incense every year, and the portrait still exists in Zhong's place. It depicts the person in casual attire, with a slightly yellow complexion, appearing frail and ill, indicating that it was drawn after he entered the monastic life. It is said that there were inscriptions by Dong Siweng before, but they have now been lost. Dong Siweng was a former official of the Yellow Gate and was related to Zhu and Chen by marriage.

    濮童
    　　　嘉庆丙子，予署篆永嘉，值江北徧灾，流民就食者载道。广陵颇多姻戚，欲询彼地情形，适见一幼童，因呼而问之。见余，长揖不拜，虽选县跣足短褐，而端谨可念，。问其姓，曰濮，问其籍，曰全椒，问其年，曰十。问何以来此，曰："家止山田一顷，丰年仅可足食，本年干旱无获，仅刈谷四十余石。一祖母，年将八十，胞伯亦诸生，已六十，偕妻待养，半菽不饱，故其父挈细小就食江南，流传至浙右也。"与之食，辞，诘之，曰："父母咽山蓣兼旬矣，不忍独饫膏梁。"乃为箪食与肉，置诸橐以遗之，出则授其母，分饷之乃食尽，甚彬彬也。予饬料理资送毕，独唤童入，劳以青蚨二百，拜而襭之襟，曰："出以奉母，童子无私藏也。此间舟夫预备所得口粮，日给一日，幸尚可不馁，以备不虞耳。

    Explanation

    126

    In the year Jiaqing, the third year of the Jiaqing era (1796), I was temporarily in charge of Yongjia. At that time, the northern regions were suffering from widespread famine, and refugees seeking food filled the roads. Guangling had many relatives, and I wanted to inquire about the situation there. I happened to see a young boy and called him over to ask about it. When he saw me, he bowed deeply without kneeling, showing great respect despite his simple attire. He was dignified and worthy of admiration. I asked his surname, and he said "Pu." I asked his hometown, and he said "Quanjiao." I asked his age, and he said "ten." I asked why he was there, and he replied: "Our family has only one hillside field, which barely yields enough to feed us in a good year. This year, due to drought, we harvested only over forty shi of grain. We have a grandmother who is nearly eighty years old, an uncle who is a scholar and is sixty years old, and his wife, who is waiting to be supported. They barely have enough to eat. Therefore, my father took the younger ones to seek food in Jiangnan, and we have spread to the right of Zhejiang."

    I offered him some food, but he declined. I questioned him further, and he said: "My parents have not eaten for over twenty days, so I cannot enjoy rich food alone." I then gave him a simple meal of rice and meat, placed it in his bag, and he gave it to his mother when he left. They shared it until it was finished. He was very courteous and well-mannered.

    After arranging for the necessary provisions, I called the boy in and gave him 200 cash coins. He bowed and tucked them into his jacket, saying: "I will give it to my mother. I have no private hoard. The boatmen here have prepared daily rations, so we will not go hungry, and we are prepared for any unforeseen circumstances."

    "予曰："吾为若先驰一溜子，俾下站亦无稽滞，何如？"仍长揖以谢，甚肃，且曰："今虽得归，未知能得安故土、长幼团聚否？"予应之曰："圣天子轸念民瘼，饬有司裕赈，济贷滋种，归里无不得所者。"童虽不解嵩呼，然意殊欣欣，若甚感恩者。时蒋峨峰太守尚未有子，闻而奇之，呼与语，大悦，欲养为假子，父母皆喜诺，童子不可，乃止。语仲曰："良知良能，孩提天性，至其不厌贫贱、不慕富贵，又居然圣童矣。"第眉宇间殊大秀慧，试以字，识亦未见了了，诚可谓礼失而将求诸野也。峨峰为虎臣先生曾孙，家世好施，乃捐三千金，市山蓣一巨舫，由海道运入南徐以助赈，且作书告戚好曰："某听濮童子言，如见郑监门《流民图》，寄语乡里，忍饥力穑，慎勿散而之四方也。"予谓濮童，一村竖耳，一念之孝，足上感太守，峨峰先生即以一念之仁应之，惠且及一郡，使数万家咸被其泽。仁人之言，其利溥哉！孝弟也者，其为仁之本欤。

    周厚基
    　　　天马山周君厚基，肖廉之族，予曾至其家，见密室中奉一栗主，祀讷公亲，旁以进士武进族兄某配焉。问之，叹息曰："基少年不慎，几遭法网，幸圣世宽仁，幸逃显戮，维族兄独任之，讷公曲贷之，四十年皆余生也，欲同袍共为殷鉴焉。"基弱冠入都，以雕花乳及璧巢书供奉怡府。世宗皇帝与怡贤亲王最睦，故小王嗣封垺于皇子，一切关税盐课均厚给焉，豫省天津河东淮北画疆而食。南汝光一路本隸河东，淮商谋攘焉，课为怡府所辖，浼朝贵请之，不可；再祈和府请之，仍不可。王一日谓幕下士曰："此脂膏地，我岂肯代人作箸，不然亦何分左右袒也。"基夙与商伙稔，露其意，欣然曰："正苦无路！"合资二十万营干此件，贮金陵客寓，事旦就，则金夕辇耳，乃因二宦者通于王，王颔之。将报商伙，族兄笑曰："未也，王不云乎我不代人作箸。

    Zhou Houji
    　　　Zhou Houji, a gentleman from Tianma Mountain, belongs to the Xiao clan. I once visited his home and saw in a secret room a wooden tablet inscribed with the name of his ancestors, which he worshiped. Beside it was a cousin who had passed the imperial examination in Wujin. When I asked him about it, he sighed and said, "In my youth, I was careless and nearly fell into the legal net. Fortunately, in this benevolent era, I was spared from public execution. My cousin took full responsibility, and my ancestors showed mercy. For forty years, I have lived, and I wish to share this lesson with my comrades as a profound warning." At the age of twenty, Zhou Houji entered the capital and served in the Prince of Yide's household, presenting him with ornate items and books. Emperor Yongzheng was very close to Prince Yide, so the prince's status was equivalent to that of a prince, and all customs duties and salt taxes were generously provided. The region of Henan, Tianjin, the eastern and northern parts of the Yellow and Huai rivers, and the southern and northern parts of the Huai river were all under the prince's jurisdiction. The merchants from the Huai region planned to take over the southern and northern parts of the Huai river, but the taxes were under the control of the Prince of Yide. They asked a high-ranking official to request it, but it was denied; they then asked the Prince of Yide directly, but it was still denied. One day, the prince told his attendants, "This fertile land, I would not act as someone else's agent, nor would I take sides." Zhou Houji had long been familiar with the merchants and disclosed the prince's words to them. They were delighted and said, "We have been struggling to find a way!" They jointly invested twenty thousand taels to undertake this matter, storing the money in a guesthouse in Nanjing. If the matter was done by morning, the money would be transported by evening. They then used two eunuchs to convey the matter to the prince, who agreed. When Zhou Houji was about to inform the merchants, his cousin laughed and said, "Not yet, the prince didn't say that I wouldn't act as someone else's agent."

    今二十万王已纳之，我二人何以自润？乃告商伙事可定，但府中总管档房及一切费用尚须加。"二伙曰："诺。"但金不齐，即遣急足取之南中，往返十余日耳。第三和邸访闻，面奏，得旨讷公查办，提商鞫之，商与基昵，且愤族兄之以加索败事也，独讦之。兄支吾间，呐谓之曰："王知汝亦死，王不知汝亦死；介两人汝亦死，介一人汝亦死，丈夫作事，何用此伈伈伣伣者为！"案遂定，兄遂见法，王以不知，罚俸一年，毙二太监于杖。稽拙修闻知，遣仆护出彰义门，密札云："幸十年无问长安道也。"和王薧逝，始敢上馆，今隔卅年，都人已无知其事者，然基感之，终不忘，故祀之，若族兄则悼其同肇衅而独受祸耳。后予在金陵，淮商欲改浦口口岸，倩族侄兆原恳予乞恩制府，予谢之，群谓循理乘势，何吝一言，予举往事告之，且笑曰："无使为周君齿冷也。"

    Now that the twenty million has been accepted by the king, how can we two enrich ourselves? We informed the merchants that the matter could be settled, but the expenses for the household manager and all other costs still needed to be added. The two merchants replied, "Yes." If the money is not ready, immediately send a swift messenger to fetch it from the southern regions, which will take over ten days. The third and fourth princes heard of this and reported it in person, receiving an edict for Nei to investigate. A man does his deeds, why should you be so timid and fickle!" The case was thus settled, and the brother was executed. The king, unaware, was fined a year's salary, and two eunuchs were beaten to death. Ji Zhuoxiu heard of this and sent a servant to escort him out of the Changle Gate, secretly writing, "May you be spared from the troubles of Chang'an for ten years." After the death of Prince He, he dared to return home. Now, thirty years have passed, and the people of the capital no longer know of this matter, but Ji remained grateful and never forgot, so he worshipped him. As for his clan brother, he mourned him for starting the trouble and yet being the only one to suffer.     五星
    　　　五星之术，达者辟之，第诚能穷其奥窍则亦有灼然不爽者。晓岚先生五种所记颇多，若东山宗伯之不验而验，验而不验，则最异，均载《阅微草堂笔记》，纪公亦有术者告之一生贵显，而不能作相。后协办令下，数日薧。得天司寇自占己造，事事不爽，惟寿多一年，五十三乃殁。王孝廉青联占沈助教坤云仅得教授，惟于五月某日引见，可用主事，分部必西曹，悉验，四命不符，而争权于一日已奇，至丁未甄别，仍改教职尤奇。王史亭编修，予祖姑丈，素精星命，乙巳春，因眷属南还，招予迁寓，与表兄盛孝廉侍坐，谈饮甚乐。至三月中，忽欲乞假南归，盛尼之，不可；倩稷堂、璞堂两先生尼之，亦不可。

    The Study of the Five Planets
    　　　The study of the five planets, though avoided by the wise, can indeed yield clear and accurate results if one truly understands its mysteries. Mr. Xiaolan, in his "Five Records," documented many such cases. For instance, there was the case of Dongshan Zongbo, whose predictions initially seemed invalid but later proved true, and vice versa—a most extraordinary phenomenon. All these accounts are recorded in the "Yue Wei Cao Tang Bi Ji." Even Mr. Ji Yun, a renowned scholar, was told by a fortune-teller that he would achieve high status but not become a chancellor. After receiving an order to serve as an assistant to the chancellor, he passed away a few days later. Tian Shikou, a judge, accurately predicted his own life, with only his lifespan being one year longer than predicted, and he died at the age of fifty-three. Wang Qinglian predicted that Shen Kuncun, a teaching assistant, would only become a professor, but he would be introduced on a certain day in May, appointed as an official, and assigned to the Western Department—all of which came true. However, four out of the five predictions were incorrect, and the fact that they all came true on the same day was still remarkable. Finally, during the year of Dingwei, Shen Kuncun was demoted back to a teaching position, which was particularly unusual.

    Wang Shiting, a revisionist and my maternal grandfather, was always skilled in astrology and fortune-telling. In the spring of the year 1775 (the year of the rabbit in the Chinese zodiac), because his family was moving south, he invited me to move into his residence. We spent a pleasant evening together with my cousin, Sheng Qinglian, discussing and drinking. In mid-March, Wang Qinglian suddenly wanted to take leave and return south. Sheng Qinglian tried to dissuade him, but he refused. Even Ji Tang and Pu Tang, two other scholars, tried to dissuade him, but he still refused.

    予乃委转白曰："公在四库馆最久，议叙班名已首列，若一抽身，资虽不移，而俸已在后，非计也。且前月越次放吴蓉塘，而公以不得引退，人且议公鞅鞅。"公乃蹙然曰："此非若所知，予自占星度，今年中秋日有难，星入某垣某度中，伤及命主，故惎之。"予慰之曰："命之理微，亦不甚可泥。"公曰："不然，予详度再三，无可解免，绍公师亦嘱予避之。计惟去官祷之，以冀延算，得渡此缺陷，尚可登四品也。"抵家颇安健，然骨见衣表，知者虑之。中秋家宴，感寒小疾，寻至不起。官身外物也，安足与命抗衡哉！盛孝廉尊人亦精此术，决孝廉甲午必售，夜半至港口，亲招报船，予笑谯之，应曰："若是科不捷，则汝表兄终身白蜡矣，故迫而出此也。"呆状可掬。惟二吴最不信此，闻史亭先生讯，叹曰："魔已中心，宜其及也。"
