    豪博
    　　　《南史》称宋太祖樗蒲一掷百万，以今准之不过千金耳，未免为今世博徒所笑。嘉庆乙丑，予以养疴寄居张甥长庚所，与长庚妇翁盛君狎，盛君告予家事无隐。一日予妹及甥媳辈于闺中戏选仙图，盛顾而叹曰："此花骨头唐丧予不小！"为述数年前丧其独子，族中无俚，辄以立后嬲之，且悲且愤，思倾产以绝觊觎，因与狎客纵博，半年博负七万金。同博者为之筹画，十偿以六，且准薄田折阅，计捐亩千五百余，已了此未完生平第一便宜事。予笑如此便宜，愿兄不必再占，然积累颇久，犹不及顾君宾臣一夕十万也。宾臣小厓侍读，八十外所举幼子，以四库馆誊录在京寓江南客寓，与辈下诸豪士习，岁首相聚，辄投琼较彩。顾好且擅，自正月至四月，百日中得博进十二万金，贮卧室高柜，皆精鏐，足兑无折色，无短平。浴佛日博徒皆聚顾窝，作长夜之戏，独是日大负，一败涂地。

    Explanation

    132

    Gambling

    The Nan Shi (History of the Southern Dynasties) recounts that Emperor Taizu of Song wagered a hundred million on a single throw of the dice, but by modern standards, it was no more than a thousand gold coins, hardly worthy of the laughter of today's gamblers. In the year Jiaqing Yichou (1805), I was convalescing and staying at my nephew Zhang Changgeng's place, where I became acquainted with his father-in-law, Mr. Sheng, who shared no secrets with me. One day, while my sister and my nephew's wife were playing a game of selecting a fairy in the inner chambers, Sheng looked around and sighed, "This gambling cost me dearly!" He recounted how a few years prior, he had lost his only son, and the family, being childless, was persistently pressured to adopt a son. Filled with both grief and anger, he decided to exhaust his wealth to prevent any further coveting. Thus, he engaged in gambling with his close friends, and within half a year, he lost seven million gold coins. His fellow gamblers helped him devise a plan: they repaid six out of every ten, and he allowed the sale of some poor land to settle the debt, donating over fifteen hundred acres of land, thus resolving what he considered the most significant and advantageous matter of his life. I laughed and told him that such an advantage was not worth repeating, but despite the long accumulation, it still fell short of Gu Binchen's winnings of ten million gold coins in a single night. Gu Binchen, a young scholar serving as a reader in the Four Treasuries Office, was the son of a man in his eighties, living in a guesthouse in Jiangnan while working in the capital. He associated with various wealthy and influential men, and every year they would gather to play dice games. Gu was both skilled and proficient, and from January to April, in just a hundred days, he won twelve million gold coins, which he stored in a high cabinet in his bedroom. All the coins were gold, sufficient to exchange without loss in value, and without small change. On Buddha's birthday, all the gamblers gathered at Gu's place, engaging in all-night games, but on this day, he suffered a significant loss, utterly defeated and ruined.

    133

    至天明，固始祝编修在坐曰："顾君资已罄，再博再负亦无以偿，不如且已。"明日白华京兆闻之，严斥之，又代搜其橐，尚万余金。摒挡报满上库，得补北城指挥，豪纵益盛。三年荐陟霸州牧，霸固冲繁，又不善经理，且肩积亏，不数载负帑且十万，已登白简，例当立决，而顾尚夷然。京兆谯之，竟是痴儿意，谓尚可一掷偿也。乃与赵砚怀谋，乘查封时具呈枢府，备陈奉职无状，不特辜负天恩，而且隳堕先德，先臣入值书房，高宗在藩邸赏赉书画颇多，今既不敢藏匿，更不敢同籍没诸物一体造册，敬谨另单封恭候呈缴。仁宗览之恻然，乃于狱上时得改长系，数年竟卒于狱，得保首领焉。夫以名臣子弟，不自检束，啖于刑辟，著之可为炯戒。至葺城诸君子景仰前徽，委转护持，全其后嗣，可入《宋人厚德录》。独圣天子之眷念甘盘，不惜屈法以全其子，侍讲有知，亦当衔涕。惜现镪十万不以偿帑亏，而以偿博负，真为盛四兄笑耳。刘毅虽俊，幸无不善学之。

    133

    Until dawn, the editor from Gushi, Zhu, was present and said, "Gu's resources are already exhausted; gambling and incurring debt again will not allow him to repay, it would be better not to continue." The next day, Baihua, the Prefect of Jingzhao, heard of it and severely rebuked him, and also searched his bag on his behalf, finding still more than ten thousand coins. He handled the matter, reported it fully to the treasury, and was appointed as the commander of the northern city, becoming even more reckless and extravagant. After three years, he was recommended for promotion to the governor of Bazhou. Bazhou is naturally busy and complex, and he was also poor at managing it, shouldering accumulated losses. Within a few years, he owed the treasury more than ten thousand, and had already been recorded in the official records of punishment, according to precedent he should have been immediately executed, but Gu remained calm. The Prefect of Jingzhao rebuked him, saying it was still the mind of a fool, thinking he could still repay with one final gamble. Then he consulted with Zhao Yanhuai, taking advantage of the time of confiscation to submit a petition to the central government, detailing his failure in his duties, not only betraying the grace of heaven but also ruining the virtue of ancestors. His late father served in the imperial library, and during the time he was a prince, Emperor Gaozong received many gifts of paintings and calligraphy. Now that he dare not hide them, he also dare not include them among the confiscated items in the inventory, respectfully sealing them separately and awaiting presentation and submission. Emperor Renzong read it with compassion and at the time of sentencing was able to transfer him to a long-term confinement. After several years, he finally died in prison, was able to keep his head. As for the son of a famous minister, not restraining himself, indulging in punishment, recorded, can serve as a warning. As for the gentlemen of Qicheng who admired the legacy of the past, entrusted to protect and support, preserving his descendants, can be included in The Book of the Benevolence of Song People. Only the sage emperor's cherishing of Gangan, sparing no effort to bend the law to save his son, if the Attendant Teacher knew, would also hold tears in. Regret that ten thousand current coins were not used to repay the treasury's loss, but to repay gambling debts, really making Sheng's fourth brother laugh. Liu Yi is talented, fortunately did not learn the wrong things.

    　　　运司鼓搂故雄敞，闻乾隆初有鹾贾程某，以肩债太多，暂避于此，孤寂无聊，凭拦静眺。逡巡至夜半，忽闻复有声橐橐然登梯者，睇之，则同业吴某，惊讯曰："君何为亦来此？"吴亦讯曰："君何为先在此？"程曰："吾今岁逋负四万，无以应付，故隐此。君本厚利广，何以亦来？"吴曰："吾今岁未了须十万金，今摒挡仅及其半，与甲则漏乙，给丁则缺丙，剖分无术，故匿此以待来年。"程曰："与君作伴，守岁良佳。

    134

    Donating Gold to Receive a Reward

    The drum tower of the salt administration, once grand and imposing, was where Cheng, a salt merchant, took refuge in the early years of the Qianlong era. Overwhelmed by his mounting debts, he sought solace in this place, feeling lonely and aimless as he leaned against the railing and gazed out into the night. Wandering until midnight, he suddenly heard the sound of footsteps climbing the stairs. Looking up, he saw Wu, a fellow salt merchant, and was startled. Wu asked, "Why are you here too?" Cheng replied, "I am here because I owe four thousand taels of silver and cannot pay it back. Why are you here?" Wu responded, "I am here because I need ten thousand taels of silver by the end of the year, but I can only manage half of it. If I give to A, I miss B, and if I give to D, I lack C. I have no way to divide it, so I am hiding here until next year." Cheng said, "It would be good to have company while waiting out the year."

    135

    "吴曰："不然，吾有金五万在家，自用则不足，济君则有余，何不假吾金去，尽可归家料理。"即作票付程，程即驰去，俄倾复来，并载酒肴，酌吴曰："吾嘱伙料理，今乃真可伴君守岁矣！"两君皆徽籍，程更良贾，工心计，是岁以海运遭风，至大折阅，兹仗吴接济，得不废业。明岁即夤缘抡办甲务，甚著猷为，名几与江广达亚。吴遂援同事，亦仍复故业，今其子孙尚为巨商，然皆光复故物耳。若李抚民之捐三千金，而陡发数百万，则获报尤奢焉。李即金衢道秉铨之父，豫章窭人子，以买笔来往粤西，粤西鹾贾某赏其勤慎，荐为商伙。阅数载，积资三千余金，因谋归娶。

    Wu said, "Not so. I have five ten-thousand pieces of gold at home; for personal use it is insufficient, but to help you there is more than enough. Why not borrow my gold to go, and you can fully go home to handle matters?" He immediately wrote out a note and gave it to Cheng, who then rushed off. Shortly, he returned, carrying wine and food, and pouring wine to Wu, he said, "I instructed the staff to handle matters, and now truly you can accompany me to guard the year!" Both gentlemen were from Anhui, and Cheng was a skilled merchant, good at planning and strategy. That year, due to a maritime venture encountering wind, he suffered a significant loss, but now relying on Wu's assistance, he was able to continue his career. The following year, through connections, he handled important matters, achieving great success, and his fame almost rivaled Jiang Guangda and others. Wu then assisted his colleagues, returning to their old careers, and today their descendants are still major merchants, though they have restored their former possessions. As for Li Fumin's donation of three thousand gold pieces, which led to a sudden acquisition of several million, he received an especially extravagant reward. Li Fumin was the father of Jinqu Dao Bingquan, a poor son from Yuzhang who traveled to Guangxi to sell brushes. A salt merchant from Guangxi commended his diligence and caution, recommending him as a merchant's assistant. After several years, he accumulated over three thousand gold pieces and planned to return home to marry.

    136

    Already weary from ferry crossings, the village had achieved a modest prosperity. So, he bought a boat and sailed to the Li River, where he found himself near an official boat. He heard a long sigh and continuous lament, and remained awake all night. He asked his servants, who said, "The owner is registered in the Eight Banners and was appointed as the governor of a prefecture in Zhili. He was sent here for duty and last winter temporarily took charge of Xilong. Unfortunately, there was a disaster, and he lost half a million taels of treasury funds. The successor refuses to take responsibility, and he will be reported to the censorate, which is why he is so anxious." Li was moved and said, "I am willing to offer my services, how about it?" The owner immediately invited him in and said, "I am Ming, I am here to settle accounts with the provincial authorities. I heard you can help me with this, which is fortunate!"     Ming immediately formed an alliance with him through incense and fire, arranging themselves in a line like geese flying in formation, and said, "Brother, you have just arrived in Guangdong and truly have no acquaintances. At that time, the salt administration was neglected, and merchants were abolished and pursued. Li handled the situation with ease, being familiar with the work, and managed it in a neat and orderly manner. Within a few years, his wealth had grown to tens of thousands, and over thirty years, he became the richest in the province. He then married in Guangdong and built a separate estate. Whenever he encountered people from Yuzhang who traveled to western Guangdong, he would always help them, saying, "I cannot forget the time of my humble beginnings with a single umbrella and a single cloth bundle!" Those in power who were stuck or stagnant would entrust him with messages, and he would always respond by saying, "I have no way to repay Ming; this is why I remember it." Li had eight sons, many of whom followed precedent to enter officialdom. His eldest grandson also passed the top examination and served as an official in the Ministry of Justice. The eighth son held the position of official selection, and along with the ninth son, both donated to become administrative officials. He finally passed away at nearly ninety years old.

    Yuan Er, the Man of Administrative Talent

    Mr. Yuan Er, known for his administrative talent, was recommended from his position as an assistant magistrate and promoted to a high-ranking official. He served for forty years, enduring all the hardships and joys. With each promotion, even those who envied him had nothing to say against him, as his advancements were not due to military achievements or the favor of the powerful. Initially, he was appointed as a county magistrate due to his involvement in the completion of the Yongle Encyclopedia. High-ranking officials saw his skill in calligraphy and familiarity with official documents, and assigned him to the sea dike project. His colleagues included Chongyao, a state magistrate; Lin, a county magistrate; and Taiceng, an official. Serving as a high-ranking official in Suzhou, he was diligent in governing. It was the twenty-eighth day of the twelfth lunar month, and he sent a servant to check if anyone was in the office. Upon arrival, the servant only saw Yuan sitting alone with a writing brush. The servant reported back, asking about the amount of treasury funds disbursed and the expenses incurred this year.

    Grasshopper Yao was strong and stubborn.

    So he sent many laborers to capture him/her, and the person still vented his/her rage, shouting angrily and using a stick. Again, they went to report, and Fu also did not get angry, saying, "Robbery and fighting, military regulations should naturally be stricter, but order the gatekeeper to urgently select replacements." After several days, when they moved camp, the carriage was already driven but the servants did not gather. Strictly supervising them, they surrounded and knelt, begging for mercy, saying, "The laborers risked their lives to run around, originally only to serve the noble person, now all the attendants can be executed, the laborers fear there will be no survivors, let the general decide." Fu blushed and immediately asked who killed the laborer, as before, saying, "Yao Lingyi did it, and Yang Kui has nothing to do with it." Fu said, "Why didn't you tell me?" They replied, "Trivial matters involving low-status people, how dare we offend you?" Fu, reluctantly, said, "Blaming him/her is certainly appropriate, but killing him/her was excessive."

    144

    "遂撤一如总理，时已保升川东道，摺已缮，并撤之，改用李鋐，则怒其对之戆也。后三年始得盐道，旋晋臬司，未到任，陟总藩，皆贝子薧后事。此节，予在都于鄂公邸闻之，为赋小乐府云："杨干仆，叔向戮，泾水兵，段尉刑，书痴白面太戆生，一怒能使三军惊。上公罽帐醉眠熟，狐鼠凭陵窃福威，就中舆皂犹狰狞，日日肩公作公足，入市手掣幼妇钗，毁垣刀揕门宫腹。监纪咨嗟车尉愁，忌器情多空跼促。

    In the end, the prime ministerial figure was dismissed and subsequently promoted to the position of salt commissioner in eastern Sichuan, with the official document already prepared.     闯然一骑来，意气颠如雪，法令先贵近，何物此重儓，呼吏捽之下，倔强奚为哉，赤棒掴盈百，血肉飞尘埃。上公惭谢首频俯，实应且憎谓予侮，从此娥眉谣诼多，鷃雀纷哓鸩鸟诉，片语何缘解忤公，三年终竟难淹我，严廓传说作奇闻，想象鬚眉争起舞。君不见，曹黄门纠刘秃子，几辈寒蝉羞欲死，不分葺城强项多，二妙同岑照青史。"刘秃子事已久见邸抄，不著录。时柳泉以富阳尉为大府所劾，闲谈至此，笑曰："一轿夫足倾成都守，何况巍巍少府乎？领首郡者真不值一钱矣！"仁皇在潜邸时，已尘天听，后来持擢职此之由。抗直小臣，抑于权臣，未必不伸于明主，彼如脂如韦者奚为哉！

    A lone rider suddenly appeared, his spirit as wild as snowflakes. Laws and decrees were first applied to the nobility, but what was this commoner doing? Officials were called to forcibly bring him down, but what was the point of his stubbornness? He was struck over a hundred times with a red stick, blood and flesh flying into the air. A high official bowed repeatedly in shame and apology, feeling both resentment and anger at being insulted. From then on, many rumors and slanders spread, like the chirping of sparrows and the cawing of crows. How could a single word have offended a high official? The people of Rui City were not to be underestimated due to their strong character, and two remarkable figures shone brightly in history.     姚秋坪守城
    　　　秋坪郡伯，予弟视之，文采不彰，明察寡断，然其保障，直可不愧古人，足称大事不糊涂矣。尹盩厔时，因公在省，忽闻王三槐来犯之信，幕中劝其且住会垣，徐商进止，君独奋然曰："我城主也，今不归，民谁与守！"乃走马旋署。至则百姓正洶洶思遁，有欲往四乡者，有欲依他邑者。君入城即下马，招父老谕：已遍地皆贼，逃将安往？不如本境，尚可背城借一。

    Yao Qiuping's Defense of the City

    Yao Qiuping, the prefectural governor, was my younger brother. Though he lacked literary talent and was indecisive, his actions in safeguarding the city were truly worthy of comparison with the ancients, and he could be called someone who was clear-headed in major matters. When he was serving as the magistrate of Zoucheng, he was on official business in the provincial capital when he suddenly heard news that Wang Sanhuai was coming to attack. His officials in his entourage advised him to stay in the provincial capital for now and to deliberate carefully on his next steps. However, Yao Qiuping spoke up resolutely: "I am the governor of this city. If I don't return, who will protect the people?" He immediately rode back to his office. Upon arrival, he found the people in a panic and thinking of fleeing; some wanted to flee to the countryside, others to seek refuge in other cities. As soon as he entered the city, Yao Qiuping dismounted and called the elders to explain: "The entire area is filled with bandits. Where can they escape to? It's better to stay in our own territory, where we can still fight one last battle."

    147

    先飞禀省城，请乌机二百杆，又照式造六百杆，发库得弓矢，募乡勇、抽丁壮得三千，民志少定，之四方者皆归，且有别邑人来依者。武弁欲拒之，君怒曰："有分土，无分民，拒之是藉寇也！"尽发仓谷给之，诸大户亦踊跃襄助。粗定而贼人探马已至，见城上旗帜，知已有备，乃分掠村庄，焚杀甚惨，君愤甚，即欲往救，父老叩马曰："寇多乘健驴，步贼亦善走，去来飘倏，惟杨军门能逐之。"乃禀省请救，贼亦畏鎗箭，不能逼，协从断伙，乃长围困之。秋坪恭人瞿尤明大义，摒挡犒赏，令健妇均登城助守。越数日，野已掠尽，渐欲肉薄，幸乡勇多百练，卒鎗箭毙数十人，然终不退。

    The lord first reported to the provincial capital, requesting 200 matchlock guns and then manufacturing 600 more according to the same model. He obtained bows and arrows from the warehouse, recruited 3,000 local volunteers, and conscripted able-bodied men. The people's morale was slightly stabilized, and those who had gone to the four directions all returned, along with people from other counties who came to rely on him. The military officers wanted to reject these newcomers, but the lord became angry and said, "There is a division of territory, but no division of people; rejecting them is aiding the enemy!" He completely released grain from the warehouse to give to them, and various wealthy households also enthusiastically assisted. Just as things were slightly settled, bandit scouts arrived and saw the flags on the city walls, knowing that preparations had already been made. They then divided and plundered villages, burning and killing very cruelly. The lord was very angry and immediately wanted to go to rescue them. Elderly men held onto his horse and said, "The bandits mostly ride strong donkeys, and foot soldiers are also good at running; they go and come swiftly and lightly. Only General Yang can chase them." The lord then reported to the provincial capital to request rescue. The bandits also feared guns and arrows and could not force their way in. They cooperated and cut off the group, laying a long siege to besiege the city. Lady Qiu Ping, who was particularly clear on great principles, prepared rewards and commanded strong women to equally climb the city walls and assist in defense. After several days, the countryside had been plundered completely, and they gradually wanted to attack in close combat. Fortunately, the local volunteers were mostly well-trained, and finally, guns and arrows killed dozens of people, but they still did not retreat.

    瞿恭人以长子彬嘱其叔挈往藏城北野寺中，有急疾驰赴省，托其姒余姊许夫人身携其女，抱次子懋坐井阑，谓秋坪曰："寇入，君殉城头，我即殉于此矣，毋相顾也！"至第九日，势愈迫，贼有乘闉上者，君亲援弓射之颠，继登者相接，方支拄无策，忽闻炮声轰然，贼有奔马来报者，众相顾失色，曰："杨鬍子至矣！"散者大众。杨至，君即开城迎接，杨遥呼曰："毋动，此一群羊不足驱也。"一少年亡命援杨马尾，即回手提之，抛入城濠，视之已毙矣，见者吐舌，各鸟兽散，无一骑一卒敢留者。杨入城，令军士先食，己亦与秋坪共饭毕，即起曰："恐贼旁逸，不可与以暇也。

    瞿 Gongren entrusted her eldest son Bin to her uncle to take him to a temple in the northern wilds of Zang City, instructing him to rush to the provincial capital in case of an urgent illness.     Liang Shanbo's Obsession with Money

    Liang Shanbo, the respected scholar and official, came from a family of the highest caliber, both in terms of lineage and personal character. However, he had a peculiar obsession, akin to that of Junzhong, which led him to suffer two humiliations at the hands of petty people, all due to matters of money. Though these incidents were unexpected, it cannot be said that criticizing a virtuous person for such minor flaws is entirely unjust.

    In the year Jiaqing Gengshen (1810), the treasury was about to be full, and at dawn, Yuan Er Ru, the Observing Officer, summoned me and instructed me to accompany my assistant, Gu Banqing, to the scene. Upon arriving, we found Xie Zhonghan Gongming, the Middle Rank Scholar, sitting in a state of anger. Yuan Er Ru turned to me and said, "You are also a disciple of the East Mountain. I respectfully request that you temporarily take charge of the situation. Gu Banqing, please draft a report to the governor and also send a message to the Qiantang prefecture to prepare for the arrival of the convoy." He then stood up and called for someone to announce our presence at the upper court.

The accumulated salary earned with integrity and the gifts and contributions made during the funeral amounted to 15,000 gold pieces, which were divided into five shares, each receiving over 3,000 gold pieces.     鄂尚书
    　　　予所见伟人如孙文定之镇定、百文敏之宏毅，皆绝伦超群。然读书数十年，酝酿有素，故充实光辉，岩廊炳耀，乃有未尝学问，且奔走戎马间，日不暇给，而能仔肩艰巨，且渐通文艺，此真天之所助矣。鄂尚书辉，世本叶赫，改隸正白旗，三十尚为白身，日卧酒肆，如史宏肇，其友申泰规之，为凑钱二十千，具冠靴，得挑马甲，乃更为计曰："子无兄弟，如宗祀何？"汉军李氏有女，年已廿七，甚淑，为聘娶之。门户初立，而准酋役起，揀赴戎行，时李夫人已抱子，均托之申。去十年奏凯归，得守备，居未几，复以游击从阿文成征金川，荐陟总兵，镇建昌。适甘肃回匪苏四十三滋事，摺请军前效力，乃赐金绮，授领队大臣，督兵攻石峰堡，见堡中一首，垂墉发枪，即援弓射之颠。正驰骑往取其级，忽标下中军启曰："请大人回营。

    Explanation

    154

    The E Grand Secretary

    The great men I have seen, such as Sun Wending's composure and Bai Wenmin's courage and determination, are all unparalleled and superior. However, those who have studied for decades, with a solid foundation, are full of brilliance and shine in the halls of power. On the other hand, there are those who have never studied, yet they rush about in the midst of military campaigns, never having time to spare, and yet they can shoulder great responsibilities and gradually become proficient in literature and art. This is truly what heaven assists them with. The E Grand Secretary, originally from the Yehe family, changed to the Yellow Banner. At thirty, he was still a commoner, lying in a wine shop, like Shi Hongzhao. His friend Shen Tai advised him, and they pooled together twenty thousand coins to buy him formal attire and boots, allowing him to be selected for a cavalry position. Then, he said, "With no brothers, what will happen to the ancestral worship?" The Han military Li family had a daughter, aged twenty-seven, who was very virtuous, and he married her. Just as his household was established, the Dzungar rebellion broke out, and he was selected to serve in the military. At that time, Li's wife had already given birth to a son, and they entrusted him to Shen. After ten years, he returned victorious, and was appointed as a guard. He did not stay long in this position before serving again as a guerrilla under A Wencheng in the campaign against Jinchuan. He was recommended for promotion to general, and stationed in Jianchang. When the Hui rebels in Gansu, led by Su Sisan, caused trouble, he petitioned to serve in the military. He was then granted gold and silk, appointed as a leading minister, and led troops to attack Shifeng Fort. Seeing a banner hanging from the wall and firing guns, he immediately drew his bow and shot it down. Just as he was riding to take the head, suddenly the standard-bearer of the middle army said, "Please return to camp, sir."

    155

    "公叱曰："堡已垂下，回营何居！"曰："大人已受重伤！"回视下体，血殷战裳，蓦然遽倒，舁归大营，呼医搜出铅丸二，始悟援弓射酋时已中枪而未觉也，文成据情入告，奉旨赏赛尚阿巴图鲁。后陛见，天语垂问，对以臣疏于卫足，幸不陨越，悉仗天威。嗣是世袭男爵，开府川滇，皆由此起也。信一如，如司命，初督成都，廓尔喀叛，群议以为督臣自合坐镇，成将军带兵往办，一如独谓不然。

    155

    The general shouted, "The fort is about to fall, why return to camp?" His subordinate replied, "The general has been seriously wounded!" Looking down, he saw blood staining his battle robe, and suddenly collapsed. He was carried back to the main camp, where a doctor removed two lead bullets. It was then that he realized he had been shot while drawing his bow to shoot the chief but did not feel it. Wen Cheng reported the situation to the emperor, who then issued an edict to award the general the title of Saisang'a Baturu. Later, he was summoned to the imperial court, where the emperor personally asked, "Why did you not protect yourself better?" The general replied, "I was negligent in protecting myself, but fortunately, I did not die or flee. All thanks to the majesty of heaven." From then on, he inherited the title of Marquis and established his headquarters in Sichuan and Yunnan, all of which started from this incident. Xin Yiru, as if he were the guardian of destiny, was initially appointed to oversee Chengdu. When the Gorkha rebelled, the general consensus was that the governor-general should remain in his seat to maintain control, and General Cheng led troops to handle the situation. Xin Yiru alone disagreed.

    后得旨切责，谓鄂辉从前办理不善，今有安坐省城，降为副都统，迅速前往，乃握一如手曰："我违子言，甚惭于子，然此行非子不可，能万里相从乎？"一如曰："此王事也，仪虽小臣，岂敢惮劳。且士为知己，虽死不避。"遂偕行。后一如之赏花翎、升知府，皆鄂所请也，故举主谊尤笃。予与春木主其家，即视如骨肉，姓碧鲁氏，本以属国从龙，犹有关东质朴故习，少不甚识字，服官久，乃渐辨清汉文。暮年位高，幕中多文士，忽胸中豁然，观纲鑑多见解，且能以浅语作诗。被谴时，与惠中丞一联云"尽容鲍子能知我，岂有曾参解杀人"，诚异人异事也。尝过春木寓斋，见南来所携香饼二匣，即撮而啖之，顾其长君鄂弥善曰："味不甚佳，黑者尤劣，何贵为？"众皆掩口，亦盛德事也。

    After receiving a stern edict, Ehuo was accused of having handled matters poorly in the past and was now sitting idly in the provincial capital, demoted to the position of deputy governor. He was ordered to rush to the destination, and then he took Yiru's hand and said, "I have gone against your advice, and I am very ashamed before you. Moreover, a man will not shun death for a friend who knows him." They then set off together. Later, Yiru was awarded a flower plume and promoted to the position of magistrate, all due to Ehuo's request. Therefore, the bond of friendship between them was particularly strong. He still retained the simple and honest customs of the Guandong region. In his youth, he did not know many characters, but after serving in office for a long time, he gradually learned to distinguish between Manchu and Chinese texts. In his old age, he held a high position, with many literati in his entourage. Suddenly, his mind became clear, and he gained many insights from reading historical records. Moreover, he could compose poetry in simple language. When he was demoted, he composed a couplet with Huizhongcheng, saying, "Even if you are as understanding as Boyi, can you truly understand me? How can Zengzi explain my actions?" This was indeed a remarkable person and a remarkable event. He once visited Chunmu's study and saw two boxes of incense cakes brought from the south.     死后为神
    　　　读昌黎《罗池庙记》，知柳州之神昭昭也，况以死勤事，殁而为灵，理非虚臆。传中丞鼎，初官普洱参军，尚留辕效力，与仲最狎，蚤鼓后，必招共话，押门迄，亦来寓剧谈。见人一善，必慕效之，手抄一如摺稿至四帙。事母至孝，交友以诚，面如傅赭，目奕奕有威光，余谓君必从神祗道中来，应掌杀伐。劫后果以同知署福将军翼长，剿贼无算，群苗畏之如雷霆，戴之如日月，为生祠以祀之。嘉庆庚申，解何半生还，便道省墓，予谒之杭寓，备述劳苦，且言生平无诳语，许此囚以不死而不得践为歉。予谓君非迦蓝，何必守五戒，如愧此囚，收之作部将可耳。嗣力化苗民，创建书院，移书延予掌教，予以道远辞之。又二年，冒暑入觐，以亚父之疾薧于途次，朝野痛惜。予嘱辰沅道张公崇奉之，复札云：无烦料理，三厅民已易生祠为总管庙而宏敞之，水旱疾疫必祷，牲醪无虚日矣。

    After Death, One Becomes a Deity

    Reading Han Yu's "Record of the Luochi Temple," I came to know clearly that the deity of Liuzhou is indeed evident. Moreover, those who die in the service of their duties and become spirits after death do so based on a principle that is not mere conjecture. The biography of Zhongcheng Ding states that he was initially appointed as a military officer in Pu'er, yet he still remained to serve diligently. He was closest friends with Zhong, and after the early drumbeat, he would certainly invite him to converse. Until the closing of the gate, he would also come to engage in lively discussions. Whenever he saw one good thing in a person, he would certainly admire and imitate it, hand-copying one like a folded draft up to four volumes. He was filial to his mother and made friends with sincerity. His face was as if painted with ochre, and his eyes were bright with a commanding presence. I believed that he must have come from the path of the divine and should be in charge of warfare. Indeed, he later served as the deputy commander of the Wing of the General of Happiness, eliminating countless bandits. The local tribes feared him like thunder and revered him like the sun and moon, building a living temple to worship him. In the year Jiaqing Gengshen (1810), after being released from service, he returned home and took a detour to visit the grave. I visited him at his residence in Hangzhou, where he detailed his hardships and mentioned that he had never told a lie in his life, promising this prisoner not to die but failing to keep the promise, feeling regret. I told him that he was not a Bodhisattva, so why should he observe the Five Precepts? If he felt ashamed of this prisoner, receiving him as a subordinate officer would be sufficient. Later, he strove to civilize the local tribes and established a school, sending a letter inviting me to teach, but I declined due to the distance. Two years later, he ventured into the heat to pay homage, dying of illness during the journey. The court and the people mourned deeply. I entrusted the governor of Chenduan to honor him, and he replied in a letter: "No need to manage; the people of the three counties have already converted the living temple into a temple of the Supreme Commander and expanded it. They pray for rain, drought, disease, and epidemics, and sacrifices and wine are offered daily."

    Dai Jun, the Duke of Yanmu, took action against the disturbances caused by the barbarians, overseeing the defense of the border. One night, he crossed a swift stream and drowned there.     平阳案
    　　　温之平阳，民风犷悍，每岁催科，绅士尤多包揽。有庄以莅者，新中武举，遂夺多士之所包而悉揽之，众不服，讼之，呼之不至，捕之则拒，又结硬手许鸿志为羽翼，阖邑畏之，且效之附之。前令蒋澄已七十，乞休去温守杨太鹤惑于庸妄，谓非武健不足胜任，访得豫章大挑班徐映台有文武才，乃荐之。徐亦觊其可越次也，欣然就之，瞰其他往，要而缚之，庄果不能匿，喜甚，亲解赴府。

    The Pingyang Case

    In Pingyang, under the jurisdiction of Wen, the local customs were fierce and wild. Each year, during the tax collection, the local gentry often acted as intermediaries. When a new magistrate, Zhuang, who had recently passed the military examination, took office, he took over what others were handling and took it all for himself. The people did not accept this and took it to court. When called upon, they did not come, and when tried to be arrested, they resisted. Zhuang then formed a strong alliance with Xu Hongzhi, who became his support. The entire city feared him and followed him. The previous magistrate, Jiang Cheng, who was 70 years old, had requested retirement, and the new governor of Wen, Yang Tahe, was misled by mediocre and foolish people, believing that only a strong and capable person could handle the job. After searching, they found Xu Yingtai from Yuchang, who had both literary and military talents, and recommended him. Xu Yingtai also hoped to be promoted and gladly accepted the position. He watched for Zhuang's absence and then captured him. Zhuang indeed could not hide and was very happy, personally taking him to the prefectural office.

    I hurried to pay respects to Wen at his residence, and he showed me the draft of the edict, which was thousands of words in detail. Such a major case was resolved in this way, not only saving countless lives but also protecting the officers from severe questioning.     袁痴
    　　　袁丹叔先生，性好游戏，酷慕唐解元祝京兆，以嘉兴太守得请家居，买宅府县间居之，即今求是堂也。一日科头敞衣，倚门闲眺，有友人遣仆通书，未识门迳，邂逅问讯此间袁痴宅安在，袁痴者戚友惎公，背呼谑字也。公闻仆言，应曰："门内即是，吾为司阍，书可付达。"少焉，偕少年扛一襆出，什袭封铃，诏其仆曰："汝主与我主假一器，器甚珍，亦颇脆，嘱汝好持之。"饬二童缚其背，约束甚固。友仆竭蹶负归，气急败坏，告劳于主，友疑其讶，发缄视巨磨一轮，题其上云："家奴无知，呼我袁痴，无法可治，石以压之。"大为拊掌。又新建一书室，用三合土，须鸡卵砑之，见一童携筐市蛋，呼入室中论价。

    164

    Mr. Yuan Danshu was a man who loved to play and deeply admired Zhu Jingzhao, known as Tang Xieyuan. After retiring from his position as the governor of Jiaxing, he bought a house between the prefectural and county areas to live in, which is now known as Qiusi Hall. Everyone burst out laughing. Yuan Chizi then built a new study, using a mixture of three materials, and needed chicken eggs to smooth it. He saw a child carrying a basket to buy eggs and called him into the room to negotiate the price.

    讼师
    　　　功令严禁讼师，今皆讼棍耳，安得云师。若真有邓思贤刀笔，有司之所畏，亦有司之所欲也。雍正间，松城有吴墨谦者，工刀笔，晓律例，人倩作呈状，必先叩实情，理曲则但为委曲稽延，劝之和解；若果理直，则虽上官当道不能抑。德清徐西湾未贵时，赘子琅琊，为熑延员外之婿，外姑剧爱之，割千亩为奁赠。后女死失欢，靳复不予，西湾尊甫方虎先生以方伯乞休，年已八十，亲来索取，遂涉讼，奁目俱载，并另有细薄号数，租额炳列，府县均袒之。吴为作诉，极言婚姻夙好，冰玉相投，为夫故家析，女已夭逝，不能给，亦不愿给也。

    Translation:

    Litigation Practitioners

    Official regulations strictly prohibit litigation practitioners, but today they are all unscrupulous ruffians—how can they be called teachers? If there were truly someone like Deng Sixian with exceptional legal skills, they would be both feared and desired by the officials. During the reign of Emperor Yongzheng, there was a man named Wu Moqian in Songcheng who excelled in legal writing and was well-versed in laws and precedents. People who commissioned him to write legal documents always inquired into the true facts first. If the case was unjust, he would only delay and evade, urging reconciliation; if the case was just, even high-ranking officials could not suppress it. When Xu Xibay from Deqing was not yet prominent, he married into a family in Langya as a son-in-law, becoming the son-in-law of an official. His mother-in-law deeply loved him and gave him a thousand acres of land as a dowry. Later, after the daughter died and the relationship soured, she refused to give back the land. Xu Xibay's father, Mr. Fang Hu, a former governor who had retired at the age of eighty, came personally to claim the land, leading to litigation. The list of dowry items was all recorded, along with detailed records of the property and clearly listed rental amounts. Both the prefecture and county favored him. Wu wrote the lawsuit, speaking highly of their long-standing friendship, pure and harmonious like ice and jade. He argued that the husband's family had divided, the daughter had died young, and he could not give it back, nor did he wish to give it back.

    夫曰奁，则非翁之所得问；夫曰赠，则非讼之所能争，亲家翁具三达尊，断不涎此，此必主计仆狡狯，料明镜高悬，决不为所眩耳。诉入，方虎翁废然返棹。又一富家，欲吞一活产，而业重价轻，未盈卅载，无可解说，乃觅一故纸，仿正找两券作一伪绝据，笔墨浓淡俱极相符，更倩铁笔摹旧契图印之，临审时呈验，失业者无以辩也。吴乃从掌案索观，反覆良久，密告曰："伪也！"即为申诉："大凡民家契券，既不可悬之于壁，又不可铺之于几，则藏之箧；复虑其污且损也，则夹之书，故蠹侵焉。然蠹所侵，蠹痕必重叠，断无能东西穿穴之理。今此契折纹与蛀穴参差，殊不可解，祈明府弔取藏券之器以对之，则情伪必现矣。"富家无可呈，乃放赎，此余族自贻翁事。

    A Woman with Two Heads and Four Arms

    During the reign of Emperor Ling, a woman from Luoyang was born with two heads and four arms.

    Translation of the Source Text

    A woman with two heads and four arms was born during the reign of Emperor Ling in Luoyang. The term "奁" is not something the husband can inquire about, and the term "赠" is not something that can be disputed in court. The father-in-law, who holds the highest respect, would not be interested in such matters. This must be the work of a cunning servant, who anticipated that the judge would be impartial and would not be swayed. After the lawsuit, the father-in-law, Fang Hu, returned home disappointed. Another wealthy family wanted to take over a living property, but the property was heavily mortgaged and its value was low, making it difficult to explain. They found an old document and forged it to create a fake deed, making the ink and color perfectly matched and having the seal copied. When the forged deed was presented during the trial, the unemployed person could not defend themselves. Wu inspected the deed and after careful examination, secretly informed that it was forged. He argued that in ordinary households, deeds are not hung on walls or placed on tables but are stored in boxes. If they are stored in books, they might be damaged by insects. Insect damage usually leaves overlapping marks, and it is impossible for insects to create patterns that go in different directions. The current deed had inconsistent patterns, which could be resolved by comparing it with the original storage container. The wealthy family had no way to present a valid deed, so they had to release the property, and this was a matter of self-inflicted harm for the family.

    Another pawnshop in New An was targeted by a local bully who intended to defraud its assets. The bully learned the pawnshop's sloppy handwriting, imitated its stamp, and copied its style to create a fake pawn ticket, writing a pearl worth one thousand gold pieces. He calculated the value at ten for five, demanding one thousand gold pieces as repayment. The pawnshop owner, a strong-willed person, took the monthly ledger and presented it. The bully then accused his accomplice, claiming that the owner was enamored with the pearl and ordered his accomplice to seize it. Mr. Mo Qian took the ticket and examined it, smiling and comforting his accomplice, saying, "Don't worry, it's easy to unravel!" He explained the rules of each pawnshop, stating that by convention, a young apprentice writes the tickets. For a large pawnshop, four clerks receive tickets; for a medium-sized one, three; and for a small one, two, each receiving a hundred tickets. They are handed out using a wooden skewer; otherwise, they would fall like leaves in autumn. He requested the magistrate to inspect the tickets from various pawnshops. It can be seen that this ticket has no hole, so it is not from a pawnshop. The bully was speechless and fled. With a few words, Mr. Mo Qian resolved the case; the honest official should serve him respectfully.

    Strange Encounters in the Examination Hall

    Encounters in the examination hall are full of unpredictable changes. Since the Tang and Song dynasties, many accounts have been recorded, and it seems that the gods and spirits toy with people, making the outcomes both understandable and inexplicable. I took the exams nine times and finally ended up with nothing, but my younger brother succeeded like plucking a hair from my beard. In the year Ding Wei, he passed the county examination, and in the year Yi You, he was recommended for the provincial examination. His exam paper had numerous flaws, with a few passages missing and his poetry lacking proper rhyme and meter. I visited my deputy examiner, Mr. He Xuzhai, and Mr. Tan Wujin, the examiner of his section, and they both said that in the examination hall, they only found his writing to be clear and coherent.

    Mr. Ji Tang, the examiner in charge, mentioned that in the year Jia Wu, he had already collected enough recommended papers by the end of August. One evening, as he leaned on his pillow, he felt a prickling sensation in his back and decided to drink alone. Suddenly, he came across Liu Tai's paper and appreciated its simplicity and purity, but it was too plain, so he set it aside. As he was about to take off his clothes, he heard a rustling sound in the box, and his servants also heard it, thinking that a mouse had entered when the box was opened. He then took Liu Tai's paper again and read it, finding every word pleasing to his heart. The next morning, he recommended it. After the results were announced, he read it again and found it to be just so-so.

    173

    I have read Qiu Ping Xin Yu, which records the unusual incident of a cut jú sprouting. Wu Xianglian Xingren, a scholar who passed the imperial examinations, describes an old scholar from Jinling who led his sons and students to enter the thorny examination hall. His seat number in the third exam was near the gate of Longmen. On the sixteenth day, he submitted his exam papers and walked respectfully and hesitantly in the passageway. He met another student who also came to submit his exam papers and called out to him, "I am very tired, please help me submit it." The student immediately took the exam papers and put them in the bag, gathered courage and went up, received a ticket, and left with his teacher. When he returned to his lodging and opened the bag, he was greatly surprised to find that in the rush, he had taken the ticket but did not submit the exam papers. He claimed to be too tired to get up, closed the curtains, took out some thread and needle, and hid the exam papers in his pillow, sewing them up. After returning home, he was still in great distress and dared not tell anyone. Soon after, his teacher's good news arrived. The student went to congratulate him but suspected a mistake and repeatedly asked if the exam papers, books, and personal details all matched. The teacher angrily said, "You failed to pass, while an old man like me should not have been lucky?" The student then said, "The matter has been revealed, I cannot help but tell you the truth. The exam papers for the third exam were not submitted and are still in the pillow."

    "取出呈之，师乃惊绝，亟走本房师所谒见，见即谓曰："正欲相问，场中因君，几酿大狱，吾荐头场七艺，荷主司已列魁首，及弔后场，而三场无有，疑其不到，则三处点册硃痕灿然，疑其帖藏毁，将劾外簾。监试大窘，不得已各员凑成五策，缮硃卷入。榜放，将召子补誊墨卷耳。"学究乃具陈其故，且出原卷以证，房考乃惊叹曰："若真命应孝廉，吾非汝师，若徒乃真师也。此卷若投，讹误百端，虽赏首场，不能不割爱矣。"更足奇者，杜副车禊，又言浙江某科，以"恭宽信敏惠"五字命题，一士文颇惬心，将交卷，复阅一过，乃大惋丧，缮首艺时脱第三股，无可如何，再四图度，于讲末赘三语，以领其意，每股末均添一句，掐入信字意。

    死有定数
    　　　凡人死生，自有定数，老寿夭折，不可强也，考终横死，不可假也，乃有同一非命，而火与火不相易；同一水死，而江与湖不相易，是遵何道欤？外祖蔡缘亭府君言居朱家角时，有鲍姓贾贩胶猪于苏，将归，以阻风留滞阊门，一夕梦中忽闻有人传语曰："朱家角大遭回禄！"梦中惊问何处，曰鲍家至曾家。俗说梦火焚者主发财，乃汲汲贸货，以趁年市。

    Explanation

    176

    Death is determined by fate. The life and death of all people are governed by their own destiny; whether they live long lives or die young, it cannot be forced. Dying naturally or dying violently, it cannot be faked. Yet, people who die under similar circumstances may experience different fates. For example, those who die by fire do not all die in the same place, and those who die by water do not all die in the same body of water. What principle is being followed? My maternal grandfather, Piao Yuan Ting, once lived in Zhuajiajiao. There was a man surnamed Bao who traded salted pork in Suzhou. On his way back, he was delayed by a storm and stayed in Suzhou for the night. In his dream, he suddenly heard someone say, "Zhuajiajiao has suffered a great fire!" He woke up and asked where it was, and the voice replied, "From Bao's house to Zeng's house." According to folk beliefs, dreaming of a fire means one will become wealthy. So, he hurriedly traded his goods to take advantage of the annual market.

    行至中途，因归心欲速，自助舟子撑篙，失足投水，迷罔间恍惚见赤面神人援之起，自揣生平奉关圣甚虔，意必武帝庇佑。至家报赛，爆竹窜入积薪，炎炎渐起，风力助之，遂不可扑。鲍已沉醉，兼以醃货塞巷，苦不得出，遂与燎毛俱熟矣，方悟援之者火德，非武帝也。又程姓贾素走汉口，一年归松渡江，舟覆，溺焉，忽闻空中语曰："此辰湖中人，何为在此？"暗中摸得一缆得济。自此过苏，必由崑山，虽捷径风利，终不敢出吴江也。一岁因事羁绁，归已迫除，程贾与友小酌山塘，归，醉卧舟中，榜人说其仆曰："腊底南风颇利，如必道迂崑山，恐岁首尚不能抵家。

    When he had traveled halfway, eager to return quickly, he helped the boatman to row with the oar. He slipped and fell into the water. The boatman was already drunk, and the alley was blocked with pickled goods, so he could not escape. From then on, when passing through Suzhou, he must go through Kunshan, although the shortcut was windy, he never dared to leave Wujiang.

The boatman told his servant, "The south wind in late winter is very favorable. If we must take the roundabout route through Kunshan, we might not reach home by the beginning of the year."

    Now, using the research and context we gathered above, produce a final, polished translation of the source text.

Apply the insights from the pre-drafting research directly — handle idiomatic expressions, cultural allusions, syntactic ambiguities, and proper nouns as you planned.

    Here are 5 examples showing the expected translation quality and style:

    Example 1

    Source: 爰及農商工賈，廝役奴隸，釣魚屠肉，飯牛牧羊，皆有先達，可為師表，博學求之，無不利於事也。

    Translation: As for farmers, merchants, artisans, and traders, as well as servants, laborers, and slaves, those engaged in fishing and butchering, feeding oxen and herding sheep—all have predecessors who can serve as role models. By seeking knowledge broadly from them, nothing is unhelpful in one's endeavors.

    Example 2

    Source: 兩頭四臂女

    Translation: A Woman with Two Heads and Four Arms

    During the reign of Emperor Ling, a woman from Luoyang was born with two heads and four arms.

    Example 3

    Source: 凡為文章，猶乘騏驥，雖有逸氣，當以銜勒制之，勿使流亂軌躅，放意填坑岸也。

    Translation: In all writing, it is like riding a swift steed — though it may possess a wild and unrestrained spirit, one must control it with bit and bridle, and must not let it run wild, straying from the proper path or indulging in aimless wanderings.

    Example 4

    Source: 自古明王聖帝，猶須勤學，況凡庶乎！此事遍於經史，吾亦不能鄭重，聊舉近世切要，以啟寤汝耳。

    Translation: From ancient times, wise kings and sage emperors still required diligent study; how much more so, then, for common people! This matter is found throughout the classics and histories. I cannot elaborate further, but I will briefly mention a few essential points of recent times in order to enlighten you.

    Example 5

    Source: 夫文章者，原出五經：詔命策檄，生於書者也；序述論議，生於易者也；歌詠賦頌，生於詩者也；祭祀哀誄，生於禮者也；書奏箴銘，生於春秋者也。朝廷憲章，軍旅誓誥，敷顯仁義，發明功德，牧民建國，不可暫無。至於陶冶性靈，從容諷諫，入其滋味，亦樂事也。行有餘力，則可習之。

    Translation: As for writings, their origin lies in the Five Classics: edicts, memorials, and military proclamations arise from the Shujing (Book of Documents); expository and argumentative writings arise from the Yijing (Book of Changes); songs, odes, and praises arise from the Shijing (Book of Poetry); ritual sacrifices, mourning, and elegies arise from the Liji (Book of Rites); memorials, admonitions, and inscriptions arise from the Chunqiu (Spring and Autumn Annals). Court regulations, military oaths and decrees, the proclamation of benevolence and righteousness, the elucidation of virtue and merit, governing the people and establishing the state—all are indispensable. As for cultivating the mind and spirit, offering gentle admonition in a relaxed manner, and savoring the flavor of such writings, these too are pleasant pursuits. When one has spare energy, then one may study them.

    179

    谢苏潭方伯长子，占者谓防水厄，故嘱令留家，乃以送葬溺小港中。又旗员阿公，少时曾梦溺水，故一生不肯舟行。又北人习乘骑，固所安也，及放郎岱同知，则万山之中，莅任宿馆，晓令眷属先行，而身自押后。料理甫毕，将登舆，舆夫禀闻将发水，恐不可行，怒叱曰："眷属已去，且火食铺盖俱往，何以住宿？"促之行，路上绝无点水也，愈责其妄。至数里，经一溪。忽闻奔雷建瓴而下，一舆一随骑转瞬不见，惟换班四夫得逃其半，则又于旱道遭水患矣，山神水神，孰实司之？始觉潘江陆海之外，山涛更不可测。

    布利
    　　　滬渎梭布，衣被天下，良贾赖以此起家。张少司马未贵前，太翁已致富，累钜万。五更篝灯，收布千匹，运售阊门，每疋可赢五十文，计一晨得五十金，所谓鸡鸣布也。曼园既贵，子少，以甥主家。长姊子蔡，即予外曾祖，性疏略，不甚精会计，为家奴干没代偿数十金，曼园知之，蹙然曰："吾之托甥曰，欲其稍益修俸，佐姊甘旨耳。今若此，是累甥也！"乃改以属妹子赵，赵公晓贸易，曼园亦倾心任之。某年横云山人假归，山人侄为曼园弟茹英员外归觞之，酒间言及闻尊府解库颇多，某积有廉俸，欲祈附存。问数，举手示之，曼园诺之。明日送汇票，则五十万也，曼园恐难于转运，召赵商之，赵曰："息若何？"曰八分。曰："舅已诺之，不可辞矣，惟为数太多，解库难存，兼走京西两标，始可得利。"曼园从之。

    180

    Silk Profit

    Silk from the Suzhou region, known as "Suzhou silk," is widely used across the land, and good merchants rely on it to build their fortunes. Before Zhang Shao, the governor, rose to prominence, his grandfather had already become wealthy, accumulating vast sums. At the fifth watch of the night, he would light lamps, collect a thousand bolts of silk, and transport them to the city gate to sell. Each bolt could yield a profit of fifty coins, amounting to fifty gold pieces in a single morning—this is what is called "dawn silk." After Zhang Shao rose to power, his son was still young, so he entrusted the management of the family to his nephew. The son of his eldest sister, Cai, was my great-great-grandfather, who was somewhat careless and not particularly skilled in accounting. He embezzled and repaid several tens of gold coins, which Zhang Shao learned about and frowned worriedly, saying, "I entrusted my nephew, hoping he would slightly increase the salary to support my sister's household. But now, this is a burden on him!" He then changed the management to his sister-in-law Zhao, who was knowledgeable about trade, and Zhang Shao entrusted her wholeheartedly. One year, the recluse from the Cloudy Mountain took leave to return home, and the recluse's nephew held a farewell banquet for him. During the banquet, the nephew mentioned that the wealthy individual's pawnshop had a large amount of money. The recluse had accumulated an honest salary and wished to deposit it. He asked how much, and the recluse showed him the amount. Zhang Shao agreed. The next day, a draft for fifty million coins was sent. Zhang Shao was concerned about the difficulty of transporting such a large sum and consulted Zhao. Zhao asked, "What is the interest rate?" The recluse replied, "Eight percent." Zhao said, "My uncle has already agreed, and I cannot refuse. However, the amount is too large to store in the pawnshop, and it will require travel to Beijing and Xi'an to make a profit." Zhang Shao followed her advice.

    182

    The weavers, driven by greed for small profits, began to praise the cloth as beautiful, and users rushed to buy it. Calculating the consumption, about a million bolts of cloth were used in one year, with each bolt yielding a profit of one hundred coins. If the loom operators were paid an additional two thousand taels, the interest would increase by twenty thousand strings of cash. Within ten years, he became the wealthiest among merchants, and the cloth spread throughout the world. Subsequently, Wang ceased his business due to his official travels and entrusted his relative Cheng. Cheng later returned to Wang. Over two hundred years, from the south of Yunnan to the north of the Gobi Desert, no place did not consider it beautiful. Five parts of the merchants were honest, while three parts were greedy. Those with long sleeves were good at dancing, showing traces of deceitful profit-making. They could not compare to Zhao Tian Shui's upright conduct, who benefited himself without harming others. As for the Wu people, they relied on the cloth to support themselves, and since the Southern Song Dynasty, it has been recorded. Lin Zhao, the Vice Censor, opined that the cloth and thread, though trivial, have been as important as grain, labor, and corvée from ancient times. He proposed setting up a special position in Suzhou and Songjiang to collect the cloth tax, which was vulgar and absurd. Critics said that the imperial court merely held empty titles. If such an official were indeed set up, one should really treat him as the Governor of the Provincial Administration. The emperor criticized and condemned it, truly wise and sage. The matter is recorded in the diary of Zhang Ru Ying, an official.

    三异笔谈卷四
    　　　靳言冥责
    　　　陆耳山副宪，性颇浑穆，讥之者谓有陈师召之风，人有诿（言垂），未尝不诺，客去已全忘之矣。犹子明经、梅砦窃议其非，因言远祖文裕公深未达时，曾梦入冥，见判案者为故人某，取其册籍一窥，见己名下注云官至一品，寿台八旬，醒而誌之。后列显要，为严嵩所忌，不得大用。至七十岁作翰林学士时，复梦入冥，仍见某谓曰："君禄已尽，生平幸无大过，可替吾职，不久来矣。"文裕大讶，诘曰："前所示册，何所两歧？"某复取册出示，见下又注曰：为惜一贼，误毙二命，降爵二品，夺算十年。盖有两富民为盗诬引，乞公一言立可省释，而公方为高山所轧，避嫌矜节，再三不可，二人均毙狱中，伯仁由我，不可贷也，未几竟卒。因思谢茂、秦顾、梁汾辈，义薄云霄，亟当铸金事之、买丝绣之。梅砦为春谷师，才子殊具侠肠，惜不永年，思之腹痛。

    Explanation

    183

    Three Strange Tales, Volume Four
    　　　Jin's Judgment in the Afterlife
    　　　Lu Ershan, a vice-governor, was of a gentle and reserved nature. Critics said he had the style of Chen Shizhao. People often asked him to mediate or speak on their behalf, and he always agreed. Once the guests left, he completely forgot about their requests. His nephews, Mingjing and Meizhai, privately criticized him for this. They recounted that their distant ancestor, Wen Yu Gong, had not yet achieved prominence when he once dreamt of entering the underworld. He saw a judge who was a deceased acquaintance, and he took a look at the ledger. He saw his own name recorded as reaching the rank of one of the highest officials and living to be eighty. Upon waking, he remembered and recorded the dream. Later, he became an important official but was disliked by Yan Song and not given significant responsibilities. When he was seventy and serving as a scholar-official in the Hanlin Academy, he dreamed again of entering the underworld. He saw the judge again, who told him, "Your official career is over. You have no major faults in life, so you can take over my position soon." Wen Yu Gong was greatly surprised and questioned, "Why are there two different entries in the ledger I saw before?" The judge then took out the ledger again and showed him, noting, "You spared a thief, which led to the wrongful deaths of two people. Therefore, your rank was reduced by two levels, and your lifespan was shortened by ten years." It was explained that two wealthy individuals were falsely accused of theft, and he could have cleared them if he had spoken up, but he avoided suspicion and maintained his integrity, leading to their deaths in prison. He lamented, "This was my fault, and I cannot be excused." Soon after, he died. Reflecting on this, he thought of figures like Xie Mao, Qin Gu, and Liang Fen, whose righteousness was as high as the sky. He believed they should be commemorated with gold and silk. Meizhai, a talented and righteous man, was a teacher to Chun Gu, but he died young, causing deep sorrow.

    184

    梅砦兄味茶，又言蔗林相国守东山，宗伯家法一生谨慎，未尝以疾言厉色加人。丁内艰归，不走府县驰道，曰我遵朝制也。投文稿主文者必厚，言府史无禄，不欲由我辈薄之。长子淇以荫官户部郎，中年夭折，相国悲咤。一日偶谓诸门下士曰："予自问生平无罪，西河之痛，天何罚之酷也！"众或引孔子伯鱼释迦摩侯罗为况者，相国愈不释。时洪稚存编修在座，最戆，率尔对曰："师何无罪？师秉国钧，上之宜法皋虁伊傅，次之亦当效房杜范韩，乃庸庸祗祗，徒效孔光、石庆之所为，不能造福，即有余殃，慎无以无罪自蒙也。"相国惘然久之。后分发掣籖一案，议穷治应讯者数十员，公方掌吏部，力言于朝，谓若等微员下士来自田间，不识忌讳，或以笠屐所经，熟其风土；或有葭莩足托，资其饔飧，与指名鬻缺者大异，请恕其既往，禁其将来。此案乃治吏而不及官，得全者甚众，相国固可谓能受荩言，编修亦可谓不愧诤友矣。仁人之言，其利溥哉！

    184

    Brother Mei Zhai enjoys tea, and he also mentioned that the high-ranking official known as Sugarcane Forest Governor, whose family rules were always cautious and never spoke harshly or angrily to others, returned home to mourn his father's death. He did not use the express roads of government offices, saying, "I am following the court regulations." Those who submitted written documents were treated generously, and he stated that government clerks had no salary, not wanting us to treat them lightly. His eldest son Qi was appointed to the position of Minister of Finance through family privilege but died prematurely in middle age, causing the Grand Master great sorrow. One day, he casually told his disciples, "I ask myself if I have ever committed any sin, yet the pain of the West River, why is the punishment so severe?" Some people cited Confucius' son and the Buddhist figure as examples, but the Grand Master became even more confused. At the time, Mr. Hong Zhi Cun, the compiler and reviser, was present, and he was known for his straightforwardness. He impulsively replied, "How can the teacher be innocent? The teacher holds the reins of state and should emulate the virtuous officials of the past, both in the highest and lower ranks. Yet, you are mediocre and diligent, only imitating the actions of Kong Guang and Shi Qing, unable to bring good fortune, only bringing remaining disaster. Do not deceive yourself into thinking you are innocent." The Grand Master was confused for a long time. Later, in a case involving the distribution of lottery tickets, it was decided to thoroughly investigate dozens of people who should be questioned. The official, who was in charge of the Ministry of Personnel, strongly argued in court that these low-ranking officials and scholars came from the countryside, did not know the taboos, or because of what they have experienced, were familiar with the local customs; or had enough to rely on, providing them with food and drink, greatly different from those who named and sold positions. He requested that their past be forgiven and their future actions prevented. This case only disciplined low-ranking officials and did not affect higher officials, saving many. The Grand Master can certainly be said to accept honest advice, and the compiler and reviser can also be said to be a true friend who offers honest criticism. The words of a benevolent person, how beneficial they are!

    185

    董传策
    　　　董幼海传策，为思翁之侄，与余家有葭莩戚，为御史时，以建言延杖事载《明史》。分宜败，起少宰，后复归里。明季缙绅多横，董氏尤甚，幼海偶饭于某氏，食火肉而甘之，主曰："此购之沈行者。"侍仆知之，归告主膳妾，妾思媚郎主，即遣人之沈行购之，以供饍。幼海味之曰："何乃似行产。"妾应曰然。饭罢即趋外舍，呼其童至，怒曰："我在外问事，何敢漏言，且以仆隶而与闺中传语，尤不可长！"另嘱一仆看守，须讯实治之。妾闻之，且惧且愤，遂乘间自缢，其仆知益恐，谓守者曰："某姨已死，我罪更重，自问无全理。汝以不觉失囚，谅无死法，生平积累数百金悉以奉汝，幸纵我！"守者以言甘币重，允之。

    Explanation

    185

    董 Yuanhai, the nephew of Sighong, was related to my family by distant kinship. As a censor, he was recorded in the History of the Ming Dynasty for being struck with a rod after proposing a suggestion. After the defeat of Fenyi, he was appointed as a junior minister and later returned to his hometown. In the late Ming dynasty, the gentry were often arrogant, and the Dong family was particularly so. One day, Yuanhai had a meal at a certain family's home and found the preserved meat delicious. The host said, "This was purchased from Shenhang." The attendant servant heard this and reported it to the mistress in charge of the kitchen. The mistress, wanting to please her master, immediately sent someone to Shenhang to buy the same meat for the meal. Yuanhai tasted it and said, "How does it taste so similar to Shenhang's product?" The mistress replied affirmatively. After the meal, Yuanhai went to the outer quarters and called his servant, scolding him angrily: "While I was out inquiring about matters, how dare you reveal what you heard? And to communicate with women in the inner quarters as a low-ranking servant, this is especially unacceptable!" He then assigned another servant to guard the area and ordered that the matter be thoroughly investigated and dealt with. The mistress, upon hearing this, was both fearful and resentful, and she took the opportunity to hang herself. The servant, knowing of her death, became even more terrified and told the guard, "My aunt has already died. My crime is even worse, and I know I have no hope of survival. You didn’t intentionally release the prisoner, so you won’t be punished with death. I have accumulated hundreds of gold coins throughout my life, which I will give to you. Please let me go!" The guard, moved by the servant’s words and the substantial bribe, agreed to let him go.

    186

    幼海索之不获，先毙守者，穷追逃者亦毙之，嗣是婢仆人人自危，均怀逆志。董微觉之，聚众而谕之曰："余性急多暴，事过辄悔之，明日当祀武安王于神前，出矢言，不责一人矣！"祀甫毕，以小忤意，执一役重挞之，众乃合谋曰："祸孔急，需事之下也！"即于是夜饰为盗衣，攻入寝室，小婢为之导，侍寝姬启扉纳之，一舆人以斧斫其首，殪。少顷复甦，谓其妾曰："吾伤至重，速邀沈某治之，或尚可图。"婢即奔告诸奴曰："速来，已能语矣！"复入，一厨役手枪刺其胸，刃出于背，乃绝。翌日，松守捕诸凶，讯别首从，厨役力辩曰："囚殴役，主人头上安敢加及！"惟胸上一伤则无可辩也。丁亥春，见武林闹漕案，囚供所击非官，但碎一红顶耳，愚民之愚，可恨可怜可笑。

    Explanation

    186

    Young Hai searched for it but failed to find it. He first killed the guards, then relentlessly pursued and killed the escapees. Afterwards, the maids and servants all lived in fear, harboring rebellious thoughts. Dong Wei became aware of this and gathered the crowd, telling them, "I am impatient and often violent, but I regret things after they happen. Tomorrow, I will worship Wu'an Wang before the deity and make a vow not to blame anyone!" Just as the sacrifice was completed, a slight displeasure arose, and he severely beat one servant. The crowd then conspired and said, "The disaster is very urgent, we need to act!" That night, they disguised themselves as bandits, attacked the bedroom, and a little maid guided them. The lady attending to the bed opened the door to let them in. A porter struck his head with an axe, and he died. A short while later, he revived and told his concubine, "My injuries are severe, quickly summon Shen to treat me, perhaps there is still hope." The maid immediately ran to tell the other servants, "Come quickly, he can already speak!" They entered again, and a kitchen worker stabbed him in the chest with a pistol, the blade came out of his back, and he died. The next day, the guards in Song caught the criminals and interrogated the leaders and followers separately. The kitchen worker strongly argued, "The prisoner beat the servant, how could the master dare to be involved?" Only the wound on his chest could not be disputed. In the spring of Dinghai, the case of the uprising in Wulin was seen. The prisoner confessed that what was hit was not an official, but only a red hat. The foolishness of the ignorant people is both hateful, pitiable, and laughable.

    斗力斗智
    　　　野二，不知始何名，以颀而黝、不操土音，故群呼之为野二。余外祖家全盛时，居青浦之永丰庄，门首置质库，以野二多力，俾司警夜。二量可兼人，酒食不能供其餍饫，即三餐均以升米为率，亦云只可点心，不堪果腹也。一日，忽有少林寺僧来募，指名蔡氏索三百金，挟一蒲团坐石桥上，来往俱不得过。与之数金数十金，不顾，云有能拉吾过桥者，我即飘然，否则且借宝典结冬矣。有强悍少年来试之，僧一举手，即已倒掷溪中，众莫敢近，乃唆二曰："若数称勇士，能挈此僧过桥去，除主翁犒赐外，我辈公备饭一斗，酒一坛，猪首一枚，以供大啖可乎？"二应曰："是何难！"即至桥上，不尽一级，问僧曰："若非少林来者乎？"僧漫应之，俯仰间已取僧，挟其首于腋，疾趋数十步，如土委地，曰："请请！可以行矣。

    Competing in Strength and Intelligence

    Ye Er, whose original name is unknown, was called Ye Er because he was tall and dark-skinned, and did not speak the local dialect. During the heyday of my maternal grandfather's family, they lived in Yongfeng Village in Qingpu, where they had a pawnshop at the front gate. Because Ye Er was strong, he was appointed to guard at night. Ye Er was so large that he could hold more than one person, and food and drink could not satisfy his hunger and thirst. Even three meals a day, consisting of only a small amount of rice, were only suitable as a snack, not enough to fill his stomach. One day, a monk from Shaolin Temple suddenly appeared to solicit donations, specifically asking the Cai family for 300 gold pieces. He sat on a stone bridge with a mat under his armpit, blocking all passersby. When given a few or several gold pieces, the monk did not care, saying that anyone who could pull him across the bridge would be rewarded, otherwise, he would use the opportunity to practice his winter retreat. A strong and brave young man tried to move the monk, but the monk, with a single hand, threw him into the stream. No one dared to approach, so they incited Ye Er, saying, "You are often called a brave warrior. If you can carry this monk across the bridge, in addition to the reward from the master, we will prepare a dou of rice, a jar of wine, and a pig head for you to feast on!" Ye Er replied, "What's so difficult about that!" He immediately went to the bridge, did not even take one step, and asked the monk, "Are you not from Shaolin Temple?" The monk answered carelessly, and in an instant, Ye Er grabbed the monk, held his head under his armpit, and ran quickly for dozens of steps, as if the monk were soil falling to the ground. He said, "Please! We can go now."

    188

    "僧起立，熟视良久，曰："拉我者汝耶？我行矣，尚当与子一角技耳！"乃取行李一檀木扁挑，置秃顶，以两手扳其末，张满如弓，飞空中数丈，乘其落势，以手接取，出不意横击二股，二固戆猛，不肯避，亦不解御，受击蹶然，幸立人丛，不得倒，大怒曰："妖僧无赖，暗袭乃公，汝惯掷人，乃公亦一掷偿汝！"乃捽僧背掷隔溪中。僧惫且惭，弃其衣钵登彼岸而遁。二乃从容饮啖，自言生平第一饱也，僧竟不复来。外祖因述明季有乔公子者，以豪勇闻，有友康飞腿，以用足称无敌。一日，有僧造焉，请与角力，乔揣僧技实胜己，因假近游，约以数日归试较。

    188

    The monk stood up and looked at him carefully for a long time, then said, "Are you the one who pulled me? I am leaving, but I still want to show you a trick!" He took a piece of luggage, a wooden pole made of sandalwood, placed it on his bald head, gripped the end with both hands, stretched it taut like a bow, and flew through the air several meters. Taking advantage of the falling momentum, he caught it with his hands and unexpectedly struck the two legs. The two were indeed stubborn and fierce, refusing to avoid and not knowing how to defend. Struck, they stumbled, but fortunately, they were standing in a crowd and did not fall over. They became very angry and said, "Cunning monk, you attacked me secretly. You are used to throwing people, so I will also throw you once to repay you!" Then, they grabbed the monk's back and threw him across the stream. The monk was exhausted and ashamed, abandoned his robe and bowl, crossed to the other side, and fled. The two then calmly drank and ate, saying it was the first time they had ever eaten so well, and the monk never came back.

    My grandfather recounted that during the late Ming dynasty, there was a young man named Qiao, known for his bravery and strength. He had a friend named Kang, who was renowned for his footwork and considered invincible. One day, a monk came to visit and asked to engage in a physical contest. Qiao thought the monk's skills were actually better than his own, so he feigned a nearby trip and agreed to return in a few days to test their skills.

    189

    居少日，僧复大言："不拘何人能挥我一拳、蹴我一足，我即推牛刀，若缩朒者非夫也！"因与康谋，乘僧闲坐，于隔墙飞腿击之，僧壁同倾，越数十步外。僧起笑曰："郎君何须壁后置人，今已矣，会有相见日，未知鹿死谁手耳！"后年余，乔与康同游天台，于石梁旁遇僧曰："此间无人，正可决一雌雄也，当互殴三拳，以判胜负。"乔方踟躇间，康目之，伪云："君素习易筋经，今何怯也？请师先之。"袒衣立石壁下，僧鼓勇拳之，时康立其旁，飞蹴乔肩，乔倏然横倒，而僧之臂已击于石壁上，成三折肱矣。此不惟斗力，亦斗智也，野二遇此僧，必洞胸矣。

    Explanation

    189

    After a short time, the monk boasted again: "Regardless of who you are, if you can strike me with a fist or kick me with a foot, I will use my full strength, and anyone who hesitates is not worthy!" Then he plotted with Kang, taking advantage of the monk's idle sitting, and struck him from behind the wall. The wall collapsed together and flew beyond dozens of steps. The monk got up and laughed, saying, "Young master, why did you need someone to hide behind the wall? It's over now, we will meet again someday, but it's uncertain who will win in the end!" A year later, Qiao and Kang traveled together to Mount TianTai, where they met the monk by the Stone Bridge and said, "There is no one here, so we can decide the winner by exchanging three punches." Qiao hesitated, and Kang looked at him and pretended to say, "You have always practiced the Yi Jin Jing, why are you so timid now? Please go first." Kang stripped and stood by the stone wall, and the monk struck with great courage. At that moment, Kang stood beside him and kicked Qiao's shoulder, causing Qiao to suddenly fall sideways, while the monk's arm struck the stone wall and was broken into three pieces. This was not only a contest of strength but also of strategy; Wild Two would surely have pierced his chest if he had met this monk.

    拳勇
    　　　拳勇之技，《武备志》列第十八，即唐宋所谓白打，其传以三峰为内家，少林为外家，如《鲒埼亭》所载，刘草堂之友王徵南事颇详，大旨以眼明手捷为要。沈铁岩师尝言白和尚者，住南郊之福庵，徒永嘉及石岩均习手博，以折伤科为业，颇能自赡，不藉檀施也。一日，偕同袍随喜见白，须眉如雪，遍袒右肩，纳凉殿中。或谓僧已八十，然余勇可贾，数十雕面少年非其敌也。好事者请小试其技，白辞曰："垂死之人，气血衰耗，无以博诸公一粲。

    Explanation

    190

    The Art of Boxing and Courage

    The art of boxing and courage, listed as the eighteenth skill in the Wubeizhi (Comprehensive Treatise on Military Preparedness), is known as "white beating" in the Tang and Song dynasties. Its transmission is divided into two main lineages: Sanfeng (Three Peaks) as the internal school and Shaolin as the external school. As recorded in Jiajiti (The Pavilion of Jiaji), the story of Wang Zhengnan, a friend of Liu Caotang, is quite detailed. The essence of this art lies in having sharp eyes and quick hands.

    Teacher Shen Tiyan once mentioned a monk named Bai, who lived at the Fu An Temple in the southern suburbs. His disciples, Yongjia and Shiyi, both practiced hand combat and made a living by treating injuries. They were quite capable of supporting themselves without relying on alms.

    One day, accompanied by fellow monks, they visited Bai. He had white hair and eyebrows, exposed his right shoulder, and sat in the coolness of the hall. Someone remarked that the monk was eighty years old, yet he still possessed considerable energy. Dozens of young men with painted faces were no match for him. Curious individuals asked him to demonstrate his skills. Bai declined, saying, "A dying person with depleted blood and qi cannot entertain you with a smile."

    191

    "请于客曰："晷已将午，荒厨蔬笋，能共饭乎？"众诺之，白供净馔数头，绝无酸鹹气也。时方盛暑，蝇飞如织，侍者挥扇。旁午，白令另取一钵来，与客且谈且饭，饭已，则钵中之蝇亦满矣，众大诧叹，白曰："无庸，不过指头活脱耳！"众益嬲之曰："此师妙法，更愿一观神勇。"白曰："本无勇也，安所得神？旧曾学一小技，未知今尚能否？"引入一精舍，舍中新铺方砖，胶以灰沙，殊甚坚緻。白方跣着棕鞋，自南至北，倚墙微步一周，则阖室之砖皆起矣，谓客曰："此砖铺本未匀，下多轩轾，省呼拙匠又需一日工也。"众者吐舌，膜拜而散。白僧郡人多见之，且述其轶事甚伙，予生已晚，不及睹矣。

    Explanation

    191

    The guest was invited to join the meal, and it was said, "The sundial is almost at noon, and we have only simple vegetables and bamboo shoots in the humble kitchen. Can we share a meal together?" The guests agreed, and the monk offered several clean dishes, which had no sour or salty taste. It was the height of summer, and flies were flying around like a woven fabric, while an attendant fanned the air. Around noon, the monk ordered another bowl to be fetched and began to talk and eat with the guests. When the meal was finished, the bowl was also full of flies, and the guests were greatly surprised and exclaimed. The monk said, "It's not necessary; they are just lively fingers!" The guests persisted, saying, "This master's marvelous method, we would also like to see his divine courage." The monk replied, "I have no courage, how could I have supernatural abilities? I once learned a small skill, but I don't know if I can still perform it now." He led the guests into a small temple or study room, where the floor was newly laid with square tiles adhered with mortar, very firm and fine. The monk, barefoot and wearing palm sandals, walked gently around the room from south to north, leaning against the wall. Then, all the tiles in the room rose, and the monk told the guests, "These tiles were not evenly laid, and there were many uneven spots underneath. Calling a clumsy worker would require another day of work." The guests stuck out their tongues in amazement and worshipped before dispersing. The monk was often seen by the people of the county, and there were many anecdotes about him. The author was born too late to witness these events.

    192

    There was a man named Tao whom I saw, Tao Qing, a scholar from the county school, who lived in the western suburbs of the city and taught students as his profession. He settled in the Yan Nan Dai with a room full of books and taught my younger sister, Qian Gong, who was a student at the Imperial College. She was the uncle of the governor of Liuquan. One day, on his way to the school, he met a waterman from a grain transport ship who was beating a boy who sold pies. When asked, he said it was because the boy didn't give him enough money. Tao glanced at him and smiled, saying, "If you use copper coins the size of goose eyes or elm seeds to buy a pie as big as a plate? The fault is on your side." The waterman angrily replied, "What business is it of yours, you little scholar, to judge right from wrong? Let me show you my fist!" As he was about to strike, Tao suddenly fell down. He got up, greatly ashamed, and left. At dusk, Tao returned home from the school and passed by the Cang Bridge. There were more than ten bad young men who surrounded him and insulted him. It was lightly raining at the time. Tao covered his feet with his hands and was wearing a robe (衤斗) and a skirt (袚). He carried an oil lamp to continue studying into the night. He smiled and said, "A chicken leg is not enough for you to hit. I will leave the oil lamp with the innkeeper; if it breaks, it will hinder my study for half the night."

    圆光
    　　　圆光一术，法颇简易，余所见二人均有奇验。一年十三岁，时春藻赵氏表姨，许字瑯琊，将报聘，购如意双置盝中，启视已失。婢妪辈咸欲自明，乃醵钱为之。术者儒衣冠，一老学究也，所需香炉一、烛台二，案上粘白纸，术者南面立，口中喃喃诵金光咒，咒外祖及沈师均习之，非黄冠秘筴也。诵半时许，以两手摩娑拂纸上，掌中若萤火纷纷散落，仿佛成一镜，则众皆见之。先是选两童，俱年十六，左右侍，至是问童曰："见镜乎？"皆应曰："见！"又问曰："镜中何见？"曰："见一马，系宅前旗竿外。"曰："谨睇之无瞬。

    The Art of Circular Light Divination

    The art of circular light divination is quite simple. There are two people I have seen who both experienced remarkable results. One was a thirteen-year-old girl, a cousin of Spring Zao Zhao, engaged to a family from Langya. She was about to reciprocate a visit, and she had purchased a pair of auspicious objects to place in a box. When the box was opened, the objects were missing. The maids and servants all wanted to prove their innocence, so they raised money to perform the ritual. The diviner, dressed in scholarly attire, was an elderly scholar. He needed a single incense burner and two candlesticks. On the table, he placed a sheet of white paper, and the diviner stood facing south. He murmured the Golden Light Spell, which is not a secret technique of Taoist priests but a common incantation. After reciting the spell for about half an hour, he rubbed his hands over the paper, and it seemed as if fireflies were scattering in his hands, forming a mirror. Two boys, both sixteen years old, were selected to stand on either side. The diviner then asked the boys, "Do you see the mirror?" They both replied, "Yes!" He then asked, "What do you see in the mirror?" They replied, "We see a horse tied to the flagpole outside the house." The diviner instructed them to carefully observe without blinking.

    沈师楼上怪
    　　　先师沈铁岩，名泰，癸酉北闱孝廉，素事佛，家北郭艾家桥。家有小楼，为习静所，置木鱼贝多焉。一日，闻阁阁有声，似童儿辈作戏，潜上伺之，则阒无其人，槌于空中自举，梵筴亦翻翻不止，大惊，扃其户，不敢登。越数日，窗隙忽飞一纸下，上云：今日太太来，需二簋享之，希为一办，置食厨中。家人不敢忤，如言置之。明晨启视，器已空，中置钱二百文。又一日复下一纸，云：太太欲听盲妇琵琶词，希致之。亦如其指，则室中横钱千余，浮于所费十之二，若以酬其烹饪奔走之劳者，所称太太，则不明其为母为妇也。后渐习之，亦不祟人，惟与沈师长子余来忤。一岁市一骚鼠帽，方置几上，俯首沐，昂首则已失之，遍觅无踪，后数月乃于瓦当中得之。

    Strange Phenomena on Master Shen's Small Upper Floor

    Master Shen Tiyan, also known as Se Tiyan, was a successful scholar from the northern examination in the year of癸酉, and he was a devout Buddhist. He lived in a house on the northern outskirts of the city, near the bridge called Aiji. In his home, there was a small upper floor where he practiced meditation and study, and he kept a wooden fish and Buddhist scriptures there. One day, he heard a sound like children playing, as if they were making mischief. He secretly went up to investigate, but found the place empty. Suddenly, a mallet in the air raised itself, and the Buddhist scriptures flipped open by themselves. He was greatly startled and locked the door, afraid to go up again. A few days later, a piece of paper suddenly flew down through a crack in the window. It read: "Today, the lady will come, and two sets of food offerings are needed. Please prepare one set and place it in the kitchen." The family, not daring to disobey, followed the instructions. The next morning, when they checked, the food containers were already empty, and inside were two hundred coins. On another day, another piece of paper fell, stating: "The lady wishes to hear a blind woman play the pipa. Please arrange for her." They followed the instructions, and after the blind woman's performance, more than a thousand coins were found scattered in the room, two tenths more than the cost, as if to reward the effort of cooking and running around. It was unclear whether the lady referred to in the notes was a mother or a wife. Over time, the strange phenomena gradually became less frequent and eventually stopped harming people. However, they only occurred when Yulai, Se Tiyan's eldest son, offended them. One year, Yulai bought a cap made of mouse fur. Just as he placed it on the table, he lowered his head to wash, and when he raised his head, the cap was already gone. He searched everywhere but found no trace of it. After several months, the cap was found among the tiles.

    杜张两家怪
    　　　杜刺史昌丁，以永春牧署泉州篆，家口留省，宜人吴氏，梅村宫詹女孙，惺斋侍御之女也，习于骄贵，饮食卧起间，不谐于众。一日，呼婢瀹茗，炭上瓦注忽不见，瞩之则集于顶槅，旋转如风，众方惊愕，霍然飞堕炉上，视其方沸之泉，已无涓滴。夜卧后，泉聚帐顶中，涓涓而下，正注吴面，一女一媳夹侍，不沾余沥也。午余进食，饭中蠕蠕动，粪蛆满其上，臭不可闻，不得已，易常住饭啖之。侍者检蛆饭，倾之则依然有秘其馨也，所祟止及吴，不忤他人。邸中设醮驱之，祟益甚，且戏弄道流，如剧中所演王法师。

    Residual Hauntings at the House of Du and Zhang

    Du Chāngdīng, the Prefect of Yongchun, was appointed to govern Quanzhou, leaving his family behind in the provincial capital. F, a woman of high social status, was the granddaughter of Mei Village's Gongjian and the daughter of Xingzai, a high-ranking official. Accustomed to luxury and privilege, F did not get along well with others in her daily routines of eating, drinking, sleeping, and waking.

    One day, she called a maid to boil tea. Suddenly, the clay pot on the charcoal disappeared. When everyone looked, it had collected on the top shelf, spinning like the wind. The crowd was startled as it suddenly fell onto the stove. Looking at the boiling water, there was not a drop left. After lying down at night, water collected on the top of the canopy, dripping slowly, directly onto F's face. One daughter and one daughter-in-law served her, but none of the drops touched them.

    At noon, when eating, the food moved, and maggots covered it, the stench unbearable. Unwillingly, she had to eat the usual rice. The servants checked the maggot-infested food, and when poured out, it still retained its fragrance. The supernatural disturbance only affected F, not others. In the residence, rituals were set up to drive it away, but the disturbance became even worse. It also played tricks on the Daoists, just like the Wang Master in the play.

    逾半载，刺史卸事回，自作一札焚之，怪答以一帖，非篆非草，不可辩，竟倏然去。二事皆得之传闻，惟张萱思家曾亲见之。张舍去外祖家一牛眠地，怪无形而有声，主人詈之为怪，怪即呼主人字，恶声必反，皆市井秽语，亦不甚祟人，惟好作神会中所谓钱旛戏者，窃人烛台为之。或伺其戏击焉，空若无物，惟烛台愈高，且出簷外，终日不倦，后萱思迁去，空其室乃已。余戏谓班昭以九等论人，怪亦有阶级焉，沈师楼上游戏三昧，即闺中口耳之欲亦不以累人，至假托乩仙，敦诗说礼，不愧风流鬼魅也。闽省邸中，因人弗顺而嬲之，能使闺襜侈泰，技无所施，且来去飘然，狡狯亦不恶。至萱思家物怪之中又有伧父焉，恐沈杜两家均不屑与之为伍矣。
