    More than half a year later, the governor returned after handing over his duties, wrote a letter and burned it himself. The ghost replied with a note, which was neither seal script nor cursive and could not be deciphered, and then suddenly disappeared. Both events were heard through hearsay, but only Zhang Xuansi’s family had seen it personally. Zhang left his maternal grandfather’s home, where a ghost was formless but made sounds. The owner cursed it as a ghost, and the ghost would call out the owner’s name. Whenever the owner spoke harshly, the ghost would always reply with foul language, all vulgar street talk, and it did not greatly harm people. However, it liked to play the money banner game as in the spiritual gathering, stealing people’s candle stands to play. Someone would sometimes try to hit it when it was playing, but it was empty as if there was nothing. Only the candle stand became higher and higher, even sticking out of the eaves, and it did not tire all day. After Zhang Xuansi moved away, the ghost stopped only when the room was empty. I jokingly said that Ban Zhao would classify people into nine ranks, and the ghost also had its hierarchy. Shen Shi played the threefold meditation on the upper floor, and even the desires of the inner chambers did not burden people. Up to pretending to be a spirit medium, teaching poetry and propriety, it was not ashamed to be a charming ghost. In the inn of Fujian Province, it annoyed people because they did not obey, making the inner chambers extravagant and showing off its skills, and it came and went lightly, its cunning was not bad. Among the strange objects in Zhang Xuansi’s family, there was also a coarse man, perhaps Shen and Du families would not associate with it.

    203

    叶参戎
    　　　乾隆五十九年，余由滇入蜀，一如姚方伯以雅州守权永宁篆，所属荣经县有殴毙胞叔逆伦重犯，解至富顺境逃脱，一如急饬悬赏购缉，叙州守吉公升保，札摄富顺令程司马煜，捐干金置堂上，旬余，一无踪迹。时孙补山以相国建节，勤于政事，卯初见官，司道寅正即集辕。予方高卧邸中西舍，一如隔垣宇呼予曰："起！我已遣人呼叶参戎来，有所言，虽杂无遗，即来节署相告。"余即起，盥漱甫毕，阍者告曰："叶总爷来。"出晤，即贺曰："囚已获矣，我一夕颇劳，幸告观察知之。"余漫谢之，叶曰："勿疑，我于鲁都游都下皆置天罗地网，不能遁也。"余曰："足下何以知之，曾见此囚否？幸先告我。

    Explanation

    203

    In the Year of the Earth Dog, the 59th year of Emperor Qianlong's reign, I traveled from Yunnan to Sichuan, much like Fangbo Yao, who served as the official in charge of Yanzhou Prefecture while holding the authority of Yongning Prefecture. Under his jurisdiction, Rongjing County had a case involving a serious crime where someone beat to death their own uncle, violating familial and moral norms. The suspect escaped after being taken to the jurisdiction of Fushun County. Immediately, a reward was issued for the capture of the fugitive. The governor of Xizhou Prefecture, Ji Gong Shengbao, issued an order for Cheng Sima Yu, the magistrate of Fushun County, to take charge. Cheng donated a thousand taels of silver and placed it on the hall, but after ten days, there was still no sign of the suspect. At that time, Sun Boshan, as the Grand Secretary, was diligent in government affairs. Officials from the provincial and prefectural levels gathered at the second watch of the day (around 3-5 AM). I was just resting in the western wing of my residence when someone from the other side of the wall called out to me, saying, "Get up! I have sent someone to call General Ye here. He has something to say, and though it may be mixed with other matters, he will come to the governor-general's office to inform you." I immediately got up, finished washing and brushing my teeth, and the doorkeeper informed me, "General Ye is here." When I went out to meet him, he greeted me, saying, "The prisoner has been captured. I worked hard all night, please inform the governor-general of this." I casually thanked him, and General Ye said, "Do not doubt it. I have set up a vast network of surveillance in both the capital and the provinces; they cannot escape." I asked, "How do you know this? Have you seen this prisoner? Please tell me first."

    204

    "叶曰："囚我于光中见之，囚初逃至一处，有中年妇赠以衣一领，钱五百，复返其家，则一翁一妪呼两青衣执之矣。今已十三，既望即就缚，我固知之，爽则谪我！"至院以告，一如曰："叶华又弄狡狯矣。"叙州去省三百里，遣仆杨驰覘之，杨诨号八百里，以其捷于侦探也。十八日，余偕胡雪方至院，与一如、肖廉共饭，饭后节相亦来共话，忽肖廉仆汪福抚掌入曰："囚果擒矣！八百里已款门。"一如遽起讯问，逾阈触于楹，几仆，节相笑曰："一如坦率，诚不如谢安石之镇定。"咸就杨细诘叶语，一一吻合。中年妇其姊，翁妪即其父母，恶囚杀叔，且贪赏，故诱之饮醉，呼里正缚之也，与茸城所见老生术正同。至于鲁都游都及天罗地网等，沈丹彩曾言之，似非叶华所及，特假以神其说。一如酬表里一，金三十，视茸城老生，真成洴澼洸矣。后叶军前效力，竟坐妖言惑众，发新疆。

    Explanation

    204

    The prisoner said, "I was imprisoned in the light and saw it. Initially, he escaped to a place where a middle-aged woman gave him a piece of clothing and five hundred coins. He returned home, and then an old man and an old woman called two attendants to seize him. Now he is thirteen years old, and on the full moon, he was bound. I indeed knew this, and if I am wrong, punish me!" Upon reaching the court, Yi Ru reported, and Yi Ru said, "Ye Hua is again playing tricks." Xuzhou is three hundred miles from the province, and a servant named Yang was sent to spy on him. Yang was nicknamed "Eight Hundred Miles" because of his quickness in detective work. On the eighteenth day, I accompanied Hu Xuefang to the court, and we had a meal with Yi Ru and Xiao Lian. After the meal, the official also came to chat. Suddenly, Xiao Lian's servant Wang Fu clapped his hands and said, "The prisoner has indeed been captured! Eight Hundred Miles has already knocked on the door." Yi Ru quickly stood up to question, stepping over the threshold, touching the pillars, and almost falling. The official laughed and said, "Yi Ru is frank, indeed not as composed as Xie An." All went to Yang to carefully question Ye Hua's words, which matched perfectly. The middle-aged woman was his sister, and the old man and old woman were his parents. They hated the prisoner for killing his uncle and coveted the reward, so they lured him to drink himself drunk and called the village head to bind him, the same as the old scholar's method seen in Rongcheng. As for the techniques of Lu Du You Du and the Heavenly Net and Earthly Net, Shen Dancai once mentioned them, seeming beyond Ye Hua's reach, but he used them to make his words seem magical. Yi Ru rewarded Yang inside and out with thirty coins, making him truly useless compared to the old scholar from Rongcheng. Later, Ye Hua served in the army, was ultimately punished for spreading false rumors, and was sent to Xinjiang.

    丐窃有癖
    　　　有不必丐、不可丐而必欲丐者，予见二丐焉，一王姓文恭相国之曾孙、幼文员外之孙，好向店铺乞钱，乞必诵制艺一首，不唱莲花落也，铺户多识之者。即与钱，亦必诵讫，乃肯顾而之他，其叔凤超，予僚婿也，为予言甚悉。父母闭之，则挟扉遁；系之，则断绠逸，夜即卧市间石上，后不知所终。一朱姓，长兄为别驾，次兄太学生，群从皆茂才，亦同此癖。两兄乃以金二百两，置秀野桥北毛大有酒店中，权其子，供乞资，见即招之来，斟酌饱满，昂藏而去，虽严寒酷暑，或大雨雪，终不家食也。

    Explanation

    205

    There is a癖好 for begging.

    There are those who do not need to beg, cannot beg, but still want to beg. I have seen two such beggars. One is the great-grandson of Wang Wen Gong, the former chancellor, and the grandson of Wang You Wen, the magistrate. He likes to beg for money from shops, and when he begs, he must recite a piece of classical prose, not singing a traditional Chinese folk song. Many shopkeepers recognize him. Even if they give him money, he will only leave after finishing his recitation. His uncle, Feng Chao, is my colleague's brother-in-law, and he told me a lot about him. If his parents lock him up, he escapes by carrying the door with him; if they tie him up, he escapes by breaking the rope. At night, he sleeps on a stone in the market, and later, no one knows what happened to him. The other is a Zhu, whose eldest brother is a local official, the second brother is a student at the Imperial Academy, and other relatives are all outstanding talents. They also have this癖好. The two brothers then entrusted their son with 200 taels of gold, placed it in a hotel north of Xiu Ye Bridge, to provide funds for begging. When they see him, they call him over, fill him up, and he leaves with a proud demeanor. Even in severe cold, heat, or heavy rain and snow, he never eats at home.

    余稽说部所书谈丐者伙矣，《书影》所载陈名春，则以一丐存万古纲常也；《觚剩》所纪吴六哥，则以一丐肇半生勋业也，二子庸庸不足比数，第较之墦间暮夜，为妻妾所羞泣，居然加人一等矣。然而丐犹可也，窃则何堪，今试立一丐于此，而呼之为贼，无不色然怒者；乃名流亦复为之，为之而仍自悔之，而仍复为之，则诚不可解矣。董五峰，宏文敏宗伯之族孙，亦文敏司寇之高弟也，生平窃癖，不讳言之，戚友知其然也，珍秘多匿之。或断墨半丸，或秃颖数管，藏置隐处，临行，乃欣然携之而去。子耕云，工缣素，尤与余外祖善，言伊父之癖，诚不可讳，更苦涓滴不饮，不能以醉为辞，幸所攫皆不及一文，尚可聊以自解耳。诵庄蒙胠箧之篇，不啻欲废蓼莪焉。

    Explanation

    206

    In my research on beggar stories, I have found many records. In Shuying, there is a story about Chen Mingchun, who preserved eternal moral principles through his actions as a beggar. In Gusheng, there is a story about Wu Liugē, who initiated half a lifetime's achievements through his actions as a beggar. Although these two men were ordinary, they were still one level higher than those who steal from the dead at night, a deed that would make their wives and concubines weep with shame. However, begging is still acceptable, but stealing is unbearable. If I were to place a beggar here and call him a thief, no one would not be visibly angry. Yet, even famous people also engage in this behavior, doing it and still regretting it, but still doing it again. This is truly inexplicable. Dong Wufeng is the grandson of Hong Wenmin, a high-ranking official, and also an outstanding student of Wenmin Sikou. He had a lifelong habit of stealing, which he openly admitted. His relatives and friends knew this and often hid many valuable and secret things. Sometimes he would steal half a lump of broken ink or several worn-out brushes, hiding them in a secret place. Before leaving, he would happily take them away. Zi Gengyun is skilled in fine silk and was especially friendly with my maternal grandfather. He said that his father also had this habit, which was truly impossible to hide. Moreover, he would not even drink a drop of water, unable to use drunkenness as an excuse. Fortunately, what he stole was always less than one coin, so he could somewhat excuse himself. Reciting the chapter "The Theft of the Box" from the Zhuangzi, I felt like I wanted to discard the Laozi.

    真人府法官
    　　　道陵之裔，屡绝屡续，幼时在松见一人，则尚三品真人也，后乃为家穆堂侍御所参；在保定见一人，则以农家入纂，已贬五品提点，曾以牧牛图索题；在武林见一人，则以县丞改授者，亦五品也。三人均儒装，且甚庸俗，不知云笈为何物，而所从法官则实有术。在松所见之三品真人，与姚氏有连，以送女子归来松，松民有投牒者，即饬法官治之。一家离城十余里，设壇行法后，告曰："妖已诛，在汝坟上树林中。"归寻之，果见巨蛇丈余，倒挂僵矣。又一家，余宗也，居北郭，一嫠病狂，易夏裘而冬葛。

    The Judge of the True Man's Mansion

    Descendant of Dao Ling, the lineage has been repeatedly interrupted and resumed. When young, in Song, I saw one person, who was still a third-rank True Man. Later, he was implicated by the family's Mu Tang Shiyu. In Baoding, I saw one person, who entered the lineage as a farmer and was demoted to a fifth-rank Inspector. He once requested a poem for a cattle-herding painting. In Wulin, I saw one person, who was reassigned as a county magistrate, also a fifth rank. All three wore Confucian attire and were quite ordinary and vulgar, not knowing what the Yunjiji was, but the judge they followed truly had skills.

    The third-rank True Man I saw in Song was connected to the Yao family, who sent a woman back to Song. Some people in Song submitted petitions, and the judge was ordered to deal with them. One family lived more than ten miles from the city. After setting up a ritual platform and performing the rites, he announced, "The demon has been slain; it is in the trees above your graves." They returned to search and indeed found a giant snake over ten feet long, hanging upside down and stiff.

    Another family was related to me, living in the northern outskirts. A widow had gone mad, wearing summer clothes in winter and winter clothes in summer.

    法官瞑坐良久曰："非妖也，冤也，非吾之所可治也！但使弗祟，向主者理诉可耳。"牒之，竟寂然，嫠不半年死。闻曾挞死一婢，投尸井中，故寒暖相背也。保定署中有废圃，一狐据焉，夜必以鸡子七枚、火酒一尊享之乃不祟。晨视之，酒与卵俱空矣。法官过，乃乞一符榜于楹，此夜二簋完然。惟武林所见法官，术尤异，友人俞君述之，言其葭莩戚叶姓，家苏之西洞庭，以贩缯五业，勾留在楚，所居爨室中忽见绣履一双，离地尺许，步虚而行。越翌日，复见湘裙六幅笼其上，自腰以上则熟视终无睹也，劻勷兼旬。

    The magistrate sat in deep thought for a long time before saying, "It is not a ghost, but a wronged spirit; it is beyond my ability to handle! If only it does not cause harm, then it can be dealt with by the authorities." After recording this, the situation finally became silent, and the widow died within half a year. It was heard that she had once beaten a maid to death and thrown her body into a well, hence the cold and warmth were in opposition. In the Baoding office, there was an abandoned garden where a fox had taken residence. At night, it would be offered seven eggs and a jug of fire wine to prevent it from causing trouble. In the morning, both the wine and the eggs were found empty. When the magistrate passed by, he asked for a talisman to be posted on the door, and that night, two bowls remained intact. Only the magistrate seen in Wulin (West Lake) had particularly unusual skills, as recounted by my friend Yu. He mentioned that the magistrate's relative, whose name was not given, lived in the western part of Dongting Lake in Suzhou, engaged in silk trading, and resided in Chu. In his dwelling, he suddenly saw a pair of embroidered shoes walking in the air, about a foot off the ground. The next day, a six-panel Xiang skirt was seen covering the shoes, and the upper part remained invisible. These strange occurrences lasted for two months.

    而叶生归，家人方聚诉，一偕归友大言曰："此必有物凭焉，当以道士驱之！"围屏上即嘤声应曰："何必道士，看汝先做和尚。"即火起帽中，燎毛灼肤，鼠窜而去。叶愈忿，奋然曰："吾归途闻天师在杭，亟往诉之！"即留原船发櫂，屏上复作声曰："汝敢行，吾即取汝子！"时子方游戏堂前，蹶然而倒，叶更毅然不顾曰："有命在天，妖何能为！"绝裾而去。至杭，投一牒，饬一法官往治，例需四十金，叶倍奉之，恳其速往。法官曰："无庸，吾受牒后，已转牒苏州土神，暨尔家中霤，布天罗地网，不能遁也。"先选二力士，用黄巾缚首，行缠束足，手三股叉，又取一鹤氅衣，叶遍身符篆，一夕而至，择于厅事结壇。

    When Ye returned home, his family was just gathering to complain. A friend who returned with him spoke loudly, saying, "There must be a spirit possessing him; we should use a Taoist priest to exorcise it!" Suddenly, a voice replied from the screen, "Why bother with a Taoist? Watch you become a monk first." Immediately, fire started in his hat, scorching his hair and skin, and he ran away like a rat. Ye became even more furious and resolutely said, "I heard on my way back that the Celestial Master is in Hangzhou, so I went to report it immediately!" He immediately left the original boat and set sail. The screen made another sound and said, "If you dare to go, I will take your son!" At that time, his son was playing in front of the hall and suddenly fell down. Ye became even more resolute and disregarded it, saying, "It is fate in heaven; how can an evil spirit do anything?" He tore his robe and left. When he arrived in Hangzhou, he submitted a petition and instructed a magistrate to handle it. It usually required forty taels of silver, but Ye doubled the amount and urged him to go quickly. The magistrate said, "There is no need. After receiving the petition, I have already sent a message to the local gods of Suzhou and the spirits in your home, setting up a heavenly net that cannot be escaped." He first selected two strong men, tied yellow turbans around their heads, bound their feet, and gave them three-pronged spears, and also took a crane robe. Ye covered himself with talismans, arrived in one night, and chose a place in the hall to set up an altar.

    另选一室，命叶氏长少咸集焉，盍其户，有隙皆缀以符，独叶及二力士从。以法水洗目，遍步壇中，良久，忽惊鸿一瞥，即发一叉，得裲裆一袭，刺绣甚工。未几，复得一物，则所见之湘裙也。至下午，又似着物而无所睹，法官捉搦之，纳诸瓶，有声啾啾然，云即婢也。傍晚复获一婢，亦纳之瓶，瓶作倾倒状，乃以符重封之，始不动。入夜，围益窄，步益速，力士忽大呼："妖逃入炭篓中矣！"法官乃吸净水，向篓一喷，觉迅雷轰然，叶亦震耳。睇其篓，细骨满中，绝似千百鳖鱼之足，妖乃绝。此事蔼庐舅亦言之，且曾亲至其家，妖附之屏、逐妖之室均宛然，惟言叶有珍赏石谷屏十二幅，为妖所焚，画烬而屏不焦，则俞君所未言者。

    Another room was selected, and all members of the Ye family, both young and old, were gathered there. The judge then sucked in ritual water and sprayed it towards the basket, causing a sudden thunderclap that also shocked Ye. Looking into the basket, fine bones were seen inside, resembling the feet of thousands of turtles or fish. The demon was thus defeated. Aunt Ai Lu also spoke of this event and had personally visited the house, confirming that the screen possessed by the demon and the room where the demon was driven out were still as they were. It is said that Ye had twelve precious stone screens, which were burned by the demon, but the paintings burned while the screens remained unscathed.

    高氏奢华
    　　　得天司寇原配夫人、高谷兰先生女，江村詹事之孙女也，归清河时，年十八。庙见后，循礼视庖，茹英太翁语之曰："厨下诸人，尚勤执事否？"曰："甚勤，然未免太劳，即如执薪一役，传薪必再四。"曰："媳家不如是乎？"曰："媳家止架薪于陘，将熄，则以膏沃之。"太翁笑曰："此金谷园中故事也！"奁赠之盛不待言，即图章亦一千具，玉石晶磁咸备，予尚见一方，乃填黄起首，因司寇常用，故独存，镌"长卿"二字甚工。

    The Luxury of the Gao Family

    The original wife of the Righteous Judge (Tian Si Kou) from the Gao family was the daughter of Mr. Gao Gulan, and the granddaughter of the Imperial Tutor of Jiang Village. She married into the Qinghe family at the age of eighteen. After the ceremony of meeting the ancestors, she followed the ritual to inspect the kitchen. Grandfather Ru Ying told her, "Are the people in the kitchen still diligent in their duties?" She replied, "Very diligent, but it is inevitably too laborious. For example, the firewood must be passed multiple times." He asked, "Is it not like this in my family?" She answered, "In my family, firewood is only placed in the hearth. When it is about to go out, it is moistened with oil." The grandfather laughed and said, "This is a story from the Jin Gu Garden!" The richness of the dowry is self-evident; there were also a thousand seals, and jade, stone, crystal, and porcelain were all present. I still see one, which is filled with yellow and starts with a header. Because the Righteous Judge used it frequently, it is the only one left. The two characters 'Changqing' are very well carved.

    一日，赴座师处庆寿，帽上珠为人所窃，太翁性严，虑有呵责，乃归谋诸妇，高夫人云："此珠本二颗，以三千金购之，一以装君帽，一以缀余帼，无辨也。"司寇大喜，然珠苦无穴，不解作用，命小奴以铁锥穿之，不入，击以巨石，珠裂为二，片刻而三千金俱失。阅岁余，夫人举一子，渤海贻外孙晬仪，有正龙头刻綵衲百幅，高氏婢媪即以供儿垫溺，儿旋殇，幻花主人闻而叹曰："此一衲以足殇儿矣！"谷兰先生与陆双柑最善，双柑荐一客往，谷兰方内值，旬余不见，供给极腆。一日阍者报曰："主人报谒！"则谷兰已入，且深道歉仄，曰："有所欲，幸即以告，双柑与我一也。"客乃请曰："愿效力门下，弗令人呼食客幸矣。

    212

    One day, he attended the celebration of his mentor's birthday, where the pearl on his hat was stolen by someone. His father-in-law, known for his strictness, worried that he might be scolded. He then returned home to consult with his wife, High Lady, who said, "This pearl originally consisted of two pieces, purchased for three thousand gold coins. One was used to decorate your hat, and one was used to adorn my headdress. There is no difference between them." The judge was greatly pleased, but the pearl had no hole, and he did not understand how to use it. He ordered a young servant to pierce it with an iron awl, but it did not go in, so he struck it with a large stone. The pearl split into two, and in a moment, the three thousand gold coins were all lost. After more than a year, his wife gave birth to a son. Bohai gave a gift to the grandson for his first birthday celebration, which included a hundred colorful patches embroidered with a dragon's head. The maids and servants of the Gao family immediately used it as a diaper for the child. The child soon died, and the owner of the Illusion Flower House heard and sighed, saying, "This one patch was enough to grieve over the deceased child!"

    Mr. Gulan was very close friends with Mr. Lü Shuanggan, who recommended a guest to visit. Gulan was just on duty inside and did not see him for more than ten days. The provisions were extremely generous. One day, the gatekeeper reported, "The guest has come to pay respects!" And Gulan had already entered, and deeply apologized for any inconvenience, saying, "If you have any desires, please let me know. Lü Shuanggan and I are one." The guest then requested, "I wish to serve under your door, and it would be fortunate if I were not called a guest who eats."

    "谷兰即呼纪纲来嘱之，对曰："府中事事有主者。"无已，惟近京芦台一带逋租，已及三万，无暇料理，但琐甚，无以为也。谷兰俯仰久之，曰："敬以奉烦可乎？"客曰："幸甚！"乃检点而往。客颇练事，往索月余，得五千金，虽未及十分之二，然此冷债，似可藉手报命矣，造册箧金归，又侯之月余，复得见，奉册呈金，方将陈说，谷兰略一劳苦，初不审视，频蹙久之。客进曰："乍往未得窽会，嗣后当渐有生色。"谷兰摇手曰："何可再也，重劳长者，殊深惶悚，即以五千金为寿，幸无嫌也！"客乃拜赐而归，居然小康矣。

    213

    When Gu Lan summoned Ji Gang and instructed him, Ji Gang replied, "Everything in the mansion has a person in charge." There was no other choice, as the arrears of rent in the area around the capital and Luotai had already reached 30,000, and there was no time to handle it, though it was very complicated. After a long pause, Gu Lan said, "May I respectfully entrust this to you?" The guest replied, "That would be very fortunate!" He then went to check the matter. The guest was quite experienced in handling affairs and, after a month of collecting, obtained 5,000 gold pieces, though this was less than a fifth of the total. However, this cold debt seemed to be manageable, so he compiled a ledger, packed the gold, and returned. After waiting another month, he was able to see Gu Lan again and presented the ledger and gold. Just as he was about to explain, Gu Lan appeared somewhat troubled and did not carefully examine the documents, frowning for a long time. The guest then said, "Just going there, I haven't yet grasped the situation, but in the future, it will gradually improve." Gu Lan shook his head and said, "How could I ask for more? It would be too much trouble for you, and I am deeply anxious and fearful. I will give you 5,000 gold pieces as a gift. Please don't take offense!" The guest then bowed to accept the gift and returned home, becoming surprisingly well-off.

    谷兰先生一生挥霍，司寇挽诗云："文人承世宠，弱冠紫宸前。性命杯中酒，生平语外禅。曾挥万镒尽，不着一丝牵。谁最伤知己？诗人孟浩然。"孟公以况双柑，皆纪实也。子三台君，已中落，豪迈犹有父风。程翰林珣假三台金，积子母已七万五千，亲自来索，馆于秀野。一日，束装欲归，外祖问之曰："程君负已清乎？"曰："清矣。"曰："何其速也？"曰："我找与二万五千，结十万金票，乃得清耳。"三台子作令陕中，以公私交累，潦倒而死，极盛而衰，果其理也。陕令为江村曾孙，"君子之泽，五世而斩"，亚圣之言，岂欺我哉！

    214

    Mr. Gu Lan was known for his lavish spending throughout his life. The official Si Kuo wrote a poem in memory of him, which says, "The scholar inherits the world's favor, standing before the Purple Palace at the age of twenty. Life and death are in a cup of wine, his lifetime transcends ordinary speech in Zen. Once he spent all a large sum of money, not attached to the slightest thing. Who is the greatest betrayer of a friend? The poet Meng Haoran." Meng Haoran is compared to two citrons, and all this is a factual record. His son, the Lord of the Three Stars, had already fallen from prosperity, yet he still retained his father's bold and unrestrained style. Cheng Hanlin Xun borrowed the gold of the Three Stars, accumulating a total of 75,000 units of money, and came personally to demand repayment, staying at Xiu Ye. One day, he packed to return, and his maternal grandfather asked him, "Has Mr. Cheng already cleared his debt?" He replied, "It is already clear." The grandfather then asked, "How fast?" He answered, "I gave 25,000 and settled with a ten-thousand gold ticket, and thus it was cleared." The Lord of the Three Stars served as a magistrate in Shaanxi, where he was burdened by both public and private debts, and died in poverty, experiencing the ultimate rise and fall. The magistrate of Shaanxi was the great-grandson of Jiangcun, and the saying "the influence of a nobleman is cut off after five generations" from the Second Sage (Mencius) is indeed true.

    冥狱果报
    　　　严生国柱业医，有时名，松江太守七闽蔡公长沄尤重之，倚为司命。一日应病家聘，至叶谢，寓一古刹中，夜梦两青衣来云："冥中有讼，需对理。"梦中祈之，问有策可免否，答以免则不能，避或能效，第须多费耳，恍惚间与之要约。晨起，即令仆从市箔镪亿万，不足，复益之邻村，焚之竟日，灰满数斛，夜复梦青衣报命曰："妥矣！"从此贴然。

    The Retribution in the Underworld

    Yán Shēng Guózhù was a renowned physician. During the reign of Governor Pú Chángyún of the Seven Min region, he was highly esteemed and relied upon as if he were the deity overseeing fate. One day, he was invited to treat a patient in Yè Xiè and stayed at an ancient temple. That night, he dreamed of two servants in blue robes who came and said, "There is a lawsuit in the underworld that requires your attention." In the dream, Yán Shēng Guózhù pleaded with them, asking if there was a way to avoid this. They replied that avoidance was impossible, but evasion might work, though it would require a great deal of expense. In a daze, he agreed to their terms. Upon waking, he immediately ordered his servants to buy millions of sheets of paper money. When this proved insufficient, they supplemented it with more from neighboring villages. They burned the paper money all day, and the ashes filled several hu. That night, he dreamed again of the servants in blue robes, who reported that everything was settled. From then on, he felt at ease.

    后十余年，重至某寺，白昼见二青衣曰："君今当行！"曰："尚可缓乎？"曰："不能！前以牒首蔡长沄未来，君列次名，故有辞可待，今蔡已關到，尚何待？"言讫瞑眩，至夜，即殉于寺中。又李君明吉，即广文樵峰之父，一生游幕三山，晚年归老家居，疾作，见众鬼丛集，或以理折之，鬼俯首而退；或以情谕之，鬼亦扪心而退。最无理者，一售茶叶筍脯人，有尾欠二缗未楚，亦寻来索取，以冥镪焚付之，即唯唯而退。惟一鬼以请保不准，羁狱待质，厥妻无依，穷困而死，腹中有胎，谓吝一批而误三命，终不肯退。时居停主亦罢官家居，李札致之曰："此狱为君而起，然待质照例，我有辞焉。

    216

    After more than ten years, he returned to a certain temple. During the day, he saw two green-robed officials and they said to him, "You must now depart!" He replied, "Can it still be delayed?" They answered, "No! Previously, because the head of the document, Cai Changyun, had not yet arrived, your name was listed second, so there was an excuse to wait. Now Cai has arrived, why wait any longer?" After speaking, he became dazed. By night, he died in the temple.

    Another person, Li Mingji, was the father of the scholar-official from Qiaofeng. He traveled as a guest official to three famous mountains throughout his life and retired to live at home in his old age. When his illness began, he saw many ghosts gathered. Some tried to persuade them with reason, and the ghosts bowed their heads and retreated; others tried to persuade them with emotion, and the ghosts also touched their hearts and retreated. The most unreasonable one was a person who sold tea leaves and dried bamboo shoots, owing two strings of coins that were not settled, and he also came to demand payment. Li burned paper money and gave it to them, and they nodded and retreated. Only one ghost asked for a guarantee but was not allowed, and was imprisoned and awaiting trial. His wife, without support, died in poverty and hardship, having a fetus in her belly. He said that being stingy with a document misled three lives, and finally refused to retreat. At that time, the host, who was also dismissed from office, was living at home. Li sent a letter to him saying, "This case was started because of you. But awaiting trial is according to the usual procedure; I have an excuse."

    速购参数钱饵我，行当理之地下。"主者乃卒。又余在保阳，邂逅一赵姓，练习案牍，而不肯就县聘，询之，曰："我先子固提刑主席，年老谢事。一日，偶梦为冥吏所追，则有讼其枉断者，谓浮收情真，乃断以诬控充发，赵抗词对曰：‘直隶辇毂，差务繁重，州县以公济公，常恐不给，敢侵渔乎？且若所言，岂真为乡里讼冤，意在恐吓胥吏，希图包揽耳！予以遣戌，尚何枉乎？'冥吏笑曰：‘诚诛心之论也！'乃叱退讼者。

    217

    A swift acquisition of parameters with money enticed me, and it should be settled in the afterlife. The official then died. Later, while I was in Baoyang, I met a man surnamed Zhao by chance, who practiced handling official documents but refused the county's appointment. When I asked him about it, he said, "My father was formerly the chairman of a high-ranking official, and he retired due to old age. One day, he had a dream in which he was pursued by officials of the underworld. Then there were people who accused him of wrongful judgment, saying that the excessive collection was indeed true. He was then judged to be falsely accused and sentenced to exile.     然我父谓身佐提刑，理直气壮，若在州县幕中，则气先馁矣，故诫子孙勿贪厚币、迁就有司也。"此三事，一得之金翁所传，一得之茅仆所闻，一得之赵子所述，三人尚称乡党自好，虽未知狱情委曲，计尚无得贿助虐诸孽，而不远千里，鬼趣纷纷。吁，可畏哉！至外祖所记蟋蟀事尤奇，枫溪人某，斗促织而负，计敌虫甚猛，乃贿持縴者，针藏草中，遂败。虫主侦知，一怒病死，死后作祟某家，某遣术者牒之城隍，竟安三月而祟复作，且曰："汝能牒我，不能牒蟋蟀也，蟋蟀为我抱告，讼城隍得直，今不能舍汝矣！"某竟卒。蜂虿有毒，洵然！

    218

    My father said that serving as an assistant to the Censorate (提刑) gives one a just cause and boldness; if one were in the county or prefecture magistrate's office, one's spirit would already be weakened. Therefore, he warned his descendants not to covet substantial bribes and to avoid seeking positions in the imperial administration. "These three matters, one I learned from Old Gold (金翁), one I heard from the humble servant (茅仆), and one I read in Zhao's account (赵子所述). These three people are still regarded as well-behaved in their hometowns. Although they did not know the full details of the case, it seems there was no bribery to aid in cruelty or evil. Yet they traveled a thousand miles, and the spirits were restless. Ah, how terrifying! The story of the crickets recorded by my maternal grandfather is even more extraordinary. A person from Fengxi (枫溪) lost a cricket fight. The opponent's cricket was very fierce. He bribed the person holding the thread and hid a needle in the grass, and thus lost. The owner of the cricket found out and died of anger. After death, he troubled the family. The family sent a magician to the City God (城隍) with a petition. It was peaceful for three months, but the trouble started again. And he said, 'You can petition me, but you cannot petition the cricket. The cricket has carried my complaint to the City God and won the case. Now I cannot let you go!' The family eventually died. Even the wasp and scorpion have poison, indeed!"

    徐氏盛衰
    　　　余娶于徐，妻祖嘉周，以保举宰陕之镇远。曾祖基，以明经秉铎萧县，再上一世为某翁，则生于明季矣，弱冠以干练为父老所推。崇祯时，土寇堉起，合族均思避寇，聚粮一月，各裒室中所畜，掘土坑埋之。料理既毕，选于众，命某探可避乱所，往返三日，归则一片瓦砾，全家被祸矣，乃孑身逋逃。幸本朝定鼎，寰宇皆庆太平，亟归检校数十家蓄聚，并于一身，田家无玩营宅兆，召地师曰："吾今已富，亦不愿贵，祈择宜子孙者埋我骨。"地师乃为卜一地曰："不富不贵，尚宰百里，未盈百丁，亦流五世。"再传而镇远君令陕西，昆季二人至外父辈十五人，内兄弟三十六人，妻伯荣尚最豪华，有土官之目。

    Explanation

    219

    The Rise and Fall of the Xu Family
    I married into the Xu family. My wife's father, Jia Zhou, was recommended for a government position and became the governor of Zhenyuan in Shaanxi. My great-grandfather, Ji, was a schoolmaster in Xiaoxian due to his knowledge of Confucian classics. His father, a certain old man, was born at the end of the Ming dynasty. At the age of 20, he was recognized for his competence and efficiency by the elders. During the reign of Emperor Chongzhen, local bandits suddenly arose, and the entire clan considered fleeing. They gathered enough food for one month, each collected what they had stored in their homes, and dug earth pits to bury the food. After completing these preparations, they selected someone from the group to find a safe place to hide. He returned after three days to find everything destroyed, and the entire family was in danger. He then fled alone. Fortunately, the new dynasty was established, and the world celebrated peace. He rushed back to inspect the accumulated wealth of dozens of families, which he found all concentrated in one person. The family did not concern themselves with the burial site, so they summoned a geomancer and said, "I am now wealthy, but I do not wish to be noble. Please choose a place suitable for my descendants to bury my bones." The geomancer then chose a plot of land and said, "You will not be wealthy or noble, but you will still be a governor of a hundred li. You will not have a hundred descendants, but your lineage will last for five generations." In the second generation, the Lord of Zhenyuan became the governor of Shaanxi. There were two brothers and fifteen uncles, and thirty-six brothers in the family. My wife's older brother, Rong, was still the most luxurious and held the title of a local official.

    220

    乾隆二十年，松郡遍灾，中丞庄滋圃勒富户领银赴川湖买米，容尚独不从，滋圃将罪以阻挠公事，容尚与袁子才有交，乃走金陵，乞子才为解。子才为进言于望山节相，极言保富有经，勒捐非故，望山相即通谕守令，茸城劝捐之示一夕俱收，富绅为之大快。容尚终不自安，乃独往汉口市米数万，载归平糶，诸绅多效之，民以大和。而徐由此中落。嗣以乐善好施，将授官，入都见诸乡衮，退而叹曰："以若所为，大不如我！"即具呈不习吏事，愿就虚衔，乃以州同放归。后东海一门寥落几尽，止妻仲弟宝瑚选楚北兴国吏目，尚能支拄。数十年前所见鳞次栉比、栋宇如云，皆一荒烟蔓草，惟墨花居暨云凤台，尚岿然独存。

    Explanation

    220

    In the 20th year of the Qianlong era, a widespread disaster struck Songjiang Prefecture. The provincial governor, Zhuang Zhipu, compelled wealthy households to take silver to Sichuan and Hubei to buy rice. However, Rong Shang refused to comply. Zhuang Zhipu intended to punish him for obstructing public affairs. Rong Shang had an acquaintance with Yuan Mei, so he went to Jinling (Nanjing) and asked Yuan Mei to mediate. Yuan Mei spoke on behalf of Rong Shang to a high-ranking official named Wangshan, strongly arguing that protecting wealth according to rules and forcing donations were unjustifiable. The high-ranking official then issued an order to all local officials, withdrawing the order to encourage donations overnight. The wealthy gentry were greatly relieved. However, Rong Shang finally felt uneasy and went alone to Hankou to buy tens of thousands of dan of rice, loaded it back, and sold it at a fair price. Many other gentry followed his example, and the people were greatly relieved. As a result, Xu fell into decline. Later, enjoying doing good deeds and being generous, he was about to be appointed an official and went to the capital to meet various officials. Upon returning, he sighed and said, "Compared to what you have done, I am far inferior!" He then submitted a petition stating that he was not familiar with administrative affairs and was willing to accept a nominal position. He was then granted the title of State Companion and sent back. Later, the entire family of the East Sea clan was almost extinct, except for his wife's younger brother Bao Hu, who was selected as an official in Xingguo, Hubei, and still managed to support the family. What was seen decades ago, buildings arranged like fish scales and tiles, houses as numerous as clouds, are now all overgrown with weeds, only the Black Flower House and the Cloud Phoenix Pavilion still stand firmly.

    秦景明
    　　　秦景明，松之泗泾人，以医名，国初，于痘疹尤验，真有造化手。一日应邻邑之招，泊舟郭外，朝暾初曜，见一女于桥阴织布，谓其僮曰："汝试往抱其腰戏之。"僮曰："有父兄在，必饱老拳！"秦曰："我在何惧！"僮如其言，潜往女后力搻之，女大骇，村人毕集，将执童，秦于鷁首遥呼曰："吾所使也。"村人多习秦者，相将登岸，询以何故，秦问若女尚未痘乎，曰然。曰："是将出痘，然毒伏于肾，见点复隐，则不可药。吾故惊之，俾毒提于肝，乃可着手。"众愈拥之，求为作剂，秦曰："某家病方亟，盼吾如岁，离此间数里，有某姓者，术颇工，可延之来。"某至，即举手贺曰："是儿我平知其痘险，今幸作惊痘，非绝症矣。"众告以秦事，某乃皈心捧手，执弟子礼终身。

    221

    Qin Jingming, a native of Songzhi, Sijing, was famed for his medical skills. In the early years of the Ming Dynasty, he was especially effective in treating smallpox and measles, truly a master of his craft. One day, he responded to an invitation from a neighboring town, mooring his boat outside the city walls. As the morning sun first shone, he saw a girl weaving cloth under a bridge. He told his servant, "Try to go and hug her waist to play with her." The servant replied, "With father and elder brother around, I will surely get beaten up." Qin said, "I am here, what to fear." The servant followed his master's instructions, secretly going behind the girl and hugging her tightly. The girl was greatly frightened, and all the villagers gathered, about to seize the boy. Qin called out from the bow of the boat, "I sent him." Most of the villagers were familiar with Qin, and they followed him to the shore, asking him why. Qin asked if the girl had not yet had smallpox. She said yes. Qin explained, "She is about to break out with smallpox, but the poison is dormant in her kidneys. If it appears and then disappears again, it cannot be treated. I intentionally frightened her to bring the poison to her liver, then I can treat her." The villagers told him that a certain family's illness was urgent, waiting for him as if it were a year. Several miles away, there was a certain Mr. who was quite skilled. Qin suggested, "You can invite him over." The man then became devoted and bowed his hands, treating Qin as a master for life.

    秦技绝人，而惟最好博，一入局戏，则天子呼来不上船也。南翔有富家弟兄均卒，妯娌共一子，年数岁出痘，其母遣仆飞舟迎之，限以晷刻。至则秦已入局，托以潮逆，迟迟而来，至翔临视，已成反关，不可为矣，拂衣而去，延宾者尼之，谓远道而来，不一饭而去，非礼也。延入别室，则儿母已出，一手提其鬚，一手握刀曰："我今飞棹来迎，黄头甚多，此间无长江大湖，何所潮汛？即畏颠簸，轻舆急控，我不吝数十金。前时许点尚显，然复隐之，故由汝致之，儿不能生，我亦不欲生，若亦不得生也！我刺若，即自刺，不忍见儿之绝，差可剖心于长姒，持面于故夫耳。"秦大窘，不敢致词，但曰孽矣。妇复激之曰："若有仙名，而不能疗一儿，半生名誉皆盗窃耳！"秦俯仰间曰："有一策，姑试之。

    222

    Qin's skills surpass all others, yet he loves gambling the most; once he enters the gambling game, not even the emperor calling him could make him leave. In Nanxiang, a wealthy family had brothers who both passed away, leaving their wives to share one son. When the boy was several years old and contracted smallpox, his mother sent a servant to fetch Qin by flying boat, with a strict time limit. Upon arrival, Qin was already in the gambling game, excusing himself with the tide being against him, and arrived late. By the time he reached Nanxiang, the boy had developed a condition where the pulse was reversed, and it was beyond treatment. Qin left in anger, but the host tried to dissuade him, saying that it was impolite to leave without having a meal after coming from afar. The host invited Qin to a separate room, where the boy's mother had already come out, holding his beard in one hand and a knife in the other, saying: "I came here by flying boat, and there were many people with yellow hair. There are no great rivers or lakes here, so what tide could there be? Even if I fear rough waters, using a light vehicle and driving quickly, I would not hesitate to spend dozens of gold pieces. Earlier, the signs were still visible, but now they have disappeared. It was your fault, and now the child cannot live, nor do I want to live, and you also cannot live! I will stab you, then stab myself. I cannot bear to see the child die. It would be better to cut my heart out for my elder sister-in-law and present my face to my deceased husband." Qin was greatly embarrassed and did not dare to speak, but said, "Fate has it." The woman further provoked him, saying: "If you have a reputation as a healer, yet cannot cure one child, half a lifetime of reputation is stolen!" Qin, after a moment's hesitation, said: "I have a plan, let's try it."

    Then he ordered a pit to be dug, placed a mat, and had the child lie on it. He covered the child's body with powdered yellow earth, leaving only the face exposed.     王协衷
    　　　上海王协衷，以医名武林，本郡亦重其名，然不悦于鲁卫，惟清河倚为尸祝。大木先生次女适姚氏，未知其为心求观察，为钧风正郎也。母载夫人，钟爱之，留之副宫，有妊，弥月，偶令小婢折花，花高婢矮，不及咫尺，乃振袖而起，一俯仰间，腹中忽作儿啼声，亟归寝室，呱呱者竟不止，举家劻勷，乃迎王君视之。王视曰易耳，遂取围棋一奁，倾之地，命两仆妇掖女公子徐步室中，一一拾起，拾至五十三着而啼止矣。共神之，王曰非也，胎十月时，儿之五腑五官皆备，胞中有蓓蕾一枚，小于莲菂，儿含之，今以攀花拽脱，故啼。然苦无从凑泊，是以使之前后左右欹侧駊騀，乳一合则则自寂然，无谬巧也。未旬而产，子母均安。又某典商席，暑月病热，如坐甑中，延王祈治，且云病不可耐，欲顷刻愈。

    Mr. Wang Xiezhong
    　　　Mr. Wang Xiezhong from Shanghai became famous as a physician in Wulin (Hangzhou). His reputation was also highly regarded in his native region, but he was not well-liked in Lu and Wei. Only in Qinghe was he relied upon like a priest or spiritual leader. The second daughter of Mr. DaMu married into the Yao family, but it is unknown whether she married the Xinqiu Observer or the Junfeng Right Attendant. The mother, Lady, favored her greatly and kept her in the secondary palace. She was pregnant, nearing full term. She happened to ask a young maid to pick flowers. The flowers were tall and the maid short, barely reaching. Suddenly, she stood up, and in a moment of bending and straightening, a baby's cry came from her belly. She quickly returned to her bedroom, but the crying continued unabated. The whole family was in a state of panic. They then invited Mr. Wang to examine her. Mr. Wang said it was easy. He then took a chessboard and tipped it onto the ground. He instructed two maidservants to support the young lady and have her slowly walk around the room, picking up each piece one by one. She picked up the pieces until the fifty-third move, and the crying stopped. Everyone was amazed. Mr. Wang said it was not a miracle. At ten months, the baby's five organs and five senses are all developed. There is a bud inside the womb, smaller than a lotus seed. The baby holds it, and now it has been pulled out by picking the flower, causing the cry. However, it is difficult to find a way to put it back. Thus, he made her move around in various directions. When she breastfed, the crying stopped immediately. There was no trickery involved. After ten days, she gave birth, and both mother and child were safe.

    Another merchant, during the hot summer month, fell ill with heatstroke. It felt like sitting in a steaming pot. He invited Mr. Wang to treat him. He said the illness was unbearable and wished for immediate relief.

    The king ordered several large jars to be set up and filled them with rotten pulp from the market. He then drank a few cups, and suddenly felt a relief in his chest and diaphragm, a refreshing sensation in his head and eyes, and suddenly felt completely recovered.

    A follower privately asked him, "Drinking spoiled pulp to cool off is a common practice, but using the sweet wave method to stir it a hundred times, what is the meaning behind this?" The king smiled and said, "If what you say is true, then everyone would be like Lu Bian. What would be the point of me doing this? Moreover, spending two strings of coins on a stingy person to cure the thirst of thousands of poor people, isn't it very satisfying!"

    He was very good friends with the physician Chen Jun from Wulin, yet they fundamentally disagreed. The king favored the River Intercourse School and often used cold and cooling treatments, while Chen Jun favored the Eastern Wall School and focused on warming and tonifying treatments. They viewed each other's prescriptions as distant as the Hu and Yue peoples, yet they never had any idle talk.

    Maternal Grandfather Puyi, known as Cai Gong, was especially close with Wang, and once teased him, saying, "Both you and Master Chen are national masters, yet you use ice to melt, while Chen uses fire to attack. Both achieve success immediately, but I don't understand." Wang replied, "You indeed cannot understand. Perfect success is rare, as the Zhou officials say. Now, I use cold to treat, and it is suitable for internal organs that are yang-biased; it cures meridians that are fire-accumulated. It transforms those who are truly hot but appear cold, and it is victorious for those who start hot and end cold. For those who are truly cold, our colleague Chen would fold his hands and retreat, but there is still a high chance of success, around 70-80%. Today, many practitioners, some are hot yesterday but cold today, others are cold in the morning but hot in the evening, and some even use hot pills and cold decoctions, where the body is cold but the medicine is hot. The medicines fight against each other, and the disease is not clearly identified, so it is no wonder that we two old men have a clear plan in our minds." Maternal Grandfather said, "On the desk, fighting with fire; in the box, using ice. Why are ancient and modern people so different?" They laughed and got up together.

    伪药致误
    　　　经明金良玉铨，工诗善医，予家小云台时，对衡望宇，先府君以叔事之，与外祖蔡尤厚，谈必移晷。作剂宗法东垣，其视药尤严，味味拣之，谓某一生谨慎，然几误人性命者已屡。一为某家五岁儿，病肺风，初用麻黄三分，不应，益以五分，又不应；第三剂益至七分，而额汗如珠，脉亦欲脱矣。急以人参五味止之，掺以牡蛎龙骨始痊。访之，则前所用皆伪者，七分则真麻黄，不觉已过重矣。一为某店一主计，病水舯，以十枣汤逐之，再剂不应，因鉴前辙，索药验之，朽败绝无气味，立饬赴别店易之，一剂而愈。金仗老医练事，故幸而免，然亦稀矣。

    Mistakes Caused by Fake Medicine

    Jing Ming Jin Liang Yu Quan, skilled in poetry and medicine, was a person of great repute. When my family lived in Xiaoyun Tai, my late father treated him as a younger brother, and my maternal grandfather was especially close to him. They often spent hours talking. In making prescriptions, he followed the methods of Dong Yuan, and he was particularly strict in selecting his medicines. He said that although he was always cautious, he had already made many mistakes that nearly cost people their lives.

    One case involved a five-year-old boy from a certain family who was suffering from lung wind. Initially, he used three parts of ephedra, but there was no response. He then increased it to five parts, but there was still no improvement. On the third dose, he increased it to seven parts, and the boy's forehead was drenched in sweat like pearls, and his pulse was about to disappear. He immediately stopped it with ginseng and five-flavor pills and added oyster shell and dragon bone, which finally helped to cure him. When he checked, he found that all the previous medicines were fake, and seven parts of ephedra was actually a large amount, which he had not realized.

    Another case involved a store manager who was suffering from fluid retention. He used ten枣汤 to eliminate it, but there was no response after two doses. He then thought back to the previous case and checked the medicines, which were rotten and had no smell. He immediately ordered to go to another store to get new ones, and the patient was cured after one dose.

    Jin Zhang, the old doctor, was experienced in dealing with such matters, so he luckily avoided it, but such cases are rare.

    In the year of Yihai, I entered the capital, where Zhang Jun, a man from the sea, was practicing medicine in the area around Beijing.     In court, the physician requested to examine the remnants of the medicine. Upon inspection, it was found that all the medicines had rotted, but the evidence was still clearly visible.     Reviewing the medical record, I gained a general understanding of the condition: the patient is a young woman, and her symptoms resemble those of postpartum complications. I roughly determined a prescription and left. The next day, a messenger came again, informing me that the prince was at the residence today and might summon me for an audience. I dressed formally and went to meet him. Prince Yi was seated on a kang, and because of his position as president, I recognized him. The princess emerged, as beautiful as peach and plum blossoms, truly a heavenly being. I was summoned again for an audience and was rewarded with a roll of silk, two pairs of pouches, and forty taels of silver. He said, "Master Cao Disha recommended you as highly skilled; indeed, he was not mistaken. From now on, my household will rely on you as the chief physician." I bowed and thanked him before leaving, thinking it better to leave once rather than twice, so I used an excuse to teach in Yang and left.     Eating heartily.

    古健啖客，裨史多述之，即近代如王觉斯、徐原一，诸书亦多记载。外祖蔡公云：曾晤马学士豫、张茹英户部以亲家宴之，俗例喜筵用双上八肴，则十六碗，见学士一下箸而碗已罄，十六碗不需片刻也。将欲离席，主人曰："尚须一饭！"一拨一碗，又罄十余碗，见陪者皆搁箸，乃起立曰："饭亦饱矣，请辞入省女。"马夫人素稔之，请曰："外间恐未餍饫？"学士答以馔肴大佳，惟饭碗太小，难为侍者耳。乃以两蹄两鸭进，即以一品碗盛饭，又盛其两蹄鸭，亦无余沥，扪腹曰："可矣！"始去。及遣使送垫犒至学署中，见马复以巨甑蒸饆饠数十，侑以白肉一冰盘，又复大啖。盖北人非麰麦不能疗饥耳，后竟以善啖贫其家。医士吴江陈君，言曹宗伯地山家食，恒苦不饱，每逢会试岁，为诸门生接场，设席会馆，取其便也。席中惟豚蹄一味，脂腻肥腯，酒后无下箸者。明日家人裒集，置巨镟中，或十或八，此公餔啜时也，即侯已暄热，肉郁且败，亦不嫌。

    Explanation

    232

    Ancient strong eaters, often described in supplementary historical records, are also frequently mentioned in various books, even in modern times, such as Wang Juesi and Xu Yuanyi. My maternal grandfather, Pailo, once said that he once met Scholar Ma Yu and Department of Revenue Zhang Ruying, who invited him to a banquet as relatives. According to custom, wedding banquets use double eight dishes, making a total of sixteen bowls. He saw Scholar Ma pick up his chopsticks, and the bowls were already empty; the sixteen bowls were finished in no time. As he was about to leave the table, the host said, "Do you still need one more meal?" Each time he took a bowl, he again emptied more than ten bowls. Seeing the guests all put down their chopsticks, he stood up and said, "I am also full. Please allow me to leave and visit my daughter." Madame Ma, who was well acquainted with him, asked, "Perhaps you are not yet satisfied outside?" Scholar Ma answered that the dishes were very good, but the rice bowls were too small, making it difficult for the servants. They then presented two duck feet and two ducks, serving rice in a first-rate bowl, and also served the duck feet and ducks, with no leftovers. He patted his stomach and said, "Enough!" Finally, he left. When a messenger was sent to deliver cushions and rewards to the scholar's office, they saw Ma again use a large steamer to steam several dozen steamed buns, accompanied by a tray of ice with white meat, and ate heartily again. It is said that northerners cannot satisfy their hunger without millet, and later, because of his voracious eating, he made his family poor. Doctor Chen Jun from Wujiang said that Scholar Cao Zongbo Dishan often complained of not being full. Every year during the imperial examinations, for his students, he set up a table at the examination hall for convenience. At the table, there was only one dish of pork trotters, which were greasy and fatty. After drinking, nobody picked up their chopsticks. The next day, family members collected some, placing them in a large pot, some ten, some eight, which was his time for eating and drinking. Even after waiting, it had become warm, and the meat was spoiled and rotten, but he still did not mind.

    233

    时稷堂师在座曰："豚蹄犹可，我昨在竹井相公家陪弔，请宗伯题主，素席三筵，亦复并吞之，知此老胸中殊不辨精粗美恶也！"然此皆熟而荐之，予所亲见乃竟有不火食者。癸卯北闱，三场坐问字号，号短而阔，一号止二十房，故三号统作一号。十四日巳刻，见一人肩生彘半体而入，意谓往供给所而误也。至则置生彘于板，告于众曰："鄙人有饥疾，故备此自给，愿诸君勿哂。"料理粗毕，即云苦饥，先揭彘中膏另悬之壁曰："此差可疗渴，我以代瀹茗也。"拔利刀割之，旋割旋啖，血尚淋漓唇吻间。割其三之一曰："勿过，须匀，供两顿餐耳。"切其余陈柳筐，尚可三十斤许，计其所食，已可兼数十人。十五日下簾誊策，不复知闻，十六早迹之，则已杳，意其料尽，亟思归食故，见其卷系旦字号，惜忘其姓名。同寓多好掉文，有以樊哙况之者。问肖濂曰："哙何足道，许子以釜甑爨，终是神农后人，斯更在燧人氏前矣！"古哉！宜小欧之震而惊之也。

    233

    At the time, Master Ji Tang was present and said, "Even pig trotters are acceptable. Yesterday, at the home of the Gentleman of Bamboo Well, I attended a mourning ceremony, where the Grand Master of Rites was asked to name the main hall. There were three simple meals spread over three tables, and they were all consumed together, knowing that this old man's heart does not distinguish between fine and coarse, good and bad!" However, these were all cooked and presented, and what I personally witnessed was someone who did not cook their food. In the year of Gui Mao, during the northern examination, the three rounds of questioning were held in a hall that was narrow but wide, with only twenty rooms per number, so the three numbers were treated as one. On the fourteenth day at dawn, I saw a person enter with half a pig's body on their shoulder, thinking they had gone to the supply place by mistake. Upon arrival, they placed the raw pig on a board and told the group, "I have a hunger disease, so I prepared this for myself. Please do not laugh." After roughly finishing the preparations, they said they were extremely hungry and first lifted the fat from the pig, hanging it on the wall and saying, "This can somewhat quench my thirst; I will use it to brew tea." They drew a sharp knife and began cutting and eating immediately, with blood still dripping from their lips. They cut one-third of the pig and said, "Do not overdo it, must be even; this is only enough for two meals." They cut the rest and placed it in a willow basket, which still weighed about thirty pounds. Calculating what he ate, it was enough for dozens of people. On the fifteenth day, when the curtains were lowered and the essays were copied, I no longer heard of him. On the sixteenth morning, I traced him but he was already gone, thinking that he had finished eating, and hurriedly thought of returning to eat. I saw that his scroll was marked with the morning number, but I forgot his name. Many of my fellow residents liked to play with words, and one compared him to Fan Kuai. I asked Xiao Lian, "What is there to talk about with Fan Kuai? If one uses pots and steamers for cooking, they are still descendants of Shen Nong, but this person is even before Suiren!" How ancient! It is fitting that the small Ou was shocked and surprised by this.

    夙慧
    　　　曹副宪剑亭先生言，得天司寇，其表丈也，为律例馆总裁时，按卯将进书，遣奴召曰："明日有暇幸助我。"时曹未入军机，内阁事简，下直即往。司寇于未初归邸，令取所征书籍，书陈床上，嘱剑亭检其中关涉律例者繙出，虽两几，计不下百本，司寇饮酒，每饭四茶杯，跣足于竹榻，少寐片时。侍童磨墨，积沈一巨砚，铺竹纸数十番，起而盥漱毕，掣所繙书，浏览一过，仍置原处，闭目静坐。少顷，即伸纸和墨，下笔如飞，顷刻间一卷书已竣，招曹曰："鸿老幸为我一校！"计阅半日而书成，惟讹一字，乃尺寸之数也。又闻曾与友数人睹记《项羽本记》，司寇及张天扉詹事均一遍，黄唐堂、桑弢甫各五遍，亦能强记。缪雪庄、陆蒪川诵之终日，迄不能举其辞也，人之赋秉相越，岂不远哉？曹公言天扉神仙中人，得天由善知识来，皆夙因也。语云

    Explanation

    Innate Wisdom

    Mr. Cao Jianting, a deputy censor, recounted that his maternal uncle, Tian Shikou, was the head of the Legal Code Office. When Tian served in this capacity, he would enter the office at a specific hour, and on one occasion, he sent a servant to call Cao and say, "If you have free time tomorrow, please help me." At that time, Cao had not yet joined the Grand Secretariat, and the duties there were relatively light, so he went immediately after finishing his work. Tian returned home around 3 PM and instructed Cao to fetch the books he had requested. The books were placed on the bed, and Tian asked Cao to review and extract sections related to the legal code. Although there were only two tables, the number of books was no less than a hundred. Tian drank alcohol, consuming four cups of tea with each meal, and would sleep briefly on a bamboo mat. The attendant ground ink, filling a large inkstone, and laid out dozens of sheets of bamboo paper. After waking and washing, Tian would take the reviewed books, browse through them once, and then place them back in their original positions. He would then close his eyes and sit quietly for a moment. Soon after, he would take up the paper, mix the ink, and write with great speed. In a moment, a volume of the book was completed. He called Cao and said, "Old Master Hong, please help me check it!" The book was finished in half a day, with only one character being incorrect, which was a specific measurement. It is also said that once, Tian and several friends studied the biography of Xiang Yu. Tian and Zhang Tiandi, a high-ranking official, each read it once, while Huang Tangtang and Sang Taofu each read it five times, and they could all remember it well. Miao Xuezhuang and Lu Chunchuan recited it all day long but still could not recall the words. How vast are the differences in people's innate abilities! Cao said that Zhang Tiandi was a person of extraordinary talent, and Tian's good fortune came from the guidance of virtuous friends, both of which were due to past karma. It is said that...

    235

    "书到今生读已迟"，良不诬也。又有更非意想所及者，曾谒章嘉呼图克图，章嘉能通汉语，工翻译，时已八十余，龙钟潦倒，举动需人。曹致词曰："钝根陋士，未悟三乘，愿即以儒宗印合。"因举一僻旨叩之，章笑曰："荒徼九流，安知大道。第君所问，现在某室某厨某卷某页，可取证也。

    Explanation

    235

    "When the book arrives, it's too late in this life to read it; indeed, it is not false. There is something even more unexpected: I once visited the 5th Panchen Lama, Lobzang Yeshe, who was proficient in Chinese and skilled in translation. He was over eighty years old, frail and disheveled, requiring assistance for his actions. I said to him: 'I am a dull-witted common scholar, not yet having understood the three vehicles of Buddhism. I wish to align Confucian principles with them.' Because of this, I asked him about a rare principle. He smiled and said: 'In remote regions, how can one know the great way? As for what you asked, it is found in a certain room, kitchen, volume, and page, where it can be verified.'"

    "初犹疑其术幻，复叩以《楞严》《华严》诸藏，均滔滔滚滚，熟如翻水，于《楞严咒》及《华严》字母尤提唱梵音，克证声闻妙谛，曹不禁顶首皈依，章膜手曰："君现宰官身，某现比邱身，总一会上人，愿祝翻身时，切勿堕落耳！"曾甚感其言，且谓得先生，亦未免有愧此语。至曹亦见班禅额尔德尼，虽现自在天身，却蠢然一物，全无智慧，无怪为枣花住持达天呵叱。至于所諗戴子荆谿、吴子梅、梁幼时皆具万夫之秉，迨嗜欲日深，聪明日减，将届知命，已较少时年渐远，稷堂师尝言：陈礼园孙三岁，能诵香山歌行，五岁能读江海诸赋，均无须再过。今计将冠，淹没无闻，所谓小时了了，大未必佳者也。司寇官詹两张公，诚夐乎不可想望矣！

    Explanation

    236

    Initially, I doubted that his art was illusory, so I again inquired about the Lengyan and Huayan scriptures and other sutras. All flowed smoothly, as if turning water, especially in reciting the Lengyan Mantra and the Huayan alphabet, where he emphasized the Sanskrit sounds, clearly demonstrating the profound truths of the hearers. Cao could not help but bow his head and take refuge, clasping his hands and saying, "You appear as a minister, I appear as a monk, but we are all one assembly of people. I wish you well when you turn over, and I hope you do not fall into decline!" He was greatly moved by his words and felt that even with the master, one cannot escape feeling ashamed of this statement. Cao also saw the Panchen Erdeni, who, although appearing as a god of freedom, was a foolish being, completely lacking in wisdom. It is no wonder that the abbot of Zao Hua Temple, Datian, scolded him. As for the respected Zi Jingxi, Wu Zimei, and Liang when young, they all had the strength of ten thousand men, but as their desires deepened, their intelligence diminished. As they approached the age of knowing their fate, they were already far removed from their youthful years. Master Jitang once said: Chen Lijuan's grandson, at three years old, could recite the Xiangshan Song and at five years old could read the Jianghai anthologies, and they did not need to study further. Now, as he is about to come of age, he has become obscure and unheard of. This is what is meant by 'bright at a young age, not necessarily good as an adult.' The officials Zhang and Zhang of the Ministry of Justice, truly, are beyond what can be hoped for.

    善饮
    　　　璞堂师偶述远祖文定公善酒，日必百觥，予告归，年已九秩余，一子少宰侍养夜膳，少宰陪五十觥，若余兴未尽，呼两老妾出，均五十余，又各陪数觥乃寝。自叹生平无可与共饮者，或举一栉工能尽烧春一埕，未见其醉，且曰:"惜贱工不足偶。"公笑曰："醉乡岂分阶级！"即令促之来，与对坐，前各置一小缸，取烧春一大瓮倾其中，泛瓯自取吸之。历半时，二缸均罄，公谓工曰："能再饮乎？"曰："能。"复取一瓮饮如前，及半，栉工私于侍者曰："厨中有齑菜，与我一茎。"公闻之哂曰："是将败，己呼救兵！"饬与蔬果。又尽之，则栉工已卧瓮侧矣，公乃洒然，但曰："今日已醉，额间何汗出也。

    Explanation

    237

    The Master Pugu once recounted that his distant ancestor, Wen Ding Gong, was an avid drinker, consuming a hundred cups of wine daily. When I returned home, he was already over ninety years old, and his son, the Junior Censor, served him at night. The Junior Censor accompanied him with fifty cups, but if his兴致 had not been exhausted, he would call out two old concubines, both around fifty years old, and they would each accompany him with several cups before going to sleep. He lamented that there was no one in his life with whom he could share a drink, and someone mentioned that a hairdresser worker could finish an entire vat of hot spring wine without getting drunk. He said, "It's a pity that the lowly worker is not worthy of a match." The Master laughed and said, "In the world of drunkenness, there are no class distinctions!" He immediately ordered the worker to be brought, and they sat opposite each other. Small jars were placed in front of them, and a large vat of hot spring wine was poured into them. They dipped bowls and drank themselves. After half an hour, both jars were empty. The Master asked the worker, "Can you drink again?" The worker replied, "Yes." They took another vat and drank as before, but by the halfway mark, the hairdresser worker privately told the attendant, "There is pickled vegetables in the kitchen; give me one stem." The Master heard this and laughed, saying, "This is about to fail, already calling for reinforcements!" He ordered vegetables and fruits to be brought. After finishing them, the hairdresser worker was lying on the side of the jar, and the Master felt refreshed, saying, "I am already drunk today, why is there sweat on my forehead?"

    "近闻姚髯悔余云："勒侯亦能尽百觥，然满十杯必涤器，一菜五行，或侑以杂剧，饮必长夜，似非雅量，早为石学士之所呵矣。"余所见下僚中，湖北应山令刘尹具斌，能以烧春敌稷堂先生，醇酒虽未满百觥，亦不下六七十举也。席罢，遣仆馈赆，则又在店中独酌矣。然其人愦愦，官应山时，白华学士其座师方督学楚北，以公事具申，大书云"钦命湖北全省学政庶吉士吴"，盖吴方教习，故讹截其职衔也。吴封还封套，手书作覆曰："贱名诚不足记，而仆乃忝叼衣钵，题名中当亦见之。且自分湖南后，湖北初非全省，仆即奉职无状，降授尚应编检，从无复行留馆者，幸明教之。"知当官以善饮名，非盛德事，子路嗑嗑，尚饮百榼，良不如颜之一瓢也。

    Recently, Yao Ren lamented to me, saying, "Luo Hou can also finish a hundred cups, but after ten cups, he must wash the vessel, with one dish arranged in five rows, sometimes accompanied by various plays, drinking must last all night, it seems not to be refined, it was already criticized by Shi Xueshi." Among the lower officials, I have seen Liu Yin, the magistrate of Ying Shan in Hubei, who can match Ji Tang Xiansheng with his fiery wine. Although his strong wine hasn't reached a hundred cups, it's still no less than sixty or seventy times. After the banquet, he sent a servant to give gifts, then he would drink alone in the inn. However, the person is rather dull. When he was the magistrate of Ying Shan, Bai Hua Xueshi, his teacher, was supervising education in Chu Bei. In an official document, it is written in large letters, "Imperial appointment to the provincial education commissioner in Hubei, Scholar Wu." Because Wu was teaching, there was an error in the title. And since I have been in Hunan, Hubei was not originally the entire province. Even if I have failed in my duties, I should still be eligible for promotion.     陈眉公
    　　　眉公先生年未三十，即纳布巾，养父母。盖当万历中叶，天下太平，而先生洞瞩先机，不待终日，履霜坚冰，诚至人之明哲也。第名望太重，耆年高爵，均折辈行师事之，机山相国之再起也，询天下要计，先生俯仰久之，怃然曰："庶几拔一毛而利天下乎？"时双岛帅毛文龙悍甚，既通款大清，纵恣部曲，扰乱辽东，孔李耿尚，皆其旧时部曲也。毛耳先生名，遣牙将持厚币乞文，先生却之，牙将怒，谓何物秀才，不识好恶，是区区者而不余畀，势将用武，乃命门下草草付去。因消息之，悉得其罪，机山入阁后，即以属经略袁崇焕。袁抵辽，察之信，乃从傅人龙策，即于座上出上方斩之，部下悉叛去。崇祯初亦不罪，后中大清反间，而崇焕向以论军政，为大璫所忌，乘间证之，遂罹惨祸。

    Explanation

    239

    Mou Gong, the Master, at the age of not yet thirty, immediately took on the cloth cap and supported his parents. During the middle period of the Wanli era, the world was peaceful, yet the Master profoundly perceived the early signs, without waiting for the day to end, he recognized the impending danger as clearly as walking on frost and knowing it would turn to ice. Truly, this was the wisdom and insight of a sage. Despite his great reputation, esteemed elders and high-ranking officials all treated him as a teacher. When Jishi, the Chancellor, was reinstated, he consulted the most important plans for the country. After a long pause, the Master sighed and said, "Can it be said that even plucking a single hair would benefit the world?" At that time, the commander of the Double Island, Mao Wenlong, was very fierce. Having made peace with the Qing, he indulged his subordinates, causing chaos in Liaodong. Kong, Li, Geng, and Shang were all his former subordinates. Hearing of the Master's name, Mao sent a lieutenant with generous gifts to request a letter. The Master rejected it. The lieutenant became angry, saying, "What kind of scholar doesn't know right from wrong?" Refusing to give even a small thing to me, he will resort to force. The Master then sent his followers to handle the matter, and they revealed all of Mao's crimes. After Jishi entered the cabinet, he entrusted the matter to the general Yuen Chonghuan. Upon arriving in Liaodong, Yuen investigated and confirmed the truth, and following the plan of Fu Renlong, he executed Mao on the spot. His subordinates all defected. In the early years of the Chongzhen era, he was not punished, but later, caught in the Qing's counterintelligence, and having been resented by the eunuchs, Yuen seized the opportunity to accuse him, and thus suffered a terrible fate.

    思宗之昧而愎，煤山之继，非不幸也，乃庸腐如草。荐先生辈，媚其宗衮，颠倒是非，至诬及先生，谤为横议，蒙垢者垂二百年。幸高宗纯皇帝于乾隆年间明降谕旨，并谍之反间，璫之阴谋灼然众著。且赐袁崇焕元孙仕籍，于是悍帅之奸、劳臣之圣，朗然揭日月而行；而若辈依草附木，滃滃泚泚，不啻见晛曰消。圣主之圣，昏主之昏，不可为万世鉴哉！今春木先生茔为白石山庄旧址，与施子野绍莘分界而居，裙屐风流，一时翕集。予旧藏合锦一卷，为山庄饮集时随笔，凡十人，内知名者陈董而外，如蓝田叔、杨龙友、陈老莲，其余即不甚著名者。亦无凡笔，内有女郎一，作竹两竿，娟娟楚楚，想见其人。董尚书红叶一树，硃砂渲染极研艳。眉公抹远山一角，用小李将军法，斜阳倒影，金碧灿然。

    Explanation

    240

    The dim-witted and stubborn Ming Emperor Chongzhen, followed by his suicide on Coal Hill, was not a matter of misfortune but rather the result of incompetence and corruption akin to grass. Scholars and officials were recommended to flatter the emperor and high-ranking officials, leading to the distortion of right and wrong, and even slander against these scholars, accusing them of reckless speech. Those who suffered unjustly endured this for nearly two hundred years. Fortunately, Emperor Qianlong issued a clear edict during the Qianlong era, exposing the spies and counterintelligence activities, as well as the plots of the eunuchs, which were clearly revealed to the public. Moreover, he bestowed official status upon the great-grandson of Yuan Chonghuan, thus revealing the treachery of a powerful general and the righteousness of a hardworking official, both clearly laid bare. These people, clinging to power, caused chaos that dissipated like dew under the sun. The wisdom of a sage ruler and the foolishness of a foolish ruler serve as lessons for future generations! Now, the grave of Mr. Chunmu is located at the site of the White Stone Villa, where he lived alongside Shi Ziyue Shaoxin, with fashionable and elegant people gathering at the same time. I have an old collection of writings, a scroll taken during gatherings at the villa, containing ten people in total, including notable figures such as Chen Dong, Lan Tian, Yang Longyou, and Chen Laolian, and others who were not as well-known. None of them were ordinary writers. Among them was a young lady who painted two bamboo stalks, her graceful and charming appearance vividly depicted. The high-ranking official Dong painted a tree of red leaves, the vivid and beautiful depiction using cinnabar. Mei Gong painted a corner of distant mountains, using the technique of the famous painter Li Sixun, the golden and brilliant reflection of the setting sun clearly visible.
